MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 1
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 1
1. A psychometrician administers a depression inventory and forwards the raw scores to the
supervising psychologist, who integrates interview data, behavioral observations, and case
history before writing conclusions. Which statement best describes this process?
A. It is purely test administration because only one formal test was used
B. It is psychological assessment because multiple data sources were integrated for
evaluation
C. It is criterion-referenced classification because a supervisor reviewed the results
D. It is informal evaluation because behavioral observation was included
✅Answer: B. It is psychological assessment because multiple data sources were integrated
for evaluation
Rationale: Psychological assessment involves integrating multiple sources of information,
such as test results, interviews, observations, and case history, to arrive at an evaluative
conclusion.
2. Which assessment situation most clearly requires the use of a portfolio rather than a single
timed test?
A. Screening applicants for clerical speed
B. Estimating current verbal reasoning under standardized conditions
C. Evaluating growth in a student’s written work across a semester
D. Comparing two job applicants on reaction time
✅Answer: C. Evaluating growth in a student’s written work across a semester
Rationale: A portfolio is best suited for documenting development and change in actual work
products over time, such as a student’s writing across a semester.
3. A school examiner wants to compare a child’s mathematics performance with that of
same-age peers nationwide. Which score interpretation is most appropriate?
A. Idiographic
B. Norm-referenced
C. Ipsative
D. Content-referenced only
✅Answer: B. Norm-referenced
Rationale: Norm-referenced interpretation compares an individual’s score with the
performance of a defined reference group, such as same-age peers nationwide.
4. Which statement reflects the best distinction between a psychological trait and a
psychological state?
A. A trait is observable, while a state is always covert
B. A trait is enduring, while a state is relatively temporary or situation-bound
C. A trait is measured by interviews only, while a state is measured by tests only
D. A trait is biological, while a state is environmental
✅Answer: B. A trait is enduring, while a state is relatively temporary or situation-bound
Rationale: Traits are relatively stable patterns or tendencies, whereas states are temporary
conditions that may vary depending on time or situation.
5. An assessor says, “This instrument has little value because it samples only behavior shown
during testing.” Which core testing assumption is the assessor questioning?
A. Test-related behavior predicts non-test-related behavior
B. Traits cannot be quantified
C. Criterion measures are always superior to tests
D. Reliability is more important than validity
✅Answer: A. Test-related behavior predicts non-test-related behavior
Rationale: Psychological testing assumes that behavior sampled in the test situation can
meaningfully predict or represent behavior outside the testing situation.
6. Which historical figure is most directly associated with the first practical intelligence test used
to identify schoolchildren needing educational assistance?
A. Francis Galton
B. Alfred Binet
C. Charles Spearman
D. Hermann Rorschach
✅Answer: B. Alfred Binet
Rationale: Alfred Binet is most directly associated with the early intelligence test developed to
identify children who needed special educational assistance.
7. A practitioner concludes that a test must be useful because it has high internal consistency.
This conclusion is flawed because utility:
A. is identical to content validity
B. concerns practical value and decision consequences, not consistency alone
C. eliminates the need for cut scores
D. depends only on face validity
✅Answer: B. concerns practical value and decision consequences, not consistency alone
Rationale: Utility refers to the practical value of a test in actual decision-making contexts and
cannot be inferred from internal consistency alone.
8. Which is the clearest example of a criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. A child ranks at the 75th percentile in reading
B. An applicant scores above the cut score for basic safety knowledge
C. A student obtains a stanine of 8
D. A patient’s memory score is one standard deviation above the mean
✅Answer: B. An applicant scores above the cut score for basic safety knowledge
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation compares performance to a defined standard or
level of mastery rather than to other people.
9. A test developer wants the norm group to represent the population for whom the test will be
used. Which concept is most critical?
A. Random assignment
B. Standard error of estimate
C. Representative norming sample
D. Parallel-form equivalence
✅Answer: C. Representative norming sample
Rationale: Norms are meaningful only when the norming sample adequately represents the
population for whom the test is intended.
10. Which score distribution characteristic is most affected when a few extremely high scores
pull the mean upward?
A. Kurtosis only
B. Negative skew
C. Positive skew
D. Bimodality
✅Answer: C. Positive skew
Rationale: A few extremely high scores create a long right tail, which indicates positive skew.
11. In a normal distribution, which score lies farthest from the mean?
A. z = 0.00
B. z = -0.50
C. z = +1.00
D. z = -2.50
✅Answer: D. z = -2.50
Rationale: The score farthest from the mean is the one with the greatest absolute z-value,
which is 2.50.
12. Which correlation is most appropriate when both variables are ranks rather than
equal-interval scores?
A. Point-biserial
B. Pearson r
C. Spearman rho
D. Phi coefficient
✅Answer: C. Spearman rho
Rationale: Spearman rho is the appropriate correlation coefficient when both variables are
ranked or ordinal.
13. A validity coefficient of .36 indicates that the test:
A. explains 36% of the variance in the criterion
B. explains about 13% of the variance in the criterion
C. has poor reliability by definition
D. is unusable in all contexts
✅Answer: B. explains about 13% of the variance in the criterion
Rationale: Squaring the validity coefficient (.36² = .1296) shows that the test explains about
13% of the variance in the criterion.
14. Which situation best illustrates restricted range reducing an observed correlation?
A. A researcher correlates height with weight in the general population
B. An employer correlates entrance exam scores with performance using only
already-selected high scorers
C. A clinician correlates two symptom scales in a psychiatric sample
D. A teacher correlates quiz and final exam scores in one class
✅Answer: B. An employer correlates entrance exam scores with performance using only
already-selected high scorers
Rationale: Restricted range occurs when variability is reduced, as in a selected sample of
high scorers, which tends to lower the observed correlation.
15. A psychometrician gives the same anxiety test to the same people twice, four weeks apart,
to estimate stability over time. Which reliability estimate is being examined?
A. Inter-scorer reliability
B. Test-retest reliability
C. Split-half reliability
D. Alternate-forms reliability
✅Answer: B. Test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability evaluates the stability of scores across time by administering
the same test to the same group on two occasions.
16. Which type of reliability is most relevant for an essay test scored by two independent raters?
A. Equivalent-forms reliability
B. Inter-scorer reliability
C. Test-retest reliability
D. Internal consistency only
✅Answer: B. Inter-scorer reliability
Rationale: Inter-scorer reliability is most relevant when consistency across independent raters
or scorers must be established.
17. A scale measuring mood shows low test-retest reliability over a month. Which is the best
interpretation?
A. The scale is necessarily invalid
B. The construct may genuinely fluctuate over time
C. The scale must have poor content validity
D. The norm sample is unrepresentative
✅Answer: B. The construct may genuinely fluctuate over time
Rationale: Mood is often a temporary, state-like construct, so lower stability across time may
reflect real changes rather than poor measurement.
18. The standard error of measurement is most useful for:
A. deciding if a test is face valid
B. creating item distractors
C. estimating the band around an obtained score within which the true score likely falls
D. converting raw scores to percentiles
✅Answer: C. estimating the band around an obtained score within which the true score
likely falls
Rationale: The standard error of measurement provides an estimate of how much an
obtained score may differ from the examinee’s true score.
19. Which statement best captures the relationship between reliability and validity?
A. A valid test may be unreliable
B. A reliable test is always valid
C. Reliability is necessary but not sufficient for validity
D. Validity and reliability are unrelated
✅Answer: C. Reliability is necessary but not sufficient for validity
Rationale: A test must be sufficiently consistent to support valid interpretation, but reliability
alone does not guarantee that the test measures what it should.
20. A panel of subject matter experts reviews whether test items adequately sample the domain
of emergency-room triage knowledge. This provides evidence of:
A. criterion validity
B. content validity
C. construct irrelevance
D. incremental validity
✅Answer: B. content validity
Rationale: Content validity is supported when experts judge that test items adequately
represent the relevant knowledge or skill domain.
21. A hospital uses current supervisor ratings and current test scores gathered at the same time
to examine whether a new screening measure relates to nursing competence. This is evidence
of:
A. predictive validity
B. concurrent validity
C. face validity
D. discriminant validity
✅Answer: B. concurrent validity
Rationale: Concurrent validity is established when test scores are related to criterion
measures collected at the same time.
22. Which finding would most strongly support construct validity of a new social anxiety scale?
A. Examinees say the items look relevant
B. The scale correlates strongly with another validated social anxiety measure and weakly
with physical strength
C. The items were written clearly
D. The scale has many reverse-scored items
✅Answer: B. The scale correlates strongly with another validated social anxiety measure
and weakly with physical strength
Rationale: Construct validity is supported by convergence with related measures and
divergence from unrelated variables.
23. An employment test produces systematically lower scores for one cultural group because of
unnecessary language complexity unrelated to job performance. This concern is most directly
about:
A. utility gain
B. test bias
C. alternate-form reliability
D. divergent validity
✅Answer: B. test bias
Rationale: The language complexity introduces irrelevant barriers that affect one group
unfairly, making this a problem of test bias.
24. In utility analysis, the base rate refers to:
A. the percentage of test items answered correctly
B. the proportion of applicants who would succeed without using the test
C. the reliability coefficient before revision
D. the standardization group’s mean score
✅Answer: B. the proportion of applicants who would succeed without using the test
Rationale: In utility analysis, the base rate refers to the proportion of people who would
succeed even if the test were not used.
25. Which factor would most likely increase the utility of a selection test?
A. Lowering validity evidence requirements
B. Using the test where selection decisions are unimportant
C. Employing it in situations with meaningful decision consequences and adequate validity
D. Ignoring the base rate
✅Answer: C. Employing it in situations with meaningful decision consequences and
adequate validity
Rationale: Utility increases when a valid test is used in contexts where selection decisions
have important practical consequences.
26. A licensure panel asks experts to estimate the probability that a minimally competent
candidate would answer each item correctly, then averages those judgments to set the passing
score. Which method is being used?
A. Known-groups method
B. Angoff method
C. Test-retest method
D. Contrasted-groups reliability
✅Answer: B. Angoff method
Rationale: The Angoff method sets a cut score by asking experts to judge how likely a
minimally competent examinee is to answer each item correctly.
27. Which item would most likely have the highest discrimination index?
A. One answered correctly by both high and low scorers equally
B. One answered correctly by almost no one
C. One answered correctly much more often by high scorers than low scorers
D. One containing two keyed answers
✅Answer: C. One answered correctly much more often by high scorers than low scorers
Rationale: An item has high discrimination when it clearly differentiates high-performing
examinees from low-performing ones.
28. An item difficulty index of .85 on a four-option multiple-choice achievement test usually
indicates that the item is:
A. very difficult
B. moderately difficult
C. relatively easy
D. invalid
✅Answer: C. relatively easy
Rationale: An item difficulty index of .85 means that 85% of examinees answered the item
correctly, indicating that it is relatively easy.
29. A test developer wants to examine how the probability of endorsing an item changes across
levels of the underlying trait. Which concept is most relevant?
A. Barnum effect
B. Item-characteristic curve
C. Halo effect
D. Criterion contamination
✅Answer: B. Item-characteristic curve
Rationale: An item-characteristic curve shows the relationship between trait level and the
probability of endorsing or answering an item correctly.
30. During item writing, which practice best improves the quality of multiple-choice distractors?
A. Making one distractor obviously absurd
B. Using grammatical clues to the key
C. Creating plausible alternatives that reflect common errors in thinking
D. Making the longest option always correct
✅Answer: C. Creating plausible alternatives that reflect common errors in thinking
Rationale: Effective distractors are plausible and attract less knowledgeable examinees by
reflecting realistic errors or misconceptions.
31. Which revision decision is most appropriate after pilot testing reveals that a keyed item is
frequently missed by high scorers because of ambiguous wording?
A. Retain the item because difficulty improves discrimination
B. Discard or rewrite the item due to probable construct-irrelevant variance
C. Change the answer key without reviewing the stem
D. Convert the raw score to a percentile
✅Answer: B. Discard or rewrite the item due to probable construct-irrelevant variance
Rationale: Ambiguous wording introduces variance unrelated to the intended construct, so
the item should be revised or discarded.
32. A psychologist describes intelligence as a broad, general capacity that contributes to
performance across many mental tasks. This most closely reflects:
A. the projective hypothesis
B. Spearman’s g
C. radical behaviorism
D. criterion contamination
✅Answer: B. Spearman’s g
Rationale: Spearman’s g refers to a general intelligence factor believed to underlie
performance across varied cognitive tasks.
33. Which is the best example of the Flynn effect?
A. Scores on some intelligence tests rise across generations, requiring periodic renorming
B. Women always outperform men on verbal intelligence tasks
C. High-IQ individuals have perfect academic outcomes
D. Intelligence scores are stable across all cultures and time periods
✅Answer: A. Scores on some intelligence tests rise across generations, requiring periodic
renorming
Rationale: The Flynn effect refers to the observed rise in intelligence test scores across
generations, which makes renorming necessary.
34. A student shows strong fluid reasoning but average acquired academic knowledge. Which
distinction best captures this pattern?
A. High criterion validity, low content validity
B. Higher gf than gc
C. Better face validity than construct validity
D. Better verbal than performance reliability
✅Answer: B. Higher gf than gc
Rationale: Fluid intelligence refers to novel reasoning ability, whereas crystallized intelligence
refers to acquired knowledge, so the student shows higher gf than gc.
35. Which practice is most consistent with culturally informed intelligence assessment?
A. Interpreting all low scores as innate deficits
B. Ignoring language background because standardized procedures are sufficient
C. Considering acculturation, opportunity to learn, and linguistic demands before drawing
conclusions
D. Substituting informal opinion for all standardized data
✅Answer: C. Considering acculturation, opportunity to learn, and linguistic demands before
drawing conclusions
Rationale: Culturally informed assessment requires attention to language, background, and
learning opportunities to avoid invalid inferences.
36. Response to Intervention (RtI) is best understood as:
A. a projective method for personality assessment
B. a framework using tiered interventions and progress monitoring before or alongside special
education decisions
C. a military screening procedure
D. a method for setting cut scores in licensure exams
✅Answer: B. a framework using tiered interventions and progress monitoring before or
alongside special education decisions
Rationale: RtI is a tiered framework that uses intervention and progress monitoring to guide
educational decisions, including special education referral.
37. Dynamic assessment differs from traditional static testing because it emphasizes:
A. strictly one-time, no-feedback administration
B. learning potential through guided interaction and responsiveness to intervention
C. personality traits rather than abilities
D. only group-administered measures
✅Answer: B. learning potential through guided interaction and responsiveness to
intervention
Rationale: Dynamic assessment focuses on how well an individual learns or improves when
provided with guided assistance.
38. Which educational assessment method is most authentic?
A. Timed true-false test on music appreciation
B. Portfolio of drafts, revisions, and final compositions
C. Random guessing-corrected aptitude battery
D. Forced-choice interest inventory
✅Answer: B. Portfolio of drafts, revisions, and final compositions
Rationale: Authentic assessment emphasizes real-world performance and meaningful work
samples, which are captured well in a portfolio.
39. A reading diagnostic test is primarily intended to:
A. compare a student to the national norm group only
B. identify specific strengths and weaknesses to guide intervention
C. replace teacher observation entirely
D. determine personality type
✅Answer: B. identify specific strengths and weaknesses to guide intervention
Rationale: Diagnostic tests are designed to locate specific areas of difficulty and strength so
that targeted intervention can be planned.
40. Which statement best distinguishes aptitude from achievement tests?
A. Aptitude tests estimate learning potential or future performance; achievement tests sample
what has been learned
B. Aptitude tests are always untimed; achievement tests are always timed
C. Aptitude tests are invalid in schools
D. Achievement tests never use norms
✅Answer: A. Aptitude tests estimate learning potential or future performance; achievement
tests sample what has been learned
Rationale: Aptitude tests are designed to estimate potential for future learning or
performance, while achievement tests assess current learned knowledge or skill.
41. A personality assessor focused on enduring patterns of thinking, feeling, and behaving is
primarily assessing:
A. symptom frequency only
B. states only
C. personality traits
D. test-taking motivation only
✅Answer: C. personality traits
Rationale: Enduring patterns of thinking, feeling, and behaving are characteristic of
personality traits rather than temporary states.
42. Which test construction strategy begins with a theory and writes items to reflect theoretical
dimensions?
A. Criterion-group strategy
B. Rational-theoretical strategy
C. Purely empirical keying without theory
D. Random item sampling
✅Answer: B. Rational-theoretical strategy
Rationale: The rational-theoretical strategy begins with a theory of the construct and develops
items to represent its dimensions.
43. An empirically keyed personality inventory is most characterized by:
A. selecting items solely because experts think they sound clinically relevant
B. choosing items that distinguish a criterion group from others, even if item content seems
unrelated
C. avoiding statistical methods
D. requiring examinees to generate stories to pictures
✅Answer: B. choosing items that distinguish a criterion group from others, even if item
content seems unrelated
Rationale: Empirical keying retains items because they statistically differentiate groups, even
when the item content does not appear obviously related.
44. Which statement best describes an objective personality measure?
A. It is free from all interpretation
B. It usually uses structured stimuli and scoring rules
C. It always has higher validity than any projective method
D. It cannot measure psychopathology
✅Answer: B. It usually uses structured stimuli and scoring rules
Rationale: Objective personality measures typically rely on structured response formats and
standardized scoring procedures.
45. The projective hypothesis assumes that when people interpret ambiguous stimuli, they:
A. respond only with socially desirable answers
B. reveal underlying needs, conflicts, or characteristic modes of perceiving
C. become incapable of deception
D. produce responses with perfect inter-rater reliability
✅Answer: B. reveal underlying needs, conflicts, or characteristic modes of perceiving
Rationale: The projective hypothesis holds that responses to ambiguous stimuli reflect inner
dynamics, motives, conflicts, or habitual ways of perceiving.
46. Which procedure is most clearly projective?
A. Likert self-report inventory
B. Behavioral checklist
C. Storytelling to ambiguous interpersonal scenes
D. Speeded clerical comparison task
✅Answer: C. Storytelling to ambiguous interpersonal scenes
Rationale: Projective methods use ambiguous stimuli, such as interpersonal scenes, to elicit
responses that may reveal underlying personality dynamics.
47. Behavioral assessment places greatest emphasis on:
A. latent symbolic meaning only
B. observable behavior and the conditions surrounding it
C. unconscious conflicts inferred from inkblots alone
D. intellectual ability as the source of all symptoms
✅Answer: B. observable behavior and the conditions surrounding it
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on directly observable behavior and the situational
factors that influence it.
48. A clinician records the antecedents and consequences of a child’s tantrums at home and
school. This is most consistent with:
A. factor analysis
B. functional behavioral assessment
C. Barnum interpretation
D. projective scoring
✅Answer: B. functional behavioral assessment
Rationale: Functional behavioral assessment examines antecedents and consequences to
understand the function of behavior.
49. Which concern is especially relevant in behavioral observation?
A. Whether the measure appears attractive to examinees
B. Whether raters drift over time and apply categories inconsistently
C. Whether items reflect unconscious wishes
D. Whether the assessor can compute a percentile
✅Answer: B. Whether raters drift over time and apply categories inconsistently
Rationale: Behavioral observation depends heavily on consistent application of categories, so
rater drift is an important concern.
50. In clinical assessment, which sequence is most defensible?
A. Diagnose first, gather data later
B. Integrate interview, history, test, and behavioral data before concluding
C. Rely on one well-known test if it has high face validity
D. Use only mechanical prediction and ignore context
✅Answer: B. Integrate interview, history, test, and behavioral data before concluding
Rationale: Sound clinical assessment requires integrating multiple relevant sources of data
before drawing conclusions.
51. A clinician uses assessment data mainly to clarify diagnosis and plan treatment. This
illustrates the:
A. recreational function of testing
B. clinical decision-making function of assessment
C. purely legal function of testing
D. anti-psychometric function of interviews
✅Answer: B. clinical decision-making function of assessment
Rationale: In clinical settings, assessment is often used to support diagnosis, case
formulation, and treatment planning.
52. Which statement about case history data is most accurate?
A. They are always more objective than test scores
B. They are useless unless verified by laboratory tests
C. They can provide important context but must be evaluated for accuracy and relevance
D. They should replace direct examination
✅Answer: C. They can provide important context but must be evaluated for accuracy and
relevance
Rationale: Case history data can be highly informative, but they must still be critically
examined for accuracy, relevance, and possible bias.
53. The Barnum effect refers to:
A. the tendency to prefer highly specific, individualized interpretations
B. the acceptance of vague, general personality descriptions as uniquely accurate
C. the inflation of reliability by repeated testing
D. the decline in performance due to stereotype threat
✅Answer: B. the acceptance of vague, general personality descriptions as uniquely
accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect occurs when people accept broad, general statements as
personally precise and accurate.
54. Which situation best illustrates a forensic assessment role?
A. Evaluating interventions for reading difficulty
B. Assessing competency to stand trial
C. Measuring job satisfaction among nurses
D. Monitoring treatment adherence in diabetes
✅Answer: B. Assessing competency to stand trial
Rationale: Forensic assessment applies psychological evaluation to legal questions, such as
competency to stand trial.
55. In custody evaluation, the assessor’s central responsibility is to:
A. advocate for the parent who first sought the referral
B. determine which parent appears more distressed
C. evaluate factors relevant to the child’s best interests
D. guarantee shared custody
✅Answer: C. evaluate factors relevant to the child’s best interests
Rationale: The central focus of custody evaluation is the welfare and best interests of the
child.
56. In suicide assessment, which factor generally warrants immediate priority?
A. Preference for projective over objective tests
B. Presence of imminent intent, plan, means, and recent escalation
C. IQ level relative to norms
D. Whether the client likes the assessor
✅Answer: B. Presence of imminent intent, plan, means, and recent escalation
Rationale: Immediate suicide risk is most strongly indicated by imminent intent, a plan,
available means, and recent escalation.
57. Which referral question most clearly indicates the need for a neuropsychological evaluation?
A. “What career field matches this student’s interests?”
B. “Does this employee prefer teamwork?”
C. “Has this older adult’s memory decline reflected possible brain dysfunction?”
D. “Is this applicant socially extroverted?”
✅Answer: C. “Has this older adult’s memory decline reflected possible brain dysfunction?”
Rationale: Neuropsychological evaluation is indicated when there is concern about cognitive
decline or possible brain dysfunction.
58. Which task is most closely associated with executive functioning?
A. Color naming only
B. Cognitive flexibility, planning, and response inhibition
C. Simple auditory acuity
D. Measuring hand size
✅Answer: B. Cognitive flexibility, planning, and response inhibition
Rationale: Executive functioning includes planning, inhibition, cognitive flexibility, and other
higher-order control processes.
59. A patient performs poorly on tasks requiring abstract concept formation and shifting mental
set. Which area is most implicated?
A. Executive function
B. Olfactory discrimination only
C. Visual acuity
D. Expressive drawing style
✅Answer: A. Executive function
Rationale: Abstract reasoning and mental set shifting are core executive functions.
60. A major goal of neuropsychological batteries is to:
A. replace medical history and examination entirely
B. sample multiple cognitive domains to detect patterns associated with brain dysfunction
C. classify personality types
D. establish vocational interests
✅Answer: B. sample multiple cognitive domains to detect patterns associated with brain
dysfunction
Rationale: Neuropsychological batteries assess multiple domains of functioning to identify
cognitive patterns consistent with brain impairment.
61. Which finding most strongly supports using repeated cognitive testing in suspected
dementia?
A. Personality is always stable
B. Serial measurement can document progressive decline over time
C. Test norms never change
D. One score is enough for all future decisions
✅Answer: B. Serial measurement can document progressive decline over time
Rationale: Repeated cognitive testing helps determine whether cognitive decline is
progressive, stable, or improving over time.
62. Which is the best example of a measure of vocational interest?
A. Strong Interest Inventory
B. WAIS-IV Digit Span
C. Rorschach Inkblot Test
D. Bender Gestalt Test
✅Answer: A. Strong Interest Inventory
Rationale: The Strong Interest Inventory is a well-known measure designed to assess
vocational interests.
63. In personnel selection, which predictor is most directly designed to sample applicant
behavior similar to job tasks?
A. Biodata scale
B. Performance test
C. Interest inventory
D. Self-esteem scale
✅Answer: B. Performance test
Rationale: Performance tests directly sample behaviors or skills similar to those required on
the job.
64. Which statement best reflects incremental validity?
A. A new test has the same reliability as an old one
B. A new predictor improves decision accuracy beyond information already available
C. A test predicts all jobs equally well
D. A cut score was set by experts
✅Answer: B. A new predictor improves decision accuracy beyond information already
available
Rationale: Incremental validity refers to the added predictive value of a new measure beyond
existing predictors.
65. A company already uses interviews and academic records. It considers adding a brief
cognitive screening measure only if it improves prediction of training success. The company is
evaluating:
A. stereotype threat
B. incremental validity
C. content underrepresentation
D. testwiseness
✅Answer: B. incremental validity
Rationale: The company is determining whether the new measure adds predictive value
beyond current selection information.
66. Which variable is most directly relevant when an organization studies whether using a
screening test leads to better hiring outcomes than selecting applicants without the test?
A. Utility
B. Skewness
C. Face validity only
D. Response acquiescence
✅Answer: A. Utility
Rationale: Utility concerns whether a test improves practical decision outcomes, such as
better hiring results.
67. Which is the strongest reason letters of recommendation are often interpreted cautiously in
personnel decisions?
A. They are always invalid
B. They may be selective, inflated, or based on nonstandard criteria
C. They cannot be read legally
D. They always show low internal consistency
✅Answer: B. They may be selective, inflated, or based on nonstandard criteria
Rationale: Letters of recommendation often vary widely in candor and standards, which limits
their comparability and objectivity.
68. An interviewer lets one impressive credential color all judgments of the applicant’s other
traits. This error is called:
A. halo effect
B. curvilinear restriction
C. criterion deficiency
D. factor loading
✅Answer: A. halo effect
Rationale: The halo effect occurs when one positive characteristic influences ratings of
unrelated characteristics.
69. Which statement about interviews is most defensible?
A. Unstructured interviews are always superior because they are more natural
B. Interviews can be informative, but reliability improves when structure and scoring rules
increase
C. Interviews are not assessment tools
D. Rapport reduces all interviewer error
✅Answer: B. Interviews can be informative, but reliability improves when structure and
scoring rules increase
Rationale: Interviews can yield valuable information, but increased structure generally
improves reliability and consistency.
70. Which situation best illustrates ecological momentary assessment?
A. Annual administration of a comprehensive IQ test
B. In-the-moment smartphone prompts tracking mood and behavior in daily life
C. One-time projective testing in a clinic
D. A paper interest inventory completed after graduation
✅Answer: B. In-the-moment smartphone prompts tracking mood and behavior in daily life
Rationale: Ecological momentary assessment collects real-time data in natural settings, often
using mobile devices.
71. According to the PAP Code of Ethics, online psychological services:
A. are exempt from the standards governing face-to-face services
B. may be provided only by psychometricians without supervision
C. remain governed by the same ethical principles that apply to face-to-face services
D. are prohibited in all cases
✅Answer: C. remain governed by the same ethical principles that apply to face-to-face
services
Rationale: The PAP Code states that psychological services delivered online remain subject
to the same ethical principles as face-to-face services.
72. Under the PAP Code, respect for dignity is most directly linked to:
A. maximizing profit from test sales
B. free and informed consent, privacy, and confidentiality
C. avoiding all collaboration with other professionals
D. limiting services to urban populations
✅Answer: B. free and informed consent, privacy, and confidentiality
Rationale: Respect for dignity includes honoring informed consent, privacy, and confidentiality
in psychological work.
73. A practitioner continues using a specialized neuropsychological procedure despite having
no training in it and no consultation. Which ethical principle is most clearly violated?
A. Justice only
B. Boundaries of competence
C. Fidelity to employer demands
D. Right to public advertising
✅Answer: B. Boundaries of competence
Rationale: Practitioners must provide services only within the boundaries of their education,
training, and supervised experience.
74. A psychometrician is asked by a relative to administer and interpret a complex battery
independently for a medico-legal case. Under RA 10029-related scope and the PAP Code, the
best response is to:
A. accept because family members may waive all requirements
B. interpret the full battery as long as raw scores are available
C. work only within lawful and competence boundaries, with appropriate supervision/referral
as needed
D. proceed if the client signs a blanket consent
✅Answer: C. work only within lawful and competence boundaries, with appropriate
supervision/referral as needed
Rationale: The psychometrician must remain within lawful scope of practice and competence
limits, and seek supervision or referral when the task exceeds those boundaries.
75. Which action best reflects proper handling of confidentiality limits?
A. Avoid discussing limits unless the client asks
B. Explain anticipated limits of confidentiality before the service begins
C. Guarantee absolute secrecy in every circumstance
D. Discuss limits only after a breach occurs
✅Answer: B. Explain anticipated limits of confidentiality before the service begins
Rationale: Ethical practice requires discussing anticipated limits of confidentiality at the outset
so the client can give informed consent.
76. A psychologist receives a third-party referral from a company to assess an employee.
Ethically, the psychologist should clarify at the outset:
A. only the fee arrangement
B. who the client is, intended uses of information, expected role, and confidentiality limits
C. that the employee has no rights to information
D. that the employer automatically owns all raw data for any purpose
✅Answer: B. who the client is, intended uses of information, expected role, and
confidentiality limits
Rationale: In third-party referrals, the psychologist must clarify roles, the identity of the client,
intended uses of information, and limits of confidentiality.
77. Which is the best example of a potentially harmful multiple relationship?
A. A psychologist teaches a workshop to a large audience
B. A psychologist conducts therapy for a client while negotiating a business partnership with
that client
C. A psychometrician administers a test under supervision
D. A clinician consults a physician about medication interactions
✅Answer: B. A psychologist conducts therapy for a client while negotiating a business
partnership with that client
Rationale: This creates a dual role that risks impaired objectivity, exploitation, and harm to the
client.
78. Which situation most clearly reflects exploitative conduct?
A. Referring beyond one’s competence
B. Using one’s authority over a supervisee to pressure the supervisee into providing personal
favors
C. Recording a session with consent
D. Consulting with colleagues using de-identified information
✅Answer: B. Using one’s authority over a supervisee to pressure the supervisee into
providing personal favors
Rationale: Using professional authority for personal benefit is exploitative and violates ethical
standards.
79. A practitioner becomes aware that personal distress is interfering with competent work
performance. The most ethical response is to:
A. continue full duties to avoid inconvenience
B. take appropriate measures such as consultation and limiting or suspending duties if
needed
C. conceal the problem unless a complaint is filed
D. shift all responsibility to the client
✅Answer: B. take appropriate measures such as consultation and limiting or suspending
duties if needed
Rationale: Ethical practice requires addressing personal problems that interfere with
competence, including seeking consultation and reducing duties when necessary.
80. When delegating work to an assistant, an ethical practitioner should:
A. delegate any task if the assistant agrees
B. ensure delegated tasks match the assistant’s education, training, or supervised capability
C. avoid informing the client
D. delegate interpretation of any complex results to save time
✅Answer: B. ensure delegated tasks match the assistant’s education, training, or
supervised capability
Rationale: Delegated work must be appropriate to the assistant’s training and competence,
with supervision as needed.
81. Which act most clearly violates ethical standards on public statements?
A. Listing office hours and services offered
B. Stating one’s earned degree accurately
C. Claiming guaranteed cure rates unsupported by evidence
D. Identifying one’s certification status truthfully
✅Answer: C. Claiming guaranteed cure rates unsupported by evidence
Rationale: False, deceptive, or exaggerated claims about services or outcomes violate ethical
standards on public statements.
82. A practitioner wants to use a client’s case details in a seminar. Which is most ethical?
A. Present identifying details because educational use overrides confidentiality
B. Disclose only if the client consents in writing, legal authority exists, or the case is
adequately disguised
C. Share the case casually if names are omitted but unusual details remain
D. Post the story on social media because it is professionally interesting
✅Answer: B. Disclose only if the client consents in writing, legal authority exists, or the case
is adequately disguised
Rationale: Confidential information may be used only with proper written consent, legal
authorization, or adequate disguise to protect identity.
83. Which statement best reflects ethical handling of recorded sessions?
A. Recording is acceptable if it improves convenience
B. Consent should be obtained before recording voices or images, with explanation of
anticipated uses
C. Recordings belong solely to the practitioner and need no safeguards
D. Verbal refusal may be ignored if treatment is ongoing
✅Answer: B. Consent should be obtained before recording voices or images, with
explanation of anticipated uses
Rationale: Recording requires prior consent and explanation of the intended use of the
recording.
84. A hospital policy conflicts with a psychologist’s ethical obligation to protect confidentiality.
According to the PAP Code, the psychologist should first:
A. immediately ignore the law and policy
B. attempt to resolve the conflict while remaining committed to the Code, then follow
governing legal authority if unresolved
C. release all records to avoid conflict
D. terminate all services automatically
✅Answer: B. attempt to resolve the conflict while remaining committed to the Code, then
follow governing legal authority if unresolved
Rationale: The PAP Code directs practitioners first to try resolving conflicts between ethics
and law or institutional demands while remaining committed to ethical principles.
85. Which action is most appropriate when consulting with a colleague about a difficult case?
A. Reveal all identifying information to speed consultation
B. Disclose only information necessary for professional purposes and avoid unnecessary
identifiers
C. Send the entire file to multiple acquaintances
D. Post anonymized excerpts publicly for crowd input
✅Answer: B. Disclose only information necessary for professional purposes and avoid
unnecessary identifiers
Rationale: Ethical consultation requires minimizing invasion of privacy by limiting disclosure to
relevant information and avoiding unnecessary identifiers.
86. A psychometrician notices that another practitioner may have committed a minor ethical
lapse that can be resolved directly without breaching confidentiality. The PAP Code suggests
first considering:
A. public accusation on social media
B. informal resolution by bringing the issue to the practitioner’s attention
C. immediate resignation from the profession
D. disclosure of client identities to the media
✅Answer: B. informal resolution by bringing the issue to the practitioner’s attention
Rationale: The PAP Code allows initial informal resolution when it is sufficient and does not
violate confidentiality rights.
87. Which of the following best reflects fairness in assessment across cultural groups?
A. Interpreting identical raw scores as equally meaningful regardless of language or
opportunity to learn
B. Considering whether culture, language, and context affect inference and test use
C. Avoiding all standardized tests with minority clients
D. Using only face validity to judge fairness
✅Answer: B. Considering whether culture, language, and context affect inference and test
use
Rationale: Fair assessment requires evaluating how culture, language, and context may
influence score meaning and interpretation.
88. A test translated into another language changes item meanings and lowers performance for
reasons unrelated to the target construct. This is primarily a problem of:
A. construct-irrelevant variance
B. utility gain
C. ipsative comparison
D. split-half improvement
✅Answer: A. construct-irrelevant variance
Rationale: The translation has introduced variance unrelated to the intended construct, which
distorts interpretation.
89. In educational testing, peer appraisal and authentic assessment are often valued because
they:
A. eliminate the need for reliability evidence
B. can capture performance in more naturalistic tasks
C. always replace standardized tests
D. are free from all bias
✅Answer: B. can capture performance in more naturalistic tasks
Rationale: Peer appraisal and authentic assessment can reflect meaningful real-world
performance in ways traditional tests may not.
90. Which statement is most accurate regarding clinical versus mechanical prediction?
A. Clinical prediction always outperforms statistical methods
B. Mechanical prediction always renders interviews useless
C. Each approach has strengths; structured actuarial methods often improve consistency, but
context-sensitive integration remains important
D. They are identical processes
✅Answer: C. Each approach has strengths; structured actuarial methods often improve
consistency, but context-sensitive integration remains important
Rationale: Structured actuarial methods often improve consistency, but careful contextual
integration remains important in many applied settings.
91. A psychologist uses the MMPI-2-RF mainly to generate hypotheses rather than final
conclusions in isolation. This practice is best because:
A. objective inventories have no validity evidence
B. test data should be integrated with other sources rather than treated as self-sufficient
C. diagnosis should ignore interviews
D. projectives are always superior
✅Answer: B. test data should be integrated with other sources rather than treated as
self-sufficient
Rationale: Even strong objective test data should be interpreted as part of a broader
assessment process that includes other sources of information.
92. Which would be the best indicator that an intelligence test score should be interpreted
cautiously?
A. The score is above average
B. The examinee had adequate motivation and understood directions
C. The examinee had limited proficiency in the test language and unfamiliarity with item
formats
D. The standardization sample was large
✅Answer: C. The examinee had limited proficiency in the test language and unfamiliarity
with item formats
Rationale: Limited language proficiency and unfamiliarity with testing formats can distort
performance and make interpretation less valid.
93. Which assessment choice best fits a patient with suspected malingering in a compensation
case?
A. Rely only on self-description
B. Integrate symptom validity data, interview findings, records, and behavioral observations
C. Avoid all formal testing because malingering cannot be assessed
D. Use a vocational interest inventory alone
✅Answer: B. Integrate symptom validity data, interview findings, records, and behavioral
observations
Rationale: Suspected malingering is best assessed through multiple converging sources of
evidence, including validity data, interviews, records, and observation.
94. A business psychologist studies organizational culture, job satisfaction, and commitment to
understand turnover. This work most directly falls under:
A. neuropsychological screening
B. industrial-organizational assessment
C. projective testing
D. forensic competency evaluation
✅Answer: B. industrial-organizational assessment
Rationale: Studying organizational culture, job satisfaction, commitment, and turnover is
central to industrial-organizational assessment.
95. Which statement most accurately reflects psychometrician supervision in Philippine
practice?
A. Psychometricians may independently perform all psychological interpretations in all
settings
B. Supervision is irrelevant if a client signs consent
C. Psychometricians must work within lawful scope and appropriate supervision
arrangements, especially for interpretation and higher-order evaluative functions
D. Psychometricians may assume psychologist functions during emergencies without limits
✅Answer: C. Psychometricians must work within lawful scope and appropriate supervision
arrangements, especially for interpretation and higher-order evaluative functions
Rationale: Philippine practice requires psychometricians to stay within legal scope and
appropriate supervision, particularly for interpretation and broader evaluative responsibilities.
96. A practitioner explains to a court-ordered examinee that the evaluation is mandated and that
confidentiality is limited. This is an example of:
A. coercive deception
B. informed consent under mandated service conditions
C. improper advertising
D. criterion contamination
✅Answer: B. informed consent under mandated service conditions
Rationale: Even in mandated services, the examinee should be informed about the nature of
the service and its confidentiality limits.
97. Which is the best example of criterion contamination in validation research?
A. The criterion includes information derived from the predictor test itself
B. The predictor has moderate internal consistency
C. The test contains too many easy items
D. The norm group is stratified by region
✅Answer: A. The criterion includes information derived from the predictor test itself
Rationale: Criterion contamination occurs when the criterion measure is influenced by the
predictor, artificially inflating the apparent relationship.
98. A measure has excellent reliability and strong evidence it predicts training success, but it is
expensive, time-consuming, and offers little improvement over cheaper existing methods. The
main question remaining concerns:
A. utility
B. item difficulty
C. test bias alone
D. inter-rater reliability
✅Answer: A. utility
Rationale: The remaining issue is whether the test provides enough practical value to justify
its costs and limited added benefit.
99. Which pioneer is most closely associated with inkblot-based personality assessment?
A. David Wechsler
B. Hermann Rorschach
C. Alfred Binet
D. Henry Murray
✅Answer: B. Hermann Rorschach
Rationale: Hermann Rorschach is the pioneer most closely associated with inkblot-based
personality assessment.
100. Which ethical and psychometric stance is best when writing a final psychological report?
A. Present dramatic conclusions beyond the data to appear decisive
B. Integrate findings carefully, communicate accurately, and avoid overinterpretation
C. Report only test scores and exclude context
D. Use vague statements so all stakeholders feel satisfied
✅Answer: B. Integrate findings carefully, communicate accurately, and avoid
overinterpretation
Rationale: A sound psychological report should be accurate, evidence-based, integrated,
and restrained in its conclusions.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 2
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 2
1. A school psychologist combines test scores, interview data, behavioral observations, and
case history before making a recommendation. This best illustrates:
A. test bias
B. psychological assessment
C. item analysis
D. test standardization
✅Answer: B. psychological assessment
Rationale: Psychological assessment is the broader process of gathering, integrating, and
interpreting multiple sources of data rather than relying on a single test.
2. Which statement best distinguishes a psychological test from psychological assessment?
A. A test always yields qualitative data, whereas assessment yields quantitative data.
B. A test is one tool, whereas assessment is the broader process of gathering and integrating
data.
C. A test is used only in schools, whereas assessment is used only in clinics.
D. A test is less scientific than assessment.
✅Answer: B. A test is one tool, whereas assessment is the broader process of gathering and
integrating data.
Rationale: A psychological test is a single instrument, while assessment is the comprehensive
process that integrates multiple tools and sources of information.
3. A clinician infers depression severity from a client’s score on a self-report inventory. The
score itself is best viewed as:
A. a trait
B. a construct
C. a sample of behavior
D. a norm group
✅Answer: C. a sample of behavior
Rationale: Test scores represent a limited sample of behavior from which inferences about
constructs such as depression are made.
4. Which of the following is the clearest example of covert behavior?
A. crying during an interview
B. pacing in the hallway
C. endorsing “I feel hopeless” on a checklist
D. silently worrying about failure
✅Answer: D. silently worrying about failure
Rationale: Covert behavior refers to internal processes such as thoughts and feelings that are
not directly observable.
5. A guidance counselor says, “This instrument is only one source of data, so I will not base my
recommendation on it alone.” This statement is most consistent with the idea that:
A. tests are perfectly objective
B. tests eliminate error variance
C. tests have strengths and weaknesses
D. criterion-referenced testing is superior to norm-referenced testing
✅Answer: C. tests have strengths and weaknesses
Rationale: No single test provides complete information; assessment requires recognizing
both the strengths and limitations of tools.
6. Which situation best reflects criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. A student scored higher than 82% of examinees in the norm group.
B. An applicant placed in the top decile of all candidates.
C. A trainee demonstrated all required safety competencies.
D. A child’s score was average for age.
✅Answer: C. A trainee demonstrated all required safety competencies.
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation compares performance to predefined standards
or competencies rather than to other individuals.
7. Which is the best example of norm-referenced interpretation?
A. “The examinee correctly demonstrated all five required procedures.”
B. “The examinee performed above the mean of the standardization sample.”
C. “The examinee met the passing standard set by subject-matter experts.”
D. “The examinee completed the intervention goals.”
✅Answer: B. “The examinee performed above the mean of the standardization sample.”
Rationale: Norm-referenced interpretation compares an individual's score to a reference group
or standardization sample.
8. A test has excellent internal consistency but poor predictive validity for college GPA. This
means:
A. the test is invalid because it is unreliable
B. the items are homogeneous, but the test may not predict the intended criterion well
C. the test has no measurement error
D. the test must be culture-fair
✅Answer: B. the items are homogeneous, but the test may not predict the intended criterion
well
Rationale: Internal consistency reflects item homogeneity, while predictive validity concerns
how well scores forecast an external criterion.
9. In classical test theory, an observed score is composed of:
A. item difficulty and item discrimination
B. true score and error
C. validity and utility
D. content and criterion
✅Answer: B. true score and error
Rationale: Classical test theory defines the observed score as the sum of the true score and
measurement error.
10. Which source of error is most likely when a student obtains a much lower score because the
room is excessively noisy?
A. construct underrepresentation
B. situation-specific error variance
C. criterion contamination
D. content sampling
✅Answer: B. situation-specific error variance
Rationale: Environmental factors like noise introduce temporary, situation-specific error
affecting test performance.
11. A psychometrician administers the same test to the same group after two weeks to examine
score stability. This procedure estimates:
A. internal consistency
B. interscorer reliability
C. test-retest reliability
D. content validity
✅Answer: C. test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability evaluates the stability of scores over time.
12. A test developer creates two equivalent forms of a test to reduce practice effects. The
reliability evidence most relevant is:
A. alternate-forms reliability
B. face validity
C. inter-item consistency
D. criterion contamination
✅Answer: A. alternate-forms reliability
Rationale: Alternate-forms reliability evaluates consistency across different but equivalent
versions of a test.
13. Which reliability method is most appropriate when the test contains items intended to
measure a single domain at one point in time?
A. test-retest
B. alternate forms
C. internal consistency
D. interrater agreement only
✅Answer: C. internal consistency
Rationale: Internal consistency measures how well items within a single test administration
assess the same construct.
14. Standard error of measurement is most useful for:
A. identifying whether a test has face validity
B. estimating the range within which a person’s true score likely falls
C. computing percentile rank directly
D. determining item distractor quality
✅Answer: B. estimating the range within which a person’s true score likely falls
Rationale: SEM provides an estimate of how much an observed score may differ from the
true score.
15. A coefficient alpha of .92 on a depression inventory most strongly suggests:
A. excellent homogeneity among items
B. high predictive validity
C. absence of faking
D. freedom from cultural bias
✅Answer: A. excellent homogeneity among items
Rationale: A high alpha coefficient indicates strong internal consistency among test items.
16. Which statement about validity is most accurate?
A. Validity is a property of the test itself and never of score interpretation.
B. Validity refers to the degree to which an interpretation of scores is appropriate for a given
purpose.
C. If a test is reliable, it is automatically valid.
D. Face validity is the strongest form of validity evidence.
✅Answer: B. Validity refers to the degree to which an interpretation of scores is appropriate
for a given purpose.
Rationale: Validity concerns the appropriateness of interpretations and uses of test scores.
17. Which is the best example of content validity evidence?
A. Scores correlate with a future criterion.
B. Test items adequately sample the defined domain of knowledge.
C. Two scorers agree in rating essays.
D. Scores differ by age group.
✅Answer: B. Test items adequately sample the defined domain of knowledge.
Rationale: Content validity is demonstrated when items represent the entire domain being
measured.
18. A hospital uses a new cognitive screening tool and correlates its scores with neurologists’
current diagnoses. This provides evidence of:
A. predictive validity
B. concurrent validity
C. face validity
D. split-half reliability
✅Answer: B. concurrent validity
Rationale: Concurrent validity is established when test scores correlate with current external
criteria.
19. A board examination is validated by showing that scores predict later training performance.
This is evidence of:
A. content validity
B. predictive validity
C. discriminant validity
D. interscorer reliability
✅Answer: B. predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity is demonstrated when scores forecast future performance.
20. Which finding best supports construct validity?
A. Test directions are easy to follow.
B. Experts say the test looks appropriate.
C. Scores correlate positively with related constructs and weakly with unrelated constructs.
D. The test has high alternate-form reliability.
✅Answer: C. Scores correlate positively with related constructs and weakly with unrelated
constructs.
Rationale: Construct validity is supported by expected relationships with similar and dissimilar
constructs.
21. A measure of social anxiety correlates highly with another social anxiety scale and weakly
with a numerical reasoning test. This pattern reflects:
A. face validity and utility
B. convergent and discriminant evidence
C. predictive and concurrent evidence
D. internal consistency and equivalence
✅Answer: B. convergent and discriminant evidence
Rationale: High correlation with similar constructs and low correlation with unrelated
constructs demonstrates convergent and discriminant validity.
22. A company selects employees using a highly valid test, but the test is too expensive relative
to the benefit gained. The issue being raised is:
A. construct validity
B. utility
C. standardization
D. interscorer reliability
✅Answer: B. utility
Rationale: Utility refers to the practical value of a test considering costs and benefits.
23. Which factor directly affects test utility in personnel selection?
A. the color of the answer sheet
B. base rate, selection ratio, and validity coefficient
C. only internal consistency
D. only the number of items
✅Answer: B. base rate, selection ratio, and validity coefficient
Rationale: These factors determine the effectiveness and usefulness of a selection
procedure.
24. A cut score is best defined as:
A. the raw mean of the standardization sample
B. the point above or below which decisions differ
C. a score transformed into a z score
D. a score adjusted for regression to the mean
✅Answer: B. the point above or below which decisions differ
Rationale: A cut score is a decision threshold used to classify examinees.
25. The Angoff method is primarily used to:
A. estimate reliability by split-half methods
B. set a defensible passing score using expert judgment
C. derive percentile norms
D. calculate item-total correlations
✅Answer: B. set a defensible passing score using expert judgment
Rationale: The Angoff method uses expert estimates to determine a minimum passing score.
26. During test conceptualization, the most fundamental first step is to:
A. print answer sheets
B. identify the domain and purpose of the test
C. compute coefficient alpha
D. establish local norms immediately
✅Answer: B. identify the domain and purpose of the test
Rationale: Test development begins with clearly defining what is to be measured and why.
27. Which item is likely to have the highest difficulty index on an achievement test?
A. the item most students answer correctly
B. the item most students leave blank
C. the item experts consider ambiguous
D. the longest item
✅Answer: A. the item most students answer correctly
Rationale: Higher difficulty index (p-value) means the item is easier and answered correctly
by many examinees.
28. An item discrimination index is most concerned with whether an item:
A. appears fair to examinees
B. differentiates high scorers from low scorers
C. is free of all guessing
D. uses simple language
✅Answer: B. differentiates high scorers from low scorers
Rationale: Discrimination indicates how well an item distinguishes between high and low
performers.
29. A distractor that no one chooses is usually considered:
A. highly functioning
B. plausible and useful
C. weak and in need of revision
D. evidence of predictive validity
✅Answer: C. weak and in need of revision
Rationale: A distractor must attract some examinees; otherwise, it is ineffective.
30. Which practice most improves item writing?
A. using unnecessarily complex wording to increase difficulty
B. writing stems with one clearly best answer and plausible distractors
C. placing grammatical clues in the correct answer
D. making all distractors obviously false
✅Answer: B. writing stems with one clearly best answer and plausible distractors
Rationale: Good item construction requires clarity and plausible alternatives to enhance
discrimination.
31. A clinician asks identical core questions of every client but also follows up flexibly as
needed. This is best described as:
A. an unstructured interview
B. a structured interview only
C. a semistructured interview
D. a projective interview
✅Answer: C. a semistructured interview
Rationale: Semistructured interviews combine standardized questions with flexible probing.
32. The mental status examination is primarily intended to:
A. estimate item discrimination
B. survey current cognitive, emotional, and behavioral functioning
C. replace all formal testing
D. measure vocational interests
✅Answer: B. survey current cognitive, emotional, and behavioral functioning
Rationale: The MSE evaluates present mental functioning including mood, cognition, and
behavior.
33. Which of the following is the clearest interview threat to reliability?
A. consistent use of standardized prompts
B. heavy dependence on interviewer impressions without clear criteria
C. audio recording with consent
D. note-taking after the session
✅Answer: B. heavy dependence on interviewer impressions without clear criteria
Rationale: Lack of structure and criteria reduces consistency across interviews.
34. Alfred Binet’s major contribution to assessment history was:
A. the development of the first projective test
B. a practical intelligence test for identifying schoolchildren needing educational support
C. the invention of factor analysis
D. the creation of the MMPI
✅Answer: B. a practical intelligence test for identifying schoolchildren needing educational
support
Rationale: Binet developed an early intelligence test to identify children needing assistance.
35. Francis Galton is most closely associated with:
A. dynamic assessment
B. sensory and psychophysical approaches to individual differences
C. the Rorschach method
D. the Wechsler scales
✅Answer: B. sensory and psychophysical approaches to individual differences
Rationale: Galton studied individual differences using sensory and measurement approaches.
36. Charles Spearman is best known for proposing:
A. multiple intelligences only
B. general intelligence or g
C. unconditional positive regard
D. the Barnum effect
✅Answer: B. general intelligence or g
Rationale: Spearman proposed a general factor underlying cognitive abilities.
37. Which statement best captures Wechsler’s view of intelligence?
A. It is identical to sensory acuity.
B. It is a single school-taught skill only.
C. It is the aggregate or global capacity to act purposefully, think rationally, and deal
effectively with the environment.
D. It cannot be measured.
✅Answer: C. It is the aggregate or global capacity to act purposefully, think rationally, and
deal effectively with the environment.
Rationale: This definition reflects Wechsler’s multidimensional view of intelligence.
38. A psychologist explains that an IQ score is no longer interpreted as mental age divided by
chronological age for modern individual tests. This refers to the shift toward:
A. ratio IQ
B. deviation IQ
C. ipsative scoring
D. domain sampling
✅Answer: B. deviation IQ
Rationale: Modern IQ scores are based on comparison with age norms rather than ratio
calculations.
39. The Flynn effect refers to:
A. the decline of test reliability over time
B. generational increases in measured intelligence test performance
C. the tendency of raters to agree
D. score inflation caused by malingering
✅Answer: B. generational increases in measured intelligence test performance
Rationale: The Flynn effect describes rising IQ scores across generations.
40. Which would most likely reduce the validity of an intelligence test for a child who does not
understand the language of administration?
A. high internal consistency
B. construct-irrelevant variance
C. deviation IQ
D. interscorer agreement
✅Answer: B. construct-irrelevant variance
Rationale: Language barriers introduce variance unrelated to the construct being measured.
41. In educational assessment, Response to Intervention is primarily used to:
A. eliminate teacher judgment
B. monitor response to increasingly intensive instruction before identifying some learning
problems
C. replace all achievement testing
D. determine personality type
✅Answer: B. monitor response to increasingly intensive instruction before identifying some
learning problems
Rationale: RTI focuses on tracking how students respond to tiered interventions before formal
identification of learning difficulties.
42. Dynamic assessment differs from traditional static testing because it emphasizes:
A. fixed administration with no interaction
B. learning potential through mediated assistance
C. only speeded performance
D. purely norm-referenced decisions
✅Answer: B. learning potential through mediated assistance
Rationale: Dynamic assessment evaluates how well an individual learns when provided with
guidance or feedback.
43. A portfolio assessment is most appropriate when the goal is to:
A. obtain one-time multiple-choice data only
B. evaluate growth and authentic performance over time
C. maximize scorer anonymity only
D. estimate test-retest reliability
✅Answer: B. evaluate growth and authentic performance over time
Rationale: Portfolio assessment captures development and real-world performance across
time.
44. Which is the best example of an aptitude test?
A. a test of mastery of last week’s algebra lessons
B. a measure intended to forecast readiness to learn or future performance
C. a symptom checklist for anxiety
D. a structured family interview
✅Answer: B. a measure intended to forecast readiness to learn or future performance
Rationale: Aptitude tests are designed to predict future learning or performance.
45. In personality assessment, traits are best understood as:
A. temporary conditions only
B. enduring tendencies to respond in certain ways
C. random behaviors with no pattern
D. scores with zero error
✅Answer: B. enduring tendencies to respond in certain ways
Rationale: Traits are relatively stable patterns of behavior, thought, and emotion.
46. Which personality test construction strategy begins with a theory of personality and derives
items from that framework?
A. criterion-group strategy
B. rational or logical-content strategy
C. theoretical strategy
D. random sampling strategy
✅Answer: C. theoretical strategy
Rationale: Theoretical construction derives items based on an underlying personality theory.
47. The MMPI is historically associated most strongly with which test construction strategy?
A. factor-analytic strategy only
B. empirical criterion-keying
C. pure rational construction
D. ipsative scaling
✅Answer: B. empirical criterion-keying
Rationale: The MMPI was developed by selecting items that empirically distinguished
between groups.
48. Which statement most accurately contrasts objective and projective methods?
A. Objective methods never require interpretation.
B. Projective methods present ambiguous stimuli to elicit responses that may reveal
personality dynamics.
C. Objective methods cannot be scored quantitatively.
D. Projective methods are always more reliable than objective methods.
✅Answer: B. Projective methods present ambiguous stimuli to elicit responses that may
reveal personality dynamics.
Rationale: Projective tests use ambiguous stimuli to access underlying psychological
processes.
49. The Rorschach is classified primarily as a:
A. self-report inventory
B. behavioral checklist
C. projective technique using inkblots
D. cognitive ability battery
✅Answer: C. projective technique using inkblots
Rationale: The Rorschach uses inkblots to elicit interpretive responses.
50. The Thematic Apperception Test mainly uses:
A. geometric puzzles
B. ambiguous pictures for story construction
C. sentence verification items
D. arithmetic subtests
✅Answer: B. ambiguous pictures for story construction
Rationale: The TAT involves creating stories based on ambiguous images.
51. Sentence completion methods are best classified as:
A. performance tests
B. objective intelligence tests
C. semistructured projective techniques
D. neurological imaging tools
✅Answer: C. semistructured projective techniques
Rationale: Sentence completion tasks provide structure but allow projective responses.
52. A behavior assessor records the frequency, duration, and antecedents of tantrums across
settings. This approach is most characteristic of:
A. projective assessment
B. behavioral assessment
C. actuarial prediction error
D. ipsative assessment
✅Answer: B. behavioral assessment
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on observable behavior and its context.
53. Reactivity is a concern in behavioral assessment because:
A. all observations are invalid
B. people may alter behavior when they know they are being observed
C. norms cannot be developed
D. scoring cannot be standardized
✅Answer: B. people may alter behavior when they know they are being observed
Rationale: Observation may influence behavior, affecting validity.
54. In clinical assessment, case history data are especially useful because they:
A. replace the need for interviews
B. provide developmental and contextual background for understanding current functioning
C. eliminate referral bias
D. ensure diagnostic accuracy by themselves
✅Answer: B. provide developmental and contextual background for understanding current
functioning
Rationale: Case history gives context to interpret current problems.
55. Which statement best describes the Barnum effect?
A. the tendency of test users to prefer actuarial prediction
B. the acceptance of vague, general statements as uniquely accurate descriptions of oneself
C. the inflation of IQ scores over generations
D. the superiority of projective methods over interviews
✅Answer: B. the acceptance of vague, general statements as uniquely accurate
descriptions of oneself
Rationale: The Barnum effect refers to accepting generalized feedback as personally
accurate.
56. Mechanical prediction is generally contrasted with clinical prediction because mechanical
prediction:
A. depends only on intuition
B. applies explicit decision rules or formulas to available data
C. is illegal in assessment
D. never uses test scores
✅Answer: B. applies explicit decision rules or formulas to available data
Rationale: Mechanical prediction uses statistical rules rather than subjective judgment.
57. A custody evaluator is asked by the court to assess parenting capacity while clarifying who
the client is and the limits of confidentiality. This best reflects:
A. free association
B. third-party request for services
C. role-play testing
D. ipsative interpretation
✅Answer: B. third-party request for services
Rationale: Court referrals involve third-party contexts requiring role clarification and
confidentiality limits.
58. A clinician conducting suicide assessment would be most concerned with:
A. percentile norms only
B. immediate risk indicators, intent, means, and protective factors
C. aesthetic preferences
D. only long-term vocational plans
✅Answer: B. immediate risk indicators, intent, means, and protective factors
Rationale: Suicide assessment prioritizes immediate safety and risk evaluation.
59. Neuropsychological assessment is most clearly indicated when there is concern about:
A. occupational interests
B. possible brain-behavior dysfunction
C. marital satisfaction alone
D. handwriting style
✅Answer: B. possible brain-behavior dysfunction
Rationale: Neuropsychological assessment evaluates brain-related cognitive functioning.
60. Executive functioning is most closely related to:
A. visual acuity only
B. planning, inhibition, cognitive flexibility, and goal-directed behavior
C. spinal reflexes
D. depth perception only
✅Answer: B. planning, inhibition, cognitive flexibility, and goal-directed behavior
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order cognitive control processes.
61. Which neuropsychological domain is most directly assessed by tasks requiring delayed
recall of word lists?
A. motor coordination
B. memory
C. visuoconstruction only
D. response bias only
✅Answer: B. memory
Rationale: Delayed recall tasks measure memory retention.
62. A neuropsychological battery is particularly useful because it:
A. eliminates the need for history taking
B. samples multiple domains of functioning systematically
C. guarantees a specific medical diagnosis
D. can be interpreted without training
✅Answer: B. samples multiple domains of functioning systematically
Rationale: Batteries assess various cognitive domains to create a comprehensive profile.
63. In career assessment, interest inventories are most useful for:
A. diagnosing psychosis
B. matching preferences with educational or occupational fields
C. measuring only general intelligence
D. establishing neurological impairment
✅Answer: B. matching preferences with educational or occupational fields
Rationale: Interest inventories guide career decisions based on preferences.
64. In personnel selection, base rate refers to:
A. the proportion of applicants selected
B. the proportion of current employees who would succeed without using a test
C. the correlation between test and criterion
D. the standard deviation of scores
✅Answer: B. the proportion of current employees who would succeed without using a test
Rationale: Base rate reflects expected success without selection tools.
65. Incremental validity asks whether:
A. a new measure adds useful predictive information beyond what is already known
B. a test has face validity
C. an item is easy enough
D. norms are local or national
✅Answer: A. a new measure adds useful predictive information beyond what is already
known
Rationale: Incremental validity evaluates added predictive value.
66. Which is the strongest psychometric argument for using structured selection methods rather
than relying only on unstructured interviews?
A. Structured methods are more entertaining.
B. Structured methods can improve reliability and predictive accuracy.
C. Unstructured interviews are illegal.
D. Structured methods require no training.
✅Answer: B. Structured methods can improve reliability and predictive accuracy.
Rationale: Structured methods reduce bias and improve consistency.
67. In consumer psychology and survey work, attitudes are typically measured using:
A. free association only
B. rating scales and related self-report formats
C. EEG recordings only
D. projective inkblots exclusively
✅Answer: B. rating scales and related self-report formats
Rationale: Attitudes are commonly assessed using rating scales.
68. A psychometrician receives a request to administer and interpret a complex instrument
outside their competence. The most ethical action is to:
A. proceed if the client insists
B. guess based on prior experience
C. decline or refer unless adequate supervision, training, or lawful role boundaries permit
involvement
D. interpret only the lowest scores
✅Answer: C. decline or refer unless adequate supervision, training, or lawful role
boundaries permit involvement
Rationale: Ethical standards require working within competence or seeking supervision.
69. Under Philippine ethical standards, psychometricians are prohibited from:
A. administering any test
B. practicing therapy except in emergency situations
C. conducting scoring
D. working in schools
✅Answer: B. practicing therapy except in emergency situations
Rationale: RA 10029 limits psychometricians from practicing psychotherapy except in
emergencies.
70. Which scenario best reflects proper informed consent in assessment?
A. The examiner withholds the purpose to prevent defensiveness.
B. The examiner explains the nature and purpose of the assessment, probable uses, and
limits of confidentiality.
C. Consent is unnecessary if the test is standardized.
D. Verbal pressure is acceptable if the referral source demands compliance.
✅Answer: B. The examiner explains the nature and purpose of the assessment, probable
uses, and limits of confidentiality.
Rationale: Informed consent requires transparency about purpose, use, and confidentiality.
71. A practitioner records an online counseling session without first obtaining permission. This
most directly violates the ethical standard on:
A. utility
B. recording and informed consent
C. criterion contamination
D. test-retest reliability
✅Answer: B. recording and informed consent
Rationale: Recording requires prior consent from clients.
72. Which statement best reflects the ethical principle of competent caring?
A. Services should be offered even when one lacks all relevant competencies and support.
B. The practitioner should maximize benefits, minimize harm, and maintain competence.
C. Confidentiality is always absolute, even when there is imminent danger.
D. Cultural context is irrelevant if the test manual is clear.
✅Answer: B. The practitioner should maximize benefits, minimize harm, and maintain
competence.
Rationale: Ethical care requires beneficence, nonmaleficence, and competence.
73. A practitioner becomes aware of another psychologist’s minor ethical lapse and can address
