it without breaching confidentiality. The Code suggests first considering:
A. public accusation on social media
B. informal resolution when sufficient and appropriate
C. automatic court action
D. destruction of records
✅Answer: B. informal resolution when sufficient and appropriate
Rationale: Ethical codes encourage resolving minor violations informally when appropriate.
74. Which of the following best reflects a conflict between ethics and law under the PAP Code?
A. The practitioner ignores the law and follows personal values.
B. The practitioner first seeks to resolve the conflict consistent with ethics, but if unresolved,
adheres to governing law.
C. Ethics always overrides law.
D. The practitioner automatically refuses service in all cases.
✅Answer: B. The practitioner first seeks to resolve the conflict consistent with ethics, but if
unresolved, adheres to governing law.
Rationale: Practitioners attempt ethical resolution first, then follow legal mandates.
75. A client’s results are discussed in a public seminar with identifying details left intact and
without written permission. This most directly violates:
A. internal consistency standards
B. use of confidential information for other purposes
C. test construction rules
D. percentile interpretation
✅Answer: B. use of confidential information for other purposes
Rationale: Confidential information must not be disclosed without consent.
76. A psychometrician allows an untrained office assistant to interpret protocols independently.
This is primarily a violation involving:
A. test fairness
B. assessment by unqualified persons and improper delegation
C. item difficulty
D. predictive validity
✅Answer: B. assessment by unqualified persons and improper delegation
Rationale: Only qualified individuals should interpret assessment data.
77. Which situation best reflects an improper multiple relationship?
A. A psychologist explains test results clearly.
B. A psychologist enters into a business partnership with a current therapy client.
C. A psychologist obtains informed consent.
D. A psychologist consults anonymously with a colleague.
✅Answer: B. A psychologist enters into a business partnership with a current therapy client.
Rationale: Dual relationships can impair objectivity and risk exploitation.
78. In telepsychology, the ethical standards in the PAP Code indicate that:
A. online services are exempt from ordinary ethics rules
B. only psychologists may use any digital platform
C. the same ethical principles that apply face-to-face also apply online
D. confidentiality risks disappear when sessions are virtual
✅Answer: C. the same ethical principles that apply face-to-face also apply online
Rationale: Ethical standards apply equally across service modalities.
79. A practitioner is physically and emotionally exhausted and notices increasing errors in
documentation. The most ethical response is to:
A. continue all duties to avoid disappointing clients
B. take appropriate measures such as consultation and limit, suspend, or modify duties if
competence is affected
C. shift all work to unqualified staff
D. ignore the issue if no complaint has yet been filed
✅Answer: B. take appropriate measures such as consultation and limit, suspend, or modify
duties if competence is affected
Rationale: Practitioners must manage personal impairment to maintain competence.
80. Which is most consistent with RA 10029-based role boundaries as reflected in the PAP
Code?
A. A psychometrician independently conducts psychotherapy as routine practice.
B. A psychometrician operates within prescribed boundaries and under supervision of a
registered psychologist when applicable.
C. A psychometrician may diagnose any mental disorder without limits.
D. A psychometrician may release all raw data to anyone who asks.
✅Answer: B. A psychometrician operates within prescribed boundaries and under
supervision of a registered psychologist when applicable.
Rationale: Psychometricians must practice within defined legal and professional limits.
81. A test score distribution with many low scores and a long tail to the right is:
A. negatively skewed
B. positively skewed
C. mesokurtic by definition
D. bimodal by definition
✅Answer: B. positively skewed
Rationale: A right tail indicates positive skew.
82. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. mode
B. median
C. mean
D. percentile rank
✅Answer: C. mean
Rationale: The mean is sensitive to outliers.
83. A z score of +1.50 means the raw score is:
A. 1.5 points above the mean
B. 1.5 standard deviations above the mean
C. at the 15th percentile
D. below the mean by 1.5 standard deviations
✅Answer: B. 1.5 standard deviations above the mean
Rationale: Z scores express distance in standard deviation units.
84. When a raw score is transformed to a T score, the usual mean and standard deviation are:
A. mean 0, SD 1
B. mean 50, SD 10
C. mean 100, SD 15
D. mean 10, SD 3
✅Answer: B. mean 50, SD 10
Rationale: T scores standardize distributions with mean 50 and SD 10.
85. Pearson r is most appropriate when:
A. both variables are nominal categories
B. both variables are measured at least at the interval level and related linearly
C. only rank ordering is available and ties are numerous
D. one variable is purely qualitative and unscored
✅Answer: B. both variables are measured at least at the interval level and related linearly
Rationale: Pearson r requires interval data and linear relationships.
86. Restricted range tends to:
A. inflate all correlations
B. reduce the magnitude of observed correlations
C. eliminate measurement error
D. guarantee fairness
✅Answer: B. reduce the magnitude of observed correlations
Rationale: Reduced variability weakens correlations.
87. The coefficient of determination indicates:
A. the percentage of variance shared by two variables
B. the number of items retained
C. the exact causal contribution of X to Y
D. the standard error of measurement
✅Answer: A. the percentage of variance shared by two variables
Rationale: r² shows shared variance between variables.
88. Which statement about correlation is correct?
A. Correlation proves causation.
B. A zero correlation always means no relationship of any kind.
C. Correlation describes degree and direction of relationship, not necessarily cause.
D. Negative correlations are psychometrically invalid.
✅Answer: C. Correlation describes degree and direction of relationship, not necessarily
cause.
Rationale: Correlation does not imply causation.
89. A psychologist wants to know whether an assessment procedure disadvantages examinees
from a linguistic minority because of language demands unrelated to the construct. The primary
concern is:
A. construct-irrelevant variance
B. ipsative scoring
C. interrater reliability
D. factor rotation
✅Answer: A. construct-irrelevant variance
Rationale: Irrelevant factors affecting scores reduce validity.
90. Which is the best example of cultural competence in assessment?
A. Using the same interpretation for all clients regardless of background
B. Considering language, acculturation, cultural beliefs, and context when selecting and
interpreting measures
C. Avoiding all standardized tests with minority clients
D. Assuming local norms never matter
✅Answer: B. Considering language, acculturation, cultural beliefs, and context when
selecting and interpreting measures
Rationale: Cultural competence requires contextualized interpretation.
91. A teacher-made classroom test yields very high pass rates because many items are
giveaways and do not sample the course objectives adequately. The strongest criticism is:
A. the test may lack content validity
B. the test is too reliable
C. the standard error is too low
D. the test is necessarily biased
✅Answer: A. the test may lack content validity
Rationale: Poor domain coverage weakens content validity.
92. Which is the best rationale for using local norms in some settings?
A. National norms are always invalid.
B. Local norms may better reflect the specific comparison group relevant to a decision.
C. Local norms eliminate the need for standardization.
D. Local norms guarantee predictive validity.
✅Answer: B. Local norms may better reflect the specific comparison group relevant to a
decision.
Rationale: Local norms provide context-specific comparisons.
93. Which statement about face validity is most accurate?
A. It is often about appearance or acceptability rather than strong technical validity evidence.
B. It is the same as construct validity.
C. It is the best evidence for legal defensibility.
D. It refers to scorer agreement.
✅Answer: A. It is often about appearance or acceptability rather than strong technical
validity evidence.
Rationale: Face validity concerns perceived relevance, not technical strength.
94. A board exam item writer avoids “all of the above,” writes one defensible best answer, and
ensures distractors are plausible. This primarily improves:
A. item-writing quality and discrimination potential
B. norm development only
C. test-retest stability only
D. interscorer reliability only
✅Answer: A. item-writing quality and discrimination potential
Rationale: Good item writing improves clarity and discrimination.
95. A practitioner is asked by a company to assess employees and report results. Before
proceeding, the practitioner should clarify:
A. only the price
B. who the client is, intended use of results, who will access the data, and limits of
confidentiality
C. only whether the employees like testing
D. only whether the company prefers paper or online forms
✅Answer: B. who the client is, intended use of results, who will access the data, and limits
of confidentiality
Rationale: Ethical practice requires clarity about roles, use, and confidentiality.
96. Which scenario best illustrates competent emergency practice by a psychometrician?
A. Providing long-term therapy without supervision after a crisis
B. Offering immediate support or referral in an emergency and discontinuing once appropriate
competent services become available
C. Refusing to help under all circumstances unless a full battery is completed
D. Releasing all notes to the family without consent
✅Answer: B. Offering immediate support or referral in an emergency and discontinuing
once appropriate competent services become available
Rationale: Emergency care is temporary and must transition to proper services.
97. Which practice best protects test security?
A. Posting full protocols online for discussion
B. Leaving booklets in a public waiting area
C. Restricting access to test materials and records to qualified persons
D. Allowing examinees to take answer keys home
✅Answer: C. Restricting access to test materials and records to qualified persons
Rationale: Test materials must be secured from unauthorized access.
98. Which of the following most clearly reflects integrity in professional assessment practice?
A. Exaggerating the accuracy of a test to gain referrals
B. Concealing conflicts of interest whenever possible
C. Giving honest, accurate, and prudent communications while avoiding exploitation
D. Promising results that no assessment can support
✅Answer: C. Giving honest, accurate, and prudent communications while avoiding
exploitation
Rationale: Integrity involves honesty and avoidance of misleading practices.
99. Which psychologist is most closely associated with the inkblot method that later became a
major projective technique?
A. Alfred Binet
B. Hermann Rorschach
C. David Wechsler
D. Charles Spearman
✅Answer: B. Hermann Rorschach
Rationale: Rorschach developed the inkblot test.
100. A newly developed test is piloted, weak items are revised or discarded, norms are
developed carefully, and validation continues after publication. This reflects the principle that:
A. test development ends after the first administration
B. test revision is an ongoing part of responsible assessment practice
C. once standardized, a test no longer needs validity evidence
D. utility replaces reliability and validity
✅Answer: B. test revision is an ongoing part of responsible assessment practice
Rationale: Test development is continuous, requiring ongoing revision and validation.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 3
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 3
1. A psychometrician is asked to administer a personality inventory to applicants for a
government post. Which action is most consistent with sound assessment practice?
A. Interpret the profile solely from cutoff scores without contextual data
B. Combine test data with relevant collateral information before making conclusions
C. Base conclusions only on the applicant’s interview performance
D. Use only one instrument to avoid conflicting data
✅Answer: B. Combine test data with relevant collateral information before making
conclusions
Rationale: Psychological assessment requires integrating multiple data sources (tests,
interviews, history) to form accurate and contextualized conclusions.
2. Which statement best distinguishes psychological testing from psychological assessment?
A. Testing is broader and always includes case formulation
B. Assessment is limited to standardized instruments
C. Testing is one tool within the broader process of assessment
D. Assessment is used only in clinical settings
✅Answer: C. Testing is one tool within the broader process of assessment
Rationale: Testing is a component of assessment, which is a broader process involving
multiple methods and data sources.
3. A guidance office wants to compare a student’s mathematics performance with that of
same-age peers nationwide. Which interpretive framework is most appropriate?
A. Criterion-referenced interpretation
B. Norm-referenced interpretation
C. Ipsative interpretation
D. Dynamic interpretation
✅Answer: B. Norm-referenced interpretation
Rationale: Norm-referenced interpretation compares an individual’s performance to a defined
reference group.
4. A test developer wants to know whether an item separates high scorers from low scorers on
the overall test. Which index is most directly relevant?
A. Item difficulty index
B. Item discrimination index
C. Standard error of measurement
D. Percentile rank
✅Answer: B. Item discrimination index
Rationale: Item discrimination indicates how well an item differentiates between high and low
performers.
5. A measure yields highly consistent scores across repeated administrations, but it does not
actually assess the intended construct. This test is:
A. Valid but unreliable
B. Reliable but invalid
C. Neither reliable nor valid
D. Useful because reliability guarantees validity
✅Answer: B. Reliable but invalid
Rationale: A test can produce consistent results (reliable) but still fail to measure the intended
construct (invalid).
6. Which situation is the clearest example of predictive validity evidence?
A. Depression test scores are correlated with clinician ratings obtained the same day
B. Aptitude test scores are compared with job performance six months after hiring
C. Reading test content is reviewed by teachers for representativeness
D. Test takers report that the items appear relevant to the construct
✅Answer: B. Aptitude test scores are compared with job performance six months after hiring
Rationale: Predictive validity is demonstrated when test scores predict future performance.
7. A psychologist claims a newly developed coping inventory is excellent because respondents
say the items “look appropriate.” This claim relies most heavily on:
A. Content validity
B. Face validity
C. Construct validity
D. Incremental validity
✅Answer: B. Face validity
Rationale: Face validity refers to the extent to which a test appears appropriate or relevant to
respondents.
8. A school-based assessor wants to reduce cultural unfairness when evaluating a student from
a linguistically diverse background. Which step is best?
A. Interpret low verbal scores as evidence of low ability
B. Use a fixed cutoff regardless of language history
C. Integrate language proficiency and cultural context into interpretation
D. Avoid testing and rely only on teacher impressions
✅Answer: C. Integrate language proficiency and cultural context into interpretation
Rationale: Fair assessment requires considering cultural and linguistic factors in interpreting
test results.
9. Which is the best example of a psychological trait rather than a state?
A. Temporary fatigue during testing
B. Anxiety felt only during today’s exam
C. Long-standing tendency toward social withdrawal
D. Hunger immediately before administration
✅Answer: C. Long-standing tendency toward social withdrawal
Rationale: Traits are enduring characteristics, whereas states are temporary conditions.
10. A clinician administers Form A of an anxiety scale and later uses an equivalent Form B to
estimate score consistency. Which reliability estimate is being examined?
A. Inter-scorer reliability
B. Alternate-forms reliability
C. Split-half reliability
D. Internal consistency
✅Answer: B. Alternate-forms reliability
Rationale: Alternate-forms reliability assesses consistency across equivalent versions of a
test.
11. The standard error of measurement is most useful because it:
A. Proves whether a test is fair
B. Indicates the likely band around an obtained score
C. Replaces the need for validity evidence
D. Shows the percentile rank of a raw score
✅Answer: B. Indicates the likely band around an obtained score
Rationale: SEM provides an estimate of the range within which the true score likely falls.
12. A test with excellent psychometric properties is too expensive, too time-consuming, and
adds little decision value beyond current procedures. The main concern is:
A. Reliability
B. Utility
C. Objectivity
D. Scaling
✅Answer: B. Utility
Rationale: Utility refers to the practical value and cost-effectiveness of using a test.
13. Which method is commonly used to set a defensible cut score by having subject-matter
experts judge item difficulty for minimally competent examinees?
A. Q-sort method
B. Angoff method
C. Split-half method
D. Factor rotation
✅Answer: B. Angoff method
Rationale: The Angoff method uses expert judgment to estimate the probability of correct
responses by minimally competent examinees.
14. In test development, pilot testing is most helpful for:
A. Eliminating the need for standardization
B. Identifying problematic items before final use
C. Proving criterion validity automatically
D. Preventing any future need for revision
✅Answer: B. Identifying problematic items before final use
Rationale: Pilot testing helps detect flawed items and improve test quality before operational
use.
15. A developer notices that nearly all examinees answer an item correctly. What is the most
likely concern?
A. The item has very high discriminating power by default
B. The item may be too easy to differentiate examinees
C. The item necessarily has strong construct validity
D. The item should be retained because easy items are always best
✅Answer: B. The item may be too easy to differentiate examinees
Rationale: Very easy items provide little discrimination between high and low performers.
16. Which statement about validity and reliability is most accurate?
A. A valid test must be perfectly reliable
B. Reliability places an upper limit on validity
C. Validity and reliability are unrelated
D. Utility is identical to validity
✅Answer: B. Reliability places an upper limit on validity
Rationale: A test cannot be more valid than it is reliable, as inconsistency limits meaningful
interpretation.
17. A board review center uses only one old norm group from decades ago to interpret current
examinee performance. What is the strongest criticism?
A. The test has no face validity
B. The norms may no longer be representative
C. The cutoff score is automatically illegal
D. Internal consistency becomes irrelevant
✅Answer: B. The norms may no longer be representative
Rationale: Outdated norms may not reflect current populations, leading to inaccurate
interpretation.
18. A psychometrician is asked to interpret results from a highly specialized forensic tool beyond
their training. The most ethical response is to:
A. Interpret it anyway because the employer requested it
B. Use online summaries as a substitute for competence
C. Decline or refer unless adequately supervised and trained
D. Base interpretation on intuition and general experience
✅Answer: C. Decline or refer unless adequately supervised and trained
Rationale: Ethical practice requires working within one’s competence and seeking supervision
or referral when needed.
19. Which of the following is the clearest example of a multiple relationship risk?
A. Explaining test results to a client in clear language
B. Assessing a person who is also the assessor’s close business partner
C. Using more than one instrument in a battery
D. Consulting literature before writing a report
✅Answer: B. Assessing a person who is also the assessor’s close business partner
Rationale: Multiple relationships can impair objectivity and create conflicts of interest.
20. A client is told before assessment who requested the evaluation, the purpose of the
assessment, and the limits of confidentiality. This primarily reflects:
A. Test bias correction
B. Informed consent
C. Utility analysis
D. Response generalization
✅Answer: B. Informed consent
Rationale: Informed consent involves explaining purpose, procedures, and limits of
confidentiality before assessment.
21. Under the PAP Code of Ethics, confidential information may be disclosed without consent
when:
A. The assessor is curious about peer feedback
B. A colleague informally asks for interesting cases
C. Disclosure is mandated by law or needed to prevent harm
D. The information may improve the assessor’s reputation
✅Answer: C. Disclosure is mandated by law or needed to prevent harm
Rationale: Confidentiality may be breached when required by law or to prevent serious harm.
22. Which action best reflects the ethical principle of competent caring?
A. Continuing services despite severe burnout to avoid inconvenience
B. Practicing beyond training because the client insists
C. Monitoring one’s competence and minimizing risk of harm
D. Sharing confidential cases for educational entertainment
✅Answer: C. Monitoring one’s competence and minimizing risk of harm
Rationale: Competent caring requires maintaining competence and minimizing potential harm
to clients.
23. A psychometrician in the Philippines is asked to provide psychotherapy to a client outside
emergency circumstances. According to the Code’s role boundaries, the psychometrician
should:
A. Proceed independently if the client consents
B. Provide therapy as long as assessment was done first
C. Refrain because therapy is outside the psychometrician’s permitted role
D. Offer therapy only through social media
✅Answer: C. Refrain because therapy is outside the psychometrician’s permitted role
Rationale: Psychometricians are not authorized to provide psychotherapy under standard
scope of practice.
24. A supervisor delegates test administration to a trainee. Which practice is most ethical?
A. Delegate any task regardless of trainee competence
B. Ensure the trainee is capable and provide adequate supervision
C. Avoid informing the client that delegation occurred
D. Allow the trainee to interpret any instrument independently
✅Answer: B. Ensure the trainee is capable and provide adequate supervision
Rationale: Delegation must consider competence and include proper supervision.
25. A test user discovers that an organization is misrepresenting the meaning of reported
assessment results. The best initial response is to:
A. Ignore it to preserve professional relationships
B. Take reasonable steps to correct or minimize the misuse
C. Publicly shame the organization immediately
D. Destroy the records
✅Answer: B. Take reasonable steps to correct or minimize the misuse
Rationale: Ethical responsibility includes correcting misuse or misinterpretation of assessment
results.
26. A. Determining whether an examinee mastered specified learning objectives
B. Norm-referenced interpretation
C. Ipsative interpretation
D. Dynamic interpretation
✅Answer: A. Determining whether an examinee mastered specified learning objectives
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation focuses on mastery of specific content or skills
rather than comparison to others.
27. A. Answered 84% of the items correctly
B. Scored higher than 84% of the norm group
C. Has a z score of +0.84
D. Is in the 84th stanine
✅Answer: B. Scored higher than 84% of the norm group
Rationale: Percentile rank indicates the percentage of the reference group that scored below
the individual.
28. A. Nominal
B. Ordinal
C. Interval
D. Ratio
✅Answer: C. Interval
Rationale: Interval scales have equal intervals but no true zero point.
29. A. Phi coefficient
B. Pearson r
C. Kendall’s W
D. Kappa
✅Answer: B. Pearson r
Rationale: Pearson r is used to measure linear relationships between two continuous
variables.
30. A. Negatively skewed
B. Positively skewed
C. Platykurtic only
D. Bimodal by definition
✅Answer: B. Positively skewed
Rationale: A distribution with a long tail toward higher values is positively skewed.
31. An intelligence test score is converted to a standard score to make interpretation easier
across forms and administrations. The main advantage is:
A. It eliminates all measurement error
B. It allows comparison using a common metric
C. It guarantees criterion validity
D. It removes cultural influences
✅Answer: B. It allows comparison using a common metric
Rationale: Standard scores transform raw scores into a common scale, allowing meaningful
comparison across tests and populations.
32. A school uses a screening test with high sensitivity but low specificity. What is the most likely
outcome?
A. Many true cases are missed
B. Few false positives occur
C. More at-risk students are identified, including many false positives
D. The test becomes invalid for all purposes
✅Answer: C. More at-risk students are identified, including many false positives
Rationale: High sensitivity detects most true cases but low specificity increases false
positives.
33. A personality inventory was built by selecting items that best distinguish a diagnosed group
from a comparison group. This strategy is primarily:
A. Rational-theoretical
B. Criterion-keying
C. Behavioral observation
D. Developmental scaling
✅Answer: B. Criterion-keying
Rationale: Criterion-keying selects items based on their ability to differentiate between
groups.
34. Which statement best characterizes projective methods?
A. They always have stronger psychometric support than objective inventories
B. They use ambiguous stimuli to elicit responses open to interpretation
C. They are immune to scorer bias
D. They replace the need for interviews
✅Answer: B. They use ambiguous stimuli to elicit responses open to interpretation
Rationale: Projective techniques rely on ambiguous stimuli to reveal underlying psychological
processes.
35. A clinician uses behavioral observation, interview data, case history, and test scores to
understand a referral question. This illustrates:
A. Mono-method assessment
B. Cross-validation by randomization
C. Multimethod assessment
D. Ipsative scoring
✅Answer: C. Multimethod assessment
Rationale: Multimethod assessment integrates multiple sources of data for more
comprehensive evaluation.
36. Which statement about the interview as an assessment tool is most accurate?
A. It is free from error if conducted by an experienced clinician
B. It can yield useful data but is vulnerable to bias and unreliability
C. It is inferior to all standardized tests
D. It should never be used in clinical assessment
✅Answer: B. It can yield useful data but is vulnerable to bias and unreliability
Rationale: Interviews are valuable but subject to biases and inconsistencies.
37. In educational assessment, dynamic assessment differs from static testing because it:
A. Avoids any interaction with the learner
B. Focuses on learning potential through guided assistance
C. Uses only group-administered tests
D. Rejects all standardized measures
✅Answer: B. Focuses on learning potential through guided assistance
Rationale: Dynamic assessment evaluates how performance changes with intervention.
38. A school implements Response to Intervention mainly to:
A. Replace all diagnostic evaluation permanently
B. Monitor response to progressively intensive instruction and support
C. Ensure all students receive the same intervention
D. Avoid documenting academic progress
✅Answer: B. Monitor response to progressively intensive instruction and support
Rationale: RtI tracks student response to varying levels of support.
39. Which of the following is most clearly an aptitude measure?
A. A test of previously learned algebra content
B. A measure intended to estimate potential for future learning
C. A checklist of depressive symptoms
D. An inventory of vocational interests only
✅Answer: B. A measure intended to estimate potential for future learning
Rationale: Aptitude tests estimate future performance or learning potential.
40. A neuropsychological evaluation is most indicated when:
A. The referral question concerns possible brain-behavior dysfunction
B. The client only wants career guidance
C. The assessor needs a quick personality profile
D. The school requires class ranking
✅Answer: A. The referral question concerns possible brain-behavior dysfunction
Rationale: Neuropsychological assessment evaluates brain-behavior relationships.
41. Which cognitive domain is most closely associated with executive functioning?
A. Simple sensory acuity alone
B. Planning, inhibition, and cognitive flexibility
C. Basic muscle strength only
D. Visual sharpness without decision-making
✅Answer: B. Planning, inhibition, and cognitive flexibility
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order cognitive control processes.
42. A person performs poorly on a memory task after recent head injury. Which additional
evidence would most strengthen interpretation?
A. Ignoring premorbid functioning
B. Comparing the result only with self-report
C. Integrating history, other cognitive findings, and behavioral observations
D. Concluding dementia from one score
✅Answer: C. Integrating history, other cognitive findings, and behavioral observations
Rationale: Interpretation requires multiple converging sources of data.
43. In clinical report writing, the Barnum effect is a warning against:
A. Using clear language
B. Offering vague statements that seem true for almost anyone
C. Including test scores in reports
D. Explaining limitations of findings
✅Answer: B. Offering vague statements that seem true for almost anyone
Rationale: The Barnum effect refers to overly general statements perceived as accurate.
44. A clinician chooses a mechanical prediction model over unaided judgment in a setting where
data consistently support it. The main rationale is that mechanical methods:
A. Are always more humane
B. Often reduce inconsistency in decision-making
C. Eliminate the need for validity studies
D. Never require clinical interpretation
✅Answer: B. Often reduce inconsistency in decision-making
Rationale: Mechanical methods improve consistency and reduce subjective bias.
45. In suicide assessment, which approach is best?
A. Rely on a single self-report item only
B. Assume denial of intent rules out all risk
C. Integrate ideation, plan, means, history, and contextual factors
D. Avoid asking direct questions to prevent suggestion
✅Answer: C. Integrate ideation, plan, means, history, and contextual factors
Rationale: Comprehensive risk assessment includes multiple dimensions of risk.
46. Which statement about intelligence testing is most accurate?
A. Intelligence is universally defined with no controversy
B. Intelligence tests are unaffected by culture
C. Competing theories influence what intelligence tests attempt to measure
D. IQ scores directly measure moral worth
✅Answer: C. Competing theories influence what intelligence tests attempt to measure
Rationale: Intelligence is conceptually debated and tests reflect different theories.
47. Which historical figure is most closely associated with the first practical intelligence scale for
identifying children needing educational support?
A. Alfred Binet
B. Sigmund Freud
C. Carl Rogers
D. Henry Murray
✅Answer: A. Alfred Binet
Rationale: Binet developed early intelligence scales for educational use.
48. Spearman is most strongly associated with:
A. The hierarchy of needs
B. General intelligence or g
C. Classical conditioning
D. Reciprocal determinism
✅Answer: B. General intelligence or g
Rationale: Spearman proposed a general intelligence factor underlying abilities.
49. The Flynn effect refers to:
A. A decline in all forms of validity over time
B. Systematic rises in intelligence test performance across generations
C. Reduced test security in digital testing
D. The tendency to fake good on personality tests
✅Answer: B. Systematic rises in intelligence test performance across generations
Rationale: The Flynn effect describes generational increases in IQ scores.
50. Which is the best interpretation of a Full Scale IQ?
A. It should always be interpreted without examining index patterns
B. It is a summary estimate that may require qualification based on subtest variability
C. It is meaningless unless exactly average
D. It directly predicts all life outcomes with precision
✅Answer: B. It is a summary estimate that may require qualification based on subtest
variability
Rationale: IQ interpretation must consider variability across subtests.
51. A psychologist compares an examinee’s verbal reasoning with visual-spatial performance to
understand cognitive strengths and weaknesses. This is an example of:
A. Profile analysis
B. Response latency analysis only
C. Item-key revision
D. Utility computation
✅Answer: A. Profile analysis
Rationale: Profile analysis examines patterns of strengths and weaknesses across scores.
52. Which intelligence test family is especially associated with verbal and
performance/task-based subtests and later index scores?
A. Rorschach scales
B. Wechsler scales
C. Strong Interest Inventory
D. MMPI scales
✅Answer: B. Wechsler scales
Rationale: Wechsler tests include verbal and performance/index-based scores.
53. A preschool child is being evaluated for readiness and developmental functioning. Which
test characteristic is most important?
A. Norms appropriate for adult workers
B. Age-appropriate tasks and developmental norms
C. Heavy reliance on abstract legal reasoning
D. Exclusive use of self-report
✅Answer: B. Age-appropriate tasks and developmental norms
Rationale: Developmentally appropriate tools are essential for young children.
54. Which assessment approach is most suitable when a counselor wants to understand
vocational preferences?
A. Neuropsychological battery
B. Interest inventory
C. Pure sensory screening
D. Projective motor battery only
✅Answer: B. Interest inventory
Rationale: Interest inventories assess preferences related to careers.
55. A person scores high on Social and Enterprising themes across vocational measures. The
most defensible interpretation is:
A. The person is guaranteed success in all leadership jobs
B. The pattern may suggest preferences for people-oriented, influence-based activities
C. The person has low intelligence
D. The person should avoid all structured work settings
✅Answer: B. The pattern may suggest preferences for people-oriented, influence-based
activities
Rationale: Interest scores indicate tendencies, not guaranteed outcomes.
56. In personnel selection, base rates and selection ratios matter because they:
A. Determine whether reliability can be ignored
B. Influence the practical value of using a test in hiring decisions
C. Automatically invalidate all interviews
D. Eliminate adverse impact concerns
✅Answer: B. Influence the practical value of using a test in hiring decisions
Rationale: These factors affect the utility of selection procedures.
57. Which document is most likely to have the weakest incremental value in employee selection
when compared with structured procedures?
A. Standardized work sample
B. Structured interview
C. Unverified letter of recommendation
D. Cognitive ability test
✅Answer: C. Unverified letter of recommendation
Rationale: Such letters are often subjective and unreliable.
58. A company wants to know whether adding a cognitive test to interviews improves hiring
decisions enough to justify cost. This is primarily a question of:
A. Face validity
B. Utility analysis
C. Test security
D. Projective depth
✅Answer: B. Utility analysis
Rationale: Utility analysis evaluates cost-benefit and decision improvement.
59. Which approach best minimizes expectancy effects in test administration?
A. Giving subtle cues to high-potential examinees
B. Standardizing instructions and examiner behavior
C. Revising scores after observing appearance
D. Allowing administrators to improvise freely
✅Answer: B. Standardizing instructions and examiner behavior
Rationale: Standardization reduces bias and expectancy effects.
60. Stereotype threat is best understood as:
A. A fixed trait of minority examinees
B. Performance impairment triggered by fear of confirming a negative stereotype
C. Proof that tests cannot measure anything
D. A method of improving motivation
✅Answer: B. Performance impairment triggered by fear of confirming a negative stereotype
Rationale: Stereotype threat affects performance due to situational pressure.
(Continuing…)
61. A. Emphasizing that failure would confirm group differences
B. Using hostile and competitive instructions
C. Creating a fair, supportive, low-cue testing context
D. Refusing accommodation requests automatically
✅Answer: C. Creating a fair, supportive, low-cue testing context
Rationale: Reducing threat cues improves performance fairness.
62. A. It has no effect on responses to assessment
B. Cultural adaptation may influence meaning, norms, and interpretation of scores
C. It matters only in forensic settings
D. It replaces the need for validity evidence
✅Answer: B. Cultural adaptation may influence meaning, norms, and interpretation of
scores
Rationale: Cultural context affects assessment outcomes.
63. A. A competent adult signs for psychotherapy
B. A corporation requests employee screening
C. A minor agrees to participate while a legal guardian provides permission
D. A test publisher authorizes purchase of materials
✅Answer: C. A minor agrees to participate while a legal guardian provides permission
Rationale: Assent involves minor agreement with guardian consent.
64. A. Item difficulty standards
B. Confidentiality safeguards
C. Parallel-form equivalence
D. Norm updating procedures
✅Answer: B. Confidentiality safeguards
Rationale: Data must be securely stored to protect client privacy.
65. A. Claiming guaranteed outcomes to attract clients
B. Exaggerating credentials to build trust
C. Presenting accurate, nondeceptive information about qualifications and services
D. Using sensationalized social media posts about clients
✅Answer: C. Presenting accurate, nondeceptive information about qualifications and
services
Rationale: Ethical communication requires honesty and accuracy.
66. A. Training use is prohibited in all cases
B. Training use may occur with adequate supervision and role limits
C. Supervision is unnecessary if the trainee has read the manual
D. Interpretation authority is unlimited during internship
✅Answer: B. Training use may occur with adequate supervision and role limits
Rationale: Supervised training is ethically acceptable.
67. A. True score plus error
B. Validity plus utility
C. Mean plus percentile
D. Norm plus deviation IQ
✅Answer: A. True score plus error
Rationale: Classical test theory defines observed score as true score plus error.
68. A. Stable construct and short suitable interval
B. Major practice effects or real change in the construct
C. Equivalent conditions at both times
D. Clear standardized instructions
✅Answer: B. Major practice effects or real change in the construct
Rationale: Changes in the construct reduce test-retest reliability.
69. A. A single relatively homogeneous construct
B. Only change across long time intervals
C. Motor speed under different raters
D. Alternate forms exclusively
✅Answer: A. A single relatively homogeneous construct
Rationale: Internal consistency is best for homogeneous constructs.
70. A. Spearman rho
B. Point-biserial only
C. Phi coefficient only
D. Eta only
✅Answer: A. Spearman rho
Rationale: Spearman rho is used for ordinal data correlations.
71. A. Concurrent validity
B. Face validity
C. Split-half reliability
D. Content sampling error only
✅Answer: A. Concurrent validity
Rationale: Concurrent validity compares test results with current criteria.
72. A. Experts judge whether items adequately represent the domain
B. Scores correlate with future GPA
C. Test takers say items look relevant
D. Two halves of the test correlate strongly
✅Answer: A. Experts judge whether items adequately represent the domain
Rationale: Content validity is based on expert judgment of item relevance.
73. A. Construct validity
B. Inter-rater reliability
C. Administrative feasibility
D. Face validity alone
✅Answer: A. Construct validity
Rationale: Construct validity is supported by theoretical relationships.
74. A. Any group difference automatically proves bias
B. Bias concerns whether scores have equivalent meaning and consequences across groups
C. Bias is identical to low reliability
D. Bias can be solved by hiding all score reports
✅Answer: B. Bias concerns whether scores have equivalent meaning and consequences
across groups
Rationale: Bias involves fairness and equivalence across groups.
75. A. Minimization of context in assessment
B. Reliance on one score regardless of conditions
C. Recognition that assessment results require contextual interpretation
D. Preference for projective data only
✅Answer: C. Recognition that assessment results require contextual interpretation
Rationale: Context is essential for accurate interpretation.
76. A. A criterion mastery checklist
B. A score compared with a preselected reference distribution
C. A dynamic mediation rating
D. A qualitative interview summary
✅Answer: B. A score compared with a preselected reference distribution
Rationale: Fixed reference systems compare scores to a norm group.
77. A. Francis Galton
B. Carl Jung
C. Aaron Beck
D. B. F. Skinner
✅Answer: A. Francis Galton
Rationale: Galton pioneered measurement of individual differences.
78. A. Jean Piaget
B. Alfred Binet
C. Raymond Cattell
D. Henry Murray
✅Answer: B. Alfred Binet
Rationale: Binet developed early intelligence tests.
79. A. Deviation IQ
B. Need-press framework and thematic interpretation
C. Operant conditioning schedules
D. Dynamic assessment
✅Answer: B. Need-press framework and thematic interpretation
Rationale: Murray developed the need-press theory.
80. A. The mean of the normative sample
B. A score used to separate categories of decision or performance
C. The correlation between form A and B
D. The standard deviation of raw scores
✅Answer: B. A score used to separate categories of decision or performance
Rationale: Cut scores define decision boundaries.
81. A. Norm-referenced aptitude measure only
B. Criterion-referenced reading measure
C. Projective verbal task
D. Interest inventory
✅Answer: B. Criterion-referenced reading measure
Rationale: Mastery decisions require criterion-referenced tools.
82. A. Guarantees absence of observer effects
B. Captures behavior in relation to antecedents and consequences
C. Replaces all need for self-report
D. Is always more reliable than objective tests
✅Answer: B. Captures behavior in relation to antecedents and consequences
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on context and contingencies.
83. A. Retrospective annual report of mood
B. Repeated sampling of experience in real time across settings
C. One-time projective interpretation
D. Purely archival IQ retrieval
✅Answer: B. Repeated sampling of experience in real time across settings
Rationale: Ecological momentary assessment collects real-time data.
84. A. Vocabulary definition only
B. Concept formation and similarity reasoning tasks
C. Grip strength only
D. Hearing screening only
✅Answer: B. Concept formation and similarity reasoning tasks
Rationale: Abstract reasoning involves conceptual thinking.
85. A. Relying only on self-report inventories
B. Integrating collateral data and behavioral observations
C. Avoiding any discussion of limitations
D. Interpreting all elevations as pathology
✅Answer: B. Integrating collateral data and behavioral observations
Rationale: Comprehensive evaluation requires multiple data sources.
86. A. To make the manual longer
B. To maintain relevance of norms, items, and validity evidence
C. To remove all difficult items
D. To avoid the need for examiner training
✅Answer: B. To maintain relevance of norms, items, and validity evidence
Rationale: Test updates ensure accuracy and relevance.
87. A. Artificiality of the testing context
B. Ecological relevance of behavioral data
C. Dependence on retrospective recall only
D. Protection from all ethical concerns
✅Answer: B. Ecological relevance of behavioral data
Rationale: Real-time data improves ecological validity.
88. A. Clear administration instructions
B. Widespread item exposure and compromised security
C. Representative norming procedures
D. Stable scoring algorithms
✅Answer: B. Widespread item exposure and compromised security
Rationale: Test security breaches threaten validity.
89. A. It refers only to whether people like the test
B. It concerns the technical quality of a test, including reliability and validity
C. It applies only to projective methods
D. It is identical to legal defensibility
✅Answer: B. It concerns the technical quality of a test, including reliability and validity
Rationale: Psychometric soundness refers to technical quality.
90. A. Predictive validity
B. Inter-scorer reliability
C. Alternate-form reliability
D. Content validity
✅Answer: B. Inter-scorer reliability
Rationale: This measures agreement between different scorers.
91. A. Collaboration should be avoided to preserve autonomy
B. Collaboration is appropriate when it helps serve clients effectively
C. Collaboration permits unrestricted sharing of all confidential data
D. Collaboration replaces the need for competence
✅Answer: B. Collaboration is appropriate when it helps serve clients effectively
Rationale: Collaboration enhances client care when appropriate.
92. A. Refuse all assistance regardless of risk
B. Provide no support whatsoever
C. Offer limited help within closely related competence while seeking consultation and
arranging proper referral
D. Expand scope permanently after one urgent case
✅Answer: C. Offer limited help within closely related competence while seeking consultation
and arranging proper referral
Rationale: Ethical action balances urgency with competence limits.
93. A. Listing verified license status
B. Describing services actually offered
C. Claiming expertise in tests one has never been trained to use
D. Explaining office hours and contact details
✅Answer: C. Claiming expertise in tests one has never been trained to use
Rationale: Misrepresentation of competence is unethical.
94. A. Test construction should be based on current scientific knowledge
B. Test construction should prioritize popularity over evidence
C. Test construction can ignore validation if items seem reasonable
D. Standardization is optional if experts wrote the items
✅Answer: A. Test construction should be based on current scientific knowledge
Rationale: Ethical test construction requires scientific grounding.
95. A. Rorschach Inkblot Test
B. Thematic Apperception Test
C. Structured self-report inventory with fixed response options
D. Unstructured life narrative
✅Answer: C. Structured self-report inventory with fixed response options
Rationale: Objective tests use structured formats.
96. A. Test-retest interval
B. Relevance of the tool to the assessment purpose
C. Whether the client can read
D. Availability of colored response sheets
✅Answer: B. Relevance of the tool to the assessment purpose
Rationale: Test selection must match the referral question.
97. A. A new test correlates with itself over time
B. A new test improves prediction beyond existing methods
C. A new test has attractive packaging
D. A new test has lower cost than all others
✅Answer: B. A new test improves prediction beyond existing methods
Rationale: Incremental validity refers to added predictive value.
98. A. Integrity and responsible interpretation
B. Criterion contamination
C. Response bias induction
D. Construct underrepresentation
✅Answer: A. Integrity and responsible interpretation
Rationale: Ethical reporting requires honesty and clarity.
99. A. Any professional may use any psychological test if a manual is available
B. Qualification depends on training, competence, and the nature of the instrument and task
C. Licensure is irrelevant in all jurisdictions
D. Test purchase alone establishes competence
✅Answer: B. Qualification depends on training, competence, and the nature of the
instrument and task
Rationale: Proper test use requires competence and qualifications.
100. A. A single score is enough when obtained from a standardized instrument
B. Assessment is a contextual, evidence-based decision process using multiple data sources
when appropriate
C. Assessment is identical to test administration
D. Assessment should avoid ethical and legal issues to remain objective
✅Answer: B. Assessment is a contextual, evidence-based decision process using multiple
data sources when appropriate
Rationale: Assessment is a comprehensive, contextual, and ethical decision-making
process.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 4
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 4
1. A psychometrician is asked to administer and score a cognitive test for a client referred by a
licensed psychologist. Which action is most consistent with lawful and ethical practice?
A. Interpret the results independently and provide treatment recommendations directly to the
client
B. Administer and score the test within assigned functions and refer interpretive integration to
the supervising psychologist
C. Revise the scoring rules when the client appears distressed
D. Give the client a copy of the test manual for transparency
✅Answer: B. Administer and score the test within assigned functions and refer interpretive
integration to the supervising psychologist
Rationale: This reflects role-appropriate practice under Philippine law and ethics because a
psychometrician may administer and score tests within lawful delegated functions, while broader
interpretive integration and treatment recommendations belong to the licensed psychologist
responsible for the case.
2. Which statement best distinguishes psychological testing from psychological assessment?
A. Testing refers only to personality measures, whereas assessment refers only to intelligence
measures
B. Testing is a broader integrative process, whereas assessment is limited to test scores
C. Testing is one tool, whereas assessment integrates multiple data sources for
decision-making
D. Testing is subjective, whereas assessment is always objective
✅Answer: C. Testing is one tool, whereas assessment integrates multiple data sources for
decision-making
Rationale: Psychological testing refers to the use of tests as measurement tools, whereas
assessment is the broader process that combines test results with interviews, observations,
records, and contextual data to support conclusions and decisions.
3. A clinician uses interview data, behavioral observations, case history, rating scales, and test
scores before reaching a diagnostic impression. This best illustrates:
A. fixed reference group scoring
B. multimethod assessment
C. ipsative evaluation
D. content sampling error
✅Answer: B. multimethod assessment
Rationale: This is multimethod assessment because it relies on several different sources and
methods of data collection rather than depending on a single test or information source.
4. Which of the following is the best example of a psychological trait rather than a state?
A. Anxiety experienced during an oral examination
B. Fatigue after a sleepless night
C. Consistent social reticence across settings and time
D. Irritability after receiving criticism that morning
✅Answer: C. Consistent social reticence across settings and time
Rationale: A trait is relatively enduring and stable across situations and time, so consistent
social reticence across different contexts best reflects a trait.
5. A school counselor says, “This student scored at the 84th percentile in reading.” This most
accurately means the student:
A. answered 84% of the items correctly
B. performed better than about 84% of the norm group
C. has an 84 IQ in reading
D. answered 16% of the items incorrectly
✅Answer: B. performed better than about 84% of the norm group
Rationale: A percentile rank indicates the student’s relative standing in a norm group, so an
84th percentile means the student performed as well as or better than about 84% of the
reference group.
6. Which scale of measurement is most appropriate for classifying examinees by blood type?
A. Nominal
B. Ordinal
C. Interval
D. Ratio
✅Answer: A. Nominal
Rationale: Blood type is a categorical classification without inherent order, so it is measured
on a nominal scale.
7. A distribution of test scores has a mean of 50 and a standard deviation of 10. A score of 70
corresponds to a z score of:
A. 1
B. 1.5
C. 2
D. 2.5
✅Answer: C. 2
Rationale: The z score is calculated as (70 − 50) ÷ 10, which equals 2, meaning the score is
two standard deviations above the mean.
8. Which statement about the normal curve is most accurate?
A. It implies that all psychological variables are normally distributed
B. It provides a useful model for understanding many test score distributions
C. It is only relevant to criterion-referenced interpretation
D. It eliminates the need for local norms
✅Answer: B. It provides a useful model for understanding many test score distributions
Rationale: The normal curve is a useful theoretical model for interpreting many score
distributions and standard scores, even though not all psychological variables are perfectly
normally distributed.
9. A correlation of -.80 between depression scores and life satisfaction scores indicates:
A. a weak inverse relationship
B. a strong inverse relationship
C. no relationship
D. a strong positive relationship
✅Answer: B. a strong inverse relationship
Rationale: A correlation of -.80 shows a strong negative relationship, meaning that as
depression scores increase, life satisfaction scores tend to decrease substantially.
10. Which situation best illustrates restricted range reducing a validity coefficient?
A. Correlating a predictor with a criterion in a highly selected group of top applicants only
B. Using a heterogeneous community sample
C. Increasing the sample size from 50 to 500
D. Comparing two tests with opposite scoring directions
✅Answer: A. Correlating a predictor with a criterion in a highly selected group of top
applicants only
Rationale: Restricted range reduces the observed relationship between variables because
there is too little variability in scores, which commonly occurs when only already-selected top
applicants are studied.
11. The primary purpose of reliability evidence is to estimate:
A. fairness in all uses of a test
B. consistency of measurement
C. cultural relevance of item content
D. social desirability in responding
✅Answer: B. consistency of measurement
Rationale: Reliability evidence indicates how consistent or dependable test scores are across
time, items, forms, or raters.
12. A researcher administers the same test to the same group after two weeks and correlates
the scores. This procedure estimates:
A. interscorer reliability
B. split-half reliability
C. test-retest reliability
D. alternate-forms reliability
✅Answer: C. test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability is estimated by giving the same test to the same people at
two points in time and correlating the two sets of scores.
13. Which source of error variance is most directly implicated when an examinee performs
poorly because the testing room is extremely noisy?
A. True score variance
B. Environmental error variance
C. Criterion contamination
D. Construct underrepresentation
✅Answer: B. Environmental error variance
Rationale: A noisy testing room is an environmental factor unrelated to the construct being
measured, so it introduces environmental error variance.
14. Internal consistency is most concerned with the degree to which:
A. items on a test measure the same construct
B. two forms of a test are identical in content
C. scorers agree with each other
D. scores remain unchanged over a lifetime
✅Answer: A. items on a test measure the same construct
Rationale: Internal consistency evaluates whether the items on a test function together as
indicators of the same underlying construct.
15. Which coefficient is commonly associated with internal consistency for dichotomously
scored items?
A. Pearson r
B. KR-20
C. Phi coefficient
D. Kappa
✅Answer: B. KR-20
Rationale: KR-20 is a standard estimate of internal consistency used for tests whose items
are scored dichotomously, such as right-wrong scoring.
16. A test has very high reliability but poor validity. This means the test:
A. consistently measures something, but not the intended construct
B. is valid because reliability guarantees validity
C. should not have norms
D. has no standard error of measurement
✅Answer: A. consistently measures something, but not the intended construct
Rationale: A highly reliable but poorly valid test produces consistent scores, but those scores
do not accurately measure the construct the test is supposed to assess.
17. The standard error of measurement is most useful for:
A. proving that a test is unbiased
B. constructing confidence intervals around observed scores
C. identifying criterion contamination
D. converting raw scores to percentile ranks
✅Answer: B. constructing confidence intervals around observed scores
Rationale: The standard error of measurement is used to estimate a range around the
observed score within which the examinee’s true score is likely to fall.
18. Face validity is best understood as:
A. a statistical estimate of criterion prediction
B. the extent to which a test appears relevant to test takers or users
C. the degree to which items represent the domain
D. evidence from factor analysis
✅Answer: B. the extent to which a test appears relevant to test takers or users
Rationale: Face validity concerns whether a test looks appropriate and relevant on its surface
to those who take or use it.
19. Which type of validity evidence is most directly relevant when a licensure examination is
judged against the content domain it is intended to sample?
A. Predictive validity
B. Concurrent validity
C. Content validity
D. Incremental validity
✅Answer: C. Content validity
Rationale: Content validity is concerned with how well the test content represents the domain
of knowledge or skills the examination is intended to sample.
20. A company wants to know whether an aptitude test predicts later job performance ratings.
The most relevant evidence is:
A. construct validity
B. predictive validity
C. face validity
D. content validity
✅Answer: B. predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity is the relevant evidence when current test scores are used to
predict future performance on an external criterion such as job ratings.
21. Concurrent validity differs from predictive validity mainly in terms of:
A. the statistical method used
B. whether the criterion is measured at approximately the same time or in the future
C. whether reliability is required
D. whether norm groups are used
✅Answer: B. whether the criterion is measured at approximately the same time or in the
future
Rationale: Concurrent validity involves a criterion measured at about the same time as the
test, whereas predictive validity uses a criterion measured later.
22. Which finding would provide the strongest support for construct validity of a new anxiety
scale?
A. Test items look serious to examinees
B. The scale correlates highly with measures of anxiety and less with unrelated constructs
C. The manual has attractive tables
D. The scale is quick to administer
✅Answer: B. The scale correlates highly with measures of anxiety and less with unrelated
constructs
Rationale: Construct validity is supported when the scale shows strong relationships with
theoretically similar constructs and weaker relationships with unrelated constructs.
23. A test may be considered biased if:
A. score differences exist between groups
B. it yields systematically less accurate or less equivalent inferences for one group than
another
C. one group dislikes taking it
D. the test is lengthy
✅Answer: B. it yields systematically less accurate or less equivalent inferences for one
group than another
Rationale: Bias is present when test-based inferences are systematically less accurate, less
equivalent, or less fair for one group than for another.
24. Which statement best characterizes criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. It compares performance against the standing of others in a reference group
B. It interprets performance relative to a defined standard or domain
C. It requires a normal distribution
D. It cannot be used in educational settings
✅Answer: B. It interprets performance relative to a defined standard or domain
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation focuses on whether performance meets a
specified standard or level of mastery, rather than on comparison with other examinees.
25. Norm-referenced interpretation is most appropriate when the purpose is to:
A. determine whether a student has mastered a specific competency
B. compare an examinee’s standing with that of a reference group
C. identify whether a license applicant meets a cut score tied to minimal competence
D. evaluate treatment goals within a single client
✅Answer: B. compare an examinee’s standing with that of a reference group
Rationale: Norm-referenced interpretation is designed to show how an examinee performs
relative to a standardization or reference group.
26. In item analysis, an item difficulty index for a multiple-choice item usually refers to:
A. the proportion of examinees who answered the item correctly
B. the variance of the total test
C. the number of distractors retained
D. the extent of scorer agreement
✅Answer: A. the proportion of examinees who answered the item correctly
Rationale: In classical item analysis, item difficulty is usually defined as the proportion of
examinees who answer the item correctly.
27. A good discrimination index indicates that an item:
A. is answered correctly by nearly everyone
B. distinguishes higher-scoring from lower-scoring examinees
C. has only one plausible distractor
D. should be removed immediately
✅Answer: B. distinguishes higher-scoring from lower-scoring examinees
Rationale: A good discrimination index means the item is effective in separating examinees
with stronger overall performance from those with weaker overall performance.
28. Which item-writing flaw is most likely to lower item quality?
A. Clear wording
B. Plausible distractors
C. Irrelevant difficulty due to complex phrasing
D. Alignment with the construct
✅Answer: C. Irrelevant difficulty due to complex phrasing
Rationale: Complex phrasing can make an item difficult for reasons unrelated to the construct
being measured, thereby reducing item quality.
29. In test development, pilot testing is valuable because it:
A. replaces the need for item analysis
B. allows preliminary evaluation of items before operational use
C. guarantees construct validity
D. eliminates sampling error
✅Answer: B. allows preliminary evaluation of items before operational use
Rationale: Pilot testing makes it possible to examine item functioning, administration
procedures, and other practical issues before the test is used operationally.
30. A test developer wants to set a cut score for minimal competence on a board-type
examination. Which method is specifically designed for this purpose?
A. Angoff method
B. Split-half method
C. Parallel-forms method
D. Factor extraction method
✅Answer: A. Angoff method
Rationale: The Angoff method is specifically used for setting cut scores based on expert
judgments about minimally competent examinees.
31. Which assumption underlies the use of tests for prediction?
A. All constructs are directly observable
B. Test-related behavior can provide information about non-test behavior
C. Error variance is irrelevant
D. All tests are culture-free
✅Answer: B. Test-related behavior can provide information about non-test behavior
Rationale: Prediction through testing depends on the assumption that behavior shown on the
test can provide information about behavior outside the testing situation.
32. In classical test theory, the observed score is understood as:
A. true score minus error
B. true score plus error
C. criterion plus bias
D. trait plus validity
✅Answer: B. true score plus error
Rationale: Classical test theory defines the observed score as the sum of the true score and
measurement error.
33. Which of the following is the best example of an objective personality measure?
A. Rorschach Inkblot Test
B. Thematic Apperception Test
C. Self-report inventory with standardized scoring
D. Free association interview
✅Answer: C. Self-report inventory with standardized scoring
Rationale: Objective personality measures use structured items and standardized scoring
procedures, which is characteristic of self-report inventories.
34. Projective techniques are generally characterized by:
A. highly structured response options
B. ambiguous stimuli intended to elicit personally meaningful material
C. absence of administration instructions
D. superiority over objective tests in all settings
✅Answer: B. ambiguous stimuli intended to elicit personally meaningful material
Rationale: Projective techniques use ambiguous stimuli so that examinees will project their
own meanings, themes, or concerns into their responses.
35. A psychologist asks an examinee to tell a story about a picture showing ambiguous social
interaction. This procedure is most consistent with:
A. a sentence-completion test
B. a projective apperception task
C. a forced-choice inventory
D. a speed test
✅Answer: B. a projective apperception task
Rationale: Asking an examinee to create a story about an ambiguous picture is a classic
projective apperception method, as seen in measures like the TAT.
36. Behavioral assessment differs from many traditional trait measures because it emphasizes:
A. inferred unconscious dynamics only
B. direct observation of behavior in context
C. elimination of self-report data in all cases
D. fixed intelligence levels
✅Answer: B. direct observation of behavior in context
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on observable behavior and the environmental
conditions surrounding it, rather than relying only on inferred traits.
37. In clinical interviewing, which practice most improves the utility of information obtained?
A. Asking leading questions to save time
B. Ignoring context to maintain neutrality
C. Integrating rapport, systematic inquiry, and attention to response style
D. Relying on first impressions only
✅Answer: C. Integrating rapport, systematic inquiry, and attention to response style
Rationale: Useful clinical interviewing requires both strong rapport and systematic, bias-aware
inquiry so that the information collected is both rich and dependable.
38. The mental status examination is primarily used to assess:
A. occupational interests
B. current cognitive, emotional, and behavioral functioning
C. item discrimination
D. family systems only
✅Answer: B. current cognitive, emotional, and behavioral functioning
Rationale: The mental status examination is used to evaluate a person’s present level of
functioning in areas such as thought, mood, cognition, perception, and behavior.
39. A psychologist relies solely on an impressive-seeming description that could fit almost
anyone. This is an example of:
A. halo effect
B. Barnum effect
C. negative skew
D. ipsative scoring
✅Answer: B. Barnum effect
Rationale: The Barnum effect occurs when vague, general descriptions are accepted as
highly accurate or uniquely applicable even though they could describe many people.
40. Mechanical prediction is often contrasted with clinical prediction because mechanical
prediction:
A. always ignores human judgment in data collection
B. combines information using explicit rules or formulas
C. is illegal in applied settings
D. is inferior whenever the case is complex
✅Answer: B. combines information using explicit rules or formulas
Rationale: Mechanical prediction uses objective, explicit rules or formulas to combine data,
unlike clinical prediction, which relies more heavily on professional judgment.
41. Which assessment approach is most appropriate when examining whether a child’s learning
potential improves with guided assistance?
A. Static norm-referenced testing only
B. Dynamic assessment
C. Projective testing
D. Purely actuarial selection
✅Answer: B. Dynamic assessment
Rationale: Dynamic assessment is designed to examine how performance changes when
support, teaching, or guided assistance is provided, making it suitable for evaluating learning
potential.
1. In psychological assessment, which statement best distinguishes assessment from testing?
A. Testing is broader because it includes interviews, records review, and behavioral observation
B. Assessment is broader because it integrates multiple sources of data for decision-making
C. Testing is broader because it includes interpretation, referral, and intervention planning
D. Assessment and testing are identical terms used interchangeably in professional practice
✅Answer: B. Assessment is broader because it integrates multiple sources of data for
decision-making
Rationale: Assessment is broader than testing because it involves integrating test scores with
interviews, observations, case history, and other relevant data to answer a referral question and
guide decisions.
2. A clinician administers a depression inventory, conducts a clinical interview, reviews school
records, and observes parent-child interaction. This activity is best described as:
A. Psychological testing only
B. Behavioral sampling
C. Psychological assessment
D. Test standardization
✅Answer: C. Psychological assessment
Rationale: Using tests plus interview, records, and observation is the hallmark of psychological
assessment rather than test administration alone.
3. Which of the following is the clearest example of a psychological trait rather than a state?
A. Anxiety before a licensure examination
B. Fatigue after an overnight duty
C. Persistent conscientiousness across settings
D. Irritability during a fever
✅Answer: C. Persistent conscientiousness across settings
Rationale: A trait is an enduring tendency. Persistent conscientiousness across settings is
relatively stable, unlike temporary emotions or conditions.
4. Which statement best reflects a core assumption of psychological measurement?
A. Every psychological construct can be measured without error
B. Test behavior can provide clues about non-test behavior
C. Scores are meaningful even without norms or criteria
D. Assessment is valid only when based on self-report
✅Answer: B. Test behavior can provide clues about non-test behavior
Rationale: A foundational assumption in assessment is that behavior shown during testing can
help predict or illuminate behavior outside the testing situation.
5. A psychometrician wants to compare an examinee’s score with the performance of a defined
reference group. Which framework is being used?
A. Criterion-referenced interpretation
B. Domain-referenced interpretation
C. Norm-referenced interpretation
D. Content-referenced interpretation
✅Answer: C. Norm-referenced interpretation
Rationale: Norm-referenced interpretation compares a person’s performance with that of a
designated reference group.
6. Which is the best description of a criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. The examinee is compared with a representative sample
B. The examinee’s score is interpreted relative to a preset level of mastery
C. The examinee’s score is adjusted for cultural background
D. The examinee’s score is interpreted using percentile ranks only
✅Answer: B. The examinee’s score is interpreted relative to a preset level of mastery
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation focuses on whether the person has met a defined
standard rather than how others performed.
7. A school uses a reading screen to determine whether students have mastered a set of
decoding skills. The most appropriate interpretation is:
A. Norm-referenced
B. Criterion-referenced
C. Ipsative
D. Projective
✅Answer: B. Criterion-referenced
Rationale: Mastery of specific reading skills is evaluated against a standard, making the
interpretation criterion-referenced.
8. In test construction, item difficulty for a multiple-choice item usually refers to:
A. The percentage of examinees who answer the item correctly
B. The extent to which the item correlates with total test score
C. The degree to which the item reflects expert judgment
D. The amount of time needed to write the item
✅Answer: A. The percentage of examinees who answer the item correctly
Rationale: For many objective items, item difficulty is indexed by the proportion or percentage of
examinees who answer correctly.
9. An item is most useful for discrimination when it:
A. Is answered correctly by almost everyone
B. Is answered incorrectly by almost everyone
C. Differentiates high scorers from low scorers
D. Requires the longest administration time
✅Answer: C. Differentiates high scorers from low scorers
Rationale: An item is discriminating when those who know more or possess more of the
construct tend to answer it correctly more often than low scorers.
10. Which statistic is most directly concerned with the stability of test scores over time?
A. Test-retest reliability
B. Interscorer reliability
C. Split-half reliability
D. Content validity
✅Answer: A. Test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability estimates stability of scores across time when the construct is
expected to remain reasonably stable.
11. A performance appraisal system yields different scores depending on who rates the same
employee. Which form of reliability is most directly at issue?
A. Alternate-forms reliability
B. Interscorer reliability
C. Internal consistency
D. Predictive validity
✅Answer: B. Interscorer reliability
Rationale: When different raters assign different scores to the same performance, the main
issue is agreement across scorers.
12. A test developer divides a 60-item test into odd and even items and correlates the two
halves. This is primarily estimating:
A. Criterion validity
B. Test-retest reliability
C. Split-half reliability
D. Face validity
✅Answer: C. Split-half reliability
Rationale: Correlating odd and even halves of the same test is a classic way to estimate
split-half reliability.
13. Which situation is the best example of error variance arising from temporary examinee
conditions?
A. A test manual is poorly written
B. The normative sample is too small
C. The examinee slept only two hours the night before testing
D. The scoring key was revised after publication
✅Answer: C. The examinee slept only two hours the night before testing
Rationale: Temporary fatigue can affect performance and introduce error variance unrelated to
the construct being measured.
14. A counselor says, “This test seems valid because the items look relevant to stress.” The
counselor is referring to:
A. Content validity
B. Construct validity
C. Face validity
D. Predictive validity
✅Answer: C. Face validity
Rationale: Face validity refers to whether the test appears, on its face, to measure what it claims
to measure.
15. Which type of validity evidence is most relevant when a board examination is intended to
sample the competencies that define the profession?
A. Face validity
B. Content validity
C. Concurrent validity
D. Ecological validity
✅Answer: B. Content validity
Rationale: A board exam should adequately sample the defined competency domain, which is
the core of content validity.
16. A hospital uses an empathy scale and finds that scores correlate strongly with actual
patient-rated empathy. This is strongest evidence of:
A. Criterion-related validity
B. Face validity
C. Content validity
D. Response bias
✅Answer: A. Criterion-related validity
Rationale: Correlating test scores with a relevant external criterion such as patient ratings is
criterion-related validity evidence.
17. A graduate admissions test is used to forecast first-year academic performance. The most
relevant type of validity is:
A. Concurrent validity
B. Predictive validity
C. Face validity
D. Construct underrepresentation
✅Answer: B. Predictive validity
Rationale: When test scores are used to forecast later performance, the relevant validity
evidence is predictive validity.
18. Evidence that a new anxiety test correlates highly with other anxiety measures and less with
unrelated constructs is most relevant to:
A. Interrater reliability
B. Construct validity
C. Parallel-forms reliability
D. Administrative utility
✅Answer: B. Construct validity
Rationale: A pattern of stronger relations with similar constructs and weaker relations with
dissimilar constructs supports construct validity.
19. Which statement about reliability and validity is most accurate?
A. A test can be valid even when it is highly unreliable
B. A valid test must have some degree of reliability
C. Reliability guarantees validity
D. Validity and reliability are interchangeable
✅Answer: B. A valid test must have some degree of reliability
Rationale: A test cannot validly measure a construct if it yields highly inconsistent scores.
Reliability is necessary, though not sufficient, for validity.
20. A selection test has excellent validity, but the organization decides not to use it because it is
too expensive and adds little practical benefit over current procedures. This concern is best
described as:
A. Fairness
B. Utility
C. Norming
D. Standardization
✅Answer: B. Utility
Rationale: Utility addresses the practical value of using a test, including cost-benefit
considerations in a specific setting.
21. In personnel assessment, a utility analysis is most concerned with:
A. Whether a test appears acceptable to applicants
B. Whether a test is theoretically sound
C. The practical value of using the test in a specific context
D. The legal status of all employment interviews
✅Answer: C. The practical value of using the test in a specific context
Rationale: Utility analysis examines whether the test improves decisions in a meaningful way
and whether its benefits justify its costs.
22. Which method is commonly used to set minimum passing scores based on expert
judgments about item difficulty for minimally competent examinees?
A. Spearman-Brown method
B. Angoff method
C. Split-half method
D. Delphi scaling
✅Answer: B. Angoff method
Rationale: The Angoff method uses expert judgments about the probability that minimally
competent examinees will answer each item correctly.
23. A test score is converted into a percentile rank of 84. This means the examinee scored:
A. 84 items correct
B. 84 standard deviations above the mean
C. Better than about 84% of the reference group
D. In the highest possible classification level
✅Answer: C. Better than about 84% of the reference group
Rationale: A percentile rank indicates relative standing in the reference group. A rank of 84
means the score equals or exceeds approximately 84% of that group.
