24. Which statement about percentile ranks is correct?
A. Equal percentile differences always represent equal raw-score differences
B. Percentile ranks are interval scores
C. Percentile ranks indicate relative standing in a reference group
D. Percentile ranks are unaffected by distribution shape
✅Answer: C. Percentile ranks indicate relative standing in a reference group
Rationale: Percentile ranks are ordinal indicators of position within a reference distribution.
25. A z score of +2.00 indicates that the obtained score is:
A. Two raw-score points above the mean
B. Two standard deviations above the mean
C. At the 2nd percentile
D. Above the mean by 20%
✅Answer: B. Two standard deviations above the mean
Rationale: A z score expresses how far a score is from the mean in standard deviation units.
26. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Median
B. Mode
C. Mean
D. Percentile rank
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean uses every score and is therefore most sensitive to extreme values.
27. In a negatively skewed distribution, the tail extends toward:
A. Higher scores
B. Lower scores
C. The median only
D. Both extremes equally
✅Answer: B. Lower scores
Rationale: A negatively skewed distribution has a longer tail toward the lower end of the score
scale.
28. If a test distribution is highly skewed, which statement is most defensible?
A. Norm-based interpretations should be made cautiously
B. Reliability is always impossible to estimate
C. Validity automatically disappears
D. Standard scores can never be used
✅Answer: A. Norm-based interpretations should be made cautiously
Rationale: Highly skewed distributions can complicate interpretation of normative standing and
standard scores, so caution is warranted.
29. Which is the best reason for using a representative normative sample?
A. To eliminate all forms of measurement error
B. To ensure that interpretations generalize appropriately to the intended population
C. To make the test shorter
D. To guarantee legal defensibility in every context
✅Answer: B. To ensure that interpretations generalize appropriately to the intended population
Rationale: Representative norm samples are essential for making defensible inferences about
how an examinee stands relative to the intended population.
30. A company normed a management test only on senior executives, then used it to screen
entry-level applicants. The main psychometric concern is:
A. Low face validity
B. Inappropriate norm group
C. Excessive interrater agreement
D. Construct redundancy
✅Answer: B. Inappropriate norm group
Rationale: Using executive norms for entry-level applicants creates a mismatch between the
reference group and the actual population of interest.
31. Which is the clearest example of ipsative interpretation?
A. Comparing an applicant with national norms
B. Comparing a student’s math score with a mastery cut score
C. Comparing a person’s verbal score with that same person’s spatial score
D. Comparing two employees from the same department
✅Answer: C. Comparing a person’s verbal score with that same person’s spatial score
Rationale: Ipsative interpretation compares parts of an individual’s own profile rather than
comparing the person with others.
32. An assessor wants to know whether an examinee’s obtained score may differ from the true
score because of measurement imprecision. The most relevant concept is:
A. Standard error of measurement
B. Percentile band
C. Item discrimination index
D. Base rate
✅Answer: A. Standard error of measurement
Rationale: The standard error of measurement estimates the extent to which an obtained score
may differ from the true score because of measurement error.
33. Which statement best captures the meaning of the standard error of measurement?
A. It indicates the average difference between two different tests
B. It estimates the amount of error expected in an obtained score
C. It is the same as standard deviation
D. It proves that the observed score is inaccurate
✅Answer: B. It estimates the amount of error expected in an obtained score
Rationale: SEM quantifies expected score imprecision and helps interpret confidence around
observed scores.
34. A test manual reports coefficient alpha. This coefficient is mainly used to estimate:
A. Temporal stability
B. Internal consistency
C. Predictive validity
D. Alternate-forms equivalence only
✅Answer: B. Internal consistency
Rationale: Coefficient alpha is commonly used to estimate how consistently items in a scale
measure the same underlying construct.
35. Which circumstance would most likely lower test-retest reliability?
A. The construct is highly stable and the interval is appropriate
B. The instructions are standardized carefully
C. The construct itself is expected to fluctuate over time
D. The sample size is increased substantially
✅Answer: C. The construct itself is expected to fluctuate over time
Rationale: If the construct changes naturally, the same person may score differently across
occasions, lowering test-retest reliability.
36. Which of the following is most likely to threaten test fairness?
A. Using standardized instructions for all examinees
B. Ensuring that items are free from construct-irrelevant language demands
C. Requiring speed when speed is unrelated to the target construct
D. Providing uniform scoring procedures
✅Answer: C. Requiring speed when speed is unrelated to the target construct
Rationale: When irrelevant factors affect scores, fairness is threatened because the test is
measuring more than the intended construct.
37. Which situation best illustrates construct-irrelevant variance?
A. A writing test includes tasks that sample writing ability
B. A math test is heavily influenced by difficult reading comprehension unrelated to math skill
C. An intelligence test correlates with school performance
D. A personality scale reflects multiple relevant facets of a trait
✅Answer: B. A math test is heavily influenced by difficult reading comprehension unrelated to
math skill
Rationale: This is construct-irrelevant variance because reading difficulty contaminates
measurement of math ability.
38. A bilingual child performs poorly on an intelligence test administered in a language the child
barely understands. The strongest concern is:
A. High predictive validity
B. Culture-fair standardization
C. Construct contamination by language demands
D. Excessive content sampling
✅Answer: C. Construct contamination by language demands
Rationale: If a child cannot understand the test language well, the score may reflect language
barriers more than the intended construct.
39. A test that underrepresents important aspects of the construct primarily shows:
A. Construct underrepresentation
B. Interscorer drift
C. Criterion contamination
D. Response acquiescence
✅Answer: A. Construct underrepresentation
Rationale: When important facets of the construct are missing from the test, the measure
underrepresents what it claims to assess.
40. Which statement best reflects culturally informed assessment?
A. Use the same interpretation for all examinees to maximize objectivity
B. Consider cultural, linguistic, and contextual variables in test selection and interpretation
C. Avoid standardized tests when working with culturally diverse clients
D. Replace all tests with interviews
✅Answer: B. Consider cultural, linguistic, and contextual variables in test selection and
interpretation
Rationale: Culturally informed assessment does not discard testing; it uses tests thoughtfully in
light of relevant contextual variables.
41. Who is most strongly associated with the first practical intelligence test used to identify
schoolchildren needing educational support?
A. Charles Spearman
B. Alfred Binet
C. David Wechsler
D. Raymond Cattell
✅Answer: B. Alfred Binet
Rationale: Binet is historically associated with the first widely influential practical intelligence test
for school placement.
42. Who proposed the concept of general intelligence, commonly represented as g?
A. Alfred Binet
B. David Wechsler
C. Charles Spearman
D. L. L. Thurstone
✅Answer: C. Charles Spearman
Rationale: Spearman proposed the general intelligence factor, or g, based on positive
correlations among mental tasks.
43. Which pioneer is most associated with the term mental test and early laboratory
measurement of sensory processes?
A. Francis Galton
B. James McKeen Cattell
C. Henry Murray
D. Hermann Rorschach
✅Answer: B. James McKeen Cattell
Rationale: Cattell is closely associated with the term mental test and early laboratory-based
measurement traditions.
44. Which statement best reflects Binet’s orientation toward intelligence assessment?
A. Intelligence is fixed and cannot be influenced by schooling
B. Intelligence should be inferred from diverse higher mental processes
C. Intelligence is best measured through sensory acuity alone
D. Intelligence is equivalent to reaction time
✅Answer: B. Intelligence should be inferred from diverse higher mental processes
Rationale: Binet emphasized practical, higher-order mental functions rather than simple sensory
measures.
45. A psychologist argues that intelligence test scores should be interpreted as an organized
profile of abilities, not only as a single global score. This view is most closely associated with:
A. Wechsler
B. Galton
C. Terman only
D. Goddard only
✅Answer: A. Wechsler
Rationale: Wechsler emphasized that intelligence is multifaceted and that score patterns and
profiles can be clinically informative.
46. Which phenomenon refers to the generational rise in measured intelligence test scores
across time?
A. Hawthorne effect
B. Barnum effect
C. Flynn effect
D. Pygmalion effect
✅Answer: C. Flynn effect
Rationale: The Flynn effect refers to the observed rise in intelligence test scores across
generations in many countries.
47. A board review teacher claims that intelligence tests are useless because culture always
invalidates them. The best response is:
A. Culture is irrelevant if norms are large enough
B. Intelligence tests must always be rejected in multicultural settings
C. Cultural influences matter, but careful selection, administration, and interpretation can still
yield useful information
D. Intelligence can only be measured through projective tests
✅Answer: C. Cultural influences matter, but careful selection, administration, and interpretation
can still yield useful information
Rationale: Culture is an important assessment variable, but it does not automatically invalidate
all intelligence testing when handled competently.
48. Which is the best example of dynamic assessment?
A. Measuring only the final score under fixed standard conditions
B. Assessing current ability, then examining learning potential through mediated teaching
C. Interpreting scores without behavioral observation
D. Using only self-report measures in school decisions
✅Answer: B. Assessing current ability, then examining learning potential through mediated
teaching
Rationale: Dynamic assessment examines not just current performance but also how
performance changes with guided assistance.
49. In educational assessment, Response to Intervention is mainly intended to:
A. Replace all psychoeducational testing
B. Identify learning needs through tiered intervention and progress monitoring
C. Eliminate teacher judgment
D. Diagnose personality disorders in schoolchildren
✅Answer: B. Identify learning needs through tiered intervention and progress monitoring
Rationale: RtI uses graduated interventions and monitoring to identify students who need
additional support and to inform decisions.
50. Portfolio assessment is most distinct from traditional timed objective testing because it
emphasizes:
A. Single-occasion performance under strict standardization
B. Longitudinal samples of meaningful work products
C. Projective interpretation of student drawings
D. Only norm-referenced scoring
✅Answer: B. Longitudinal samples of meaningful work products
Rationale: Portfolio assessment emphasizes authentic work collected over time, not just
one-time performance.
51. Which of the following is the clearest example of an aptitude test?
A. A final exam in abnormal psychology
B. A spelling quiz on last week’s lesson
C. A measure used to estimate readiness for learning future tasks
D. A checklist of current depressive symptoms
✅Answer: C. A measure used to estimate readiness for learning future tasks
Rationale: Aptitude tests are designed to estimate potential for future learning or performance,
not merely past achievement.
52. A psychoeducational battery is most likely to be used when the referral question concerns:
A. Only temporary mood state
B. A broad pattern of cognitive and academic functioning
C. Whether the examinee prefers introversion
D. The projective meaning of ambiguous stimuli
✅Answer: B. A broad pattern of cognitive and academic functioning
Rationale: Psychoeducational batteries are used to evaluate multiple related domains relevant
to learning and school performance.
53. In personality assessment, objective methods are called objective primarily because:
A. They are always free from bias
B. Scoring and administration are standardized more than in projective methods
C. They do not require interpretation
D. They measure only observable behavior
✅Answer: B. Scoring and administration are standardized more than in projective methods
Rationale: Objective methods rely more heavily on standard procedures and explicit scoring
rules, though interpretation still requires judgment.
54. Which statement best characterizes projective techniques?
A. They use fixed-response items with explicit scoring keys
B. They assume that responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying dynamics
C. They are always superior to self-report inventories
D. They eliminate examiner judgment
✅Answer: B. They assume that responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying
dynamics
Rationale: Projective methods are based on the idea that ambiguous stimuli evoke responses
shaped by underlying personality processes.
55. The Rorschach is best classified as a:
A. Structured interview
B. Performance-based projective technique using inkblots
C. Criterion-referenced aptitude battery
D. Neuropsychological screening test
✅Answer: B. Performance-based projective technique using inkblots
Rationale: The Rorschach uses ambiguous inkblot stimuli and asks the person to describe what
is seen, making it a performance-based projective technique.
56. The Thematic Apperception Test primarily uses:
A. Word associations to verbal stimuli only
B. Drawings scored for motor coordination
C. Picture stimuli that elicit stories
D. Timed arithmetic reasoning tasks
✅Answer: C. Picture stimuli that elicit stories
Rationale: The TAT presents pictures and asks examinees to create stories, which are then
interpreted for thematic content.
57. A psychologist wants to reduce impression management in personality assessment. Which
approach is most appropriate?
A. Ignore validity indicators
B. Combine multiple methods and consider response style indicators
C. Use only a single self-report inventory
D. Assume all respondents are fully candid
✅Answer: B. Combine multiple methods and consider response style indicators
Rationale: Because personality responses can be affected by defensiveness or exaggeration,
multimethod assessment and validity indicators are prudent.
58. Validity scales in personality inventories are primarily intended to:
A. Raise reliability automatically
B. Detect response patterns such as exaggeration, defensiveness, or inconsistency
C. Replace the clinical scales
D. Convert raw scores to percentiles
✅Answer: B. Detect response patterns such as exaggeration, defensiveness, or inconsistency
Rationale: Validity scales help the examiner evaluate how the person approached the test and
whether interpretations should be qualified.
59. Which is the best example of behavioral assessment?
A. Interpreting dreams as symbolic material
B. Observing the frequency and antecedents of classroom disruption
C. Asking for free associations to inkblots
D. Using only trait labels in diagnosis
✅Answer: B. Observing the frequency and antecedents of classroom disruption
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on observable behavior and the contexts in which it
occurs.
60. A functional analysis in behavioral assessment is most concerned with:
A. Historical chronology only
B. The relations among antecedents, behavior, and consequences
C. Normative standing relative to peers
D. Projective symbolism
✅Answer: B. The relations among antecedents, behavior, and consequences
Rationale: Functional analysis seeks to understand how behavior is triggered and maintained in
context.
61. Which statement best differentiates clinical from mechanical prediction?
A. Clinical prediction uses no data
B. Mechanical prediction combines information using explicit rules or formulas
C. Clinical prediction is always more accurate
D. Mechanical prediction cannot be used in assessment
✅Answer: B. Mechanical prediction combines information using explicit rules or formulas
Rationale: Mechanical or actuarial prediction relies on systematic rules, unlike purely intuitive
clinical judgment.
62. The Barnum effect is most relevant when:
A. A test has low internal consistency
B. People accept vague, general personality descriptions as uniquely accurate
C. A clinician uses actuarial formulas
D. An examiner obtains informed consent
✅Answer: B. People accept vague, general personality descriptions as uniquely accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect occurs when broad statements are experienced as personally
precise.
63. In suicide assessment, which approach is most defensible?
A. Rely on one self-report item only
B. Base conclusions solely on test scores
C. Integrate interview data, risk factors, protective factors, and clinical judgment
D. Avoid direct questioning to prevent suggestion
✅Answer: C. Integrate interview data, risk factors, protective factors, and clinical judgment
Rationale: Suicide assessment requires comprehensive, clinically grounded integration rather
than reliance on any single source.
64. In forensic assessment, the practitioner should be especially attentive to:
A. Therapeutic alliance only
B. Role clarity, legal standards, and limits of confidentiality
C. Avoiding all record review
D. Using only unstructured interviews
✅Answer: B. Role clarity, legal standards, and limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Forensic assessment requires clarity about the evaluator’s role, the legal context,
and who will receive the findings.
65. Which clinical referral question is best answered by neuropsychological assessment?
A. Which job best fits the client’s interests?
B. Is there evidence of cognitive dysfunction associated with brain impairment?
C. What is the client’s preferred love language?
D. Which projective theme dominates the client’s fantasies?
✅Answer: B. Is there evidence of cognitive dysfunction associated with brain impairment?
Rationale: Neuropsychological assessment is designed to evaluate cognitive functioning in
relation to known or suspected brain dysfunction.
66. Executive functioning is most directly implicated when a patient shows marked difficulty with:
A. Color vision only
B. Planning, inhibition, set shifting, and problem solving
C. Pure-tone hearing thresholds
D. Handedness preference
✅Answer: B. Planning, inhibition, set shifting, and problem solving
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order control processes such as planning,
inhibitory control, flexibility, and strategic problem solving.
67. A patient can recall remote childhood events but cannot retain newly learned information
after a head injury. Which domain is most directly implicated?
A. Procedural motor function
B. Immediate and recent memory processes
C. Visual acuity only
D. Social desirability
✅Answer: B. Immediate and recent memory processes
Rationale: Difficulty retaining new information after injury is a classic memory-related concern,
especially for recent learning.
68. Which neuropsychological finding most strongly suggests the need for caution in interpreting
low scores as global intellectual decline?
A. Strong effort and consistent motivation
B. Sensory or motor limitations affecting test performance
C. Stable educational background
D. Multiple converging indicators across domains
✅Answer: B. Sensory or motor limitations affecting test performance
Rationale: Low cognitive scores may be misleading if poor vision, hearing, or motor limitations
interfere with performance.
69. A dementia evaluation often includes attention to orientation, memory, language, and
everyday functioning because:
A. Neuropsychological conclusions should never involve daily functioning
B. Cognitive deficits must be interpreted in relation to real-world impairment
C. Personality inventories are sufficient for diagnosis
D. Only laboratory imaging matters in dementia workups
✅Answer: B. Cognitive deficits must be interpreted in relation to real-world impairment
Rationale: Neuropsychological conclusions are most meaningful when tied to functional
consequences in daily life.
70. In career assessment, measures of interest are most directly intended to identify:
A. Current psychiatric diagnosis
B. Preferred activities and occupational themes
C. Exact future job performance
D. Only cognitive aptitude
✅Answer: B. Preferred activities and occupational themes
Rationale: Interest measures assess likes, dislikes, and activity preferences relevant to
occupational exploration.
71. Which statement best describes the role of aptitude measures in career assessment?
A. They assess only current job satisfaction
B. They estimate the likelihood of learning or succeeding in certain training or occupations
C. They are identical to projective tests
D. They replace interviews and background review in all cases
✅Answer: B. They estimate the likelihood of learning or succeeding in certain training or
occupations
Rationale: Aptitude measures are meant to estimate potential for future acquisition or success.
72. A career counselor uses interest inventory results as one source of information but also
considers values, abilities, and life context. This is best described as:
A. Overreliance on psychometrics
B. Multimethod assessment
C. Criterion contamination
D. Mechanical scoring error
✅Answer: B. Multimethod assessment
Rationale: Combining interests with values, abilities, and context reflects a multimethod,
integrative approach to career assessment.
73. Which is the best example of a performance test in personnel selection?
A. Asking applicants whether they are hardworking
B. Requiring applicants to complete a job-relevant task under structured conditions
C. Interpreting a projective story
D. Using only reference letters
✅Answer: B. Requiring applicants to complete a job-relevant task under structured conditions
Rationale: Performance tests directly sample behavior relevant to the job, making them valuable
in selection.
74. Why are letters of recommendation often interpreted cautiously in selection settings?
A. They are always invalid
B. They may be affected by leniency, impression management, and variable standards
C. They do not count as assessment data
D. They are illegal in all settings
✅Answer: B. They may be affected by leniency, impression management, and variable
standards
Rationale: Letters are often positively biased and lack uniform standards, which limits their
interpretive strength.
75. Which concept refers to the added value of a test beyond information already available from
existing procedures?
A. Incremental validity
B. Face validity
C. Split-half reliability
D. Item difficulty
✅Answer: A. Incremental validity
Rationale: Incremental validity refers to the additional predictive or decision-making value
contributed by a measure beyond existing information.
76. An organization adopts a cognitive ability test that improves hiring decisions when combined
with interviews and application data. The added benefit is best described as:
A. Construct underrepresentation
B. Incremental validity
C. Response set
D. Content balancing
✅Answer: B. Incremental validity
Rationale: If a new test improves decisions after existing data are already considered, it
demonstrates incremental validity.
77. Which statement best explains validity generalization in personnel selection?
A. Validity evidence from one setting can never inform another
B. A selection method may show broadly consistent validity across jobs or settings under certain
conditions
C. Generalization is equivalent to standardization
D. It removes the need for local validation considerations entirely
✅Answer: B. A selection method may show broadly consistent validity across jobs or settings
under certain conditions
Rationale: Validity generalization refers to evidence that certain predictors can retain usefulness
across multiple contexts, though local conditions still matter.
78. Job satisfaction refers most directly to:
A. A stable intelligence trait
B. A person’s evaluative or affective reaction to work
C. A neuropsychological capacity
D. A measure of productivity only
✅Answer: B. A person’s evaluative or affective reaction to work
Rationale: Job satisfaction refers to how positively or negatively a person experiences or
appraises the job.
79. Organizational commitment is best understood as:
A. A person’s attachment to and identification with the organization
B. The same as cognitive ability
C. A measure of psychopathology
D. A validity scale score
✅Answer: A. A person’s attachment to and identification with the organization
Rationale: Organizational commitment reflects the employee’s bond with the organization and
willingness to remain involved.
80. Consumer psychology often uses attitude measurement because attitudes can help predict:
A. Only neurological status
B. Responses to products, brands, and persuasive messages
C. Only unconscious conflicts
D. Exact individual destiny
✅Answer: B. Responses to products, brands, and persuasive messages
Rationale: Attitude measures are widely used in consumer psychology because attitudes help
explain and predict preferences and reactions.
81. According to RA 10029 and the PAP Code, which statement is most defensible?
A. Any psychology graduate may independently practice psychological services
B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally practice within
the law’s boundaries
C. Registration is optional if the client consents
D. Licensure matters only in hospital settings
✅Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally
practice within the law’s boundaries
Rationale: RA 10029 and the PAP Code emphasize lawful professional practice within one’s
licensed role and competence boundaries.
82. Under the PAP Code, when practitioners work beyond existing competence in a new
technique or population, the most ethical course is to:
A. Proceed without preparation if demand is high
B. Undertake relevant education, training, supervision, consultation, or study
C. Avoid all innovation permanently
D. Delegate the work to an untrained assistant
✅Answer: B. Undertake relevant education, training, supervision, consultation, or study
Rationale: The ethical response to a new method or population is to build competence before or
while carefully engaging in the work.
83. A psychometrician is asked to provide a service in an emergency where no other mental
health professional is available. Which is most ethical?
A. Refuse automatically because emergencies suspend ethics
B. Provide cautious, necessary assistance and discontinue when emergency conditions end,
ensuring proper referral
C. Continue indefinitely even after the emergency ends
D. Offer services outside any reasonable limits without consultation
✅Answer: B. Provide cautious, necessary assistance and discontinue when emergency
conditions end, ensuring proper referral
Rationale: The PAP Code allows emergency assistance so needed services are not withheld,
but it also requires caution, limits, and referral once the emergency ends.
84. Which practice best satisfies the informed consent standard in assessment?
A. Administer the test first, explain later only if results are poor
B. Explain the nature and purpose of assessment, probable uses, and limits of confidentiality
beforehand
C. Provide only the test name
D. Skip consent when using standardized measures
✅Answer: B. Explain the nature and purpose of assessment, probable uses, and limits of
confidentiality beforehand
Rationale: Ethical informed consent requires understandable explanation of what will happen,
why it is being done, how information may be used, and confidentiality limits.
85. A school contracts a psychologist to evaluate a child at the request of the school
administration. Ethically, the psychologist should clarify:
A. Only the child’s IQ score
B. Who the client is, the expected role, the probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
C. Only the teacher’s expectations
D. Nothing, because third-party requests remove the need for explanation
✅Answer: B. Who the client is, the expected role, the probable uses of information, and limits
of confidentiality
Rationale: Third-party requests require clarification of relationships, roles, and confidentiality so
all parties understand the nature of the service.
86. Which action best reflects the ethical duty of confidentiality?
A. Storing case files on an unsecured public computer
B. Discussing client information in class with identifying details
C. Protecting records through secure storage and limiting disclosure to necessary purposes
D. Releasing all data to any referring person upon request
✅Answer: C. Protecting records through secure storage and limiting disclosure to necessary
purposes
Rationale: Confidentiality includes safeguarding information and disclosing only what is
necessary for valid professional or legal purposes.
87. A practitioner posts a disguised case vignette on social media but leaves enough details for
identification. This most clearly violates:
A. Standardization
B. Confidentiality and privacy protections
C. Test-retest reliability
D. Parallel-forms equivalence
✅Answer: B. Confidentiality and privacy protections
Rationale: Even if a case is nominally disguised, details that permit identification violate the duty
to protect client confidentiality.
88. Which statement best reflects the PAP Code regarding telepsychology?
A. Ethical standards do not apply online
B. Online services are exempt from confidentiality rules
C. The same ethical principles governing face-to-face services also apply to online modalities
D. Telepsychology may be done without consent if convenient
✅Answer: C. The same ethical principles governing face-to-face services also apply to online
modalities
Rationale: The PAP Code explicitly extends ethical duties, including consent and confidentiality,
to telepsychology and other online services.
89. A psychometrician begins assessing a close friend for a high-stakes employment matter.
The strongest ethical concern is:
A. Norm obsolescence
B. Multiple relationship and impaired objectivity
C. Low face validity
D. Construct underrepresentation
✅Answer: B. Multiple relationship and impaired objectivity
Rationale: Assessing a close friend in a high-stakes matter creates a multiple relationship that
may impair objectivity and risk exploitation or bias.
90. Which is the best example of avoiding harm in assessment?
A. Using the first available test regardless of fit
B. Selecting methods appropriate to the referral question and examinee characteristics
C. Interpreting scores without checking contextual variables
D. Giving feedback only to third parties without explanation to the examinee when explanation is
appropriate
✅Answer: B. Selecting methods appropriate to the referral question and examinee
characteristics
Rationale: Avoiding harm in assessment involves careful test selection, competent use, and
sensitivity to examinee needs and context.
91. A practitioner discovers that a colleague’s conduct may substantially harm a client. Under
the PAP Code, the practitioner should:
A. Ignore it to protect collegiality
B. Consider appropriate action, including reporting to proper authorities if substantial harm is
likely and confidentiality is not violated
C. Publicly shame the colleague online
D. File a complaint without factual basis
✅Answer: B. Consider appropriate action, including reporting to proper authorities if
substantial harm is likely and confidentiality is not violated
Rationale: The PAP Code allows informal resolution when sufficient, but if substantial harm is
likely, further action may be needed, provided confidentiality is respected.
92. Which is the most ethical response when an organization demands that a psychologist alter
findings to favor a preferred applicant?
A. Comply because the employer pays
B. Make the Code of Ethics known and maintain commitment to accurate reporting
C. Change the report slightly to avoid conflict
D. Delegate the decision to clerical staff
✅Answer: B. Make the Code of Ethics known and maintain commitment to accurate reporting
Rationale: When ethics conflict with organizational pressure, the practitioner should state the
ethical obligation and avoid distorting professional findings.
93. A psychologist is asked to issue an expert opinion about a person without examination,
based only on incomplete summaries. Ethically, the psychologist should:
A. Issue a definitive diagnosis anyway
B. Discuss the limitations of the opinion and basis of conclusions
C. Refuse to mention any limitations
D. Replace all assessment data with intuition
✅Answer: B. Discuss the limitations of the opinion and basis of conclusions
Rationale: Ethical assessment requires that opinions without direct examination be qualified and
limited to what the available evidence can support.
94. Which practice is most consistent with ethical delegation of work?
A. Assigning complex scoring to an untrained assistant without supervision
B. Delegating only tasks that the person can competently perform with appropriate supervision
C. Delegating confidential interpretation to anyone available
D. Hiding delegation from the client
✅Answer: B. Delegating only tasks that the person can competently perform with appropriate
supervision
Rationale: Delegation is ethical only when the delegated person is competent for the task and
appropriate supervision is provided.
95. Under the PAP Code, recording a client’s voice or image during assessment requires:
A. Only verbal permission from office staff
B. Consent from the client or legal representative and explanation of anticipated uses
C. No permission if the psychologist owns the device
D. Automatic permission when the setting is educational
✅Answer: B. Consent from the client or legal representative and explanation of anticipated
uses
Rationale: The PAP Code requires consent before recording voices or images and requires
clear explanation of how the recording will be used.
96. A practitioner advertises guaranteed test outcomes and certain career success for all
clients. This most clearly violates the rule against:
A. False or deceptive statements
B. Criterion referencing
C. Response bias
D. Item difficulty
✅Answer: A. False or deceptive statements
Rationale: Ethical advertising must avoid fraud, exaggeration, or guarantees that misrepresent
what psychological services can deliver.
97. Which of the following is the clearest example of a psychometrically sound board-exam
item?
A. A vague item with two plausible best answers
B. An item requiring guessing between culturally unfamiliar distractors unrelated to the construct
C. A clearly worded item with one best answer and plausible distractors tied to the target
competency
D. An item that uses trick wording to increase difficulty artificially
✅Answer: C. A clearly worded item with one best answer and plausible distractors tied to the
target competency
Rationale: Good licensure items are clear, competency-based, and psychometrically defensible,
with one best answer and credible distractors.
98. In a licensure exam, overemphasizing trivial recall while neglecting application and analysis
would primarily threaten:
A. Content representativeness of the competency domain
B. Interscorer reliability only
C. Face validity only
D. Standard error of measurement only
✅Answer: A. Content representativeness of the competency domain
Rationale: If a licensure exam neglects application and analysis in favor of trivial recall, it fails to
represent the intended professional competency domain adequately.
99. Which situation best illustrates the principle that assessment conclusions should be based
on converging evidence?
A. Making a diagnosis from one elevated scale score alone
B. Integrating test data, interview findings, behavioral observations, and records before forming
conclusions
C. Preferring intuition over data
D. Ignoring contradictory evidence
✅Answer: B. Integrating test data, interview findings, behavioral observations, and records
before forming conclusions
Rationale: Strong assessment conclusions are based on converging evidence from multiple
relevant sources rather than any single datum.
100. Which statement best captures professional judgment in psychological assessment?
A. It is simply the examiner’s personal opinion
B. It involves reasoned interpretation grounded in data, psychometric evidence, context, and
ethical standards
C. It replaces the need for standardized procedures
D. It is unnecessary when computer scoring is available
✅Answer: B. It involves reasoned interpretation grounded in data, psychometric evidence,
context, and ethical standards
Rationale: Professional judgment in assessment is disciplined judgment. It integrates
measurement principles, contextual understanding, and ethical practice rather than personal
impression alone.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 5
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 5
1. In psychological assessment, which statement best distinguishes assessment from testing?
A. Testing is broader because it includes interviews, records review, and behavioral observation
B. Assessment is broader because it integrates multiple sources of data for decision-making
C. Testing is broader because it includes interpretation, referral, and intervention planning
D. Assessment and testing are identical terms used interchangeably in professional practice
✅Answer: B. Assessment is broader because it integrates multiple sources of data for
decision-making
Rationale: Assessment is broader than testing because it involves integrating test scores with
interviews, observations, case history, and other relevant data to answer a referral question and
guide decisions.
2. A clinician administers a depression inventory, conducts a clinical interview, reviews school
records, and observes parent-child interaction. This activity is best described as:
A. Psychological testing only
B. Behavioral sampling
C. Psychological assessment
D. Test standardization
✅Answer: C. Psychological assessment
Rationale: Using tests plus interview, records, and observation is the hallmark of psychological
assessment rather than test administration alone.
3. Which of the following is the clearest example of a psychological trait rather than a state?
A. Anxiety before a licensure examination
B. Fatigue after an overnight duty
C. Persistent conscientiousness across settings
D. Irritability during a fever
✅Answer: C. Persistent conscientiousness across settings
Rationale: A trait is an enduring tendency. Persistent conscientiousness across settings is
relatively stable, unlike temporary emotions or conditions.
4. Which statement best reflects a core assumption of psychological measurement?
A. Every psychological construct can be measured without error
B. Test behavior can provide clues about non-test behavior
C. Scores are meaningful even without norms or criteria
D. Assessment is valid only when based on self-report
✅Answer: B. Test behavior can provide clues about non-test behavior
Rationale: A foundational assumption in assessment is that behavior shown during testing can
help predict or illuminate behavior outside the testing situation.
5. A psychometrician wants to compare an examinee’s score with the performance of a defined
reference group. Which framework is being used?
A. Criterion-referenced interpretation
B. Domain-referenced interpretation
C. Norm-referenced interpretation
D. Content-referenced interpretation
✅Answer: C. Norm-referenced interpretation
Rationale: Norm-referenced interpretation compares a person’s performance with that of a
designated reference group.
6. Which is the best description of a criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. The examinee is compared with a representative sample
B. The examinee’s score is interpreted relative to a preset level of mastery
C. The examinee’s score is adjusted for cultural background
D. The examinee’s score is interpreted using percentile ranks only
✅Answer: B. The examinee’s score is interpreted relative to a preset level of mastery
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation focuses on whether the person has met a defined
standard rather than how others performed.
7. A school uses a reading screen to determine whether students have mastered a set of
decoding skills. The most appropriate interpretation is:
A. Norm-referenced
B. Criterion-referenced
C. Ipsative
D. Projective
✅Answer: B. Criterion-referenced
Rationale: Mastery of specific reading skills is evaluated against a standard, making the
interpretation criterion-referenced.
8. In test construction, item difficulty for a multiple-choice item usually refers to:
A. The percentage of examinees who answer the item correctly
B. The extent to which the item correlates with total test score
C. The degree to which the item reflects expert judgment
D. The amount of time needed to write the item
✅Answer: A. The percentage of examinees who answer the item correctly
Rationale: For many objective items, item difficulty is indexed by the proportion or percentage of
examinees who answer correctly.
9. An item is most useful for discrimination when it:
A. Is answered correctly by almost everyone
B. Is answered incorrectly by almost everyone
C. Differentiates high scorers from low scorers
D. Requires the longest administration time
✅Answer: C. Differentiates high scorers from low scorers
Rationale: An item is discriminating when those who know more or possess more of the
construct tend to answer it correctly more often than low scorers.
10. Which statistic is most directly concerned with the stability of test scores over time?
A. Test-retest reliability
B. Interscorer reliability
C. Split-half reliability
D. Content validity
✅Answer: A. Test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability estimates stability of scores across time when the construct is
expected to remain reasonably stable.
11. A performance appraisal system yields different scores depending on who rates the same
employee. Which form of reliability is most directly at issue?
A. Alternate-forms reliability
B. Interscorer reliability
C. Internal consistency
D. Predictive validity
✅Answer: B. Interscorer reliability
Rationale: When different raters assign different scores to the same performance, the main
issue is agreement across scorers.
12. A test developer divides a 60-item test into odd and even items and correlates the two
halves. This is primarily estimating:
A. Criterion validity
B. Test-retest reliability
C. Split-half reliability
D. Face validity
✅Answer: C. Split-half reliability
Rationale: Correlating odd and even halves of the same test is a classic way to estimate
split-half reliability.
13. Which situation is the best example of error variance arising from temporary examinee
conditions?
A. A test manual is poorly written
B. The normative sample is too small
C. The examinee slept only two hours the night before testing
D. The scoring key was revised after publication
✅Answer: C. The examinee slept only two hours the night before testing
Rationale: Temporary fatigue can affect performance and introduce error variance unrelated to
the construct being measured.
14. A counselor says, “This test seems valid because the items look relevant to stress.” The
counselor is referring to:
A. Content validity
B. Construct validity
C. Face validity
D. Predictive validity
✅Answer: C. Face validity
Rationale: Face validity refers to whether the test appears, on its face, to measure what it claims
to measure.
15. Which type of validity evidence is most relevant when a board examination is intended to
sample the competencies that define the profession?
A. Face validity
B. Content validity
C. Concurrent validity
D. Ecological validity
✅Answer: B. Content validity
Rationale: A board exam should adequately sample the defined competency domain, which is
the core of content validity.
16. A hospital uses an empathy scale and finds that scores correlate strongly with actual
patient-rated empathy. This is strongest evidence of:
A. Criterion-related validity
B. Face validity
C. Content validity
D. Response bias
✅Answer: A. Criterion-related validity
Rationale: Correlating test scores with a relevant external criterion such as patient ratings is
criterion-related validity evidence.
17. A graduate admissions test is used to forecast first-year academic performance. The most
relevant type of validity is:
A. Concurrent validity
B. Predictive validity
C. Face validity
D. Construct underrepresentation
✅Answer: B. Predictive validity
Rationale: When test scores are used to forecast later performance, the relevant validity
evidence is predictive validity.
18. Evidence that a new anxiety test correlates highly with other anxiety measures and less with
unrelated constructs is most relevant to:
A. Interrater reliability
B. Construct validity
C. Parallel-forms reliability
D. Administrative utility
✅Answer: B. Construct validity
Rationale: A pattern of stronger relations with similar constructs and weaker relations with
dissimilar constructs supports construct validity.
19. Which statement about reliability and validity is most accurate?
A. A test can be valid even when it is highly unreliable
B. A valid test must have some degree of reliability
C. Reliability guarantees validity
D. Validity and reliability are interchangeable
✅Answer: B. A valid test must have some degree of reliability
Rationale: A test cannot validly measure a construct if it yields highly inconsistent scores.
Reliability is necessary, though not sufficient, for validity.
20. A selection test has excellent validity, but the organization decides not to use it because it is
too expensive and adds little practical benefit over current procedures. This concern is best
described as:
A. Fairness
B. Utility
C. Norming
D. Standardization
✅Answer: B. Utility
Rationale: Utility addresses the practical value of using a test, including cost-benefit
considerations in a specific setting.
21. In personnel assessment, a utility analysis is most concerned with:
A. Whether a test appears acceptable to applicants
B. Whether a test is theoretically sound
C. The practical value of using the test in a specific context
D. The legal status of all employment interviews
✅Answer: C. The practical value of using the test in a specific context
Rationale: Utility analysis examines whether the test improves decisions in a meaningful way
and whether its benefits justify its costs.
22. Which method is commonly used to set minimum passing scores based on expert
judgments about item difficulty for minimally competent examinees?
A. Spearman-Brown method
B. Angoff method
C. Split-half method
D. Delphi scaling
✅Answer: B. Angoff method
Rationale: The Angoff method uses expert judgments about the probability that minimally
competent examinees will answer each item correctly.
23. A test score is converted into a percentile rank of 84. This means the examinee scored:
A. 84 items correct
B. 84 standard deviations above the mean
C. Better than about 84% of the reference group
D. In the highest possible classification level
✅Answer: C. Better than about 84% of the reference group
Rationale: A percentile rank indicates relative standing in the reference group. A rank of 84
means the score equals or exceeds approximately 84% of that group.
24. Which statement about percentile ranks is correct?
A. Equal percentile differences always represent equal raw-score differences
B. Percentile ranks are interval scores
C. Percentile ranks indicate relative standing in a reference group
D. Percentile ranks are unaffected by distribution shape
✅Answer: C. Percentile ranks indicate relative standing in a reference group
Rationale: Percentile ranks are ordinal indicators of position within a reference distribution.
25. A z score of +2.00 indicates that the obtained score is:
A. Two raw-score points above the mean
B. Two standard deviations above the mean
C. At the 2nd percentile
D. Above the mean by 20%
✅Answer: B. Two standard deviations above the mean
Rationale: A z score expresses how far a score is from the mean in standard deviation units.
26. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Median
B. Mode
C. Mean
D. Percentile rank
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean uses every score and is therefore most sensitive to extreme values.
27. In a negatively skewed distribution, the tail extends toward:
A. Higher scores
B. Lower scores
C. The median only
D. Both extremes equally
✅Answer: B. Lower scores
Rationale: A negatively skewed distribution has a longer tail toward the lower end of the score
scale.
28. If a test distribution is highly skewed, which statement is most defensible?
A. Norm-based interpretations should be made cautiously
B. Reliability is always impossible to estimate
C. Validity automatically disappears
D. Standard scores can never be used
✅Answer: A. Norm-based interpretations should be made cautiously
Rationale: Highly skewed distributions can complicate interpretation of normative standing and
standard scores, so caution is warranted.
29. Which is the best reason for using a representative normative sample?
A. To eliminate all forms of measurement error
B. To ensure that interpretations generalize appropriately to the intended population
C. To make the test shorter
D. To guarantee legal defensibility in every context
✅Answer: B. To ensure that interpretations generalize appropriately to the intended population
Rationale: Representative norm samples are essential for making defensible inferences about
how an examinee stands relative to the intended population.
30. A company normed a management test only on senior executives, then used it to screen
entry-level applicants. The main psychometric concern is:
A. Low face validity
B. Inappropriate norm group
C. Excessive interrater agreement
D. Construct redundancy
✅Answer: B. Inappropriate norm group
Rationale: Using executive norms for entry-level applicants creates a mismatch between the
reference group and the actual population of interest.
31. Which is the clearest example of ipsative interpretation?
A. Comparing an applicant with national norms
B. Comparing a student’s math score with a mastery cut score
C. Comparing a person’s verbal score with that same person’s spatial score
D. Comparing two employees from the same department
✅Answer: C. Comparing a person’s verbal score with that same person’s spatial score
Rationale: Ipsative interpretation compares parts of an individual’s own profile rather than
comparing the person with others.
32. An assessor wants to know whether an examinee’s obtained score may differ from the true
score because of measurement imprecision. The most relevant concept is:
A. Standard error of measurement
B. Percentile band
C. Item discrimination index
D. Base rate
✅Answer: A. Standard error of measurement
Rationale: The standard error of measurement estimates the extent to which an obtained score
may differ from the true score because of measurement error.
33. Which statement best captures the meaning of the standard error of measurement?
A. It indicates the average difference between two different tests
B. It estimates the amount of error expected in an obtained score
C. It is the same as standard deviation
D. It proves that the observed score is inaccurate
✅Answer: B. It estimates the amount of error expected in an obtained score
Rationale: SEM quantifies expected score imprecision and helps interpret confidence around
observed scores.
34. A test manual reports coefficient alpha. This coefficient is mainly used to estimate:
A. Temporal stability
B. Internal consistency
C. Predictive validity
D. Alternate-forms equivalence only
✅Answer: B. Internal consistency
Rationale: Coefficient alpha is commonly used to estimate how consistently items in a scale
measure the same underlying construct.
35. Which circumstance would most likely lower test-retest reliability?
A. The construct is highly stable and the interval is appropriate
B. The instructions are standardized carefully
C. The construct itself is expected to fluctuate over time
D. The sample size is increased substantially
✅Answer: C. The construct itself is expected to fluctuate over time
Rationale: If the construct changes naturally, the same person may score differently across
occasions, lowering test-retest reliability.
36. Which of the following is most likely to threaten test fairness?
A. Using standardized instructions for all examinees
B. Ensuring that items are free from construct-irrelevant language demands
C. Requiring speed when speed is unrelated to the target construct
D. Providing uniform scoring procedures
✅Answer: C. Requiring speed when speed is unrelated to the target construct
Rationale: When irrelevant factors affect scores, fairness is threatened because the test is
measuring more than the intended construct.
37. Which situation best illustrates construct-irrelevant variance?
A. A writing test includes tasks that sample writing ability
B. A math test is heavily influenced by difficult reading comprehension unrelated to math skill
C. An intelligence test correlates with school performance
D. A personality scale reflects multiple relevant facets of a trait
✅Answer: B. A math test is heavily influenced by difficult reading comprehension unrelated to
math skill
Rationale: This is construct-irrelevant variance because reading difficulty contaminates
measurement of math ability.
38. A bilingual child performs poorly on an intelligence test administered in a language the child
barely understands. The strongest concern is:
A. High predictive validity
B. Culture-fair standardization
C. Construct contamination by language demands
D. Excessive content sampling
✅Answer: C. Construct contamination by language demands
Rationale: If a child cannot understand the test language well, the score may reflect language
barriers more than the intended construct.
39. A test that underrepresents important aspects of the construct primarily shows:
A. Construct underrepresentation
B. Interscorer drift
C. Criterion contamination
D. Response acquiescence
✅Answer: A. Construct underrepresentation
Rationale: When important facets of the construct are missing from the test, the measure
underrepresents what it claims to assess.
40. Which statement best reflects culturally informed assessment?
A. Use the same interpretation for all examinees to maximize objectivity
B. Consider cultural, linguistic, and contextual variables in test selection and interpretation
C. Avoid standardized tests when working with culturally diverse clients
D. Replace all tests with interviews
✅Answer: B. Consider cultural, linguistic, and contextual variables in test selection and
interpretation
Rationale: Culturally informed assessment does not discard testing; it uses tests thoughtfully in
light of relevant contextual variables.
41. Who is most strongly associated with the first practical intelligence test used to identify
schoolchildren needing educational support?
A. Charles Spearman
B. Alfred Binet
C. David Wechsler
D. Raymond Cattell
✅Answer: B. Alfred Binet
Rationale: Binet is historically associated with the first widely influential practical intelligence test
for school placement.
42. Who proposed the concept of general intelligence, commonly represented as g?
A. Alfred Binet
B. David Wechsler
C. Charles Spearman
D. L. L. Thurstone
✅Answer: C. Charles Spearman
Rationale: Spearman proposed the general intelligence factor, or g, based on positive
correlations among mental tasks.
43. Which pioneer is most associated with the term mental test and early laboratory
measurement of sensory processes?
A. Francis Galton
B. James McKeen Cattell
C. Henry Murray
D. Hermann Rorschach
✅Answer: B. James McKeen Cattell
Rationale: Cattell is closely associated with the term mental test and early laboratory-based
measurement traditions.
44. Which statement best reflects Binet’s orientation toward intelligence assessment?
A. Intelligence is fixed and cannot be influenced by schooling
B. Intelligence should be inferred from diverse higher mental processes
C. Intelligence is best measured through sensory acuity alone
D. Intelligence is equivalent to reaction time
✅Answer: B. Intelligence should be inferred from diverse higher mental processes
Rationale: Binet emphasized practical, higher-order mental functions rather than simple sensory
measures.
45. A psychologist argues that intelligence test scores should be interpreted as an organized
profile of abilities, not only as a single global score. This view is most closely associated with:
A. Wechsler
B. Galton
C. Terman only
D. Goddard only
✅Answer: A. Wechsler
Rationale: Wechsler emphasized that intelligence is multifaceted and that score patterns and
profiles can be clinically informative.
46. Which phenomenon refers to the generational rise in measured intelligence test scores
across time?
A. Hawthorne effect
B. Barnum effect
C. Flynn effect
D. Pygmalion effect
✅Answer: C. Flynn effect
Rationale: The Flynn effect refers to the observed rise in intelligence test scores across
generations in many countries.
47. A board review teacher claims that intelligence tests are useless because culture always
invalidates them. The best response is:
A. Culture is irrelevant if norms are large enough
B. Intelligence tests must always be rejected in multicultural settings
C. Cultural influences matter, but careful selection, administration, and interpretation can still
yield useful information
D. Intelligence can only be measured through projective tests
✅Answer: C. Cultural influences matter, but careful selection, administration, and interpretation
can still yield useful information
Rationale: Culture is an important assessment variable, but it does not automatically invalidate
all intelligence testing when handled competently.
48. Which is the best example of dynamic assessment?
A. Measuring only the final score under fixed standard conditions
B. Assessing current ability, then examining learning potential through mediated teaching
C. Interpreting scores without behavioral observation
D. Using only self-report measures in school decisions
✅Answer: B. Assessing current ability, then examining learning potential through mediated
teaching
Rationale: Dynamic assessment examines not just current performance but also how
performance changes with guided assistance.
49. In educational assessment, Response to Intervention is mainly intended to:
A. Replace all psychoeducational testing
B. Identify learning needs through tiered intervention and progress monitoring
C. Eliminate teacher judgment
D. Diagnose personality disorders in schoolchildren
✅Answer: B. Identify learning needs through tiered intervention and progress monitoring
Rationale: RtI uses graduated interventions and monitoring to identify students who need
additional support and to inform decisions.
50. Portfolio assessment is most distinct from traditional timed objective testing because it
emphasizes:
A. Single-occasion performance under strict standardization
B. Longitudinal samples of meaningful work products
C. Projective interpretation of student drawings
D. Only norm-referenced scoring
✅Answer: B. Longitudinal samples of meaningful work products
Rationale: Portfolio assessment emphasizes authentic work collected over time, not just
one-time performance.
51. Which of the following is the clearest example of an aptitude test?
A. A final exam in abnormal psychology
B. A spelling quiz on last week’s lesson
C. A measure used to estimate readiness for learning future tasks
D. A checklist of current depressive symptoms
✅Answer: C. A measure used to estimate readiness for learning future tasks
Rationale: Aptitude tests are designed to estimate potential for future learning or performance,
not merely past achievement.
52. A psychoeducational battery is most likely to be used when the referral question concerns:
A. Only temporary mood state
B. A broad pattern of cognitive and academic functioning
C. Whether the examinee prefers introversion
D. The projective meaning of ambiguous stimuli
✅Answer: B. A broad pattern of cognitive and academic functioning
Rationale: Psychoeducational batteries are used to evaluate multiple related domains relevant
to learning and school performance.
53. In personality assessment, objective methods are called objective primarily because:
A. They are always free from bias
B. Scoring and administration are standardized more than in projective methods
C. They do not require interpretation
D. They measure only observable behavior
✅Answer: B. Scoring and administration are standardized more than in projective methods
Rationale: Objective methods rely more heavily on standard procedures and explicit scoring
rules, though interpretation still requires judgment.
54. Which statement best characterizes projective techniques?
A. They use fixed-response items with explicit scoring keys
B. They assume that responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying dynamics
C. They are always superior to self-report inventories
D. They eliminate examiner judgment
✅Answer: B. They assume that responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying
dynamics
Rationale: Projective methods are based on the idea that ambiguous stimuli evoke responses
shaped by underlying personality processes.
55. The Rorschach is best classified as a:
A. Structured interview
B. Performance-based projective technique using inkblots
C. Criterion-referenced aptitude battery
D. Neuropsychological screening test
✅Answer: B. Performance-based projective technique using inkblots
Rationale: The Rorschach uses ambiguous inkblot stimuli and asks the person to describe what
is seen, making it a performance-based projective technique.
56. The Thematic Apperception Test primarily uses:
A. Word associations to verbal stimuli only
B. Drawings scored for motor coordination
C. Picture stimuli that elicit stories
D. Timed arithmetic reasoning tasks
✅Answer: C. Picture stimuli that elicit stories
Rationale: The TAT presents pictures and asks examinees to create stories, which are then
interpreted for thematic content.
57. A psychologist wants to reduce impression management in personality assessment. Which
approach is most appropriate?
A. Ignore validity indicators
B. Combine multiple methods and consider response style indicators
C. Use only a single self-report inventory
D. Assume all respondents are fully candid
✅Answer: B. Combine multiple methods and consider response style indicators
Rationale: Because personality responses can be affected by defensiveness or exaggeration,
multimethod assessment and validity indicators are prudent.
58. Validity scales in personality inventories are primarily intended to:
A. Raise reliability automatically
B. Detect response patterns such as exaggeration, defensiveness, or inconsistency
C. Replace the clinical scales
D. Convert raw scores to percentiles
✅Answer: B. Detect response patterns such as exaggeration, defensiveness, or inconsistency
Rationale: Validity scales help the examiner evaluate how the person approached the test and
whether interpretations should be qualified.
59. Which is the best example of behavioral assessment?
A. Interpreting dreams as symbolic material
B. Observing the frequency and antecedents of classroom disruption
C. Asking for free associations to inkblots
D. Using only trait labels in diagnosis
✅Answer: B. Observing the frequency and antecedents of classroom disruption
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on observable behavior and the contexts in which it
occurs.
60. A functional analysis in behavioral assessment is most concerned with:
A. Historical chronology only
B. The relations among antecedents, behavior, and consequences
C. Normative standing relative to peers
D. Projective symbolism
✅Answer: B. The relations among antecedents, behavior, and consequences
Rationale: Functional analysis seeks to understand how behavior is triggered and maintained in
context.
61. Which statement best differentiates clinical from mechanical prediction?
A. Clinical prediction uses no data
B. Mechanical prediction combines information using explicit rules or formulas
C. Clinical prediction is always more accurate
D. Mechanical prediction cannot be used in assessment
✅Answer: B. Mechanical prediction combines information using explicit rules or formulas
Rationale: Mechanical or actuarial prediction relies on systematic rules, unlike purely intuitive
clinical judgment.
62. The Barnum effect is most relevant when:
A. A test has low internal consistency
B. People accept vague, general personality descriptions as uniquely accurate
C. A clinician uses actuarial formulas
D. An examiner obtains informed consent
✅Answer: B. People accept vague, general personality descriptions as uniquely accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect occurs when broad statements are experienced as personally
precise.
63. In suicide assessment, which approach is most defensible?
A. Rely on one self-report item only
B. Base conclusions solely on test scores
C. Integrate interview data, risk factors, protective factors, and clinical judgment
D. Avoid direct questioning to prevent suggestion
✅Answer: C. Integrate interview data, risk factors, protective factors, and clinical judgment
Rationale: Suicide assessment requires comprehensive, clinically grounded integration rather
than reliance on any single source.
64. In forensic assessment, the practitioner should be especially attentive to:
A. Therapeutic alliance only
B. Role clarity, legal standards, and limits of confidentiality
C. Avoiding all record review
D. Using only unstructured interviews
✅Answer: B. Role clarity, legal standards, and limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Forensic assessment requires clarity about the evaluator’s role, the legal context,
and who will receive the findings.
65. Which clinical referral question is best answered by neuropsychological assessment?
A. Which job best fits the client’s interests?
B. Is there evidence of cognitive dysfunction associated with brain impairment?
C. What is the client’s preferred love language?
D. Which projective theme dominates the client’s fantasies?
✅Answer: B. Is there evidence of cognitive dysfunction associated with brain impairment?
Rationale: Neuropsychological assessment is designed to evaluate cognitive functioning in
relation to known or suspected brain dysfunction.
66. Executive functioning is most directly implicated when a patient shows marked difficulty with:
A. Color vision only
B. Planning, inhibition, set shifting, and problem solving
C. Pure-tone hearing thresholds
D. Handedness preference
✅Answer: B. Planning, inhibition, set shifting, and problem solving
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order control processes such as planning,
inhibitory control, flexibility, and strategic problem solving.
67. A patient can recall remote childhood events but cannot retain newly learned information
after a head injury. Which domain is most directly implicated?
A. Procedural motor function
B. Immediate and recent memory processes
C. Visual acuity only
D. Social desirability
✅Answer: B. Immediate and recent memory processes
Rationale: Difficulty retaining new information after injury is a classic memory-related concern,
especially for recent learning.
68. Which neuropsychological finding most strongly suggests the need for caution in interpreting
low scores as global intellectual decline?
A. Strong effort and consistent motivation
B. Sensory or motor limitations affecting test performance
C. Stable educational background
D. Multiple converging indicators across domains
✅Answer: B. Sensory or motor limitations affecting test performance
Rationale: Low cognitive scores may be misleading if poor vision, hearing, or motor limitations
interfere with performance.
69. A dementia evaluation often includes attention to orientation, memory, language, and
everyday functioning because:
A. Neuropsychological conclusions should never involve daily functioning
B. Cognitive deficits must be interpreted in relation to real-world impairment
C. Personality inventories are sufficient for diagnosis
D. Only laboratory imaging matters in dementia workups
✅Answer: B. Cognitive deficits must be interpreted in relation to real-world impairment
Rationale: Neuropsychological conclusions are most meaningful when tied to functional
consequences in daily life.
70. In career assessment, measures of interest are most directly intended to identify:
A. Current psychiatric diagnosis
B. Preferred activities and occupational themes
C. Exact future job performance
D. Only cognitive aptitude
✅Answer: B. Preferred activities and occupational themes
Rationale: Interest measures assess likes, dislikes, and activity preferences relevant to
occupational exploration.
71. Which statement best describes the role of aptitude measures in career assessment?
A. They assess only current job satisfaction
B. They estimate the likelihood of learning or succeeding in certain training or occupations
C. They are identical to projective tests
D. They replace interviews and background review in all cases
✅Answer: B. They estimate the likelihood of learning or succeeding in certain training or
occupations
Rationale: Aptitude measures are meant to estimate potential for future acquisition or success.
72. A career counselor uses interest inventory results as one source of information but also
considers values, abilities, and life context. This is best described as:
A. Overreliance on psychometrics
B. Multimethod assessment
C. Criterion contamination
D. Mechanical scoring error
✅Answer: B. Multimethod assessment
Rationale: Combining interests with values, abilities, and context reflects a multimethod,
integrative approach to career assessment.
73. Which is the best example of a performance test in personnel selection?
A. Asking applicants whether they are hardworking
B. Requiring applicants to complete a job-relevant task under structured conditions
C. Interpreting a projective story
D. Using only reference letters
✅Answer: B. Requiring applicants to complete a job-relevant task under structured conditions
Rationale: Performance tests directly sample behavior relevant to the job, making them valuable
in selection.
74. Why are letters of recommendation often interpreted cautiously in selection settings?
A. They are always invalid
B. They may be affected by leniency, impression management, and variable standards
C. They do not count as assessment data
D. They are illegal in all settings
✅Answer: B. They may be affected by leniency, impression management, and variable
standards
Rationale: Letters are often positively biased and lack uniform standards, which limits their
interpretive strength.
75. Which concept refers to the added value of a test beyond information already available from
existing procedures?
A. Incremental validity
B. Face validity
C. Split-half reliability
D. Item difficulty
✅Answer: A. Incremental validity
Rationale: Incremental validity refers to the additional predictive or decision-making value
contributed by a measure beyond existing information.
76. An organization adopts a cognitive ability test that improves hiring decisions when combined
with interviews and application data. The added benefit is best described as:
A. Construct underrepresentation
B. Incremental validity
C. Response set
D. Content balancing
✅Answer: B. Incremental validity
Rationale: If a new test improves decisions after existing data are already considered, it
demonstrates incremental validity.
77. Which statement best explains validity generalization in personnel selection?
A. Validity evidence from one setting can never inform another
B. A selection method may show broadly consistent validity across jobs or settings under certain
conditions
C. Generalization is equivalent to standardization
D. It removes the need for local validation considerations entirely
✅Answer: B. A selection method may show broadly consistent validity across jobs or settings
under certain conditions
Rationale: Validity generalization refers to evidence that certain predictors can retain usefulness
across multiple contexts, though local conditions still matter.
78. Job satisfaction refers most directly to:
A. A stable intelligence trait
B. A person’s evaluative or affective reaction to work
C. A neuropsychological capacity
D. A measure of productivity only
✅Answer: B. A person’s evaluative or affective reaction to work
Rationale: Job satisfaction refers to how positively or negatively a person experiences or
appraises the job.
79. Organizational commitment is best understood as:
A. A person’s attachment to and identification with the organization
B. The same as cognitive ability
C. A measure of psychopathology
D. A validity scale score
✅Answer: A. A person’s attachment to and identification with the organization
Rationale: Organizational commitment reflects the employee’s bond with the organization and
willingness to remain involved.
80. Consumer psychology often uses attitude measurement because attitudes can help predict:
A. Only neurological status
B. Responses to products, brands, and persuasive messages
C. Only unconscious conflicts
D. Exact individual destiny
✅Answer: B. Responses to products, brands, and persuasive messages
Rationale: Attitude measures are widely used in consumer psychology because attitudes help
explain and predict preferences and reactions.
81. According to RA 10029 and the PAP Code, which statement is most defensible?
A. Any psychology graduate may independently practice psychological services
B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally practice within
the law’s boundaries
C. Registration is optional if the client consents
D. Licensure matters only in hospital settings
✅Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may legally
practice within the law’s boundaries
Rationale: RA 10029 and the PAP Code emphasize lawful professional practice within one’s
licensed role and competence boundaries.
82. Under the PAP Code, when practitioners work beyond existing competence in a new
technique or population, the most ethical course is to:
A. Proceed without preparation if demand is high
B. Undertake relevant education, training, supervision, consultation, or study
C. Avoid all innovation permanently
D. Delegate the work to an untrained assistant
✅Answer: B. Undertake relevant education, training, supervision, consultation, or study
Rationale: The ethical response to a new method or population is to build competence before or
while carefully engaging in the work.
83. A psychometrician is asked to provide a service in an emergency where no other mental
health professional is available. Which is most ethical?
A. Refuse automatically because emergencies suspend ethics
B. Provide cautious, necessary assistance and discontinue when emergency conditions end,
ensuring proper referral
C. Continue indefinitely even after the emergency ends
D. Offer services outside any reasonable limits without consultation
✅Answer: B. Provide cautious, necessary assistance and discontinue when emergency
conditions end, ensuring proper referral
Rationale: The PAP Code allows emergency assistance so needed services are not withheld,
but it also requires caution, limits, and referral once the emergency ends.
84. Which practice best satisfies the informed consent standard in assessment?
A. Administer the test first, explain later only if results are poor
B. Explain the nature and purpose of assessment, probable uses, and limits of confidentiality
beforehand
C. Provide only the test name
D. Skip consent when using standardized measures
✅Answer: B. Explain the nature and purpose of assessment, probable uses, and limits of
confidentiality beforehand
Rationale: Ethical informed consent requires understandable explanation of what will happen,
why it is being done, how information may be used, and confidentiality limits.
85. A school contracts a psychologist to evaluate a child at the request of the school
administration. Ethically, the psychologist should clarify:
A. Only the child’s IQ score
B. Who the client is, the expected role, the probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
C. Only the teacher’s expectations
D. Nothing, because third-party requests remove the need for explanation
✅Answer: B. Who the client is, the expected role, the probable uses of information, and limits
of confidentiality
Rationale: Third-party requests require clarification of relationships, roles, and confidentiality so
all parties understand the nature of the service.
86. Which action best reflects the ethical duty of confidentiality?
A. Storing case files on an unsecured public computer
B. Discussing client information in class with identifying details
C. Protecting records through secure storage and limiting disclosure to necessary purposes
D. Releasing all data to any referring person upon request
✅Answer: C. Protecting records through secure storage and limiting disclosure to necessary
purposes
Rationale: Confidentiality includes safeguarding information and disclosing only what is
necessary for valid professional or legal purposes.
87. A practitioner posts a disguised case vignette on social media but leaves enough details for
identification. This most clearly violates:
A. Standardization
B. Confidentiality and privacy protections
C. Test-retest reliability
D. Parallel-forms equivalence
✅Answer: B. Confidentiality and privacy protections
Rationale: Even if a case is nominally disguised, details that permit identification violate the duty
to protect client confidentiality.
88. Which statement best reflects the PAP Code regarding telepsychology?
A. Ethical standards do not apply online
B. Online services are exempt from confidentiality rules
C. The same ethical principles governing face-to-face services also apply to online modalities
D. Telepsychology may be done without consent if convenient
✅Answer: C. The same ethical principles governing face-to-face services also apply to online
modalities
Rationale: The PAP Code explicitly extends ethical duties, including consent and confidentiality,
to telepsychology and other online services.
89. A psychometrician begins assessing a close friend for a high-stakes employment matter.
The strongest ethical concern is:
A. Norm obsolescence
B. Multiple relationship and impaired objectivity
C. Low face validity
D. Construct underrepresentation
✅Answer: B. Multiple relationship and impaired objectivity
Rationale: Assessing a close friend in a high-stakes matter creates a multiple relationship that
may impair objectivity and risk exploitation or bias.
90. Which is the best example of avoiding harm in assessment?
A. Using the first available test regardless of fit
