B. Selecting methods appropriate to the referral question and examinee characteristics
C. Interpreting scores without checking contextual variables
D. Giving feedback only to third parties without explanation to the examinee when explanation is
appropriate
✅Answer: B. Selecting methods appropriate to the referral question and examinee
characteristics
Rationale: Avoiding harm in assessment involves careful test selection, competent use, and
sensitivity to examinee needs and context.
91. A practitioner discovers that a colleague’s conduct may substantially harm a client. Under
the PAP Code, the practitioner should:
A. Ignore it to protect collegiality
B. Consider appropriate action, including reporting to proper authorities if substantial harm is
likely and confidentiality is not violated
C. Publicly shame the colleague online
D. File a complaint without factual basis
✅Answer: B. Consider appropriate action, including reporting to proper authorities if
substantial harm is likely and confidentiality is not violated
Rationale: The PAP Code allows informal resolution when sufficient, but if substantial harm is
likely, further action may be needed, provided confidentiality is respected.
92. Which is the most ethical response when an organization demands that a psychologist alter
findings to favor a preferred applicant?
A. Comply because the employer pays
B. Make the Code of Ethics known and maintain commitment to accurate reporting
C. Change the report slightly to avoid conflict
D. Delegate the decision to clerical staff
✅Answer: B. Make the Code of Ethics known and maintain commitment to accurate reporting
Rationale: When ethics conflict with organizational pressure, the practitioner should state the
ethical obligation and avoid distorting professional findings.
93. A psychologist is asked to issue an expert opinion about a person without examination,
based only on incomplete summaries. Ethically, the psychologist should:
A. Issue a definitive diagnosis anyway
B. Discuss the limitations of the opinion and basis of conclusions
C. Refuse to mention any limitations
D. Replace all assessment data with intuition
✅Answer: B. Discuss the limitations of the opinion and basis of conclusions
Rationale: Ethical assessment requires that opinions without direct examination be qualified and
limited to what the available evidence can support.
94. Which practice is most consistent with ethical delegation of work?
A. Assigning complex scoring to an untrained assistant without supervision
B. Delegating only tasks that the person can competently perform with appropriate supervision
C. Delegating confidential interpretation to anyone available
D. Hiding delegation from the client
✅Answer: B. Delegating only tasks that the person can competently perform with appropriate
supervision
Rationale: Delegation is ethical only when the delegated person is competent for the task and
appropriate supervision is provided.
95. Under the PAP Code, recording a client’s voice or image during assessment requires:
A. Only verbal permission from office staff
B. Consent from the client or legal representative and explanation of anticipated uses
C. No permission if the psychologist owns the device
D. Automatic permission when the setting is educational
✅Answer: B. Consent from the client or legal representative and explanation of anticipated
uses
Rationale: The PAP Code requires consent before recording voices or images and requires
clear explanation of how the recording will be used.
96. A practitioner advertises guaranteed test outcomes and certain career success for all
clients. This most clearly violates the rule against:
A. False or deceptive statements
B. Criterion referencing
C. Response bias
D. Item difficulty
✅Answer: A. False or deceptive statements
Rationale: Ethical advertising must avoid fraud, exaggeration, or guarantees that misrepresent
what psychological services can deliver.
97. Which of the following is the clearest example of a psychometrically sound board-exam
item?
A. A vague item with two plausible best answers
B. An item requiring guessing between culturally unfamiliar distractors unrelated to the construct
C. A clearly worded item with one best answer and plausible distractors tied to the target
competency
D. An item that uses trick wording to increase difficulty artificially
✅Answer: C. A clearly worded item with one best answer and plausible distractors tied to the
target competency
Rationale: Good licensure items are clear, competency-based, and psychometrically defensible,
with one best answer and credible distractors.
98. In a licensure exam, overemphasizing trivial recall while neglecting application and analysis
would primarily threaten:
A. Content representativeness of the competency domain
B. Interscorer reliability only
C. Face validity only
D. Standard error of measurement only
✅Answer: A. Content representativeness of the competency domain
Rationale: If a licensure exam neglects application and analysis in favor of trivial recall, it fails to
represent the intended professional competency domain adequately.
99. Which situation best illustrates the principle that assessment conclusions should be based
on converging evidence?
A. Making a diagnosis from one elevated scale score alone
B. Integrating test data, interview findings, behavioral observations, and records before forming
conclusions
C. Preferring intuition over data
D. Ignoring contradictory evidence
✅Answer: B. Integrating test data, interview findings, behavioral observations, and records
before forming conclusions
Rationale: Strong assessment conclusions are based on converging evidence from multiple
relevant sources rather than any single datum.
100. Which statement best captures professional judgment in psychological assessment?
A. It is simply the examiner’s personal opinion
B. It involves reasoned interpretation grounded in data, psychometric evidence, context, and
ethical standards
C. It replaces the need for standardized procedures
D. It is unnecessary when computer scoring is available
✅Answer: B. It involves reasoned interpretation grounded in data, psychometric evidence,
context, and ethical standards
Rationale: Professional judgment in assessment is disciplined judgment. It integrates
measurement principles, contextual understanding, and ethical practice rather than personal
impression alone.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 6
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 6
1. A psychometrician says that a client’s score on a depression inventory proves that the client
has major depressive disorder. The most appropriate criticism is that the statement:
A. confuses screening with diagnosis
B. ignores the need for alternate-form reliability
C. assumes all self-report tests are invalid
D. treats depression as a purely neurological condition
✅Answer: A. confuses screening with diagnosis
Rationale: A test score may contribute to clinical decision-making, but diagnosis requires
integration of broader assessment data and clinical judgment rather than equating a single
inventory score with a psychiatric diagnosis.
2. Which statement best captures the distinction between psychological testing and
psychological assessment?
A. Testing is individualized, whereas assessment is standardized
B. Testing is one tool, whereas assessment is a broader decision-making process
C. Testing is qualitative, whereas assessment is always quantitative
D. Testing is only for clinical settings, whereas assessment is for schools and industry
✅Answer: B. Testing is one tool, whereas assessment is a broader decision-making process
Rationale: Testing is only one component of the larger assessment enterprise, which may
include interview, observation, history, and multiple data sources.
3. A school counselor combines interview data, classroom observations, rating scales, and an
achievement test before making recommendations. This practice primarily illustrates:
A. ipsative interpretation
B. fixed-reference scoring
C. multimethod assessment
D. projective assessment
✅Answer: C. multimethod assessment
Rationale: Using several sources and methods before arriving at a conclusion exemplifies
multimethod assessment and strengthens interpretive decisions.
4. In psychological measurement, a trait is best understood as:
A. a temporary reaction to a specific situation
B. an enduring disposition to behave in a certain way
C. a response set caused by social desirability
D. a score derived only from factor analysis
✅Answer: B. an enduring disposition to behave in a certain way
Rationale: A trait is a relatively stable characteristic or tendency, unlike a temporary state or
situational reaction.
5. Which scenario best reflects a state rather than a trait?
A. A child is typically shy across most situations
B. A student feels intense anxiety during today’s oral exam
C. An employee is consistently conscientious at work
D. A patient has long-standing suspiciousness in relationships
✅Answer: B. A student feels intense anxiety during today’s oral exam
Rationale: A state refers to a temporary, situation-linked condition; acute exam anxiety is a
good example.
6. A clinician wants to predict future college performance from an admissions test. The issue
most directly involved is:
A. content balancing
B. predictive validity
C. face validity
D. split-half reliability
✅Answer: B. predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity concerns how well current test scores forecast future outcomes
such as college performance.
7. A test has excellent internal consistency but poor predictive validity for job success. The best
conclusion is that the test:
A. is reliable but may not be useful for selection
B. is invalid because all reliable tests are predictive
C. cannot be revised without changing its norms
D. has high utility because consistency is sufficient
✅Answer: A. is reliable but may not be useful for selection
Rationale: Reliability alone does not guarantee that a test predicts the criterion or is practically
useful; selection decisions require validity and often utility evidence.
8. Which is the best example of criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. Maria scored higher than 82% of examinees her age
B. Paulo obtained a T score of 60
C. Liza met 18 of 20 mastery objectives in algebra
D. Ben’s IQ falls within the average range
✅Answer: C. Liza met 18 of 20 mastery objectives in algebra
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation compares performance to a defined standard or
mastery requirement rather than to other examinees.
9. A norm group that does not adequately represent the intended test population most directly
threatens:
A. test security
B. score comparability
C. content sampling
D. examiner objectivity
✅Answer: B. score comparability
Rationale: If the norm group is unrepresentative, comparisons of an individual’s score to that
norm base become questionable.
10. A psychometrician says a test is fair because all examinees took the same form under the
same time limit. This statement is incomplete because fairness also requires attention to:
A. copyright registration
B. cultural and interpretive issues
C. projective scoring systems
D. the absence of all measurement error
✅Answer: B. cultural and interpretive issues
Rationale: Fairness is not exhausted by identical administration conditions; cultural
accessibility, relevance, and interpretation also matter.
11. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Median
B. Mode
C. Mean
D. Percentile rank
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean is most influenced by extreme values because every score contributes
directly to its calculation.
12. When test scores cluster around the mean in a bell-shaped pattern, the distribution is most
likely:
A. bimodal
B. normal
C. platykurtic only
D. negatively skewed only
✅Answer: B. normal
Rationale: A bell-shaped symmetrical clustering around the mean describes a normal
distribution.
13. A z score of +2.00 indicates that the examinee scored:
A. 2 raw-score units above the mean
B. 2 standard deviations above the mean
C. in the 2nd percentile
D. 20 T-score points below average
✅Answer: B. 2 standard deviations above the mean
Rationale: A z score expresses distance from the mean in standard deviation units.
14. Which correlation coefficient is most appropriate for two rank-ordered variables?
A. Pearson r
B. Spearman rho
C. Coefficient alpha
D. Phi coefficient for true-score variance
✅Answer: B. Spearman rho
Rationale: Spearman rho is appropriate for rank-ordered data and ordinal relationships.
15. If two variables correlate at -.70, the most defensible interpretation is that:
A. one variable causes the other to decrease
B. the variables move in opposite directions
C. 70% of the variance is shared
D. the relationship is too weak to interpret
✅Answer: B. the variables move in opposite directions
Rationale: A negative correlation indicates an inverse relationship: as one variable increases,
the other tends to decrease.
16. A coefficient of determination of .36 means:
A. 36% of the variance is shared
B. the test is 36% reliable
C. error variance is exactly 64%
D. 36% of test items are discriminating
✅Answer: A. 36% of the variance is shared
Rationale: The coefficient of determination represents the proportion of variance in common
between two variables.
17. A test-retest reliability coefficient is likely to be spuriously lowered when:
A. the construct is highly stable
B. the retest interval allows real change in the trait
C. the same examinees are retested
D. items are scored dichotomously
✅Answer: B. the retest interval allows real change in the trait
Rationale: When the underlying construct changes between administrations, test-retest
reliability decreases because instability is real, not merely measurement error.
18. Parallel-forms reliability is most useful when the assessor wants to minimize:
A. practice effects
B. halo effects
C. criterion contamination
D. acquiescence bias
✅Answer: A. practice effects
Rationale: Parallel forms help reduce memory and practice effects by using equivalent but
nonidentical content.
19. Internal consistency reliability is primarily concerned with the extent to which:
A. raters agree with one another
B. items measure the same construct
C. test scores predict an external criterion
D. the same results emerge after therapy
✅Answer: B. items measure the same construct
Rationale: Internal consistency asks whether test items hang together as indicators of the
same domain or construct.
20. Inter-scorer reliability is especially critical for:
A. speeded arithmetic tests only
B. highly structured multiple-choice tests
C. tests requiring clinical judgment in scoring
D. criterion-referenced classroom quizzes
✅Answer: C. tests requiring clinical judgment in scoring
Rationale: When scoring involves subjective interpretation, agreement among scorers
becomes essential.
21. The standard error of measurement is most useful for:
A. identifying causal variables
B. estimating a band around an observed score
C. proving content validity
D. converting raw scores to percentiles
✅Answer: B. estimating a band around an observed score
Rationale: The standard error of measurement helps build confidence bands around
observed scores to estimate likely true-score range.
22. Which statement about validity is most accurate?
A. A test is either valid or invalid in all situations
B. Validity refers to the consistency of test scores
C. Validity concerns the appropriateness of interpretations
D. Validity is established once at publication and never revisited
✅Answer: C. Validity concerns the appropriateness of interpretations
Rationale: Modern validity focuses on whether score interpretations and resulting decisions
are justified for a particular use.
23. A table of specifications is most directly associated with:
A. construct underrepresentation
B. content validation
C. criterion contamination
D. utility analysis
✅Answer: B. content validation
Rationale: A table of specifications helps ensure adequate sampling of content areas and
cognitive levels, which supports content validity.
24. Concurrent validity is demonstrated when test scores are related to:
A. future performance measured much later
B. a criterion obtained at about the same time
C. item-total correlations within the test
D. judges’ impressions of face value
✅Answer: B. a criterion obtained at about the same time
Rationale: Concurrent validity examines correlation with a criterion measured in the present
or near-present.
25. Construct validity is most strongly supported by evidence that a test:
A. looks acceptable to examinees
B. samples all textbook topics
C. behaves as theory predicts across studies
D. has equal means across all groups
✅Answer: C. behaves as theory predicts across studies
Rationale: Construct validity is supported when relationships with other variables conform to
theoretical expectations.
26. A measure of social anxiety correlates positively with fear of negative evaluation and
negatively with social confidence. This pattern most directly supports:
A. face validity
B. convergent and discriminant evidence
C. test security
D. utility gain
✅Answer: B. convergent and discriminant evidence
Rationale: Positive relation with related constructs and negative or low relation with
contrasting constructs supports construct validity through convergent/discriminant patterns.
27. A personnel test predicts job performance moderately well, but using it does not improve
hiring decisions over current methods. This problem is best framed as one of:
A. utility
B. scaling
C. standardization
D. item homogeneity
✅Answer: A. utility
Rationale: Even with validity, a test may add little practical value if it does not improve
decisions relative to costs and existing methods.
28. In utility analysis, a cut score is primarily used to:
A. reduce reliability coefficients
B. divide examinees into decision categories
C. eliminate the need for validation
D. equalize subgroup means
✅Answer: B. divide examinees into decision categories
Rationale: Cut scores are used to classify examinees, such as pass/fail or accept/reject.
29. The Angoff method is commonly used to:
A. estimate test-retest stability
B. set defensible cut scores
C. derive factor loadings
D. calculate percentile ranks
✅Answer: B. set defensible cut scores
Rationale: The Angoff method is a recognized standard-setting approach for determining
passing or proficiency thresholds.
30. During test conceptualization, the most important first step is to:
A. publish norms immediately
B. define the construct clearly
C. compute inter-item correlations
D. write difficult items first
✅Answer: B. define the construct clearly
Rationale: Sound test development starts with clear conceptualization of what is to be
measured before writing items or norming.
31. Which item would most likely have the highest difficulty index in classical test theory?
A. An item answered correctly by 20% of examinees
B. An item answered correctly by 35% of examinees
C. An item answered correctly by 60% of examinees
D. An item answered correctly by 95% of examinees
✅Answer: D. An item answered correctly by 95% of examinees
Rationale: In classical test theory, item difficulty index usually reflects proportion answering
correctly; higher p values mean easier items.
32. An item discrimination index is most useful because it helps determine whether an item:
A. differentiates high scorers from low scorers
B. measures a legally protected category
C. will produce a normal distribution
D. has face validity for respondents
✅Answer: A. differentiates high scorers from low scorers
Rationale: Discrimination indicates how well an item separates examinees with strong overall
performance from those with weak performance.
33. Which practice best improves the quality of multiple-choice items?
A. Using implausible distractors to speed answering
B. Including clues to the correct answer in wording
C. Writing distractors that reflect common errors
D. Making the longest option always correct
✅Answer: C. Writing distractors that reflect common errors
Rationale: Plausible distractors based on common misconceptions improve item functioning
and discrimination.
34. Item response theory is especially valuable because it focuses on:
A. legal rights of testtakers
B. the interaction between person ability and item properties
C. replacement of validity evidence
D. observation-based scoring only
✅Answer: B. the interaction between person ability and item properties
Rationale: IRT models probability of a response based on both examinee trait level and item
characteristics such as difficulty and discrimination.
35. A psychologist argues that intelligence is a single general ability underlying diverse cognitive
tasks. This position is most associated with:
A. Spearman
B. Thurstone
C. Maslow
D. Rogers
✅Answer: A. Spearman
Rationale: Spearman is most associated with general intelligence, or g.
36. Which pioneer is most directly associated with the first practical intelligence tests for
identifying schoolchildren needing assistance?
A. Galton
B. Binet
C. Cattell
D. Murray
✅Answer: B. Binet
Rationale: Binet developed early practical intelligence tests for school placement and
educational assistance.
37. Galton’s early work on intelligence emphasized:
A. unconscious conflict
B. sensory and psychophysical processes
C. social learning histories
D. mastery testing in schools
✅Answer: B. sensory and psychophysical processes
Rationale: Galton’s approach to intelligence emphasized sensory acuity and psychophysical
performance.
38. The Flynn effect refers to:
A. declining reliability coefficients over time
B. rising average IQ scores across generations
C. the superiority of individual over group tests
D. the elimination of culture from intelligence testing
✅Answer: B. rising average IQ scores across generations
Rationale: The Flynn effect refers to long-term generational increases in measured IQ scores.
39. A major criticism of intelligence testing in multicultural contexts is that:
A. all intelligence tests measure only memory
B. measured intelligence can be affected by cultural experience
C. IQ tests cannot be standardized
D. group tests are always fairer than individual tests
✅Answer: B. measured intelligence can be affected by cultural experience
Rationale: A longstanding issue in intelligence testing is that cultural, linguistic, and
experiential differences may affect measured performance.
40. A clinician comparing verbal comprehension, working memory, and processing speed
patterns is most likely using:
A. projective interpretation
B. profile analysis within an intelligence battery
C. criterion-keyed personality assessment
D. ipsative vocational matching
✅Answer: B. profile analysis within an intelligence battery
Rationale: Comparing index scores within a battery is a form of profile analysis to identify
relative cognitive strengths and weaknesses.
41. Response to Intervention is primarily important in educational assessment because it:
A. replaces all standardized testing permanently
B. emphasizes early support and progress monitoring
C. is designed only for gifted children
D. makes norm-referenced data unnecessary in all cases
✅Answer: B. emphasizes early support and progress monitoring
Rationale: RtI focuses on early intervention, repeated progress data, and responsiveness to
instruction before or alongside categorical decisions.
42. Dynamic assessment differs from traditional static testing because it emphasizes:
A. fixed time limits
B. learning potential during mediated interaction
C. interpretation without examiner involvement
D. elimination of feedback during administration
✅Answer: B. learning potential during mediated interaction
Rationale: Dynamic assessment evaluates how performance changes with assistance,
emphasizing modifiability and learning potential.
43. Which is the best example of an aptitude test?
A. A test of current mastery of algebra lessons already taught
B. A measure intended to estimate potential for future learning
C. A checklist of depressive symptoms
D. A behavioral observation log of classroom conduct
✅Answer: B. A measure intended to estimate potential for future learning
Rationale: Aptitude tests are designed to estimate capacity or potential for future learning or
performance.
44. Portfolio assessment is most useful when the goal is to:
A. derive deviation IQs
B. evaluate performance across time and contexts
C. replace teacher judgment entirely
D. estimate split-half reliability quickly
✅Answer: B. evaluate performance across time and contexts
Rationale: Portfolio assessment captures accumulated work products and development over
time.
45. In personality assessment, an objective test is called “objective” mainly because:
A. it is free of all interpretation
B. scoring and administration are relatively standardized
C. it measures only observable behavior
D. it cannot be faked
✅Answer: B. scoring and administration are relatively standardized
Rationale: Objective methods are termed objective mainly because administration, scoring,
and response formats are more structured and standardized than projective methods.
46. The MMPI is best described as having been developed mainly through:
A. rational-content keying only
B. criterion-group or empirical keying
C. projective hypothesis testing
D. pure factor analysis alone
✅Answer: B. criterion-group or empirical keying
Rationale: The MMPI is the classic example of criterion-group empirical keying, selecting
items that distinguish known groups.
47. A validity scale on a personality inventory is primarily intended to:
A. assess item difficulty
B. detect response styles or unusual responding
C. replace clinical interpretation
D. determine intellectual giftedness
✅Answer: B. detect response styles or unusual responding
Rationale: Validity scales help evaluate defensiveness, exaggeration, inconsistency, and
other response-style issues.
48. Which statement about projective techniques is most accurate?
A. They eliminate examiner subjectivity
B. They use ambiguous stimuli to elicit meaning-laden responses
C. They are always superior to objective inventories
D. They require no reliability evidence
✅Answer: B. They use ambiguous stimuli to elicit meaning-laden responses
Rationale: Projective techniques present ambiguous material and assume responses reflect
internal themes, needs, or conflicts.
49. The Thematic Apperception Test primarily uses:
A. geometric designs
B. paired comparisons
C. ambiguous pictures for storytelling
D. timed arithmetic tasks
✅Answer: C. ambiguous pictures for storytelling
Rationale: The TAT uses picture cards that invite narrative stories to reveal themes and
motives.
50. Behavioral assessment places greatest emphasis on:
A. inferred unconscious dynamics only
B. directly observed behavior in context
C. deviation IQ interpretation
D. factor-analytic scoring keys
✅Answer: B. directly observed behavior in context
Rationale: Behavioral assessment emphasizes what the person does, under what conditions,
and with what consequences.
51. A psychologist asks what behavior occurs, under what conditions, and with what
consequences. This question pattern reflects:
A. actuarial prediction
B. functional behavioral assessment
C. criterion contamination
D. ipsative scaling
✅Answer: B. functional behavioral assessment
Rationale: The who-what-when-where-why approach seeks functional relations among
antecedents, behaviors, and consequences.
52. In clinical assessment, case history data are most useful because they:
A. guarantee diagnosis
B. provide contextual information for interpretation
C. are more valid than all tests
D. eliminate the need for interviews
✅Answer: B. provide contextual information for interpretation
Rationale: Case history data add background, developmental, and situational context that
helps interpret current findings.
53. The Barnum effect refers to the tendency of people to:
A. reject all personality feedback
B. accept vague, general descriptions as uniquely accurate
C. perform better on individual than group tests
D. distort responses under timed conditions
✅Answer: B. accept vague, general descriptions as uniquely accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect describes acceptance of generic personality statements as
personally precise.
54. Clinical prediction differs from mechanical prediction in that clinical prediction:
A. always outperforms actuarial methods
B. relies more heavily on professional judgment
C. excludes test data
D. cannot be evaluated empirically
✅Answer: B. relies more heavily on professional judgment
Rationale: Clinical prediction depends more on clinician interpretation, whereas mechanical
prediction uses formal rules or equations.
55. Which situation best illustrates criterion contamination in validation?
A. The criterion includes information derived from the predictor test itself
B. The sample is too large for the study design
C. The predictor has low internal consistency
D. The test manual lacks a glossary
✅Answer: A. The criterion includes information derived from the predictor test itself
Rationale: Criterion contamination occurs when the criterion is not independent and is
influenced by the predictor, inflating apparent validity.
56. A suicide assessment is most ethically defensible when the clinician:
A. ignores collateral information to preserve rapport
B. relies on intuition without structured inquiry
C. evaluates ideation, plan, means, intent, and protective factors
D. avoids documentation to reduce liability
✅Answer: C. evaluates ideation, plan, means, intent, and protective factors
Rationale: Comprehensive suicide assessment requires structured evaluation of risk and
protective elements, not intuition alone.
57. In forensic assessment, the psychologist should be especially careful to:
A. act as both therapist and expert witness whenever possible
B. clarify role expectations and limits of confidentiality
C. guarantee complete confidentiality regardless of court order
D. interpret results without regard to legal standards
✅Answer: B. clarify role expectations and limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Forensic practice requires role clarity and explicit discussion of limits of
confidentiality.
58. A patient with suspected frontal lobe dysfunction is most likely to have difficulty with:
A. color perception only
B. executive functions such as planning and set shifting
C. pure-tone hearing thresholds only
D. all forms of long-term memory equally
✅Answer: B. executive functions such as planning and set shifting
Rationale: Frontal lobe dysfunction is strongly associated with deficits in executive control
processes.
59. The Halstead-Reitan and Luria-Nebraska are best classified as:
A. interest inventories
B. neuropsychological batteries
C. criterion-keyed personality tests
D. vocational aptitude tests
✅Answer: B. neuropsychological batteries
Rationale: Both Halstead-Reitan and Luria-Nebraska are classic neuropsychological test
batteries.
60. A neuropsychological evaluation is most indicated when there is concern about:
A. simple career indecision
B. possible brain-behavior dysfunction
C. ordinary classroom boredom
D. social desirability in self-report only
✅Answer: B. possible brain-behavior dysfunction
Rationale: Neuropsychological evaluation is indicated when there are concerns about
neurological impairment and its behavioral effects.
61. Which result would most strongly suggest memory impairment rather than low motivation
alone?
A. Uniformly poor performance on every task
B. Marked weakness on delayed recall relative to intact attention and language
C. High variability across all tasks without pattern
D. Elevated validity-scale scores on a personality inventory
✅Answer: B. Marked weakness on delayed recall relative to intact attention and language
Rationale: A patterned deficit in delayed recall with relatively preserved other functions is
more suggestive of memory impairment than generalized low effort.
62. A psychometrician in an industrial setting wants to know whether a selection test improves
hiring outcomes enough to justify its cost. The key concept is:
A. convergent validity
B. utility analysis
C. response bias
D. projective depth
✅Answer: B. utility analysis
Rationale: Utility analysis evaluates whether a measure adds enough practical benefit to
justify use.
63. Letters of recommendation are often criticized in personnel assessment because they:
A. are always illegal
B. may be affected by leniency and impression management
C. have better validity than structured interviews
D. cannot be read by psychologists
✅Answer: B. may be affected by leniency and impression management
Rationale: Recommendation letters often suffer from positivity bias, selective disclosure, and
limited comparability.
64. Which interview format generally provides the strongest basis for comparing job applicants
fairly?
A. Unstructured interview with spontaneous questions
B. Structured interview anchored to job-relevant competencies
C. Interview based on intuition and chemistry
D. Free-association interview
✅Answer: B. Structured interview anchored to job-relevant competencies
Rationale: Structured interviews improve standardization, comparability, and fairness by
focusing on predetermined job-relevant dimensions.
65. An organization wants to classify applicants into jobs that match their strengths after hire.
This is most directly an issue of:
A. placement
B. malingering
C. norming
D. content balancing
✅Answer: A. placement
Rationale: Placement involves assigning accepted applicants or employees to roles matching
their capacities or characteristics.
66. In career assessment, interest inventories are most useful because they:
A. directly measure skill mastery
B. estimate preference patterns related to occupational environments
C. replace aptitude measures completely
D. diagnose personality disorders
✅Answer: B. estimate preference patterns related to occupational environments
Rationale: Interest inventories help identify vocational likes/dislikes and person-environment
fit patterns.
67. Which statement best reflects the relation among reliability, validity, and utility?
A. A test can be useful even if it is clearly unreliable
B. Validity guarantees utility in every setting
C. Reliability is necessary but not sufficient for validity and utility
D. Utility and validity are identical concepts
✅Answer: C. Reliability is necessary but not sufficient for validity and utility
Rationale: A test must first produce dependable scores, but dependable scores alone do not
guarantee correct interpretation or practical value.
68. A test with high face validity but poor construct validity would most likely:
A. appear relevant while failing to support intended interpretations
B. be impossible to administer
C. show perfect criterion-related evidence
D. be useful only for projective scoring
✅Answer: A. appear relevant while failing to support intended interpretations
Rationale: Face validity concerns apparent relevance; construct validity concerns evidence
that the test actually measures the intended construct.
69. If an examinee’s percentile rank is 84, the best interpretation is that the examinee scored:
A. 84 raw-score points
B. better than approximately 84% of the norm group
C. 1.84 standard deviations above the mean
D. at the mastery level set by the test author
✅Answer: B. better than approximately 84% of the norm group
Rationale: A percentile rank indicates relative standing compared with the norm group.
70. In a negatively skewed score distribution, most scores are:
A. low, with a tail extending toward high scores
B. high, with a tail extending toward low scores
C. split into two equal peaks
D. exactly symmetrical around the mean
✅Answer: B. high, with a tail extending toward low scores
Rationale: Negative skew means most scores are toward the upper end, with fewer low
scores stretching the tail leftward.
71. Which statement about multiple relationships is most consistent with ethical practice?
A. They are always acceptable if the client agrees
B. They should be avoided when they risk impaired objectivity or exploitation
C. They apply only to sexual relationships
D. They are irrelevant in small communities
✅Answer: B. They should be avoided when they risk impaired objectivity or exploitation
Rationale: The PAP Code warns against multiple relationships when they may impair
objectivity, competence, effectiveness, or create exploitation or harm.
72. A psychometrician is asked by a relative to assess the relative’s child for school placement.
The strongest ethical concern is:
A. low face validity
B. multiple relationship and possible loss of objectivity
C. absence of a criterion measure
D. fixed-reference scoring
✅Answer: B. multiple relationship and possible loss of objectivity
Rationale: Assessing a relative’s child creates dual-role concerns and risks biased judgment.
73. Under the PAP Code of Ethics, informed consent in assessment generally requires:
A. no explanation if the form is standardized
B. understandable language and discussion of limits when relevant
C. verbal consent only for all cases
D. explanation after the assessment, not before
✅Answer: B. understandable language and discussion of limits when relevant
Rationale: Informed consent requires language reasonably understandable to the person and
includes discussion of relevant limits of confidentiality.
74. A practitioner stores identifiable client test data in an easily accessible shared folder. This
most directly violates the ethical duty to:
A. maximize utility
B. maintain confidentiality and secure information
C. prefer mechanical prediction
D. use criterion-referenced scores
✅Answer: B. maintain confidentiality and secure information
Rationale: The PAP Code specifically emphasizes safeguarding client information and
keeping it from easy access by unqualified persons.
75. Which action is most appropriate if a practitioner becomes aware of another psychologist’s
ethical violation and informal resolution is insufficient and substantial harm is likely?
A. Ignore it to protect collegiality
B. Publicly post the concern online
C. Report it to appropriate authorities, subject to confidentiality limits
D. Share the full client record with anyone asking for proof
✅Answer: C. Report it to appropriate authorities, subject to confidentiality limits
Rationale: When substantial harm is likely and informal resolution is insufficient, further
reporting is appropriate, while still respecting confidentiality boundaries.
76. A psychometrician is asked to administer a specialized instrument for a population outside
the psychometrician’s training. The most ethical response is to:
A. proceed because the manual is self-explanatory
B. decline or obtain proper supervision/training and refer if needed
C. guess the interpretation conservatively
D. rely on internet summaries of the test
✅Answer: B. decline or obtain proper supervision/training and refer if needed
Rationale: Ethical competence requires practicing within training boundaries and making
referrals when needed.
77. According to ethical standards on delegated work, delegated tasks should be assigned only
to persons who:
A. are personally known to the client
B. can reasonably perform them competently with appropriate supervision if needed
C. charge lower fees
D. work in the same institution regardless of training
✅Answer: B. can reasonably perform them competently with appropriate supervision if
needed
Rationale: Delegated work should be assigned only to persons expected to perform
competently based on training, experience, and supervision.
78. A practitioner’s personal distress is interfering with concentration during assessment
sessions. Ethically, the practitioner should:
A. continue working to avoid disappointing clients
B. take measures such as consultation and consider limiting duties
C. administer only objective tests
D. avoid documentation of the problem
✅Answer: B. take measures such as consultation and consider limiting duties
Rationale: The Code directs practitioners to act when personal problems may interfere with
competent work.
79. Which statement is most accurate regarding telepsychology under the PAP Code?
A. Ethical rules do not apply equally online
B. Online services are exempt from informed consent
C. Core ethical principles still apply to virtual services
D. Telepsychology is prohibited for all assessment work
✅Answer: C. Core ethical principles still apply to virtual services
Rationale: The PAP Code explicitly states that ethical principles governing face-to-face
services apply to telepsychology as well.
80. A psychologist receives a court order to release assessment data. The best ethical
response is to:
A. refuse automatically because confidentiality is absolute
B. release all records to everyone involved
C. disclose only what is legally required and pertinent
D. destroy the records to protect the client
✅Answer: C. disclose only what is legally required and pertinent
Rationale: When disclosure is legally mandated, release should be limited to what is pertinent
to the legitimate request.
81. Which situation best illustrates unfair discrimination in professional practice?
A. Using multiple data sources in assessment
B. Denying service because of a client’s socioeconomic status
C. Explaining limits of confidentiality
D. Referring a case due to lack of competence
✅Answer: B. Denying service because of a client’s socioeconomic status
Rationale: The Code prohibits unfair discrimination on bases including socioeconomic status.
82. A practitioner uses exaggerated claims on social media about guaranteed treatment
outcomes and flawless test accuracy. This most directly violates standards against:
A. criterion keying
B. false or deceptive public statements
C. dynamic assessment
D. inter-scorer disagreement
✅Answer: B. false or deceptive public statements
Rationale: Ethical advertising requires accurate, nonexaggerated, nonfraudulent public
statements.
83. The most defensible reason to use a battery rather than a single test is that:
A. more tests always guarantee accuracy
B. different tools can provide complementary evidence
C. batteries eliminate the need for theory
D. examinees prefer longer testing
✅Answer: B. different tools can provide complementary evidence
Rationale: No single method captures all relevant information; batteries allow convergence
and cross-checking of findings.
84. Cross-validation is important because an obtained validity coefficient may:
A. increase indefinitely in new samples
B. fail to generalize as strongly in another sample
C. replace the need for criterion measures
D. prove causation
✅Answer: B. fail to generalize as strongly in another sample
Rationale: Validity coefficients can shrink when tested in new samples, so cross-validation
checks generalizability.
85. An item with very low discrimination but moderate difficulty should generally be:
A. retained automatically
B. reviewed for possible revision or deletion
C. interpreted as evidence of high construct validity
D. used as an anchor item without review
✅Answer: B. reviewed for possible revision or deletion
Rationale: Weak discrimination suggests the item is not functioning well and should be
examined qualitatively and quantitatively.
86. The logic of criterion-group personality test construction depends on:
A. selecting items that distinguish known groups
B. choosing only items that look clinically relevant
C. using no empirical data
D. requiring examinees to tell stories
✅Answer: A. selecting items that distinguish known groups
Rationale: Criterion-group construction empirically selects items that separate identified
criterion groups from others.
87. Which personality theorist is most directly linked to needs and the TAT tradition?
A. Spearman
B. Henry Murray
C. Thorndike
D. Galton
✅Answer: B. Henry Murray
Rationale: Murray’s personology and need-press concepts strongly influenced TAT
interpretation traditions.
88. A school psychologist who uses only one test score to decide that a child has a learning
disability is making an error primarily because sound assessment requires:
A. elimination of all standardized tests
B. integration of converging evidence
C. ipsative interpretation only
D. exclusive reliance on teacher intuition
✅Answer: B. integration of converging evidence
Rationale: High-stakes educational decisions should be based on multiple converging
sources rather than one score alone.
89. A test manual reports strong evidence of content validity but no evidence relating scores to
external criteria or constructs. The best conclusion is that:
A. the test is fully validated
B. evidence is promising but incomplete
C. the test is invalid for every purpose
D. criterion evidence is unnecessary
✅Answer: B. evidence is promising but incomplete
Rationale: Strong content evidence is useful, but external and construct-related evidence are
still needed for fuller validation.
90. Which of the following is the best example of discriminant validity evidence?
A. An anxiety scale correlates highly with another anxiety scale
B. A reading test predicts later reading grades
C. A depression scale shows low correlation with a physical agility test
D. A job test correlates with supervisor ratings collected simultaneously
✅Answer: C. A depression scale shows low correlation with a physical agility test
Rationale: Discriminant validity is shown when a measure relates weakly to constructs it
should differ from.
91. A clinician chooses a culturally adapted measure and also examines the client’s language,
acculturation, and sociocultural context during interpretation. This best reflects:
A. test bias by design
B. culturally informed assessment
C. projective hypothesis testing
D. pure actuarial decision-making
✅Answer: B. culturally informed assessment
Rationale: Culturally informed assessment considers adaptation, language, acculturation, and
sociocultural context in interpretation.
92. If all examinees from one group receive lower scores because test instructions are
linguistically inaccessible rather than because of the target construct, the strongest concern is:
A. criterion deficiency
B. construct-irrelevant variance
C. semantic differential scaling
D. ipsative distortion
✅Answer: B. construct-irrelevant variance
Rationale: If linguistic barriers influence scores apart from the intended construct, the test
contains construct-irrelevant variance.
93. A teacher-made quiz has very limited use in supporting high-stakes conclusions partly
because:
A. all teacher-made tests are unethical
B. evidence for reliability and validity may be insufficient for such decisions
C. classroom tests cannot have content validity
D. only commercial publishers can write items
✅Answer: B. evidence for reliability and validity may be insufficient for such decisions
Rationale: Teacher-made quizzes may be fine for classroom use but often lack the
psychometric support needed for high-stakes decisions.
94. Which interpretation of a T score is correct?
A. It has a mean of 100 and SD of 15
B. It has a mean of 50 and SD of 10
C. It is always equivalent to a percentile rank
D. It can be used only with criterion-referenced tests
✅Answer: B. It has a mean of 50 and SD of 10
Rationale: The T-score metric is conventionally scaled to mean 50 and standard deviation 10.
95. In report writing, the best practice is to:
A. state conclusions without noting limits
B. integrate findings with referral questions and context
C. avoid mentioning conflicting data
D. use jargon so only psychologists understand it
✅Answer: B. integrate findings with referral questions and context
Rationale: A sound report answers the referral question using integrated data while
acknowledging context and limits.
96. Which practice would most improve the defensibility of assessment conclusions?
A. Basing conclusions on the highest score obtained
B. Ignoring behavioral observations because they are subjective
C. Documenting methods, results, limits, and rationale clearly
D. Eliminating all clinical judgment
✅Answer: C. Documenting methods, results, limits, and rationale clearly
Rationale: Transparent documentation strengthens defensibility, reproducibility, and ethical
accountability.
97. A selection measure yields small but consistent prediction of performance and is
inexpensive, easy to administer, and used with a large applicant pool. Its practical value may
still be substantial because:
A. even modest validity can have meaningful utility in high-volume decisions
B. small validity coefficients are useless by definition
C. utility is unrelated to base rates and costs
D. inexpensive tests are automatically fair
✅Answer: A. even modest validity can have meaningful utility in high-volume decisions
Rationale: In large applicant pools, modest validity may still yield substantial practical gain
depending on base rates, costs, and selection ratios.
98. Which statement best reflects an ethical approach to confidentiality with minors?
A. Minors have no confidentiality rights
B. Limits should be explained, and guardians informed as appropriate
C. All information must be shared immediately with teachers
D. Test results should never be discussed with the minor
✅Answer: B. Limits should be explained, and guardians informed as appropriate
Rationale: With minors, confidentiality is not absent; rather, limits should be explained and
guardians involved appropriately.
99. A psychometrician is pressured by an employer to change a report so the applicant appears
more suitable. Ethically, the psychometrician should primarily rely on the principle of:
A. integrity in truthful and accurate communication
B. projective flexibility
C. criterion contamination
D. fixed reference scoring
✅Answer: A. integrity in truthful and accurate communication
Rationale: Integrity requires honest, accurate, and nondeceptive communication even when
organizational pressure exists.
100. A fresh mock exam intended for board preparation should ideally contain a balanced mix of
recall, understanding, application, and analysis because:
A. all board items are purely memory-based
B. competency-based testing samples different levels of cognition
C. analysis items eliminate the need for definitions
D. application questions are less valid than recall questions
✅Answer: B. competency-based testing samples different levels of cognition
Rationale: A balanced exam blueprint should sample not only recall but also understanding,
application, and analysis to reflect professional competence.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 7
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 7
1. A psychologist describes psychological assessment as a process, whereas psychological
testing is only one component of that process. Which statement best reflects this distinction?
A. Assessment refers only to the scoring of standardized tests
B. Testing and assessment are identical and may always be used interchangeably
C. Assessment integrates test data with interviews, observations, records, and other relevant
information
D. Testing is broader than assessment because it includes all decision-making activities
✅Answer: C. Assessment integrates test data with interviews, observations, records, and
other relevant information
Rationale: Assessment is broader than testing and involves integrating multiple data sources
such as interviews, observations, and records to make informed decisions.
2. Which of the following is the best example of an ability test rather than a personality test?
A. A scale measuring preference for social gatherings
B. A measure of verbal reasoning and quantitative problem solving
C. A checklist of depressive symptoms
D. An inventory of vocational interests
✅Answer: B. A measure of verbal reasoning and quantitative problem solving
Rationale: Ability tests measure what a person can do, such as reasoning and
problem-solving skills.
3. A psychometrician administers a cognitive screening tool in a clinic and later interprets the
score as proof that the client has a neurocognitive disorder. What is the most defensible
criticism of this conclusion?
A. A single test score should be interpreted within a broader assessment context
B. Screening tools are useful only in schools
C. Cognitive tests cannot be scored objectively
D. All screening tools are projective methods
✅Answer: A. A single test score should be interpreted within a broader assessment context
Rationale: Screening tools are not diagnostic by themselves and must be interpreted
alongside other assessment data.
4. Which statement best expresses the meaning of standardization in psychological testing?
A. Every examinee receives the same raw score
B. Uniform procedures are used in administration and scoring
C. All tests must use multiple-choice items
D. Norms are unnecessary if instructions are standardized
✅Answer: B. Uniform procedures are used in administration and scoring
Rationale: Standardization ensures consistency in administration and scoring procedures
across examinees.
5. A counselor wants to know whether a student’s test performance should be compared with
that of a reference group or against a defined performance standard. This distinction refers to:
A. projective versus objective testing
B. speed versus power testing
C. norm-referenced versus criterion-referenced interpretation
D. ipsative versus adaptive testing
✅Answer: C. norm-referenced versus criterion-referenced interpretation
Rationale: This distinction refers to comparing scores to norms or to a defined standard.
6. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Mode
B. Median
C. Mean
D. Percentile rank
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean is influenced by all values, making it sensitive to extreme scores.
7. A psychometrician wants to know how much examinees’ scores vary around the average.
Which statistic is most directly useful?
A. Mean
B. Standard deviation
C. Percentile rank
D. Correlation coefficient
✅Answer: B. Standard deviation
Rationale: Standard deviation measures variability or spread of scores around the mean.
8. In a perfectly normal distribution, the mean, median, and mode are:
A. all equal
B. unrelated to each other
C. arranged from lowest to highest in that order
D. impossible to determine without the raw scores
✅Answer: A. all equal
Rationale: In a normal distribution, mean, median, and mode coincide at the center.
9. A score located two standard deviations above the mean corresponds to a z score of:
A. -2.00
B. -1.00
C. +1.00
D. +2.00
✅Answer: D. +2.00
Rationale: A z score indicates standard deviation units from the mean; +2 means two SDs
above.
10. Which type of correlation coefficient is most appropriate when both variables are measured
at the ordinal level?
A. Pearson r
B. Spearman rho
C. Coefficient alpha
D. Phi coefficient
✅Answer: B. Spearman rho
Rationale: Spearman rho is used for ordinal or ranked data.
11. A validity study shows a correlation of .64 between entrance exam scores and first-year
academic performance. The coefficient of determination is:
A. .16
B. .36
C. .41
D. .80
✅Answer: C. .41
Rationale: The coefficient of determination is the square of the correlation (.64² ≈ .41).
12. A test has high reliability. Which statement is most accurate?
A. It is automatically valid for all purposes
B. It yields relatively consistent scores under similar conditions
C. It is free from all measurement error
D. It measures only one construct
✅Answer: B. It yields relatively consistent scores under similar conditions
Rationale: Reliability refers to consistency of measurement under similar conditions.
13. A psychometrician administers the same test to the same group twice, with a reasonable
interval between administrations, and correlates the scores. This procedure estimates:
A. interscorer reliability
B. alternate-forms reliability
C. test-retest reliability
D. internal consistency only
✅Answer: C. test-retest reliability
Rationale: This method assesses stability of scores over time.
14. Which reliability method is most appropriate when the concern is consistency among raters
scoring essay responses?
A. Split-half reliability
B. Interscorer reliability
C. Test-retest reliability
D. Alternate-forms reliability
✅Answer: B. Interscorer reliability
Rationale: Interscorer reliability measures agreement among different raters.
15. A scale intended to measure a single construct yields highly correlated items on one
administration. Which estimate is most relevant?
A. Internal consistency
B. Predictive validity
C. Face validity
D. Content validity
✅Answer: A. Internal consistency
Rationale: Internal consistency reflects how well items measure the same construct.
16. The standard error of measurement is most useful because it:
A. proves that the true score has been observed directly
B. estimates the range within which an examinee’s true score likely falls
C. converts raw scores into percentile ranks
D. replaces the need for reliability evidence
✅Answer: B. estimates the range within which an examinee’s true score likely falls
Rationale: SEM provides an estimate of the error around observed scores.
17. Which statement about validity is most accurate?
A. Validity refers only to how a test looks to the examinee
B. Validity concerns the degree to which evidence supports interpretations of test scores
C. Validity is identical to reliability
D. Validity is established once and never reexamined
✅Answer: B. Validity concerns the degree to which evidence supports interpretations of test
scores
Rationale: Validity is about the appropriateness and support for score interpretations.
18. A board review test is developed from a detailed table of specifications to ensure all relevant
competency areas are sampled adequately. This primarily supports:
A. criterion-related validity
B. content validity
C. ecological validity
D. face validity
✅Answer: B. content validity
Rationale: Content validity ensures adequate representation of the domain.
19. If a depression scale correlates highly with another well-established depression scale
administered at the same time, this is evidence of:
A. concurrent validity
B. discriminant validity
C. face validity
D. interrater reliability
✅Answer: A. concurrent validity
Rationale: Concurrent validity is established when two measures correlate at the same time.
20. A company uses an aptitude test for hiring and later correlates applicants’ scores with job
performance ratings collected six months after hiring. This is evidence of:
A. content validity
B. predictive validity
C. face validity
D. split-half reliability
✅Answer: B. predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity refers to how well scores predict future performance.
21. Which finding would best support construct validity?
A. Examinees say the test appears relevant
B. Test items are easy to score
C. Scores relate to other variables as theory predicts
D. The manual is professionally formatted
✅Answer: C. Scores relate to other variables as theory predicts
Rationale: Construct validity is supported when test results align with theoretical expectations
and relationships.
22. Which of the following most directly reflects test bias?
A. A test is difficult for most examinees
B. A test shows different predictive accuracy for groups in a way unrelated to the construct
C. A test has many items
D. A test uses percentile norms
✅Answer: B. A test shows different predictive accuracy for groups in a way unrelated to the
construct
Rationale: Bias occurs when a test unfairly favors or disadvantages groups in ways unrelated
to the construct being measured.
23. In test development, the stage that comes first is usually:
A. item analysis
B. test conceptualization
C. norm updating
D. cross-validation
✅Answer: B. test conceptualization
Rationale: Test development begins by defining the construct, purpose, and specifications.
24. A test developer removes an item because high scorers and low scorers answer it correctly
at about the same rate. The item is weak mainly because it has poor:
A. readability
B. item discrimination
C. face validity
D. item homogeneity by definition alone
✅Answer: B. item discrimination
Rationale: Poor discrimination means the item does not differentiate between high and low
performers.
25. An item with a p-value of .95 on a moderately difficult exam is best described as:
A. highly difficult
B. moderately discriminating by necessity
C. very easy
D. invalid automatically
✅Answer: C. very easy
Rationale: A high p-value indicates that most examinees answered correctly, making the item
easy.
26. Which statement about distractors in a multiple-choice test is best?
A. Distractors should be absurd to prevent guessing
B. Distractors should be plausible and attractive to less knowledgeable examinees
C. Distractors should vary greatly in length from the correct answer
D. Distractors should test unrelated content to widen coverage
✅Answer: B. Distractors should be plausible and attractive to less knowledgeable
examinees
Rationale: Effective distractors attract those who do not know the correct answer.
27. A psychologist wants a brief screening instrument during disaster response, even though a
more comprehensive battery would be preferable later. This illustrates concern with test:
A. utility
B. projective value
C. face validity only
D. ipsative interpretation
✅Answer: A. utility
Rationale: Utility refers to the practical usefulness of a test in a given situation.
28. A cutoff score for certification should ideally be set using a defensible standard-setting
method because:
A. any cutoff is acceptable if chosen by senior staff
B. cutoff scores determine who passes and fails and therefore require justification
C. cutoffs eliminate the need for validity evidence
D. lower cutoffs always improve fairness
✅Answer: B. cutoff scores determine who passes and fails and therefore require justification
Rationale: Cut scores have important consequences and must be justified.
29. Which psychologist is most closely associated with the early intelligence testing movement
through the Binet-Simon scale?
A. Alfred Binet
B. Carl Rogers
C. B. F. Skinner
D. Hermann Rorschach
✅Answer: A. Alfred Binet
Rationale: Alfred Binet co-developed the first practical intelligence test.
30. The concept of general intelligence, or g, is most closely associated with:
A. Spearman
B. Thorndike
C. Maslow
D. Murray
✅Answer: A. Spearman
Rationale: Spearman proposed the general intelligence factor (g).
31. An intelligence score derived by comparing mental age with chronological age reflects the
older concept of:
A. deviation IQ
B. ratio IQ
C. T score
D. stanine
✅Answer: B. ratio IQ
Rationale: Ratio IQ is calculated using mental age divided by chronological age.
32. Which is the best description of an aptitude test?
A. A test designed only to diagnose mental disorder
B. A measure of developed knowledge exclusively
C. A measure intended to forecast future performance or learning potential
D. A purely projective measure of motivation
✅Answer: C. A measure intended to forecast future performance or learning potential
Rationale: Aptitude tests predict future ability or performance.
33. A school psychologist wants to evaluate a child’s current academic skills in reading and
math. Which class of test is most appropriate?
A. Achievement test
B. Interest inventory
C. Projective personality test
D. Neuropsychological battery only
✅Answer: A. Achievement test
Rationale: Achievement tests assess learned knowledge and skills.
34. Which is a common criticism of interpreting IQ scores without cultural context?
A. IQ tests can never be standardized
B. Intelligence is measured only through interviews
C. Scores may reflect cultural, linguistic, and educational experiences as well as ability
D. IQ scores are always random
✅Answer: C. Scores may reflect cultural, linguistic, and educational experiences as well as
ability
Rationale: IQ scores may be influenced by contextual factors beyond intelligence.
35. In educational assessment, response to intervention (RtI) is best understood as:
A. a projective method for identifying personality patterns
B. a model emphasizing monitoring of student progress and intervention before formal
placement decisions
C. a legal doctrine prohibiting testing
D. a method of replacing all standardized tests with interviews
✅Answer: B. a model emphasizing monitoring of student progress and intervention before
formal placement decisions
Rationale: RtI focuses on early intervention and progress monitoring.
36. Which approach is most consistent with dynamic assessment?
A. Evaluating only static final performance under fixed conditions
B. Focusing on learning potential through mediated assistance
C. Using only group-administered achievement tests
D. Avoiding examiner feedback entirely
✅Answer: B. Focusing on learning potential through mediated assistance
Rationale: Dynamic assessment emphasizes learning potential and responsiveness to
intervention.
37. A teacher assembles samples of a student’s work over time to evaluate growth in writing.
This is an example of:
A. portfolio assessment
B. projective testing
C. error variance
D. ipsative scoring
✅Answer: A. portfolio assessment
Rationale: Portfolio assessment involves evaluating collected work over time.
38. In personality assessment, objective methods are called “objective” primarily because:
A. they are free from all response bias
B. scoring and interpretation procedures are more standardized than projective methods
C. they measure only observable behavior
D. they cannot assess personality traits
✅Answer: B. scoring and interpretation procedures are more standardized than projective
methods
Rationale: Objectivity refers to standardized scoring procedures.
39. Which is the clearest example of a projective technique?
A. MMPI-2
B. NEO-PI
C. Rorschach Inkblot Method
D. Strong Interest Inventory
✅Answer: C. Rorschach Inkblot Method
Rationale: The Rorschach uses ambiguous stimuli to elicit personality projections.
40. A major assumption underlying projective methods is that when presented with ambiguous
stimuli, people:
A. respond randomly
B. reveal aspects of their personality through their interpretations
C. always exaggerate symptoms
D. produce responses unrelated to psychological functioning
✅Answer: B. reveal aspects of their personality through their interpretations
Rationale: Projective methods assume responses reflect underlying personality traits.
41. Behavioral assessment differs from many traditional trait approaches because it
emphasizes:
A. unconscious symbolism only
B. direct observation of behavior and situational variables
C. fixed personality types exclusively
D. interpretation of all behavior through one global trait
✅Answer: B. direct observation of behavior and situational variables
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on observable behavior and the environmental
conditions influencing it.
42. Which format is most characteristic of the MMPI tradition?
A. Inkblot interpretation
B. Empirically keyed self-report inventory
C. Performance-based block design only
D. Sentence completion without scoring rules
✅Answer: B. Empirically keyed self-report inventory
Rationale: The MMPI uses empirical keying based on group differences.
43. Which personality theorist is most associated with needs and personology, influencing
thematic assessment approaches?
A. Henry Murray
B. David Wechsler
C. Charles Spearman
D. Lewis Terman
✅Answer: A. Henry Murray
Rationale: Murray’s theory of needs influenced thematic techniques like the TAT.
44. A clinician uses repeated observations of a child’s tantrums across home and school
settings before planning intervention. This best reflects:
A. behavioral assessment
B. content validation
C. projective hypothesis testing
D. ipsative vocational profiling
✅Answer: A. behavioral assessment
Rationale: Observing behavior across contexts is central to behavioral assessment.
45. In clinical assessment, the Barnum effect refers to the tendency for people to:
A. reject feedback that is too general
B. accept vague, general descriptions as uniquely accurate for themselves
C. perform poorly on timed tests
D. improve after rapport building
✅Answer: B. accept vague, general descriptions as uniquely accurate for themselves
Rationale: The Barnum effect involves accepting general statements as personally accurate.
46. Which of the following is a major strength of structured interviews in diagnostic settings?
A. They eliminate all interviewer bias
B. They improve consistency in the coverage of relevant symptoms
C. They are always superior to all other data sources
D. They do not require clinical judgment
✅Answer: B. They improve consistency in the coverage of relevant symptoms
Rationale: Structured interviews standardize questioning, improving reliability.
47. A psychologist is asked to conduct a custody evaluation. Which principle is most important
at the outset?
A. Promise absolute confidentiality to each parent
B. Clarify role, referral question, probable uses of information, and limits of confidentiality
C. Avoid reviewing collateral records
D. Rely solely on one parent’s report to preserve neutrality
✅Answer: B. Clarify role, referral question, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
Rationale: Clear role definition and limits of confidentiality are essential in forensic contexts.
48. Suicide assessment is most ethically appropriate when the clinician:
A. avoids discussing suicidal thoughts to prevent suggestion
B. assesses ideation, plan, means, intent, and protective factors
C. guarantees that hospitalization will never occur
D. assumes no risk if the client appears calm
✅Answer: B. assesses ideation, plan, means, intent, and protective factors
Rationale: Comprehensive risk assessment is necessary for ethical suicide evaluation.
49. Which finding most strongly suggests a need for neuropsychological evaluation?
A. A client wants help choosing a major
B. A previously high-functioning adult shows new memory, executive, and attention problems
after head injury
C. A student requests a personality inventory for self-exploration
D. An applicant needs a routine employment interview
✅Answer: B. A previously high-functioning adult shows new memory, executive, and
attention problems after head injury
Rationale: Cognitive decline after brain injury indicates need for neuropsychological
assessment.
50. Which cognitive domain is most closely associated with executive functioning?
A. Color perception only
B. Planning, inhibition, set shifting, and problem solving
C. Auditory acuity exclusively
D. Handedness only
✅Answer: B. Planning, inhibition, set shifting, and problem solving
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order cognitive control processes.
51. A neuropsychological battery is most useful because it:
A. guarantees diagnosis without other information
B. samples multiple domains of cognitive functioning systematically
C. eliminates the need for history taking
D. is administered only by physicians
✅Answer: B. samples multiple domains of cognitive functioning systematically
Rationale: Batteries assess multiple cognitive domains to identify patterns of strengths and
weaknesses.
52. Which instrument is most associated with memory assessment rather than personality?
A. Thematic Apperception Test
B. California Verbal Learning Test
C. Sentence Completion Test
D. NEO-PI
✅Answer: B. California Verbal Learning Test
Rationale: The CVLT measures verbal learning and memory.
53. In vocational assessment, interest inventories are most useful for:
A. diagnosing psychosis
B. predicting with certainty whether a person will succeed in a job
C. identifying occupational environments and activities a person may prefer
D. measuring maximal intellectual ability only
✅Answer: C. identifying occupational environments and activities a person may prefer
Rationale: Interest inventories help identify preferred work environments and activities.
54. Which statement best reflects the relation between interests and abilities?
A. Interests and abilities are identical constructs
B. A person may show strong interest in an area without having corresponding high ability
C. High ability automatically creates strong interest
D. Interests are more stable than all personality traits in every case
✅Answer: B. A person may show strong interest in an area without having corresponding
high ability
Rationale: Interests and abilities are distinct constructs.
55. An employer wants to know whether a selection battery adds value beyond interview
impressions. This concerns:
A. ecological fallacy
B. incremental validity
C. projective scaling
D. face validity only
✅Answer: B. incremental validity
Rationale: Incremental validity assesses added predictive value of a measure.
56. Which is the best example of a performance test in personnel selection?
A. Asking applicants to describe themselves in three adjectives
B. Having applicants complete a simulated work task relevant to the job
C. Asking applicants about favorite hobbies
D. Requesting a narrative dream report
✅Answer: B. Having applicants complete a simulated work task relevant to the job
Rationale: Performance tests require demonstration of job-related tasks.
57. Utility analysis is primarily concerned with:
A. whether a test appears acceptable to examinees
B. the practical value and consequences of using a test in decision-making
C. whether a test is projective or objective
D. converting raw scores to z scores
✅Answer: B. the practical value and consequences of using a test in decision-making
Rationale: Utility analysis evaluates cost-benefit and effectiveness of testing.
58. Which statement about interviews in selection is most accurate?
A. Unstructured interviews are always more reliable than structured interviews
B. Structured interviews often improve fairness and predictive consistency
C. Interviews are invalid by definition
D. Interviews should replace all cognitive measures regardless of job demands
✅Answer: B. Structured interviews often improve fairness and predictive consistency
Rationale: Structured interviews enhance reliability and fairness.
59. In forensic assessment, a key difference from therapeutic practice is that the evaluator’s
primary obligation is to:
A. provide ongoing treatment
B. advocate only for the examinee
C. address the legal referral question with impartiality
D. maintain absolute confidentiality under all conditions
✅Answer: C. address the legal referral question with impartiality
Rationale: Forensic evaluators must remain objective and address legal questions.
60. Which of the following best illustrates malingering concern?
A. An examinee carefully completes all tasks
B. An examinee may be intentionally exaggerating symptoms for external gain
C. An examinee reports mild anxiety before testing
D. An examinee asks about the purpose of assessment
✅Answer: B. An examinee may be intentionally exaggerating symptoms for external gain
Rationale: Malingering involves intentional exaggeration for gain.
61. According to ethical principles, when a psychologist’s personal problems are likely to impair
competence, the psychologist should:
A. continue practice because clients need services
B. ignore the problem unless a complaint is filed
C. obtain assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or terminating duties as needed
D. delegate all work regardless of supervisee competence
✅Answer: C. obtain assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or terminating duties as
needed
Rationale: Ethical practice requires managing personal impairment to protect clients and
maintain competence.
62. Which action best reflects competent caring in telepsychology?
A. Assuming online services are exempt from ethical standards that apply in person
B. Applying the same ethical principles while also addressing privacy and technology risks
C. Refusing all virtual services as unethical
D. Using unsecured platforms whenever clients agree
✅Answer: B. Applying the same ethical principles while also addressing privacy and
technology risks
Rationale: Telepsychology requires adherence to ethical standards plus additional safeguards
for privacy and technology.
63. A practitioner advertises guaranteed score increases and certain employment success after
using a proprietary assessment package. Ethical analysis suggests this is most problematic
because it may involve:
A. acceptable advocacy
B. deceptive public statements
C. criterion-referenced reporting
D. informed consent
✅Answer: B. deceptive public statements
Rationale: Guaranteeing outcomes misleads the public and violates ethical standards on
honesty.
64. A psychologist uses a test with a client population for which the psychologist has no training
or supervised experience. Which ethical principle is most directly violated?
A. Boundaries of competence
B. Integrity in billing only
C. Right to test access
D. Multiple role neutrality
✅Answer: A. Boundaries of competence
Rationale: Professionals must work within areas of training and competence.
65. A practitioner discovers that an organization demands release of full raw test data to
unqualified staff for personnel decisions. What is the best initial ethical response?
A. Comply immediately because organizations always control test data
B. Clarify ethical obligations and limits, and attempt to resolve the conflict responsibly
C. Destroy all records
D. Publicly accuse the organization on social media
✅Answer: B. Clarify ethical obligations and limits, and attempt to resolve the conflict
responsibly
Rationale: Ethical conflicts should first be addressed through clarification and resolution
efforts.
66. Which is the best example of a multiple relationship that may impair objectivity?
A. Administering a standardized test according to manual instructions
B. Conducting therapy for a close friend while also evaluating that friend for court
C. Consulting with another professional about a case using de-identified information
D. Referring a client to a specialist outside one’s competence
✅Answer: B. Conducting therapy for a close friend while also evaluating that friend for court
Rationale: Dual roles can impair objectivity and create conflicts of interest.
67. Before recording a client’s interview for training purposes, the psychologist should first:
A. record secretly to preserve spontaneity
B. obtain informed consent and explain anticipated uses
C. ask only the intern for permission
D. proceed if the clinic owns the camera
✅Answer: B. obtain informed consent and explain anticipated uses
Rationale: Recording requires prior informed consent and clear explanation of use.
68. Which situation best justifies breaching confidentiality without consent?
A. A colleague is curious about an interesting case
B. The client poses imminent danger to self or others and disclosure is necessary to protect
against harm
C. The psychologist wants to use the case in a lecture
D. The client scored low on an achievement test
✅Answer: B. The client poses imminent danger to self or others and disclosure is necessary
to protect against harm
Rationale: Confidentiality may be breached to prevent serious and imminent harm.
69. When consulting with a colleague about a difficult case, the psychologist should:
A. reveal every identifying detail to improve consultation quality
B. limit disclosure to information necessary for the consultation purpose
C. avoid consultation because it is always a breach
D. post the case anonymously online without safeguards
✅Answer: B. limit disclosure to information necessary for the consultation purpose
Rationale: Ethical consultation requires minimal necessary disclosure.
70. Informed consent is best understood as:
A. a signed form only
B. a process of providing understandable information and obtaining voluntary agreement
C. optional whenever testing is brief
D. unnecessary with adults
✅Answer: B. a process of providing understandable information and obtaining voluntary
agreement
