Rationale: Informed consent is an ongoing communication process.
71. Which of the following is most consistent with fairness in assessment?
A. Using the same test interpretation procedures regardless of linguistic or cultural differences
B. Ignoring disability accommodations to preserve standardization
C. Considering relevant cultural, linguistic, and disability factors while maintaining test
integrity
D. Assuming all group score differences reflect innate ability
✅Answer: C. Considering relevant cultural, linguistic, and disability factors while maintaining
test integrity
Rationale: Fair assessment accounts for individual differences while maintaining validity.
72. A psychologist receives a court order to evaluate a litigant. Which statement to the
examinee is most appropriate?
A. “Everything you say is fully confidential.”
B. “This evaluation is court-ordered, and there are limits to confidentiality.”
C. “You may choose any results you want disclosed.”
D. “I am your therapist in this matter.”
✅Answer: B. “This evaluation is court-ordered, and there are limits to confidentiality.”
Rationale: Court-ordered evaluations require clear explanation of limits to confidentiality.
73. Under Republic Act No. 10029, which statement is most accurate?
A. Anyone with psychology units may independently practice psychology without registration
B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may lawfully practice
within the scope allowed by law
C. Psychometricians may practice all functions reserved for psychologists without supervision
limits
D. Registration is optional if the employer permits practice
✅Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians may lawfully
practice within the scope allowed by law
Rationale: RA 10029 regulates lawful practice and requires licensure within defined scope.
74. Which task most clearly falls within psychological assessment practice regulated by RA
10029?
A. Selling office supplies
B. Administering and interpreting psychological tests as part of professional services
C. Encoding demographic data only
D. Performing unrelated laboratory imaging procedures
✅Answer: B. Administering and interpreting psychological tests as part of professional
services
Rationale: Psychological assessment is a regulated professional activity.
75. A registered psychometrician is asked to independently conduct psychotherapy and issue a
comprehensive psychological diagnosis without supervision. Under RA 10029, the best
response is:
A. Accept because any license in psychology allows all functions
B. Decline because these functions exceed the lawful scope of psychometric practice
C. Accept if the client agrees
D. Accept only if no psychologist is available anywhere
✅Answer: B. Decline because these functions exceed the lawful scope of psychometric
practice
Rationale: Psychometricians must practice within legally defined scope.
76. A clinic assigns a psychometrician to administer tests, score them, and prepare data for
review by a psychologist who will integrate and interpret findings. This arrangement is generally
most consistent with:
A. unlawful delegation
B. role confusion under all circumstances
C. lawful practice within scope and supervision parameters
D. a prohibited multiple relationship
✅Answer: C. lawful practice within scope and supervision parameters
Rationale: This reflects appropriate role delegation under supervision.
77. A professional shares a client’s raw test results with the client’s employer without consent
and without legal basis. Which principle is most clearly violated?
A. Standardization
B. Confidentiality
C. Utility
D. Scaling
✅Answer: B. Confidentiality
Rationale: Unauthorized disclosure violates confidentiality.
78. Which action by a psychologist best demonstrates integrity?
A. Selectively reporting only findings that support a preferred conclusion
B. Openly acknowledging limits of data and possible alternative interpretations
C. Guaranteeing outcomes to increase client trust
D. Avoiding documentation to reduce liability
✅Answer: B. Openly acknowledging limits of data and possible alternative interpretations
Rationale: Integrity involves honesty and transparency in reporting.
79. Which is the most appropriate reason to refer a client to another professional?
A. To avoid all difficult cases
B. When the referral question exceeds the practitioner’s competence or available tools
C. Because referrals increase income automatically
D. Only when the client requests it in writing
✅Answer: B. When the referral question exceeds the practitioner’s competence or available
tools
Rationale: Referral is appropriate when competence limits are reached.
80. A practitioner is asked to evaluate a bilingual child using a test normed only on monolingual
adults. The best course is to:
A. use the test anyway and interpret scores as definitive
B. refuse all assessment permanently
C. carefully consider appropriateness, limitations, alternative procedures, and need for
referral
D. translate items ad lib without documentation
✅Answer: C. carefully consider appropriateness, limitations, alternative procedures, and
need for referral
Rationale: Ethical assessment requires appropriate tools and cautious interpretation.
81. Which statement about norms is most accurate?
A. Norms are unnecessary if a test is reliable
B. Norms should be based on a representative sample relevant to the intended population
C. Older norms are always superior because they are historically stable
D. Norms eliminate cultural considerations
✅Answer: B. Norms should be based on a representative sample relevant to the intended
population
Rationale: Norms must match the target population for meaningful interpretation.
82. When test performance changes systematically because of prior exposure to the same
material, this is called:
A. regression to the mean
B. practice effect
C. ipsative drift
D. criterion contamination
✅Answer: B. practice effect
Rationale: Practice effects occur when repeated exposure improves performance.
83. Which method is specifically designed to reduce stereotype threat during testing?
A. Emphasizing that poor performance confirms group differences
B. Presenting the test as a neutral problem-solving exercise and fostering supportive
conditions
C. Increasing time pressure and public ranking
D. Avoiding all instructions
✅Answer: B. Presenting the test as a neutral problem-solving exercise and fostering
supportive conditions
Rationale: Reducing threat cues improves fairness and performance.
84. An examiner unintentionally cues the examinee through tone and facial expressions. This
illustrates:
A. expectancy effects
B. content validity
C. construct underrepresentation
D. semantic differential scaling
✅Answer: A. expectancy effects
Rationale: Examiner expectations can influence examinee responses.
85. Which score interpretation is most appropriate for a percentile rank of 84?
A. The examinee answered 84% of items correctly
B. The examinee scored as well as or better than 84% of the norm group
C. The examinee is 84 points above the mean
D. The score has a z value of .84
✅Answer: B. The examinee scored as well as or better than 84% of the norm group
Rationale: Percentile rank indicates relative standing in a norm group.
86. Which type of evidence would be most useful when evaluating whether a new employee
selection test is worth keeping despite administrative cost?
A. Face validity only
B. Utility evidence, including decision benefits and costs
C. Personal preference of supervisors
D. Number of pages in the manual
✅Answer: B. Utility evidence, including decision benefits and costs
Rationale: Utility evaluates practical value and cost-effectiveness.
87. Which statement about computer-based assessment is most accurate?
A. It automatically improves validity in every setting
B. It may enhance efficiency, but psychometric quality and security still require evaluation
C. It removes all concerns about privacy
D. It can never be used in psychological assessment ethically
✅Answer: B. It may enhance efficiency, but psychometric quality and security still require
evaluation
Rationale: Technology requires validation and safeguards.
88. Computer-adaptive testing differs from traditional fixed-form testing because:
A. every examinee receives identical items in identical order
B. item selection adjusts to the examinee’s estimated ability level
C. it does not require item calibration
D. it is always untimed
✅Answer: B. item selection adjusts to the examinee’s estimated ability level
Rationale: Adaptive testing tailors items based on performance.
89. Which is the best example of criterion contamination?
A. A predictor test includes content unrelated to the criterion
B. Supervisors rating job performance know employees’ selection test scores and are
influenced by them
C. A criterion is measured six months after hiring
D. A test manual contains several tables
✅Answer: B. Supervisors rating job performance know employees’ selection test scores and
are influenced by them
Rationale: Criterion contamination occurs when criterion ratings are biased by predictor
knowledge.
90. Which of the following would most threaten predictive validity in personnel testing?
A. Using a relevant criterion collected later
B. Restricted range caused by hiring only applicants with high test scores before validation
C. Adequate sample size
D. Standardized administration
✅Answer: B. Restricted range caused by hiring only applicants with high test scores before
validation
Rationale: Restricted range reduces variability and weakens validity estimates.
91. A clinician wants to determine whether a child’s low score is meaningfully different from the
child’s own average performance across domains, rather than from the norm group alone. This
is closest to:
A. criterion-referenced interpretation
B. ipsative interpretation
C. face-valid interpretation
D. actuarial irrelevance
✅Answer: B. ipsative interpretation
Rationale: Ipsative interpretation compares an individual’s scores to their own performance
across domains to identify relative strengths and weaknesses.
92. Which statement best reflects the distinction between clinical and mechanical prediction?
A. Mechanical prediction uses no data
B. Clinical prediction always outperforms actuarial methods
C. Mechanical prediction applies explicit rules, whereas clinical prediction relies more on
professional judgment
D. They are identical processes with different labels
✅Answer: C. Mechanical prediction applies explicit rules, whereas clinical prediction relies
more on professional judgment
Rationale: Mechanical prediction uses statistical or rule-based methods, while clinical
prediction depends on expert judgment.
93. A practitioner bases conclusions on case history, interview, collateral reports, observation,
and test results that converge on the same finding. This strengthens confidence through:
A. triangulation of assessment data
B. semantic drift
C. item homogenization
D. acquiescence bias only
✅Answer: A. triangulation of assessment data
Rationale: Triangulation involves using multiple sources of information to support conclusions.
94. Which is the strongest reason for careful report writing in psychological assessment?
A. Reports are merely administrative requirements
B. Reports communicate findings that may affect major decisions about people
C. Reports are intended only for other psychologists
D. Reports should include every detail gathered regardless of relevance
✅Answer: B. Reports communicate findings that may affect major decisions about people
Rationale: Assessment reports inform significant decisions, making accuracy and clarity
critical.
95. Which of the following is the best example of an ethical dilemma rather than simple
misconduct?
A. Forgetting to bring a pencil to testing
B. Facing conflicting obligations between client confidentiality and risk of serious harm
C. Failing to score a completed answer sheet
D. Arriving early to an appointment
✅Answer: B. Facing conflicting obligations between client confidentiality and risk of serious
harm
Rationale: Ethical dilemmas involve conflicts between important principles requiring
judgment.
96. A psychologist learns that another practitioner may have committed an ethical violation.
According to ethical standards, which response is generally most appropriate first, if feasible
and confidentiality is not violated?
A. Immediately post the allegation online
B. Consider informal resolution by bringing the concern to the practitioner’s attention
C. Ignore the matter completely
D. Assume the allegation is false because the person is licensed
✅Answer: B. Consider informal resolution by bringing the concern to the practitioner’s
attention
Rationale: Ethical guidelines often encourage informal resolution first when appropriate.
97. Which of the following best illustrates an assessment use in health psychology?
A. Interest matching for career choice only
B. Neuropsychological and quality-of-life assessment in medical care
C. Exclusive use of projective tests for all patients
D. Replacing clinical interviews with horoscope reading
✅Answer: B. Neuropsychological and quality-of-life assessment in medical care
Rationale: Health psychology assessment includes cognitive and quality-of-life evaluations in
medical settings.
98. When a test is used with a population that differs substantially from the norm group, the
most defensible stance is that:
A. norms remain equally applicable in all cases
B. interpretation should consider the limits of generalizability and possible need for alternative
data
C. the test becomes invalid automatically
D. raw scores should be reported without interpretation
✅Answer: B. interpretation should consider the limits of generalizability and possible need
for alternative data
Rationale: Differences from the norm group require cautious interpretation and possibly
alternative approaches.
99. Which pioneer is most closely associated with the Wechsler intelligence scales?
A. David Wechsler
B. Lewis Terman
C. John Holland
D. Raymond Cattell
✅Answer: A. David Wechsler
Rationale: David Wechsler developed the Wechsler intelligence scales.
100. Which overall practice best reflects high-quality psychological assessment at board exam
level?
A. Relying on one preferred test for all referral questions
B. Integrating scientifically grounded tools, ethical principles, cultural sensitivity, and legally
appropriate practice
C. Avoiding documentation to maintain flexibility
D. Using only the most popular instrument regardless of purpose
✅Answer: B. Integrating scientifically grounded tools, ethical principles, cultural sensitivity,
and legally appropriate practice
Rationale: High-quality assessment requires integration of sound methods, ethics, cultural
awareness, and legal compliance.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 8
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 8
1. Psychological assessment is best described as:
A. The scoring of standardized tests only
B. A process of collecting and integrating data to answer a referral question
C. The interpretation of intelligence test scores only
D. The diagnosis of mental disorders based solely on symptoms
✅Answer: B. A process of collecting and integrating data to answer a referral question
Rationale: Psychological assessment is broader than test scoring alone. It involves gathering,
integrating, and interpreting information from multiple sources in order to address a specific
referral question.
2. Which of the following is the clearest distinction between a psychological test and
psychological assessment?
A. A test is always objective, whereas assessment is always subjective
B. A test is one tool, whereas assessment is the broader process in which multiple tools may
be used
C. A test requires a manual, whereas assessment does not
D. A test is quantitative, whereas assessment is qualitative
✅Answer: B. A test is one tool, whereas assessment is the broader process in which
multiple tools may be used
Rationale: A psychological test is only one instrument used in evaluation, while assessment is
the larger process that may include tests, interviews, observations, and record review.
3. In psychological measurement, a trait is best defined as:
A. A temporary emotional condition
B. A stable tendency to respond in a characteristic way
C. An examiner’s interpretation of behavior
D. A score derived from a norm group
✅Answer: B. A stable tendency to respond in a characteristic way
Rationale: A trait refers to a relatively enduring disposition or pattern of responding, in contrast
to a temporary state or condition.
4. A psychometrician is asked to administer a test to a client who speaks a language the
psychometrician does not understand. The most defensible first step is to:
A. Proceed with administration because standardization is more important than
comprehension
B. Use gestures and improvised explanations
C. Refer or obtain competent assistance consistent with ethical and legal limits
D. Translate the test freely during administration
✅Answer: C. Refer or obtain competent assistance consistent with ethical and legal limits
Rationale: Ethical and competent practice requires that assessment be conducted in a way
the client can understand, while also staying within professional and legal boundaries.
5. Which source of data is most useful for obtaining detailed background information about
developmental, medical, educational, and family history?
A. Projective test
B. Case history
C. Rating scale only
D. Behavioral checklist only
✅Answer: B. Case history
Rationale: Case history is specifically intended to gather contextual background data such as
developmental, medical, educational, and family information that informs interpretation.
6. A clinician wants to know how a child behaves during free play, transitions, and peer
interaction in a natural school setting. The best primary method is:
A. Structured interview
B. Naturalistic behavioral observation
C. Sentence completion test
D. Achievement testing
✅Answer: B. Naturalistic behavioral observation
Rationale: Naturalistic observation is the best method when the goal is to examine actual
behavior in the setting where it naturally occurs.
7. The main purpose of norms in testing is to:
A. Eliminate error variance
B. Convert raw scores into meaningful comparative information
C. Guarantee validity
D. Replace clinical judgment
✅Answer: B. Convert raw scores into meaningful comparative information
Rationale: Norms make raw scores interpretable by showing how an individual compares with
a defined reference group.
8. Which is the best example of a criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. Maria scored higher than 84% of Grade 6 pupils
B. Jose obtained a T score of 60
C. Ana correctly answered 90% of multiplication items and met mastery criterion
D. Ben’s stanine score is 7
✅Answer: C. Ana correctly answered 90% of multiplication items and met mastery criterion
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation focuses on whether a person has met a defined
standard or mastered a specific skill area, not on comparison with others.
9. In a negatively skewed distribution of test scores, one would expect:
A. Many low scores and a tail toward the high end
B. Many high scores and a tail toward the low end
C. Mean lower than median in all cases
D. No effect on percentile ranks
✅Answer: B. Many high scores and a tail toward the low end
Rationale: A negatively skewed distribution is characterized by clustering of scores at the high
end and a longer tail extending toward lower scores.
10. A raw score converted to a z score of +2.00 means the score is:
A. Two raw-score units above the mean
B. Two standard deviations above the mean
C. At the 2nd percentile
D. Equal to the mean plus 20 points in all scales
✅Answer: B. Two standard deviations above the mean
Rationale: A z score expresses distance from the mean in standard deviation units, so +2.00
means the score is two standard deviations above the mean.
11. Which correlation coefficient is most appropriate for two continuous variables measured at
interval level?
A. Phi
B. Spearman rho
C. Pearson r
D. Point-biserial only
✅Answer: C. Pearson r
Rationale: Pearson r is the standard correlation coefficient used when both variables are
continuous and measured at the interval or ratio level.
12. A coefficient of determination of .49 indicates that:
A. 49% of the variance is unexplained
B. 49% of the variance in one variable is associated with variance in the other
C. The test has 49% validity
D. The correlation is .49 squared by error
✅Answer: B. 49% of the variance in one variable is associated with variance in the other
Rationale: The coefficient of determination, r², reflects the proportion of shared variance
between two variables.
13. Restriction of range usually:
A. Inflates the correlation
B. Has no effect on the correlation
C. Lowers the obtained correlation
D. Guarantees predictive validity
✅Answer: C. Lowers the obtained correlation
Rationale: Restricting the range reduces variability, which usually attenuates or lowers the
correlation coefficient.
14. Reliability refers primarily to:
A. The fairness of a test across cultures
B. The consistency of measurement
C. The usefulness of a test for decision-making
D. The degree to which a test measures what it claims to measure
✅Answer: B. The consistency of measurement
Rationale: Reliability refers to the dependability or consistency of scores across time, forms,
items, or raters.
15. A school uses the same test with the same students two weeks apart to estimate stability
over time. This is:
A. Split-half reliability
B. Interrater reliability
C. Test-retest reliability
D. Alternate-forms reliability
✅Answer: C. Test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability evaluates the stability of scores over time by administering the
same test to the same individuals on two occasions.
16. When equivalent forms of a test are administered and correlated, the resulting estimate is
most useful for examining:
A. Temporal stability only
B. Consistency across forms
C. Rater bias only
D. Standard error only
✅Answer: B. Consistency across forms
Rationale: Equivalent or alternate forms reliability assesses whether two versions of a test
produce similar results.
17. Which method is most appropriate for estimating the agreement between two essay
scorers?
A. Test-retest reliability
B. Interscorer reliability
C. Split-half reliability
D. KR-20 only
✅Answer: B. Interscorer reliability
Rationale: Interscorer reliability is specifically concerned with the consistency of judgments
made by different scorers.
18. The standard error of measurement is most directly useful for:
A. Determining whether a test has face validity
B. Estimating the range within which a person’s true score likely falls
C. Comparing group means only
D. Converting raw scores to percentiles
✅Answer: B. Estimating the range within which a person’s true score likely falls
Rationale: The standard error of measurement helps estimate the likely range around an
observed score within which the person’s true score lies.
19. A reliability coefficient of .50 for a high-stakes licensure screening tool is generally:
A. Excellent because all psychological tests contain error
B. Adequate if the sample is large
C. Questionable because important decisions require stronger score consistency
D. Irrelevant if the test appears valid
✅Answer: C. Questionable because important decisions require stronger score consistency
Rationale: High-stakes decisions require strong score consistency, and a reliability coefficient
of .50 is generally too low for such important uses.
20. Validity is best understood as:
A. The aesthetic acceptability of test materials
B. The degree to which evidence supports the interpretation and use of scores
C. The stability of scores over time
D. The ease of administration
✅Answer: B. The degree to which evidence supports the interpretation and use of scores
Rationale: Validity concerns whether available evidence justifies the meaning assigned to
scores and the decisions based on them.
21. Face validity refers to:
A. Statistical evidence that the test predicts a criterion
B. The extent to which the test appears relevant to what it intends to measure
C. Internal consistency among items
D. Evidence from factor analysis only
✅Answer: B. The extent to which the test appears relevant to what it intends to measure
Rationale: Face validity is about the apparent relevance or acceptability of the test content as
judged at a surface level.
22. Which type of validity evidence is most relevant when a mathematics licensure exam is
reviewed to ensure adequate sampling of the domain?
A. Predictive validity
B. Concurrent validity
C. Content validity
D. Face validity
✅Answer: C. Content validity
Rationale: Content validity is concerned with how well test items represent the domain of
knowledge or skills that the test is intended to cover.
23. A company wants to know whether an aptitude test predicts future job performance after
hiring. The most relevant evidence is:
A. Concurrent validity
B. Predictive validity
C. Face validity
D. Content validity
✅Answer: B. Predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity examines how well test scores forecast a future criterion such as
later job performance.
24. Construct validity is most directly concerned with:
A. Whether the test looks acceptable to examinees
B. Whether the test adequately samples instructional content
C. Whether the test behaves as expected in relation to theory and related variables
D. Whether two scorers agree
✅Answer: C. Whether the test behaves as expected in relation to theory and related
variables
Rationale: Construct validity concerns whether the test functions in a manner consistent with
theoretical expectations about the construct being measured.
25. Test bias exists when:
A. A test is difficult
B. Group differences in scores automatically appear
C. The test systematically leads to invalid interpretations for a particular group
D. The manual reports standardization data
✅Answer: C. The test systematically leads to invalid interpretations for a particular group
Rationale: Test bias is present when score interpretations are systematically inaccurate or
unfair for members of a particular group.
26. In item analysis, an item difficulty index usually refers to:
A. The percentage of examinees who answer the item correctly
B. The correlation of the item with another test
C. The examiner’s judgment of wording complexity
D. The item’s face validity rating
✅Answer: A. The percentage of examinees who answer the item correctly
Rationale: In classical test theory, item difficulty is typically indexed by the proportion of
examinees who answer the item correctly.
27. A good discrimination index indicates that an item:
A. Is answered correctly by everyone
B. Distinguishes high scorers from low scorers
C. Is highly correlated with age
D. Is easy to administer
✅Answer: B. Distinguishes high scorers from low scorers
Rationale: An item with good discrimination helps separate examinees who perform well on
the overall test from those who perform poorly.
28. The primary goal of pilot testing in test development is to:
A. Finalize norms immediately
B. Obtain preliminary evidence about item functioning and administration issues
C. Eliminate the need for validation
D. Guarantee legal defensibility
✅Answer: B. Obtain preliminary evidence about item functioning and administration issues
Rationale: Pilot testing allows developers to examine how items work and identify problems in
instructions, content, or administration before finalizing the test.
29. Which is the best guideline in writing multiple-choice test items?
A. Use implausible distractors to speed scoring
B. Make the stem vague to increase difficulty
C. Ensure one clear best answer and plausible distractors
D. Use “all of the above” frequently
✅Answer: C. Ensure one clear best answer and plausible distractors
Rationale: High-quality multiple-choice items should contain one clearly correct answer and
distractors that are believable and relevant.
30. Utility of a test refers to:
A. Its internal consistency only
B. Its practical value for making decisions
C. Its theoretical elegance
D. Its percentile ranking system
✅Answer: B. Its practical value for making decisions
Rationale: Utility refers to the practical usefulness of a test in real decision-making contexts.
31. Alfred Binet is most closely associated with:
A. Development of the first modern intelligence test for identifying children needing
educational assistance
B. Discovery of the unconscious
C. Creation of the first projective inkblot test
D. Development of factor analysis
✅Answer: A. Development of the first modern intelligence test for identifying children
needing educational assistance
Rationale: Alfred Binet is known for developing an early modern intelligence test to help
identify children who needed special educational support.
32. Charles Spearman is best known for proposing:
A. Multiple intelligences
B. Fluid and crystallized intelligence
C. General intelligence or g
D. Triarchic intelligence
✅Answer: C. General intelligence or g
Rationale: Spearman proposed that performance across cognitive tasks reflects a general
mental ability, or g.
33. The deviation IQ was developed primarily to:
A. Replace percentile ranks with raw scores
B. Express performance relative to an age-based normative distribution
C. Eliminate measurement error
D. Measure personality more accurately
✅Answer: B. Express performance relative to an age-based normative distribution
Rationale: Deviation IQ expresses an individual’s performance relative to others of the same
age in the normative sample.
34. A major advantage of Wechsler scales over early age-scale formats is that they:
A. Avoid all cultural influences
B. Use deviation scores and multiple subtests representing varied abilities
C. Can only be used individually
D. Eliminate the need for norms
✅Answer: B. Use deviation scores and multiple subtests representing varied abilities
Rationale: Wechsler scales improved intelligence testing by using multiple subtests and
deviation-based interpretation rather than simple age-scale comparisons.
35. Which statement best reflects current views of intelligence testing?
A. Intelligence tests measure a single, culture-free essence
B. Intelligence tests provide no meaningful information
C. Intelligence test results should be interpreted in light of theory, context, and cultural factors
D. Intelligence and achievement are identical constructs
✅Answer: C. Intelligence test results should be interpreted in light of theory, context, and
cultural factors
Rationale: Modern intelligence testing recognizes that scores can be useful, but they must be
interpreted within theoretical, cultural, and situational context.
36. The Flynn effect refers to:
A. Decline in reliability with repeated testing
B. Gradual rise in intelligence test scores across generations
C. Inflation of validity coefficients
D. Examiner expectancy effects in IQ testing
✅Answer: B. Gradual rise in intelligence test scores across generations
Rationale: The Flynn effect refers to the long-observed increase in average intelligence test
scores over successive generations.
37. In educational assessment, response to intervention is primarily used to:
A. Replace all standardized testing
B. Provide tiered intervention and monitor student response before or alongside special
education decisions
C. Diagnose personality disorders in schoolchildren
D. Eliminate teacher judgment
✅Answer: B. Provide tiered intervention and monitor student response before or alongside
special education decisions
Rationale: Response to intervention uses increasingly intensive instructional support and
progress monitoring to guide educational decisions.
38. A diagnostic test differs from a broad achievement test because it is designed primarily to:
A. Rank students nationally
B. Identify specific strengths and weaknesses in a skill area
C. Predict long-term occupational success
D. Measure general intelligence
✅Answer: B. Identify specific strengths and weaknesses in a skill area
Rationale: Diagnostic tests are designed to pinpoint specific areas of mastery and difficulty for
instructional planning.
39. Portfolio assessment is especially useful for:
A. Estimating test-retest reliability
B. Capturing performance and products over time
C. Measuring only reading comprehension
D. Replacing all norm-referenced data
✅Answer: B. Capturing performance and products over time
Rationale: Portfolio assessment allows evaluation of a person’s work samples, development,
and performance across time.
40. Dynamic assessment places greatest emphasis on:
A. Static measurement under fixed conditions
B. Learning potential and responsiveness to guided assistance
C. Projective interpretation
D. Blind scoring
✅Answer: B. Learning potential and responsiveness to guided assistance
Rationale: Dynamic assessment focuses on how well an examinee learns or improves when
provided with help or mediation.
41. Personality assessment is concerned primarily with:
A. Maximum performance only
B. Typical behavior, traits, states, and related characteristics
C. Neurological reflexes
D. Sensory thresholds only
✅Answer: B. Typical behavior, traits, states, and related characteristics
Rationale: Personality assessment focuses on relatively typical patterns of behavior, emotion,
motivation, and disposition rather than maximum performance.
42. Which pair correctly contrasts objective and projective methods?
A. Objective methods use ambiguous stimuli; projective methods use fixed-response items
B. Objective methods are always invalid; projective methods are always valid
C. Objective methods tend to use structured scoring; projective methods often use more
ambiguous stimuli and interpretive responses
D. Objective methods cannot assess personality
✅Answer: C. Objective methods tend to use structured scoring; projective methods often
use more ambiguous stimuli and interpretive responses
Rationale: Objective methods are generally more structured in format and scoring, whereas
projective methods rely more on responses to ambiguous stimuli.
43. The projective hypothesis proposes that:
A. Test scores are free from unconscious influence
B. Responses to ambiguous stimuli may reflect underlying needs, motives, and conflicts
C. Only objective tests can reveal personality
D. Personality is fixed after childhood
✅Answer: B. Responses to ambiguous stimuli may reflect underlying needs, motives, and
conflicts
Rationale: The projective hypothesis holds that people project inner motives, conflicts, and
needs when responding to ambiguous material.
44. The Rorschach is classified primarily as a:
A. Behavioral rating scale
B. Projective technique using inkblots
C. Neuropsychological battery
D. Structured inventory of interests
✅Answer: B. Projective technique using inkblots
Rationale: The Rorschach is a projective method in which individuals respond to inkblot
stimuli.
45. The Thematic Apperception Test mainly uses:
A. Mazes
B. Incomplete sentences only
C. Ambiguous pictures for story production
D. Arithmetic problems
✅Answer: C. Ambiguous pictures for story production
Rationale: The TAT presents ambiguous pictures and asks the examinee to create stories,
which are then interpreted for personality themes.
46. A major limitation of projective techniques is that they often raise stronger questions about:
A. Item scoring speed only
B. Standardization, reliability, and validity compared with more structured methods
C. Need for rapport
D. Test security only
✅Answer: B. Standardization, reliability, and validity compared with more structured
methods
Rationale: Projective techniques are often criticized because their psychometric foundations
may be less consistent and more difficult to establish than those of structured tests.
47. Behavioral assessment differs from many traditional approaches because it focuses more
on:
A. Unconscious symbolism only
B. Observable behavior, situational antecedents, and consequences
C. IQ profiles only
D. Historical pioneers
✅Answer: B. Observable behavior, situational antecedents, and consequences
Rationale: Behavioral assessment emphasizes what behavior occurs, under what conditions
it occurs, and what consequences maintain it.
48. Functional analysis in behavioral assessment examines:
A. Subtest scaled scores
B. The relationship between behavior and antecedents/consequences
C. Latent traits only
D. Projective symbols
✅Answer: B. The relationship between behavior and antecedents/consequences
Rationale: Functional analysis identifies the conditions that precede and follow a behavior in
order to understand and modify it.
49. A self-monitoring diary of panic episodes is most consistent with:
A. Behavioral assessment
B. Purely projective testing
C. Factor analytic personality theory only
D. Forensic malingering detection only
✅Answer: A. Behavioral assessment
Rationale: Self-monitoring is a common behavioral assessment procedure because it tracks
observable patterns and circumstances surrounding target behaviors.
50. The interview in clinical assessment is especially valuable because it:
A. Eliminates all response bias
B. Allows flexible, interactive data gathering and hypothesis generation
C. Replaces psychological tests entirely
D. Is always more reliable than standardized measures
✅Answer: B. Allows flexible, interactive data gathering and hypothesis generation
Rationale: The interview is valuable because it permits clarification, probing, rapport building,
and the generation of clinical hypotheses.
51. Mental status examination is most directly concerned with:
A. Childhood attachment only
B. Current cognitive, emotional, and behavioral functioning
C. Long-term occupational values
D. Test fairness
✅Answer: B. Current cognitive, emotional, and behavioral functioning
Rationale: The mental status examination focuses on the person’s present functioning,
including mood, thought processes, orientation, memory, and behavior.
52. Case history data are especially important in clinical assessment because they:
A. Guarantee diagnosis
B. Provide contextual information relevant to interpretation and treatment planning
C. Replace informed consent
D. Are always objective
✅Answer: B. Provide contextual information relevant to interpretation and treatment
planning
Rationale: Case history supplies background information that gives meaning to current
symptoms, behaviors, and test results.
53. The Barnum effect refers to:
A. Improved accuracy through test interpretation
B. Tendency to accept vague, general descriptions as uniquely accurate
C. Reduced measurement error
D. Increased test utility
✅Answer: B. Tendency to accept vague, general descriptions as uniquely accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect occurs when people believe broad, general statements are
specifically true of them.
54. Mechanical prediction generally refers to:
A. Diagnosis by machine without data
B. Combining data through fixed rules or algorithms rather than unaided clinical intuition
C. The use of projective techniques only
D. Interview rapport
✅Answer: B. Combining data through fixed rules or algorithms rather than unaided clinical
intuition
Rationale: Mechanical prediction uses explicit, consistent rules for combining data, often
improving objectivity and consistency.
55. In suicide assessment, which factor generally calls for the highest immediate concern?
A. Mild work stress without distress
B. Passive wish to rest with no other indicators
C. Specific plan, access to means, and recent intent
D. Average academic performance
✅Answer: C. Specific plan, access to means, and recent intent
Rationale: A specific plan, access to means, and clear intent indicate elevated acute risk and
require immediate attention.
56. In custody evaluation, the evaluator’s most important obligation is to:
A. Advocate for whichever parent first requested the evaluation
B. Determine which parent is wealthier
C. Remain objective and focus on the best interests and welfare of the child
D. Guarantee joint custody
✅Answer: C. Remain objective and focus on the best interests and welfare of the child
Rationale: Custody assessment requires impartial evaluation centered on the child’s welfare
rather than allegiance to either parent.
57. Forensic assessment differs from therapeutic assessment in that it more often:
A. Avoids documentation
B. Requires role clarification, awareness of legal standards, and limits of confidentiality
C. Assumes a treatment relationship
D. Uses no standardized tools
✅Answer: B. Requires role clarification, awareness of legal standards, and limits of
confidentiality
Rationale: Forensic assessment occurs in a legal context, so the evaluator must clearly
define roles, legal purpose, and confidentiality limits.
58. A neuropsychological evaluation is most indicated when there is suspicion of:
A. Vocational indecision only
B. Brain-based impairment affecting cognition or behavior
C. Poor study habits only
D. Normal variation in interests
✅Answer: B. Brain-based impairment affecting cognition or behavior
Rationale: Neuropsychological evaluation is used when neurological dysfunction is suspected
to be affecting cognitive, emotional, or behavioral functioning.
59. Executive functions are most closely associated with abilities such as:
A. Color discrimination only
B. Planning, inhibition, set shifting, and problem solving
C. Auditory threshold only
D. Muscle strength alone
✅Answer: B. Planning, inhibition, set shifting, and problem solving
Rationale: Executive functions refer to higher-order control processes involved in planning,
self-regulation, cognitive flexibility, and organized problem solving.
60. Which task is most directly aimed at assessing memory functioning?
A. Digit span learning or list-learning tasks
B. Sentence completion
C. Strong Interest Inventory
D. Rorschach inquiry only
✅Answer: A. Digit span learning or list-learning tasks
Rationale: Memory tasks such as digit span and list learning directly assess encoding,
storage, and retrieval functions.
61. Aphasia most directly concerns impairment in:
A. Vision
B. Language
C. Motor strength
D. Interest patterns
✅Answer: B. Language
Rationale: Aphasia is a disorder affecting language comprehension, expression, or both.
62. A patient with intact recognition but poor free recall may be showing difficulty mainly in:
A. Encoding or retrieval processes related to memory
B. Visual acuity only
C. Moral reasoning only
D. Interest development
✅Answer: A. Encoding or retrieval processes related to memory
Rationale: A pattern of poor recall but better recognition commonly suggests difficulty with
memory processes such as encoding or retrieval rather than total storage loss.
63. In career assessment, interest inventories are designed primarily to:
A. Diagnose psychosis
B. Measure preferences for activities, occupations, and work environments
C. Replace aptitude measures
D. Measure current mood only
✅Answer: B. Measure preferences for activities, occupations, and work environments
Rationale: Interest inventories assess what kinds of activities and occupational settings a
person tends to like or prefer.
64. Aptitude tests are most useful when the goal is to estimate:
A. Current personality style only
B. Potential to learn or perform in a particular area
C. Past emotional trauma only
D. Ethical decision-making only
✅Answer: B. Potential to learn or perform in a particular area
Rationale: Aptitude tests are used to estimate a person’s capacity or potential for future
learning or performance.
65. In personnel selection, validity generalization refers to the finding that:
A. All tests are valid for all jobs
B. Evidence of test validity may generalize across similar jobs and settings
C. Validity and reliability are identical
D. Interviews are always superior to tests
✅Answer: B. Evidence of test validity may generalize across similar jobs and settings
Rationale: Validity generalization means that evidence supporting a test in one context may
also apply in other similar contexts.
66. Job analysis is important in employee selection because it:
A. Makes all tests culture-free
B. Identifies job-relevant knowledge, skills, abilities, and other characteristics
C. Replaces the need for interviews
D. Ensures a high base rate
✅Answer: B. Identifies job-relevant knowledge, skills, abilities, and other characteristics
Rationale: Job analysis provides the foundation for selection by specifying the competencies
and demands relevant to successful job performance.
67. Which would most likely improve fairness in personnel testing?
A. Using irrelevant but difficult items
B. Basing selection on job-related constructs derived from job analysis
C. Selecting only top scorers from one school
D. Ignoring adverse impact data
✅Answer: B. Basing selection on job-related constructs derived from job analysis
Rationale: Fairness is enhanced when testing is tied directly to job-relevant requirements
established through systematic job analysis.
68. A résumé and interview are best viewed as:
A. Completely psychometrically equivalent to standardized tests
B. Additional assessment tools that may contribute information but vary in structure and
reliability
C. Useless in selection
D. Measures of neurological impairment
✅Answer: B. Additional assessment tools that may contribute information but vary in
structure and reliability
Rationale: Résumés and interviews can provide useful selection information, but they differ in
structure and psychometric strength from standardized tests.
69. Which statement best describes stereotype threat?
A. It improves performance through competition
B. It is a legal doctrine under RA 10029
C. It is performance impairment linked to fear of confirming a negative group stereotype
D. It affects only children
✅Answer: C. It is performance impairment linked to fear of confirming a negative group
stereotype
Rationale: Stereotype threat occurs when concern about confirming a negative stereotype
interferes with actual performance.
70. In a multicultural assessment context, the best practice is to:
A. Assume the same score meaning across all groups
B. Ignore acculturation and language factors
C. Interpret scores within cultural, linguistic, and contextual background
D. Replace all standardized tests with interviews
✅Answer: C. Interpret scores within cultural, linguistic, and contextual background
Rationale: Appropriate multicultural assessment requires interpreting results in light of the
person’s culture, language, and contextual background.
71. Under the PAP Code of Ethics, only licensed and registered psychologists and
psychometricians are legally allowed to practice their profession as provided by:
A. RA 7877
B. RA 10029
C. RA 10912
D. RA 11036
✅Answer: B. RA 10029
Rationale: RA 10029, the Philippine Psychology Act of 2009, governs the legal practice of
psychology and psychometrics in the Philippines.
72. A psychometrician is asked to independently interpret complex test results and issue a
diagnostic report without supervision from a psychologist when such interpretation exceeds his
or her lawful scope. The most ethical response is to:
A. Accept because experience can substitute for legal limits
B. Proceed if the client agrees
C. Decline and act within lawful and professional boundaries
D. Interpret only the parts that seem easy and diagnose tentatively
✅Answer: C. Decline and act within lawful and professional boundaries
Rationale: Ethical practice requires professionals to work only within the boundaries of lawful
scope and competence.
73. According to ethical standards, informed consent in assessment generally includes
explaining:
A. Only the test name
B. The nature and purpose of services, probable uses, and relevant limits including
confidentiality
C. The examiner’s personal opinions
D. Raw score conversion formulas only
✅Answer: B. The nature and purpose of services, probable uses, and relevant limits
including confidentiality
Rationale: Informed consent requires that the client understand what the service is, why it is
being done, how the information may be used, and any limits to confidentiality.
74. When the client is legally incapable of giving informed consent, the psychology practitioner
should generally:
A. Proceed without explanation
B. Obtain assent when possible and permission from a legally authorized person, while
protecting the individual’s welfare
C. Ignore the person’s preferences
D. Administer all tests secretly
✅Answer: B. Obtain assent when possible and permission from a legally authorized person,
while protecting the individual’s welfare
Rationale: Ethical practice requires protecting vulnerable individuals by seeking assent when
possible, obtaining authorized permission, and safeguarding the person’s rights and welfare.
75. Which situation most clearly justifies breaching confidentiality?
A. A colleague is curious about the case
B. The examiner wants to use the case in class without disguise
C. There is imminent danger to the client or community and disclosure is limited to what is
necessary
D. The client scored low on an aptitude test
✅Answer: C. There is imminent danger to the client or community and disclosure is limited
to what is necessary
Rationale: Confidentiality may be breached when necessary to prevent serious imminent
harm, provided disclosure is restricted to what is essential.
76. Before recording a client’s voice or image during assessment, the practitioner should:
A. Record first, explain later
B. Obtain consent and explain anticipated uses of the recording
C. Record only if the device is secure
D. Do so only with verbal reassurance to staff
✅Answer: B. Obtain consent and explain anticipated uses of the recording
Rationale: Recording requires prior consent and clear explanation of how the recording will
be used.
77. A practitioner posts disguised but still potentially identifiable client details on social media for
educational discussion. This is primarily an issue of:
A. Utility
B. Confidentiality and privacy
C. Alternate-forms reliability
D. Standardization
✅Answer: B. Confidentiality and privacy
Rationale: Even if details are partly disguised, sharing identifiable client information risks
violating privacy and confidentiality.
78. Multiple relationships are ethically problematic mainly when they:
A. Always exist in small communities
B. Reasonably risk impairing objectivity, competence, or effectiveness, or create exploitation
or harm
C. Involve no exchange of money
D. Occur only in therapy
✅Answer: B. Reasonably risk impairing objectivity, competence, or effectiveness, or create
exploitation or harm
Rationale: Multiple relationships become ethically problematic when they threaten
professional judgment or expose the client to exploitation or harm.
79. A psychometrician feels emotionally overwhelmed and sleep-deprived but continues
administering complex assessments without consultation. This most directly violates:
A. Age norms
B. Personal problems and maintaining competent practice
C. Parallel-forms reliability
D. Utility analysis
✅Answer: B. Personal problems and maintaining competent practice
Rationale: Ethical practice requires professionals to monitor personal problems that may
interfere with competent performance and to take appropriate action.
80. Delegation of assessment work to another person is ethical only when:
A. The delegate is cheaper
B. The client does not need to know
C. Responsibilities match the person’s competence and appropriate supervision is provided
D. The delegate is a friend of the client
✅Answer: C. Responsibilities match the person’s competence and appropriate supervision
is provided
Rationale: Delegation is ethical only when the delegated tasks fit the person’s education,
training, or experience and proper supervision is ensured.
81. In an emergency setting where no qualified specialist is immediately available, the ethical
standard allows psychology practitioners to:
A. Provide no assistance at all
B. Offer cautious emergency help, support, information, or referral, then discontinue when
appropriate competent services become available
C. Begin long-term treatment beyond competence
D. Ignore referral needs
✅Answer: B. Offer cautious emergency help, support, information, or referral, then
discontinue when appropriate competent services become available
Rationale: In emergencies, practitioners may provide limited assistance to avoid depriving a
person of needed help, but must stop once competent services can take over.
82. A court orders an assessment. Before proceeding, the practitioner should inform the
examinee about:
A. How to fake good performance
B. The mandated nature of the service and limits of confidentiality
C. The correct answers
D. The judge’s expected findings
✅Answer: B. The mandated nature of the service and limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Court-ordered assessment requires clear explanation that the service is mandated
and that confidentiality is limited by the legal context.
83. A third-party referral from an employer requires the assessor to clarify at the outset:
A. Only the test fee
B. The role of the assessor, who the client is, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
C. Only the employee’s weaknesses
D. That all findings are confidential from the employer
✅Answer: B. The role of the assessor, who the client is, probable uses of information, and
limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Third-party services require clear role definition and explanation of how information
will be used and who will receive it.
84. Which is the best example of avoiding harm during assessment?
A. Administering a lengthy battery despite severe fatigue because the schedule is fixed
B. Ignoring cultural barriers to save time
C. Choosing procedures that minimize foreseeable harm and modifying plans when risk
increases
D. Releasing all raw data to unqualified persons
✅Answer: C. Choosing procedures that minimize foreseeable harm and modifying plans
when risk increases
Rationale: Avoiding harm means anticipating risk, minimizing it, and adjusting procedures
when the client’s welfare may be compromised.
85. Continuing Professional Development is ethically linked to:
A. Increasing face validity
B. Maintaining competence in practice
C. Improving only test speed
D. Avoiding documentation
✅Answer: B. Maintaining competence in practice
Rationale: Continuing Professional Development supports the practitioner’s ongoing
competence and relevance of knowledge and skills.
86. Which statement is most accurate regarding telepsychology or teleassessment under the
PAP Code?
A. Ethical rules apply only to face-to-face services
B. Online services are exempt from confidentiality rules
C. Ethical principles governing in-person services also apply to online modalities
D. Teleassessment can never be used for decisions
✅Answer: C. Ethical principles governing in-person services also apply to online modalities
Rationale: The PAP Code explicitly states that the same ethical principles governing
face-to-face services apply to online services.
87. A practitioner receives a request to release school-based assessment records to an outside
party. Ethically, the practitioner should:
A. Release everything immediately
B. Refuse all releases under any circumstance
C. Follow applicable consent, institutional approval, and confidentiality standards, limiting
disclosure to what is necessary
D. Post a summary online for transparency
✅Answer: C. Follow applicable consent, institutional approval, and confidentiality standards,
limiting disclosure to what is necessary
Rationale: Release of records must comply with consent requirements, institutional rules, and
confidentiality limits, with disclosure restricted to necessary information.
88. Which is the best example of improper complaint behavior under ethical rules?
A. Reporting a documented and serious violation to proper authorities
B. Informally speaking to a colleague about a minor breach when confidentiality is protected
C. Filing an ethics complaint with reckless disregard for facts and without supporting evidence
D. Cooperating with an ethics investigation
✅Answer: C. Filing an ethics complaint with reckless disregard for facts and without
supporting evidence
Rationale: Ethical rules prohibit complaints made irresponsibly, without adequate factual
basis, or in reckless disregard of the truth.
89. A test user explains results to a client using highly technical jargon the client cannot
understand. This primarily violates the ethical expectation of:
A. Practical utility
B. Clear, understandable communication and informed participation
C. Interscorer reliability
D. Item homogeneity
✅Answer: B. Clear, understandable communication and informed participation
Rationale: Ethical communication requires that results and procedures be explained in
language the client can reasonably understand.
90. A psychometrician is asked by a supervisor to administer a test in a way that departs from
standard instructions merely to save time. The best response is to:
A. Follow instructions because the supervisor is responsible
B. Modify administration and note nothing
C. Explain the concern and adhere to standard procedures unless a justified and documented
exception exists
D. Allow the client to choose procedures
✅Answer: C. Explain the concern and adhere to standard procedures unless a justified and
documented exception exists
Rationale: Standardized administration protects validity and fairness, so unjustified deviations
should be resisted and only properly justified exceptions should be made.
91. Which psychologist is most associated with the two-factor theory involving general and
specific abilities?
A. Alfred Binet
B. Charles Spearman
C. David Wechsler
D. Henry Murray
✅Answer: B. Charles Spearman
Rationale: Spearman proposed the two-factor theory, consisting of general intelligence and
specific abilities.
92. David Wechsler is best known for:
A. Developing inkblot cards
B. Proposing the projective hypothesis
C. Developing major intelligence scales using verbal and performance tasks
D. Creating the first behavior checklist
✅Answer: C. Developing major intelligence scales using verbal and performance tasks
Rationale: David Wechsler developed influential intelligence scales that used multiple
subtests representing different cognitive abilities.
93. Henry Murray is most closely associated with:
A. Thematic Apperception Test and needs/press concepts
B. Stanford-Binet deviation IQ
C. MMPI validity scales
D. Classical conditioning
✅Answer: A. Thematic Apperception Test and needs/press concepts
Rationale: Henry Murray is strongly associated with the TAT and his concepts of needs and
environmental press in personality theory.
94. The MMPI is historically notable because it was largely developed using which strategy?
A. Logical-content only
B. Factor analytic only
C. Criterion-keying or empirical criterion-group approach
D. Pure projective method
✅Answer: C. Criterion-keying or empirical criterion-group approach
Rationale: The MMPI is a classic example of empirical criterion-keyed test construction, in
which items were selected based on their ability to distinguish groups.
95. In test interpretation, a percentile rank of 84 means that the examinee:
A. Answered 84% of items correctly
B. Scored higher than approximately 84% of the norm group
C. Has an IQ of 84
D. Is exactly 84 points above the mean
✅Answer: B. Scored higher than approximately 84% of the norm group
Rationale: A percentile rank indicates relative standing in the normative sample, showing the
percentage of the group scoring at or below the examinee.
96. Which score metric has a mean of 50 and a standard deviation of 10?
A. z score
B. T score
C. IQ score
D. Stanine
✅Answer: B. T score
Rationale: The T score is a standardized score metric with a mean of 50 and a standard
deviation of 10.
97. If two tests correlate at .80, this means:
A. They are identical
B. One causes the other
C. They share a strong positive relationship, but not perfect overlap
D. They are both valid
✅Answer: C. They share a strong positive relationship, but not perfect overlap
Rationale: A correlation of .80 indicates a strong positive association, but it does not mean
the tests are identical or measure exactly the same thing.
98. Which is the best reason to combine interview data, test results, observations, and case
history?
A. One source is always sufficient
B. Converging evidence generally strengthens understanding of the referral question
C. More data always eliminate bias
D. It guarantees legal immunity
✅Answer: B. Converging evidence generally strengthens understanding of the referral
question
Rationale: Using multiple sources of data allows findings to be cross-checked and integrated,
leading to more defensible conclusions.
99. Which of the following is the most defensible interpretation of a single test score?
A. It reveals the whole person completely
B. It should be interpreted in context, considering reliability, validity, norms, and collateral data
C. It is meaningless without a projective test
D. It is equivalent to diagnosis
✅Answer: B. It should be interpreted in context, considering reliability, validity, norms, and
collateral data
Rationale: A single score must be interpreted cautiously within the larger context of
psychometric quality, norms, background information, and other assessment data.
100. In professional psychological assessment, the final goal is ideally to:
A. Produce the longest possible report
B. Maximize testing time
C. Answer the referral question in a scientifically grounded, ethical, and useful manner
D. Rely exclusively on the examiner’s intuition
✅Answer: C. Answer the referral question in a scientifically grounded, ethical, and useful
manner
Rationale: The central goal of assessment is to provide accurate, ethical, and practically
useful answers to the referral question based on sound evidence.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 9
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 9
1. Which statement best distinguishes psychological testing from psychological assessment?
A. Testing and assessment are identical terms referring only to standardized instruments
B. Testing is one tool, whereas assessment is a broader process that may integrate multiple
sources of data
C. Assessment refers only to clinical interviews, whereas testing refers only to
paper-and-pencil measures
D. Testing is broader than assessment because it includes interpretation and intervention
planning
✅Answer: B. Testing is one tool, whereas assessment is a broader process that may
integrate multiple sources of data
Rationale: Psychological assessment is broader than testing. Testing refers to the use of tests,
while assessment integrates test data with interviews, observations, case history, and other
relevant information to answer a referral question.
2. A psychologist combines interview data, behavioral observations, test scores, and collateral
information before making a recommendation. This best illustrates:
A. Criterion contamination
B. A fixed reference group approach
C. Psychological assessment
D. Item analysis
✅Answer: C. Psychological assessment
Rationale: Using multiple methods and data sources to make an evaluative conclusion is the
essence of psychological assessment rather than testing alone.
3. Which is the best example of a psychological trait rather than a state?
A. Fatigue after an all-night shift
B. Temporary anxiety before an interview
C. Chronic conscientiousness across settings
D. Sadness after receiving bad news
✅Answer: C. Chronic conscientiousness across settings
Rationale: A trait is an enduring disposition or tendency, whereas a state is a temporary
condition. Chronic conscientiousness is relatively stable across situations.
4. In psychometrics, an item refers to:
A. A complete battery of tests given to one client
B. A specific stimulus or question to which a person responds
C. The norm group used in test development
D. The final report written by the examiner
✅Answer: B. A specific stimulus or question to which a person responds
Rationale: An item is a specific question, prompt, or stimulus on a test that elicits a scorable
response from the examinee.
5. Which tool of assessment is most useful when the referral question concerns how a child
interacts with peers during recess?
A. A case history alone
B. Behavioral observation in the natural setting
C. A self-report inventory only
D. A projective technique only
✅Answer: B. Behavioral observation in the natural setting
Rationale: If the question concerns real-time peer interaction during recess, direct observation
in the natural environment provides the most ecologically valid data.
6. The primary reason standardized procedures are important in test administration is that they:
A. Eliminate all measurement error
B. Guarantee perfect validity
C. Help ensure comparability of scores across examinees
D. Remove the need for professional judgment
✅Answer: C. Help ensure comparability of scores across examinees
Rationale: Standardization reduces unwanted procedural variation so that differences in
scores are more likely to reflect examinee differences rather than administration differences.
7. A norm-referenced interpretation answers the question:
A. Did the examinee master a defined body of content?
B. How did the examinee perform relative to others in the reference group?
C. What intervention should automatically follow?
D. Is the test free from all cultural influence?
✅Answer: B. How did the examinee perform relative to others in the reference group?
Rationale: Norm-referenced interpretation compares an individual’s performance with that of a
normative sample.
8. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Median
B. Mode
C. Mean
D. Percentile rank
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean is most sensitive to extreme values because every score contributes
directly to the total.
9. Which scale of measurement has equal intervals but no true zero?
A. Nominal
B. Ordinal
C. Interval
D. Ratio
✅Answer: C. Interval
Rationale: Interval scales have equal intervals but lack a true zero point, unlike ratio scales.
10. A test score converted to a percentile rank of 84 means that the examinee:
A. Answered 84% of the items correctly
B. Performed as well as or better than 84% of the norm group
C. Obtained an IQ of 84
D. Is in the average range
✅Answer: B. Performed as well as or better than 84% of the norm group
Rationale: A percentile rank indicates relative standing in the normative group, not percent
correct.
11. The correlation coefficient primarily indicates:
A. Cause and effect
B. The direction and degree of relationship between two variables
C. The average of a distribution
D. The number of items missed
✅Answer: B. The direction and degree of relationship between two variables
Rationale: Correlation quantifies how strongly and in what direction two variables vary
together.
12. Which statement about correlation is correct?
A. A high correlation proves one variable causes the other
B. A zero correlation always means the measures are unreliable
C. Correlation does not by itself establish causation
D. Negative correlation means the measures are invalid
✅Answer: C. Correlation does not by itself establish causation
Rationale: Correlation may arise from direct influence, reverse influence, third variables, or
coincidence; therefore it cannot by itself prove causation.
13. In classical test theory, observed score is best expressed as:
A. True score minus error
B. True score plus error
C. Reliability plus validity
D. Validity minus error
✅Answer: B. True score plus error
Rationale: Classical test theory states that the observed score consists of the true score plus
measurement error.
14. Which reliability estimate is most appropriate when evaluating score stability over time using
the same test?
A. Inter-scorer reliability
B. Test-retest reliability
C. Split-half reliability
D. Alternate-forms validity
✅Answer: B. Test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability estimates stability across time by administering the same test
to the same individuals on two occasions.
15. A test with highly subjective scoring would make which type of reliability especially
important?
A. Criterion validity
B. Inter-scorer reliability
C. Parallel-forms reliability
D. Face validity
✅Answer: B. Inter-scorer reliability
Rationale: When scoring requires judgment, the consistency of scores across raters becomes
crucial.
16. Internal consistency evidence is most directly concerned with:
A. Whether the test predicts future performance
B. The degree to which items measure the same construct
C. Whether scores remain stable across years
D. Whether the test appears acceptable to clients
✅Answer: B. The degree to which items measure the same construct
Rationale: Internal consistency asks whether items on a scale are sufficiently homogeneous
and function together as indicators of the same construct.
17. The standard error of measurement is most useful for:
A. Transforming raw scores into percentiles
B. Estimating a band around an obtained score
C. Determining item difficulty
D. Establishing content validity
✅Answer: B. Estimating a band around an obtained score
Rationale: The standard error of measurement helps estimate the likely range in which the
examinee’s true score lies.
18. Face validity is best described as:
A. Statistical evidence that the test measures a construct
B. The degree to which test content samples a domain
C. The extent to which the test appears relevant on its surface
D. Evidence based on correlation with a criterion
✅Answer: C. The extent to which the test appears relevant on its surface
Rationale: Face validity concerns apparent relevance or plausibility, usually from a lay or
practical perspective, not deep empirical evidence.
19. A licensure examination blueprint is reviewed by subject matter experts to ensure adequate
content coverage. This is strongest evidence of:
A. Predictive validity
B. Content validity
C. Concurrent validity
D. Incremental validity
✅Answer: B. Content validity
Rationale: Blueprinting and expert review assess whether items adequately sample the
intended domain, which is central to content validity.
20. When a depression inventory correlates highly with an established depression measure
administered at the same time, this supports:
A. Face validity
B. Concurrent validity
C. Utility analysis
D. Split-half reliability
✅Answer: B. Concurrent validity
Rationale: When a new measure correlates with an established measure of the same
construct taken at the same time, concurrent validity is supported.
21. A college entrance examination is validated by showing it predicts first-year GPA. This is
evidence of:
A. Predictive validity
B. Content validity
C. Inter-rater reliability
D. Alternate-forms reliability
✅Answer: A. Predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity is shown when test scores forecast a future criterion such as
first-year GPA.
22. Construct validity is most directly supported by evidence that:
A. The test looks professional
B. Test items were written carefully
C. Scores relate to other variables as theory predicts
D. The test manual is lengthy
✅Answer: C. Scores relate to other variables as theory predicts
Rationale: Construct validity accumulates from evidence that score patterns fit theoretical
expectations, including convergent and discriminant relations.
23. Test bias refers most accurately to:
A. Any test that members of the public dislike
B. Systematic error that leads to unfair or invalid inferences for a group
C. Any group difference in mean scores
D. Any test requiring reading
✅Answer: B. Systematic error that leads to unfair or invalid inferences for a group
Rationale: Bias concerns systematic distortion in test use or interpretation that disadvantages
a group in ways not justified by the construct being measured.
24. Which statement is most accurate regarding fairness in testing?
A. A fair test produces identical mean scores for all groups
B. Fairness concerns the appropriateness of score interpretation and use
C. Fairness is irrelevant if reliability is high
D. Fairness and validity are unrelated
✅Answer: B. Fairness concerns the appropriateness of score interpretation and use
Rationale: Fairness is not merely about identical outcomes; it concerns whether the test and
its use support appropriate, non-discriminatory inferences.
25. The utility of a test is best understood as its:
A. Aesthetic appeal
B. Practical value for a specific decision-making purpose
C. Internal consistency only
D. Resistance to coaching only
✅Answer: B. Practical value for a specific decision-making purpose
Rationale: Utility refers to the real-world usefulness of a test for decisions such as selection,
screening, or classification.
26. A hospital is deciding whether adding a brief cognitive screener improves referral decisions
beyond interview data alone. This is primarily a question of:
A. Face validity
B. Utility
C. Item difficulty
D. Test bias
✅Answer: B. Utility
Rationale: The hospital is asking whether the screener adds practical value to decision
making beyond existing data, which is a utility question.
27. A cut score is best defined as:
A. The average score of the norm group
B. The score dividing one decision category from another
C. The highest possible raw score
D. A score that guarantees diagnostic accuracy
✅Answer: B. The score dividing one decision category from another
Rationale: A cut score sets the threshold for categories such as pass/fail, refer/not refer, or
qualified/not qualified.
28. In item analysis, an easy item tends to have:
A. A high difficulty index when difficulty is defined as proportion correct
B. A low proportion of keyed responses
C. A negative item-total correlation by definition
D. No role in test construction
✅Answer: A. A high difficulty index when difficulty is defined as proportion correct
Rationale: When difficulty index is proportion answering correctly, easier items have higher
values.
29. A good discrimination index indicates that an item:
A. Is offensive to some groups
B. Distinguishes high scorers from low scorers
C. Has the highest face validity
D. Should always be removed
✅Answer: B. Distinguishes high scorers from low scorers
Rationale: A good discrimination index indicates that those with higher total test performance
are more likely to answer the item correctly.
30. Which is the best rationale for pilot testing items before operational use?
A. To eliminate the need for norms
B. To examine item functioning and revise weak items
C. To prove criterion validity immediately
D. To avoid all future test revisions
✅Answer: B. To examine item functioning and revise weak items
Rationale: Pilot testing helps identify poorly functioning items before the test is finalized.
31. Item response theory differs from classical test theory in that IRT:
A. Cannot be used in test development
B. Focuses on item-level functioning in relation to latent trait level
C. Rejects the concept of measurement error
D. Makes standardization unnecessary
✅Answer: B. Focuses on item-level functioning in relation to latent trait level
Rationale: IRT models item performance as a function of the examinee’s latent trait level and
item parameters.
32. Alfred Binet is most closely associated with:
A. The development of the first widely influential intelligence test for identifying children
needing educational support
B. The first projective inkblot method
C. The Minnesota Multiphasic Personality Inventory
D. The first behavior checklist for adults
✅Answer: A. The development of the first widely influential intelligence test for identifying
children needing educational support
Rationale: Binet is historically associated with early intelligence testing for educational
placement and support.
33. Charles Spearman proposed:
A. Multiple intelligences with no general factor
B. A general intelligence factor, g
C. Triarchic intelligence theory
D. Emotional intelligence as the sole basis of success
✅Answer: B. A general intelligence factor, g
Rationale: Spearman proposed that performance across cognitive tasks reflects a general
factor, g, along with specific factors.
34. Which best captures the Flynn effect?
A. Intelligence is determined solely by heredity
B. Average intelligence test scores have risen across generations in many populations
C. IQ tests are entirely culture free
D. Older adults always score lower than younger adults on all cognitive tasks
✅Answer: B. Average intelligence test scores have risen across generations in many
populations
Rationale: The Flynn effect describes generational gains in measured intelligence test
performance in many settings.
35. Deviation IQ differs from ratio IQ because deviation IQ is based on:
A. Mental age divided by chronological age
B. Relative standing within an age-based normative group
C. Number correct multiplied by 100
D. Performance on verbal items only
✅Answer: B. Relative standing within an age-based normative group
Rationale: Deviation IQ reflects where an individual stands relative to age peers in a
standardized distribution.
36. A major advantage of individually administered intelligence tests is that they:
A. Require no trained examiner
B. Allow detailed observation of test-taking behavior
C. Are always cheaper than group tests
D. Eliminate examiner effects
✅Answer: B. Allow detailed observation of test-taking behavior
Rationale: Individually administered tests permit close observation of effort, strategy,
frustration tolerance, impulsivity, and qualitative behavior.
37. Which is a key interpretive caution in intelligence testing?
A. IQ scores should be interpreted without regard to language or culture
B. One score alone should determine a child’s educational placement
C. Test results should be integrated with background, behavior, and referral context
D. Valid intelligence tests never need revision
✅Answer: C. Test results should be integrated with background, behavior, and referral
context
Rationale: Best practice requires integrating scores with relevant history, context, and
observations rather than treating scores as self-sufficient.
38. Achievement tests are designed primarily to measure:
A. Capacity to learn with future training
B. Acquired knowledge or skills
C. Unconscious conflict
D. Temperament
✅Answer: B. Acquired knowledge or skills
Rationale: Achievement tests assess what has been learned or mastered.
39. Aptitude tests are intended primarily to estimate:
A. Current mastery only
B. Potential for future learning or performance
C. Mood state
D. Response bias
✅Answer: B. Potential for future learning or performance
Rationale: Aptitude tests aim to estimate probable future performance or trainability rather
than current mastery alone.
40. In educational assessment, Response to Intervention is most closely associated with:
A. Replacing all standardized testing
B. Using tiered supports and monitoring student response before high-stakes classification
C. Measuring only personality traits
D. Eliminating teacher judgment
✅Answer: B. Using tiered supports and monitoring student response before high-stakes
classification
Rationale: RtI emphasizes progressive interventions and monitoring response to guide
educational decisions.
41. Dynamic assessment differs from traditional static testing because it:
A. Avoids all teaching during assessment
B. Focuses on learning process and responsiveness to assistance
C. Uses only objective personality inventories
D. Is norm-referenced by definition
✅Answer: B. Focuses on learning process and responsiveness to assistance
Rationale: Dynamic assessment evaluates how a person learns when provided prompts,
mediation, or teaching.
