42. A psychoeducational battery is most appropriate when the referral question concerns:
A. Employment motivation only
B. The relationship among cognitive, achievement, and processing variables in learning
C. Marital conflict only
D. Consumer preferences
✅Answer: B. The relationship among cognitive, achievement, and processing variables in
learning
Rationale: Psychoeducational batteries are used to understand learning strengths,
weaknesses, and educational needs.
43. Personality assessment is concerned with:
A. Temporary neurological impairment only
B. Characteristic patterns of thinking, feeling, and behaving
C. Academic achievement only
D. Visual-motor coordination only
✅Answer: B. Characteristic patterns of thinking, feeling, and behaving
Rationale: Personality assessment focuses on enduring or characteristic ways of functioning
across situations.
44. Objective personality measures are called “objective” mainly because they:
A. Have no scoring rules
B. Use structured stimuli and standardized scoring procedures
C. Never rely on self-report
D. Cannot be faked
✅Answer: B. Use structured stimuli and standardized scoring procedures
Rationale: Objective personality tests are “objective” mainly because administration and
scoring are structured and standardized.
45. Projective techniques are based on the assumption that:
A. Highly structured items yield the richest personality data
B. Responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying needs, conflicts, or themes
C. Intelligence and personality are identical
D. Only children can be assessed validly
✅Answer: B. Responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying needs, conflicts, or
themes
Rationale: Projective techniques rest on the idea that people impose meaning on ambiguous
stimuli in psychologically informative ways.
46. Which test is most strongly associated with inkblot stimuli?
A. Thematic Apperception Test
B. Rorschach
C. MMPI
D. CPI
✅Answer: B. Rorschach
Rationale: The Rorschach uses inkblot stimuli and is one of the best-known projective
methods.
47. Which assessment method is most directly behaviorally anchored?
A. Direct observation with antecedent-behavior-consequence recording
B. Free association
C. Word association only
D. Unstructured autobiography only
✅Answer: A. Direct observation with antecedent-behavior-consequence recording
Rationale: Behavioral assessment is grounded in direct observation and functional analysis of
observable behavior.
48. A major advantage of behavioral assessment is that it:
A. Focuses on observable behavior in context
B. Eliminates reactivity in all settings
C. Requires no operational definitions
D. Is always superior to all other methods
✅Answer: A. Focuses on observable behavior in context
Rationale: Behavioral assessment is valued for linking behavior to real-world antecedents
and consequences.
49. The Barnum effect refers to the tendency of clients to:
A. Resist all feedback
B. Accept vague, general statements as uniquely descriptive
C. Underreport symptoms
D. Score randomly on tests
✅Answer: B. Accept vague, general statements as uniquely descriptive
Rationale: The Barnum effect explains why generic personality feedback can feel personally
accurate.
50. In clinical assessment, mechanical prediction refers to:
A. Judgment made only by machines with no formulas
B. Combining data according to explicit rules or statistical procedures
C. Intuition based on long experience
D. Diagnosis based solely on interview rapport
✅Answer: B. Combining data according to explicit rules or statistical procedures
Rationale: Mechanical prediction uses predetermined formulas or rules rather than intuition
alone.
51. Which is a core purpose of the clinical interview?
A. To replace all test data
B. To gather relevant history, current concerns, and behavioral observations
C. To generate percentile ranks
D. To establish item difficulty
✅Answer: B. To gather relevant history, current concerns, and behavioral observations
Rationale: The interview is fundamental for understanding presenting problems, context,
history, and observable behavior.
52. A culturally informed assessment is most likely to require the examiner to:
A. Ignore cultural variables to preserve objectivity
B. Interpret all behaviors according to the examiner’s own norms
C. Consider language, acculturation, context, and cultural meaning in interpretation
D. Use only translated tests regardless of quality
✅Answer: C. Consider language, acculturation, context, and cultural meaning in
interpretation
Rationale: Culturally informed assessment requires attention to cultural identity, context,
language, and the meaning of behavior and scores.
53. Which is the best example of a forensic assessment role?
A. School guidance about study habits
B. Court-related evaluation of competency or custody
C. Routine career counseling
D. Customer satisfaction surveying
✅Answer: B. Court-related evaluation of competency or custody
Rationale: Forensic assessment involves evaluations for legal purposes such as competency,
criminal responsibility, or custody.
54. In suicide assessment, the most immediate priority is to determine:
A. The client’s favorite coping style
B. Current risk factors such as intent, plan, means, and history
C. The client’s IQ classification
D. Whether the client likes the therapist
✅Answer: B. Current risk factors such as intent, plan, means, and history
Rationale: In suicide assessment, immediate risk determination is critical for safety planning
and intervention.
55. Neuropsychological assessment is most directly concerned with:
A. Measuring only personality disorders
B. The relationship between brain functioning and behavior
C. Replacing neurological examination
D. Vocational matching only
✅Answer: B. The relationship between brain functioning and behavior
Rationale: Neuropsychological assessment examines cognitive and behavioral
consequences of brain functioning or dysfunction.
56. Which finding most strongly suggests the need for neuropsychological evaluation?
A. A desire to change jobs
B. Cognitive decline following head injury
C. Mild shyness in new groups
D. Interest in personality testing
✅Answer: B. Cognitive decline following head injury
Rationale: Cognitive decline after neurological insult is a classic indication for
neuropsychological evaluation.
57. Executive functions are most closely related to:
A. Basic visual acuity only
B. Planning, inhibition, mental flexibility, and problem solving
C. Finger dexterity alone
D. Hearing threshold
✅Answer: B. Planning, inhibition, mental flexibility, and problem solving
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order control processes used for organized
goal-directed behavior.
58. A neuropsychological battery is especially useful because it:
A. Assesses patterns across multiple cognitive domains
B. Eliminates the need for history taking
C. Can diagnose all psychiatric disorders by itself
D. Is culture-free
✅Answer: A. Assesses patterns across multiple cognitive domains
Rationale: A battery allows pattern analysis across domains such as memory, language,
executive function, and visuospatial skills.
59. In career assessment, interest inventories are most useful for:
A. Measuring current psychosis
B. Identifying preferred activity patterns and occupational themes
C. Diagnosing neurocognitive disorder
D. Assessing malingering
✅Answer: B. Identifying preferred activity patterns and occupational themes
Rationale: Interest inventories are used to identify areas and activities a person is likely to
find engaging.
60. Measures of aptitude in occupational settings are primarily used to:
A. Assess unconscious wishes
B. Estimate potential for training or job performance
C. Replace interviews in every hiring decision
D. Measure organizational climate
✅Answer: B. Estimate potential for training or job performance
Rationale: Occupational aptitude measures are used to estimate probable success in training
or work tasks.
61. In personnel selection, validity generalization refers to the finding that:
A. All tests are equally valid for all jobs
B. Validity evidence for some predictors may generalize across similar settings
C. Criterion validity is unnecessary
D. Interviews are always invalid
✅Answer: B. Validity evidence for some predictors may generalize across similar settings
Rationale: Validity generalization examines whether predictor validity found in one setting
applies across comparable jobs or contexts.
62. Which best describes incremental validity?
A. The extent to which a new predictor improves decision accuracy beyond existing
information
B. The increase in score from one grade level to another
C. The percentage of easy items on a test
D. The degree of face validity
✅Answer: A. The extent to which a new predictor improves decision accuracy beyond
existing information
Rationale: Incremental validity asks whether an added measure contributes useful predictive
information beyond what is already known.
63. A structured employment interview is generally preferred over an unstructured one because
it:
A. Is less vulnerable to bias and increases consistency
B. Requires less preparation
C. Guarantees no legal challenge
D. Eliminates the need for job analysis
✅Answer: A. Is less vulnerable to bias and increases consistency
Rationale: Structured interviews improve standardization and help reduce irrelevant
interviewer variability.
64. Job analysis is important in personnel testing because it:
A. Identifies the work-related knowledge, skills, abilities, and characteristics relevant to the
job
B. Replaces validation studies
C. Makes all applicants equal
D. Prevents faking on personality tests
✅Answer: A. Identifies the work-related knowledge, skills, abilities, and characteristics
relevant to the job
Rationale: Job analysis links selection procedures to actual job demands, supporting validity
and defensibility.
65. Which of the following best distinguishes reliability from validity?
A. Reliability concerns usefulness; validity concerns score consistency
B. Reliability concerns score consistency; validity concerns whether the intended inference is
supported
C. Reliability and validity are identical
D. Validity is easier to establish when reliability is low
✅Answer: B. Reliability concerns score consistency; validity concerns whether the intended
inference is supported
Rationale: Reliability is about consistency of scores, while validity concerns whether
interpretation and use of scores are justified.
66. A test may be highly reliable but invalid when it:
A. Consistently measures the wrong construct
B. Produces variable results across administrations
C. Has too few items to score
D. Uses standardized instructions
✅Answer: A. Consistently measures the wrong construct
Rationale: A test can yield highly consistent scores while still failing to measure what it is
supposed to measure.
67. Which scenario best illustrates criterion contamination?
A. The predictor and criterion are measured years apart
B. The criterion includes information derived from the predictor itself
C. The test has low internal consistency
D. The examiner follows the manual closely
✅Answer: B. The criterion includes information derived from the predictor itself
Rationale: Criterion contamination occurs when the criterion is not independent and is
influenced by the predictor or knowledge of predictor scores.
68. Which statement about norms is most accurate?
A. Norms never become outdated
B. Norms should be based on a sample relevant to the intended population
C. Local norms are always superior to national norms
D. Norms are unnecessary for intelligence tests
✅Answer: B. Norms should be based on a sample relevant to the intended population
Rationale: Norms are only meaningful when the normative sample matches the population for
whom interpretations will be made.
69. A psychologist notices that a client’s verbal score is much lower than expected because the
client is not proficient in the test language. The best conclusion is that:
A. The score should be interpreted normally because standardization controls everything
B. Language factors may limit the validity of the interpretation
C. Reliability automatically compensates for language limitations
D. The client likely has low general intelligence
✅Answer: B. Language factors may limit the validity of the interpretation
Rationale: When language proficiency affects performance, the score may not represent the
intended construct accurately.
70. Which is the best example of situational assessment in personality or behavioral evaluation?
A. Asking about childhood memories only
B. Observing the person in a role-play relevant to the referral problem
C. Scoring a norm table
D. Computing a z score
✅Answer: B. Observing the person in a role-play relevant to the referral problem
Rationale: Situational assessment uses behavior in a standardized or semi-standardized
relevant situation to infer functioning.
71. The MMPI is best classified as a:
A. Projective technique
B. Structured objective personality inventory
C. Pure aptitude measure
D. Neuropsychological battery
✅Answer: B. Structured objective personality inventory
Rationale: The MMPI is a standardized, structured self-report personality inventory, not a
projective test.
72. A client endorses extreme symptom items indiscriminately, suggesting exaggerated
responding. The examiner should be most concerned with:
A. Test security
B. Response validity
C. Ratio IQ
D. Nominal scaling
✅Answer: B. Response validity
Rationale: Indiscriminate endorsement raises concern that the profile may not validly reflect
actual symptoms or traits.
73. Which statement about test security is most accurate?
A. Test materials may be freely shared online if done for educational purposes
B. Protecting test materials helps preserve the integrity of assessment procedures
C. Raw scores should routinely be posted publicly
D. Security matters only for intelligence tests
✅Answer: B. Protecting test materials helps preserve the integrity of assessment
procedures
Rationale: Test security prevents compromise of items, procedures, and interpretations,
thereby protecting validity and fairness.
74. Which professional issue is most directly raised when a practitioner uses a test beyond their
training?
A. Norm obsolescence
B. Boundary of competence
C. Percentile interpretation
D. Utility analysis
✅Answer: B. Boundary of competence
Rationale: Using a test beyond one’s education, training, and competence raises a direct
competence issue.
75. A psychometrician is asked to conduct psychotherapy independently in a non-emergency
situation. Under RA 10029-aligned ethical boundaries, the most appropriate response is to:
A. Proceed if the client agrees
B. Proceed if supervised informally by any mental health worker
C. Decline and refer or coordinate appropriately because therapy is outside the usual
psychometrician scope
D. Proceed only if the fee is low
✅Answer: C. Decline and refer or coordinate appropriately because therapy is outside the
usual psychometrician scope
Rationale: Psychometricians generally do not independently practice psychotherapy except
under limited emergency circumstances; ethical practice requires staying within lawful scope
and arranging appropriate referral or coordination.
76. A psychometrician administers assessment tools in a setting where a registered
psychologist is the supervising professional when applicable. This is most consistent with:
A. Violating professional boundaries
B. Practicing within legally defined scope
C. Ignoring RA 10029
D. Unauthorized independent diagnosis by anyone
✅Answer: B. Practicing within legally defined scope
Rationale: Administering assessment within RA 10029-aligned boundaries and under a
registered psychologist’s supervision when applicable reflects lawful, ethical practice.
77. Which statement best reflects ethical informed consent in assessment?
A. It is required only when the client asks for it
B. It includes explaining the nature and purpose of assessment, risks, and limits of
confidentiality
C. It is unnecessary when tests are standardized
D. It applies only to therapy, not testing
✅Answer: B. It includes explaining the nature and purpose of assessment, risks, and limits
of confidentiality
Rationale: Informed consent is meaningful only when the client understands what will
happen, why, possible risks, and how information will be used.
78. Before recording an assessment feedback session, the practitioner should:
A. Record automatically because documentation is useful
B. Obtain consent from the client or legal representative
C. Ask the receptionist to decide
D. Record only the audio but not the image without consent
✅Answer: B. Obtain consent from the client or legal representative
Rationale: Recording voices or images in professional work requires prior informed consent,
except for limited lawful exceptions.
79. Which action is most ethical when an interpreter is needed during assessment?
A. Use any available bilingual person without further concern
B. Ensure confidentiality and discuss limitations of the obtained data
C. Avoid documenting interpreter involvement
D. Ignore the effect of translation on interpretation
✅Answer: B. Ensure confidentiality and discuss limitations of the obtained data
Rationale: Interpreter use introduces confidentiality and validity concerns, so these must be
managed explicitly.
80. A psychologist is asked by a school administrator to release a student’s raw test responses
to unqualified staff for “faster decision-making.” The best response is to:
A. Release all materials immediately
B. Release only if the staff promise confidentiality
C. Decline because raw test data should be protected from unqualified persons except as
legally required
D. Post the summary in a group chat for transparency
✅Answer: C. Decline because raw test data should be protected from unqualified persons
except as legally required
Rationale: Raw test data and protocols must be safeguarded to protect test security,
confidentiality, and proper interpretation.
81. Which is the most ethical response when outdated or obsolete tests have been used?
A. Interpret them confidently if the client insists
B. Base conclusions solely on those scores
C. Avoid relying on obsolete tests or outdated results for current conclusions
D. Use them as long as they are easy to administer
✅Answer: C. Avoid relying on obsolete tests or outdated results for current conclusions
Rationale: Ethical assessment requires avoiding conclusions based on obsolete instruments
or stale results that no longer support current inference.
82. When providing services through telepsychology or teleassessment, practitioners should:
A. Assume ethics are less strict online
B. Apply the same core ethical principles that govern face-to-face services
C. Ignore internet-related risks
D. Avoid informed consent because sessions are remote
✅Answer: B. Apply the same core ethical principles that govern face-to-face services
Rationale: Telepsychology and teleassessment remain subject to the same core ethical
standards, with added attention to technology-related risks.
83. A court orders an evaluation. Ethically, the examinee should be informed:
A. Only of the test schedule
B. That the service is mandated and that confidentiality may be limited
C. That the results will always remain fully private
D. That they may choose any diagnosis
✅Answer: B. That the service is mandated and that confidentiality may be limited
Rationale: When services are court ordered, the examinee must understand the mandated
nature of the evaluation and the limits of confidentiality.
84. Which is the best example of a multiple relationship that may impair objectivity?
A. Testing a stranger referred by a physician
B. Evaluating your close friend’s child for a contested custody case
C. Referring a client to a neurologist
D. Using standardized instructions
✅Answer: B. Evaluating your close friend’s child for a contested custody case
Rationale: This situation presents a substantial risk of impaired objectivity and role conflict
due to a personal relationship.
85. A practitioner becomes aware that personal stress is significantly impairing concentration
during evaluations. The most ethical action is to:
A. Continue working and conceal the problem
B. Increase caseload to build tolerance
C. Seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting duties
D. Let clients decide whether the work is acceptable
✅Answer: C. Seek consultation or assistance and consider limiting duties
Rationale: When personal problems interfere with competence, ethical practice requires
addressing the issue and protecting clients from compromised service.
86. Which statement best reflects ethical assessment tool selection?
A. Use the longest battery available for every case
B. Select only tests directly relevant to the referral question and appropriate for the client
C. Prefer familiar tests even if unsupported
D. Use photocopied materials if originals are costly
✅Answer: B. Select only tests directly relevant to the referral question and appropriate for
the client
Rationale: Ethical assessment requires relevance, appropriateness, and parsimony rather
than routine overtesting.
87. Which of the following best reflects culturally competent interpretation?
A. Scores should be interpreted without regard to contextual factors
B. Cultural and situational factors may influence meaning and should be considered in
conclusions
C. Norms override all cultural concerns
D. Translation alone ensures validity
✅Answer: B. Cultural and situational factors may influence meaning and should be
considered in conclusions
Rationale: Culturally competent interpretation recognizes that context affects performance
and meaning.
88. A psychologist issues a public claim on social media that their test “guarantees success in
work and relationships.” This is most clearly:
A. Acceptable advertising
B. A deceptive public statement
C. Required marketing language
D. Protected because it is online
✅Answer: B. A deceptive public statement
Rationale: Claims of guaranteed outcomes are misleading and inconsistent with truthful,
accurate professional communication.
89. Which is the best reason confidentiality may sometimes be limited?
A. Because practitioners own all client information
B. Because disclosure may be mandated by law or necessary to prevent harm
C. Because family members are always entitled to records
D. Because test publishers require disclosure
✅Answer: B. Because disclosure may be mandated by law or necessary to prevent harm
Rationale: Confidentiality is fundamental but not absolute; lawful mandates and serious risk
situations can justify limited disclosure.
90. In reporting assessment results, the clearest ethical principle is that practitioners should:
A. Use highly technical language even for lay recipients
B. Report without regard to test limitations
C. Communicate findings accurately and appropriately for the audience
D. Share every note and raw response with everyone involved
✅Answer: C. Communicate findings accurately and appropriately for the audience
Rationale: Ethical feedback and reporting require accuracy, clarity, and adaptation of
language to the recipient’s level of understanding.
91. A student’s score falls two standard deviations below the mean on a normally distributed
measure. This score is approximately:
A. At the 50th percentile
B. In the lower extreme relative to the norm group
C. Above average
D. Uninterpretable by definition
✅Answer: B. In the lower extreme relative to the norm group
Rationale: A score two standard deviations below the mean is typically well below average
and falls in the lower extreme portion of the distribution.
92. Which situation best illustrates criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. Comparing an applicant with the national norm sample
B. Determining whether a trainee met a predefined competency standard
C. Ranking students from highest to lowest
D. Computing a z score from a norm table
✅Answer: B. Determining whether a trainee met a predefined competency standard
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation compares performance against a defined
standard rather than against other examinees.
93. An examiner wants to know whether a reading screening test yields similar classifications
when scored by two trained raters. The most relevant index is:
A. Inter-rater reliability
B. Predictive validity
C. Face validity
D. Utility coefficient
✅Answer: A. Inter-rater reliability
Rationale: When the concern is agreement between raters or scorers, inter-rater reliability is
the relevant index.
94. Which of the following is the best example of convergent evidence for construct validity?
A. An anxiety measure correlates positively with other measures of anxiety
B. An anxiety measure shows a neat cover page
C. The test manual is detailed
D. The items are easy to read
✅Answer: A. An anxiety measure correlates positively with other measures of anxiety
Rationale: Convergent evidence is shown when measures that should be related actually
correlate.
95. Which would most strongly threaten the validity of an interpretation from a timed cognitive
test delivered online?
A. Standardized instructions
B. Stable internet and quiet environment
C. Significant connectivity interruptions during timed subtests
D. Use of original digital materials
✅Answer: C. Significant connectivity interruptions during timed subtests
Rationale: Timed online cognitive testing depends on stable connectivity; interruptions can
undermine score meaning and comparability.
96. In a selection setting, a low base rate for successful employees generally means that:
A. Even a valid predictor may yield fewer correct positive decisions than expected
B. Validity is irrelevant
C. The Taylor-Russell approach cannot be discussed
D. Interviews become perfectly accurate
✅Answer: A. Even a valid predictor may yield fewer correct positive decisions than
expected
Rationale: With a low base rate, many applicants may fail despite valid predictors, affecting
practical utility and decision outcomes.
97. Which pair is correctly matched?
A. Binet — g factor only
B. Spearman — general intelligence factor
C. Wechsler — projective storytelling method
D. Rorschach — self-report personality inventory
✅Answer: B. Spearman — general intelligence factor
Rationale: Spearman is correctly associated with the general intelligence factor, g.
98. Which statement about assessment conclusions is most defensible?
A. Test scores alone are always sufficient for diagnosis
B. Assessment conclusions should rest on substantial information and appropriate methods
C. Clinical judgment should ignore data when experience is strong
D. Raw scores are more meaningful than integrated interpretation
✅Answer: B. Assessment conclusions should rest on substantial information and
appropriate methods
Rationale: Defensible conclusions require adequate information, sound methods, and careful
interpretation rather than narrow reliance on any single source.
99. A practitioner is asked to give an expert opinion about a person without conducting an
examination and based only on old records. The most ethical response is to:
A. Give definitive conclusions without qualification
B. State the limitations of the opinion and basis of any conclusions
C. Refuse to mention limitations to preserve authority
D. Replace records with intuition
✅Answer: B. State the limitations of the opinion and basis of any conclusions
Rationale: When no direct examination has been conducted, ethical practice requires caution
and explicit acknowledgment of limitations.
100. Which statement best reflects high-quality board exam reasoning in psychological
assessment?
A. The best answer is usually the most absolute statement
B. Sound assessment requires integrating psychometric evidence, referral context, ethics,
and professional judgment
C. Memorization is enough for all applied cases
D. One test can answer every referral question
✅Answer: B. Sound assessment requires integrating psychometric evidence, referral
context, ethics, and professional judgment
Rationale: High-level assessment reasoning does not rely on isolated facts alone. It
synthesizes reliability, validity, appropriateness, context, culture, ethics, and judgment in
answering the referral question.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 10
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 10
1. Which statement best distinguishes psychological testing from psychological assessment?
A. Testing and assessment are exactly synonymous in professional practice.
B. Testing refers only to intelligence measures, whereas assessment refers only to personality
measures.
C. Testing is one tool within the broader process of assessment.
D. Assessment is limited to informal judgment, whereas testing is always standardized.
✅Answer: C. Testing is one tool within the broader process of assessment.
Rationale: Assessment is a comprehensive process that integrates multiple sources of
information, while testing refers specifically to the use of standardized instruments within that
broader process.
2. A psychometrician is asked to summarize a client’s performance using raw scores from
several unrelated tests. Which is the best reason this is inappropriate?
A. Raw scores are always normally distributed.
B. Raw scores from different tests are often not directly comparable.
C. Raw scores are more valid than standard scores.
D. Raw scores eliminate measurement error.
✅Answer: B. Raw scores from different tests are often not directly comparable.
Rationale: Raw scores are test-specific and lack a common scale, making comparisons
across different tests invalid without standardization.
3. A school guidance office wants to compare a student’s mathematics performance with that of
same-age peers nationwide. Which score is most useful?
A. Raw score
B. Percentile rank
C. Frequency count
D. Item difficulty index
✅Answer: B. Percentile rank
Rationale: Percentile rank indicates an individual’s relative standing within a norm group,
allowing direct comparison with peers.
4. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Median
B. Mode
C. Mean
D. Interquartile range
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean incorporates all values in a distribution and is therefore most influenced
by extreme scores or outliers.
5. In a negatively skewed distribution of test scores, the mean is usually:
A. higher than the median
B. equal to the mode in all cases
C. lower than the median
D. unaffected by the skew
✅Answer: C. lower than the median
Rationale: In a negatively skewed distribution, extreme low scores pull the mean downward,
making it lower than the median.
6. A psychologist wants to know how consistently two raters score the same set of essay
responses. The most relevant reliability evidence is:
A. test-retest reliability
B. alternate-forms reliability
C. interscorer reliability
D. criterion-related validity
✅Answer: C. interscorer reliability
Rationale: Interscorer reliability evaluates the degree of agreement between different raters
scoring the same material.
7. Which situation is the clearest example of random measurement error?
A. A test systematically underestimates the ability of one language group
B. A poorly worded item confuses almost all examinees
C. A testtaker guesses correctly on some difficult items by chance
D. A test publisher intentionally excludes difficult items
✅Answer: C. A testtaker guesses correctly on some difficult items by chance
Rationale: Random error involves unpredictable fluctuations, such as guessing, which may
artificially raise or lower scores.
8. A test yields highly consistent scores over repeated administrations, but it does not measure
the trait it claims to measure. This test is:
A. valid but unreliable
B. reliable but not valid
C. neither reliable nor valid because reliability guarantees validity
D. fair because consistency is the only psychometric requirement
✅Answer: B. reliable but not valid
Rationale: A test can be consistent (reliable) but still fail to measure the intended construct,
meaning it lacks validity.
9. Which statement about validity is most accurate?
A. Validity is a property of a test that never changes across uses
B. Validity refers to the consistency of test scores across time
C. Validity concerns the appropriateness of interpretations made from test scores
D. Validity is established once face validity is demonstrated
✅Answer: C. Validity concerns the appropriateness of interpretations made from test scores
Rationale: Validity focuses on how well test scores support intended interpretations in a
specific context.
10. A licensure exam committee asks subject matter experts to judge whether test items
adequately sample the domain of required knowledge and skills. This primarily provides
evidence of:
A. content validity
B. predictive validity
C. concurrent validity
D. interrater reliability
✅Answer: A. content validity
Rationale: Content validity is established through expert judgment that test items represent
the intended domain.
11. A company uses an aptitude test to predict which applicants will successfully complete a
six-month training program. The correlation between test scores and later training grades is
evidence of:
A. face validity
B. predictive validity
C. content validity
D. split-half reliability
✅Answer: B. predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity is demonstrated when test scores accurately forecast future
performance.
12. A depression inventory correlates strongly with other established depression measures and
weakly with unrelated constructs such as spatial ability. This pattern most strongly supports:
A. construct validity
B. face validity
C. test-retest reliability
D. utility analysis
✅Answer: A. construct validity
Rationale: Construct validity is supported by convergence with similar measures and
divergence from unrelated constructs.
13. Which statement best reflects the relationship between reliability and validity?
A. A test can be valid even if it is completely unreliable
B. Reliability is necessary but not sufficient for validity
C. Validity is necessary but not sufficient for reliability
D. Reliability and validity are identical concepts
✅Answer: B. Reliability is necessary but not sufficient for validity
Rationale: A test must be reliable to be valid, but reliability alone does not ensure it measures
the intended construct.
14. The standard error of measurement is most useful for:
A. converting raw scores to percentiles
B. estimating the range within which a person’s true score likely falls
C. identifying cultural bias in test items
D. computing item discrimination
✅Answer: B. estimating the range within which a person’s true score likely falls
Rationale: SEM quantifies the amount of error in measurement and helps estimate a
confidence range around the true score.
15. Which item would generally be considered too easy for a selection test designed to
differentiate high-performing applicants?
A. An item answered correctly by 98% of examinees
B. An item answered correctly by 55% of examinees
C. An item answered correctly by 48% of examinees
D. An item answered correctly by 52% of examinees
✅Answer: A. An item answered correctly by 98% of examinees
Rationale: Items that nearly all examinees answer correctly provide little discrimination among
high-performing individuals.
16. An item discriminates well when it:
A. is answered correctly by everyone
B. is answered correctly by almost no one
C. distinguishes high scorers from low scorers on the total test
D. produces a negatively skewed total score distribution
✅Answer: C. distinguishes high scorers from low scorers on the total test
Rationale: Good discrimination means the item differentiates between stronger and weaker
examinees.
17. A test developer revises items after pilot testing because several distractors are never
chosen. The best justification is that:
A. nonfunctioning distractors reduce item effectiveness
B. distractors should always be equally difficult as the keyed answer
C. distractors must be absurd to improve validity
D. rarely chosen distractors increase discrimination
✅Answer: A. nonfunctioning distractors reduce item effectiveness
Rationale: Distractors that are never selected do not function effectively in distinguishing
between examinees.
18. Which practice is most consistent with sound test construction?
A. Writing items before defining the construct
B. Defining the construct and intended use before item writing
C. Standardizing the test before tryout administration
D. Choosing a scoring key based only on examiner preference
✅Answer: B. Defining the construct and intended use before item writing
Rationale: Clear definition of the construct ensures that items are relevant and aligned with
the test’s purpose.
19. In norm-referenced interpretation, an examinee’s score is understood primarily in relation to:
A. a fixed mastery standard
B. a criterion domain of performance
C. the performance of a relevant reference group
D. the examiner’s clinical judgment alone
✅Answer: C. the performance of a relevant reference group
Rationale: Norm-referenced interpretation compares an individual’s score to that of a defined
group.
20. A certification body wants to determine whether each examinee has met a minimum
competency standard, regardless of how others perform. The most appropriate framework is:
A. norm-referenced testing
B. criterion-referenced testing
C. ipsative assessment
D. projective assessment
✅Answer: B. criterion-referenced testing
Rationale: Criterion-referenced testing evaluates whether an individual meets predefined
performance standards.
21. Which statement best reflects a major concern in developing norms?
A. Any large sample automatically produces appropriate norms
B. Norms are useful only for intelligence tests
C. The norm group must be relevant to the population for whom the test will be used
D. Local norms are always inferior to national norms
✅Answer: C. The norm group must be relevant to the population for whom the test will be
used
Rationale: Norms must accurately represent the population to ensure valid interpretation.
22. A psychologist uses a translated test with clients from a different cultural group without
checking language equivalence, normative appropriateness, or construct relevance. The
primary psychometric concern is:
A. halo effect
B. test fairness
C. ipsative scoring
D. acquiescence
✅Answer: B. test fairness
Rationale: Using tests without ensuring cultural and linguistic appropriateness threatens
fairness and validity of interpretations.
23. Which is the best example of a fixed reference group scoring system?
A. Percentile ranks based on current local norms
B. Age norms based on annually updated samples
C. Standard scores based on a previously defined reference group
D. Criterion cut scores set by expert judges
✅Answer: C. Standard scores based on a previously defined reference group
Rationale: Fixed reference group scoring uses a specific, established norm group for
comparison.
24. A counselor says, “This test must be excellent because the items look relevant.” This
statement overvalues:
A. predictive validity
B. face validity
C. content validity
D. criterion contamination
✅Answer: B. face validity
Rationale: Face validity refers only to the apparent relevance of items, not actual evidence of
validity.
25. The view that intelligence reflects a general mental ability underlying performance across
many tasks is most closely associated with:
A. Spearman
B. Skinner
C. Maslow
D. Rogers
✅Answer: A. Spearman
Rationale: Spearman proposed the concept of general intelligence (g) underlying
performance across tasks.
26. Which statement best captures a modern perspective on intelligence?
A. Intelligence is universally agreed to be a single simple trait
B. Intelligence has been conceptualized in multiple ways, including general and multifactor
models
C. Intelligence cannot be measured at all
D. Intelligence tests measure only acquired school knowledge
✅Answer: B. Intelligence has been conceptualized in multiple ways, including general and
multifactor models
Rationale: Contemporary views recognize multiple theoretical models of intelligence,
including general intelligence and multifactor approaches.
27. Alfred Binet’s early work was most directly associated with:
A. constructing projective personality tests
B. identifying children needing educational assistance
C. developing behavior therapy techniques
D. creating the first neuropsychological battery
✅Answer: B. identifying children needing educational assistance
Rationale: Binet developed early intelligence tests to identify children who required special
educational support.
28. Which statement about IQ is most accurate?
A. IQ is a pure measure of innate ability unaffected by context
B. IQ scores are interpreted without reference to norms
C. IQ scores are derived through standardized comparison with a reference group
D. IQ scores are identical to percentile ranks
✅Answer: C. IQ scores are derived through standardized comparison with a reference
group
Rationale: IQ scores are meaningful only when interpreted relative to standardized norms.
29. A child shows average verbal comprehension but much lower working memory and
processing speed. The most defensible interpretation is:
A. the Full Scale IQ should always be ignored
B. analysis of index-level strengths and weaknesses may be clinically informative
C. the child is malingering
D. intelligence cannot be interpreted when scores differ across subtests
✅Answer: B. analysis of index-level strengths and weaknesses may be clinically informative
Rationale: Variability across cognitive domains can provide important insights into strengths
and weaknesses.
30. Which is the best reason to avoid overinterpreting small differences among subtest scores?
A. Subtests are never valid
B. Score differences may reflect measurement error and normal variability
C. Subtests are always culturally biased
D. Subtests can only be interpreted in group testing
✅Answer: B. Score differences may reflect measurement error and normal variability
Rationale: Small score differences may fall within expected measurement error and should
not be overinterpreted.
31. An examiner assessing a preschool child with limited expressive language would most need
to consider:
A. only the child’s raw scores
B. developmental level, language demands, and test appropriateness
C. whether the child’s parents have college degrees
D. whether the child has taken personality tests before
✅Answer: B. developmental level, language demands, and test appropriateness
Rationale: Assessment must match the child’s developmental and language capabilities to
ensure valid results.
32. In educational assessment, achievement tests are primarily intended to measure:
A. future learning potential only
B. mastery of previously taught knowledge or skills
C. unconscious motives
D. neurological impairment
✅Answer: B. mastery of previously taught knowledge or skills
Rationale: Achievement tests assess what has already been learned through instruction.
33. Aptitude tests are generally used to estimate:
A. current symptom severity
B. potential for future learning or performance
C. honesty in self-report
D. preference for specific occupations only
✅Answer: B. potential for future learning or performance
Rationale: Aptitude tests predict an individual’s capacity to learn or perform in future tasks.
34. Dynamic assessment is distinguished from many traditional approaches because it
emphasizes:
A. fixed scores obtained without examiner interaction
B. learning potential as revealed through mediated assistance
C. projective interpretation of ambiguous stimuli
D. only group-administered school tests
✅Answer: B. learning potential as revealed through mediated assistance
Rationale: Dynamic assessment evaluates how individuals learn when provided with
guidance or support.
35. A teacher uses student work samples collected across the semester to evaluate progress,
strengths, and areas for improvement. This is best described as:
A. ipsative neuropsychological testing
B. portfolio assessment
C. criterion contamination
D. forced-choice personality measurement
✅Answer: B. portfolio assessment
Rationale: Portfolio assessment uses accumulated work samples to evaluate learning over
time.
36. Response to Intervention is most concerned with:
A. assigning labels before any instruction is attempted
B. monitoring students’ progress under increasingly targeted instruction
C. replacing all standardized testing with interviews
D. using only aptitude tests to plan instruction
✅Answer: B. monitoring students’ progress under increasingly targeted instruction
Rationale: RtI focuses on tracking student response to tiered interventions.
37. Which statement best distinguishes objective and projective personality methods?
A. Objective methods always have no scoring rules
B. Projective methods typically use ambiguous stimuli with less structured responding
C. Objective methods cannot assess personality traits
D. Projective methods always have higher validity than objective methods
✅Answer: B. Projective methods typically use ambiguous stimuli with less structured
responding
Rationale: Projective tests rely on ambiguous stimuli to elicit open-ended responses.
38. The MMPI is best known as a:
A. projective measure based on inkblots
B. structured objective personality inventory
C. sensorimotor screening battery
D. pure measure of intellectual giftedness
✅Answer: B. structured objective personality inventory
Rationale: The MMPI is a standardized self-report inventory used to assess personality and
psychopathology.
39. A personality inventory developed by selecting items that distinguish a clinical group from a
nonclinical group reflects which strategy?
A. Rational/content strategy only
B. Criterion-group strategy
C. Projective hypothesis strategy
D. Behavioral observation strategy only
✅Answer: B. Criterion-group strategy
Rationale: This strategy selects items based on their ability to differentiate known groups.
40. A clinician interprets an inventory profile without considering response style, defensiveness,
or exaggeration. The most important weakness is failure to evaluate:
A. item difficulty
B. profile validity
C. ipsative preference
D. standard error of the mean
✅Answer: B. profile validity
Rationale: Evaluating validity scales ensures that the test results reflect genuine responding.
41. The Rorschach and TAT are most similar in that both:
A. are speeded intelligence tests
B. rely on structured true-false responding
C. use relatively ambiguous stimuli to elicit responses
D. are group-administered achievement tests
✅Answer: C. use relatively ambiguous stimuli to elicit responses
Rationale: Both are projective techniques using ambiguous stimuli.
42. A major criticism of projective techniques is that:
A. they can never generate clinically useful hypotheses
B. some applications raise concerns about reliability, validity, and incremental utility
C. they contain no stimuli
D. they are always easier to score than objective tests
✅Answer: B. some applications raise concerns about reliability, validity, and incremental
utility
Rationale: Projective tests have been criticized for limited empirical support in some uses.
43. Behavioral assessment differs from many traditional trait approaches because it focuses
strongly on:
A. global labels without context
B. directly observed behavior and its antecedents and consequences
C. dream symbolism
D. fixed intelligence differences
✅Answer: B. directly observed behavior and its antecedents and consequences
Rationale: Behavioral assessment emphasizes observable actions and environmental factors.
44. Which question is most central in behavioral assessment?
A. What unconscious conflict caused the symptom?
B. What stable type does this person belong to?
C. Under what conditions does the behavior occur, and what maintains it?
D. Which projective sign is most diagnostically pure?
✅Answer: C. Under what conditions does the behavior occur, and what maintains it?
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on functional relationships of behavior.
45. A psychologist conducting a clinical interview should generally:
A. assume interview impressions are always accurate
B. integrate interview data with collateral and test information
C. avoid rapport to reduce bias
D. use only closed-ended questions in every case
✅Answer: B. integrate interview data with collateral and test information
Rationale: Interviews should be combined with other sources to improve accuracy.
46. Case history data are most useful when the clinician remembers that they:
A. can replace all testing
B. should be interpreted in context and corroborated when possible
C. are always objective
D. are irrelevant if a standardized test is available
✅Answer: B. should be interpreted in context and corroborated when possible
Rationale: Case history information may be biased or incomplete and should be verified.
47. A patient gives socially desirable answers throughout a clinical evaluation. Which concept is
most relevant?
A. Criterion contamination
B. Response bias
C. Interquartile range
D. Alternate-forms coefficient
✅Answer: B. Response bias
Rationale: Social desirability is a form of response bias that affects accuracy of self-report.
48. In suicide assessment, which action is most appropriate when there is credible imminent
risk?
A. Promise absolute confidentiality and end the interview
B. Delay intervention until formal testing is completed
C. Take protective action consistent with safety and ethical limits of confidentiality
D. Avoid asking direct questions to prevent suggestion
✅Answer: C. Take protective action consistent with safety and ethical limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Protecting life takes priority, and confidentiality may be limited when there is
imminent danger.
49. Which is the clearest example of the Barnum effect in assessment?
A. A client rejects all feedback from a report
B. A client accepts vague, general personality statements as uniquely accurate
C. A test manual reports high reliability
D. An examiner uses local norms
✅Answer: B. A client accepts vague, general personality statements as uniquely accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect involves accepting generalized statements as personally
meaningful.
50. Mechanical prediction is often contrasted with clinical prediction because mechanical
prediction:
A. ignores all data from tests
B. combines information using explicit rules rather than intuitive judgment alone
C. is always less accurate than clinical judgment
D. can only be used in educational settings
✅Answer: B. combines information using explicit rules rather than intuitive judgment alone
Rationale: Mechanical prediction uses systematic rules to integrate data rather than relying
solely on intuition.
51. A neuropsychological evaluation is most clearly indicated when there is concern about:
A. occupational interests only
B. brain-behavior relationships and cognitive functioning
C. marital satisfaction only
D. response acquiescence on personality scales
✅Answer: B. brain-behavior relationships and cognitive functioning
Rationale: Neuropsychological assessment focuses on how brain functioning relates to
cognition, behavior, and neurological status.
52. Executive function tests are especially relevant when evaluating:
A. visual acuity only
B. planning, set shifting, inhibition, and problem solving
C. reading comprehension only
D. interest congruence
✅Answer: B. planning, set shifting, inhibition, and problem solving
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order cognitive processes such as planning,
flexibility, and inhibition.
53. A patient performs poorly on a memory task, but the clinician fails to consider language
barriers, fatigue, and emotional distress. The main interpretive error is:
A. overreliance on construct validity
B. failure to consider contextual variables affecting performance
C. using too many norms
D. choosing a criterion-referenced score
✅Answer: B. failure to consider contextual variables affecting performance
Rationale: External factors such as language, fatigue, and emotional state can significantly
affect test performance and must be considered.
54. Which statement about neuropsychological batteries is most accurate?
A. They eliminate the need for clinical judgment
B. They may aid systematic evaluation, but results still require integration with history and
observations
C. They are useful only with dementia
D. They are always culture-free
✅Answer: B. They may aid systematic evaluation, but results still require integration with
history and observations
Rationale: Test results must be interpreted alongside clinical history and behavioral
observations.
55. In vocational assessment, interest inventories are most useful for:
A. measuring neurological impairment
B. identifying patterns of occupational preference
C. diagnosing psychosis
D. replacing all aptitude measures
✅Answer: B. identifying patterns of occupational preference
Rationale: Interest inventories help identify preferred activities and career-related inclinations.
56. Which result would most strongly support a career recommendation?
A. High occupational interest only, with no regard for ability or values
B. Consistent convergence of interests, abilities, and relevant personality characteristics
C. One unusually high subtest score from an unrelated measure
D. A counselor’s intuition without data
✅Answer: B. Consistent convergence of interests, abilities, and relevant personality
characteristics
Rationale: Strong career recommendations rely on multiple converging data sources.
57. In personnel selection, a major reason organizations value cognitive ability tests is that they
often:
A. have no legal implications
B. are unrelated to job performance
C. predict training and job performance in many contexts
D. replace the need for structured interviews
✅Answer: C. predict training and job performance in many contexts
Rationale: Cognitive ability tests are widely supported as predictors of job and training
success.
58. Which practice is most defensible in employment testing?
A. Using tests with no evidence of job relevance
B. Selecting measures linked to job analysis and intended decisions
C. Preferring any commercially popular test
D. Rejecting standardized methods in favor of unstructured impressions
✅Answer: B. Selecting measures linked to job analysis and intended decisions
Rationale: Employment testing must be job-relevant and supported by evidence to ensure
fairness and legality.
59. Utility analysis is primarily concerned with:
A. whether a test looks professional
B. whether a test is worth using given costs, benefits, and decision outcomes
C. whether a test correlates with itself
D. whether a test contains enough difficult items
✅Answer: B. whether a test is worth using given costs, benefits, and decision outcomes
Rationale: Utility analysis evaluates the practical value of a test in decision-making contexts.
60. A cutoff score that is set too high in personnel screening may increase:
A. false negatives
B. true negatives only
C. interrater agreement
D. item homogeneity
✅Answer: A. false negatives
Rationale: A high cutoff may exclude qualified candidates, increasing false negatives.
61. Which statement best reflects current understanding of cultural issues in assessment?
A. Fairness is achieved by giving exactly the same test under the same conditions to
everyone
B. Culture is irrelevant if a test has good reliability
C. Assessment should consider language, acculturation, norms, and construct equivalence
D. Test bias and test fairness are identical to item difficulty
✅Answer: C. Assessment should consider language, acculturation, norms, and construct
equivalence
Rationale: Fair assessment requires consideration of cultural and contextual factors affecting
performance.
62. An examiner concludes that a low score necessarily reflects low ability, without considering
limited proficiency in the language of testing. This error most directly reflects:
A. regression to the mean
B. construct underrepresentation
C. invalid inference due to language confounding
D. ipsative interpretation
✅Answer: C. invalid inference due to language confounding
Rationale: Language barriers can distort performance, leading to incorrect conclusions about
ability.
63. Which approach most helps reduce bias in assessment?
A. Using only translated instructions without further adaptation
B. Integrating multiple data sources and considering contextual and cultural factors
C. Ignoring acculturation because it is subjective
D. Using outdated local norms for all groups
✅Answer: B. Integrating multiple data sources and considering contextual and cultural
factors
Rationale: Using diverse data sources and context-aware interpretation reduces bias.
64. Informed consent in assessment primarily requires that the client be told about:
A. only the exact test items in advance
B. the nature and purpose of services, relevant risks, and limits of confidentiality
C. only the fees
D. only the examiner’s credentials
✅Answer: B. the nature and purpose of services, relevant risks, and limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Informed consent ensures clients understand the purpose, procedures, risks, and
limits of confidentiality.
65. Under the PAP Code of Ethics, psychological services delivered through telepsychology are:
A. exempt from ordinary ethical rules because they are online
B. prohibited for assessment purposes
C. governed by the same ethical principles that apply to face-to-face services
D. allowed only for intelligence testing
✅Answer: C. governed by the same ethical principles that apply to face-to-face services
Rationale: Ethical standards apply equally to telepsychology and traditional services.
66. A psychologist receives a court order to release records. Ethically, the most appropriate
response is to:
A. refuse automatically because confidentiality is absolute
B. release all records publicly
C. disclose only information pertinent to the legitimate legal request
D. destroy the file to protect the client
✅Answer: C. disclose only information pertinent to the legitimate legal request
Rationale: Disclosure should be limited to what is necessary and legally required.
67. A clinician discusses an identifiable client case in a public seminar without consent and
without adequately disguising details. This most directly violates:
A. test-retest reliability
B. confidentiality
C. utility analysis
D. predictive validity
✅Answer: B. confidentiality
Rationale: Sharing identifiable client information without consent breaches confidentiality.
68. Under the PAP Code, when using assessment tools, the practitioner should:
A. prefer photocopied materials if cost is lower
B. select only tests pertinent to the referral question and supported by sound psychometric
qualities
C. use any test as long as it is widely known online
D. avoid considering language and client characteristics
✅Answer: B. select only tests pertinent to the referral question and supported by sound
psychometric qualities
Rationale: Ethical practice requires appropriate, valid, and relevant test selection.
69. Which practice is most consistent with ethical release of assessment results?
A. Giving raw scores to any interested school employee
B. Releasing findings only to authorized recipients and explaining results in understandable
language when appropriate
C. Posting results in the waiting area for transparency
D. Allowing unqualified staff to interpret findings
✅Answer: B. Releasing findings only to authorized recipients and explaining results in
understandable language when appropriate
Rationale: Results must be shared responsibly with authorized individuals and explained
clearly.
70. A psychology practitioner becomes aware of a colleague’s ethical violation that is likely to
cause substantial harm. Under the PAP Code, the next step beyond informal resolution may be
to:
A. ignore the matter to preserve collegiality
B. report the violation to appropriate authorities
C. post allegations on social media
D. destroy the evidence
✅Answer: B. report the violation to appropriate authorities
Rationale: Serious ethical violations require formal reporting when informal resolution is
insufficient.
71. A psychometrician independently administers and interprets a projective test without
supervision. Under RA 10029, this is inappropriate primarily because psychometricians are
authorized only for:
A. all psychological services if they have enough experience
B. objective and structured personality tests, excluding projective and other higher-level tests,
under supervision of a licensed psychologist
C. psychotherapy but not testing
D. projective testing with school clients only
✅Answer: B. objective and structured personality tests, excluding projective and other
higher-level tests, under supervision of a licensed psychologist
Rationale: RA 10029 limits psychometricians to specific assessment tasks under supervision
and excludes independent projective testing.
72. Which statement best reflects RA 10029 regarding the practice of psychology and
psychometrics?
A. Any psychology graduate may practice independently without licensure
B. Licensure is required for professional practice, subject to the law’s provisions
C. Only psychologists need licensure, not psychometricians
D. Registration is optional if a person works in a private institution
✅Answer: B. Licensure is required for professional practice, subject to the law’s provisions
Rationale: RA 10029 mandates licensure for professional psychological practice.
73. A registered psychometrician conducts a preparatory intake interview for a client referred for
testing, under the supervision of a licensed psychologist. Under RA 10029, this is:
A. outside the scope of psychometrics
B. allowed as part of authorized functions under supervision
C. allowed only in hospitals
D. prohibited if the interview is written
✅Answer: B. allowed as part of authorized functions under supervision
Rationale: Psychometricians may perform intake functions under supervision as part of their
authorized role.
74. Which situation best illustrates practice within boundaries of competence?
A. Accepting every referral regardless of training
B. Providing services in a new specialty area without consultation or preparation
C. Referring or obtaining supervision when the case exceeds one’s current competence
D. Relying solely on one’s academic degree from many years ago
✅Answer: C. Referring or obtaining supervision when the case exceeds one’s current
competence
Rationale: Ethical practice requires recognizing limits and seeking supervision or referral
when needed.
75. A psychologist is asked to conduct a forensic evaluation but has little knowledge of legal
standards relevant to the case. Ethically, the psychologist should first:
A. proceed immediately because assessment principles are universal
B. become reasonably familiar with the relevant judicial or administrative rules
C. delegate interpretation to the attorney
D. avoid documenting limitations
✅Answer: B. become reasonably familiar with the relevant judicial or administrative rules
Rationale: Practitioners must ensure competence by understanding relevant legal
frameworks before proceeding.
76. Which is the best example of a multiple relationship that could impair objectivity?
A. Testing an anonymous examinee in a standardized setting
B. Assessing a close relative for a high-stakes custody dispute
C. Explaining score results in plain language
D. Using collateral information in a clinical case
✅Answer: B. Assessing a close relative for a high-stakes custody dispute
Rationale: Multiple relationships can impair objectivity and increase risk of bias or conflict of
interest.
77. A psychologist employed by a company is asked to assess an employee at management’s
request. Ethically, which clarification is most important at the outset?
A. The psychologist’s favorite theory of personality
B. Who the client is, the probable uses of the information, and limits of confidentiality
C. The employee’s raw scores from past tests
D. The company’s profit goals
✅Answer: B. Who the client is, the probable uses of the information, and limits of
confidentiality
Rationale: Clarifying roles, purpose, and confidentiality is essential in third-party assessment
situations.
78. Which statement best reflects ethical record handling in the PAP Code?
A. Confidential information may be stored anywhere if the device has a password
B. Confidential information should be safeguarded so that unqualified persons cannot easily
access it
C. Only paper records require protection
D. Digital files are exempt from confidentiality rules
✅Answer: B. Confidential information should be safeguarded so that unqualified persons
cannot easily access it
Rationale: Ethical standards require safeguarding all client information from unauthorized
access.
79. When a client is legally incapable of giving informed consent, the practitioner should
generally:
A. abandon the assessment automatically
B. obtain appropriate permission from a legally authorized person while also seeking the
person’s assent and protecting welfare
C. proceed without explanation because assent is irrelevant
D. give full decision-making authority to any available friend
✅Answer: B. obtain appropriate permission from a legally authorized person while also
seeking the person’s assent and protecting welfare
Rationale: Ethical practice requires substitute consent and respect for the individual’s welfare
and assent.
80. A test administrator subtly nods whenever the examinee appears to be approaching the
correct response. This most directly threatens:
A. standardization of administration
B. criterion validity
C. percentile interpretation
D. content representativeness
✅Answer: A. standardization of administration
Rationale: Unequal cues violate standardized procedures and compromise score validity.
81. Which practice best supports standardization in test administration?
A. Modifying instructions casually to motivate each testtaker
B. Following uniform procedures consistent with the test manual
C. Allowing unlimited prompts during all subtests
D. Scoring according to the examiner’s intuition
✅Answer: B. Following uniform procedures consistent with the test manual
Rationale: Standardization ensures consistency and comparability of test results.
82. Stereotype threat is most likely to affect performance when:
A. examinees believe a negative stereotype about their group is relevant to the task
B. items have high internal consistency
C. the test is individually administered
D. the examiner uses local norms
✅Answer: A. examinees believe a negative stereotype about their group is relevant to the
task
Rationale: Stereotype threat occurs when awareness of negative stereotypes interferes with
performance.
83. A clinician wants to know whether a newly introduced cognitive screening tool adds useful
information beyond an existing interview and record review. The key question concerns:
A. incremental validity
B. face validity
C. split-half reliability
D. social desirability
✅Answer: A. incremental validity
Rationale: Incremental validity assesses whether a new measure adds value beyond existing
methods.
84. Which statement about interviews is most accurate?
A. Interviews are free from error because they are flexible
B. Interviews can be valuable but are subject to bias and should be conducted skillfully
C. Interviews are never considered assessment tools
D. Interviews cannot be standardized at all
✅Answer: B. Interviews can be valuable but are subject to bias and should be conducted
skillfully
Rationale: Interviews are useful but must be conducted carefully due to potential biases.
85. A test has excellent validity evidence, but its use is too expensive relative to the small gain
in decision accuracy it provides. From a practical perspective, the main issue is:
A. reliability
B. utility
C. scaling
D. rapport
✅Answer: B. utility
Rationale: Utility concerns the cost-effectiveness and practical value of using a test.
86. A psychologist bases a diagnostic conclusion on one test score alone despite conflicting
history, interview data, and behavioral observations. The best criticism is that:
A. diagnosis should rely on integrated multimethod evidence
B. one high-quality test always outweighs all other data
C. behavioral observations are never useful
D. collateral information lowers validity
✅Answer: A. diagnosis should rely on integrated multimethod evidence
Rationale: Accurate diagnosis requires integrating multiple sources of information.
87. Which is the strongest argument against using obsolete tests?
A. They are longer than modern tests
B. Their norms, items, or constructs may no longer support defensible interpretations
C. They are always cheaper
D. They cannot be scored by computer
✅Answer: B. Their norms, items, or constructs may no longer support defensible
interpretations
Rationale: Outdated tests may produce invalid conclusions due to obsolete norms or
constructs.
88. A client’s obtained score corresponds to the 84th percentile. This means that the client
scored:
A. 84% correct
B. above approximately 84% of the norm group
C. two standard deviations above the mean
D. at the maximum possible score
✅Answer: B. above approximately 84% of the norm group
Rationale: Percentile rank reflects the percentage of the norm group scoring below the
individual.
89. Which score has a mean of 50 and a standard deviation of 10 in many common testing
contexts?
A. z score
B. T score
C. percentile rank
D. stanine
✅Answer: B. T score
Rationale: T scores are standardized scores with a mean of 50 and SD of 10.
90. A z score of -1.00 indicates that the score is:
A. one standard deviation below the mean
B. one standard deviation above the mean
C. at the 99th percentile
D. equal to the raw score mean regardless of scale
✅Answer: A. one standard deviation below the mean
Rationale: A z score of -1 indicates the score is one standard deviation below the mean.
91. Which correlation coefficient is most appropriate for assessing the relationship between two
continuous variables measured at least at the interval level?
A. Pearson r
B. Phi coefficient
C. Kappa
D. Percentile coefficient
✅Answer: A. Pearson r
Rationale: Pearson r is the standard correlation coefficient used to measure linear
relationships between continuous variables.
92. A correlation of .00 between test scores and a criterion indicates that:
A. the test is maximally valid
B. no linear relationship was found
C. the test is unreliable
D. the criterion has perfect variance
✅Answer: B. no linear relationship was found
Rationale: A correlation of zero indicates no linear association between variables, though
nonlinear relationships may still exist.
93. If a predictor test is validated on one sample and then performs less well on a new sample,
this decrease is called:
A. inflation
B. shrinkage
C. compensation
D. acceleration
✅Answer: B. shrinkage
Rationale: Shrinkage refers to the reduction in predictive validity when a model is applied to a
new sample.
94. Which statement about clinical and mechanical prediction is most defensible?
A. Clinical judgment is always superior because humans detect subtlety
B. Mechanical methods often perform as well as or better than unaided judgment when
combining data
C. Mechanical methods are invalid if they use test scores
D. Clinical prediction and mechanical prediction never differ
✅Answer: B. Mechanical methods often perform as well as or better than unaided judgment
when combining data
Rationale: Research shows that statistical or mechanical methods can equal or outperform
clinical judgment in many predictive contexts.
95. Which is the best example of criterion contamination?
A. A predictor test and criterion both include overlapping content or are influenced by the
same knowledge of predictor scores
B. A test has a low alpha coefficient
C. The norm group is too small
D. A distribution is positively skewed
✅Answer: A. A predictor test and criterion both include overlapping content or are
influenced by the same knowledge of predictor scores
Rationale: Criterion contamination occurs when the criterion is not independent of the
predictor, artificially inflating validity.
96. In personality assessment, a self-report inventory designed to measure normal trait
dimensions such as Neuroticism, Extraversion, Openness, Agreeableness, and
Conscientiousness is most closely associated with:
A. the Five-Factor Model
B. classical conditioning
C. the projective hypothesis
D. the Binet tradition
✅Answer: A. the Five-Factor Model
Rationale: These five traits define the Five-Factor Model of personality.
97. Which statement best describes the role of behavioral observation in assessment?
A. It is useless unless formally quantified
B. It can provide valuable contextual data about actual performance and interaction
C. It should never be combined with tests
D. It replaces the need for informed consent
✅Answer: B. It can provide valuable contextual data about actual performance and
interaction
Rationale: Behavioral observation offers real-time contextual information that complements
other assessment methods.
98. A practitioner is asked to release raw test data to an unqualified third party simply because
that person is curious about the client’s performance. Ethically, the best response is to:
A. release everything to avoid conflict
B. refuse because raw data are not for unauthorized use and may only be released under
proper legal or professional conditions
C. post only the scaled scores
D. let office staff decide
✅Answer: B. refuse because raw data are not for unauthorized use and may only be
released under proper legal or professional conditions
Rationale: Ethical standards restrict release of raw data to authorized individuals under
appropriate conditions.
99. Which is the best reason assessment findings should be explained in nontechnical language
when appropriate?
A. Technical language is unethical in all professional communication
B. Clients and authorized recipients should be able to understand the meaning and
implications of results
C. Nontechnical summaries replace formal reports
D. It improves test reliability
✅Answer: B. Clients and authorized recipients should be able to understand the meaning
and implications of results
Rationale: Clear communication ensures that assessment results are meaningful and usable
by intended recipients.
100. A well-constructed psychological report should primarily:
A. list scores without interpretation
B. contain jargon to demonstrate expertise
C. integrate relevant data into clear, answerable conclusions tied to the referral question
D. avoid mentioning limitations to preserve confidence
✅Answer: C. integrate relevant data into clear, answerable conclusions tied to the referral
question
Rationale: Effective reports synthesize data and directly address the referral question with
clear, meaningful conclusions.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 11
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 11
1. A school counselor says, “Miguel scored at the 75th percentile in reading.” Which statement
is most accurate?
A. Miguel answered 75% of the items correctly.
B. Miguel performed better than 75% of the norm group.
C. Miguel has mastered 75% of the reading curriculum.
D. Miguel scored 1.5 standard deviations above the mean.
✅Answer: B. Miguel performed better than 75% of the norm group.
Rationale: Percentile rank indicates relative standing within the normative group. A 75th
percentile score means Miguel performed as well as or better than about 75% of the reference
group.
2. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Mode
B. Median
C. Mean
D. Quartile deviation
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean is highly sensitive to very high or very low scores because every score
contributes directly to its value.
3. A psychologist wants to know whether scores from Form A and Form B of the same test are
consistent. Which estimate is most appropriate?
A. Test-retest reliability
B. Parallel-forms reliability
C. Interrater reliability
D. Split-half reliability
✅Answer: B. Parallel-forms reliability
Rationale: Parallel-forms reliability evaluates consistency between two equivalent forms
intended to measure the same construct.
4. A test may be highly reliable yet still lack validity because it:
A. yields consistent scores but does not measure the intended construct.
B. is too short to be standardized.
C. contains items with moderate difficulty.
D. was normed on a representative sample.
✅Answer: A. yields consistent scores but does not measure the intended construct.
Rationale: Reliability concerns consistency, while validity concerns whether the test actually
measures what it claims to measure. A test can be consistent yet consistently wrong.
5. Which statement best distinguishes psychological testing from psychological assessment?
A. Testing always uses interviews, whereas assessment never does.
B. Testing refers only to objective tests, whereas assessment refers only to projective tests.
C. Testing is one tool, whereas assessment is a broader process that integrates multiple data
sources.
D. Testing is qualitative, whereas assessment is exclusively quantitative.
✅Answer: C. Testing is one tool, whereas assessment is a broader process that integrates
multiple data sources.
Rationale: Testing is one component of assessment. Assessment is broader and may include
interviews, records, observation, and multiple test data integrated for decision-making.
6. A personality test manual reports that its items adequately sample the domain of
interpersonal trust. This is strongest evidence of:
A. criterion validity
B. content validity
C. predictive validity
D. concurrent validity
✅Answer: B. content validity
Rationale: Content validity refers to how adequately the test content samples the relevant
domain or universe of behavior.
7. A company uses a cognitive ability test to predict future training success of applicants. This is
an example of:
A. concurrent validity
B. face validity
C. predictive validity
D. construct underrepresentation
✅Answer: C. predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity is demonstrated when test scores predict future performance,
such as later training success.
8. Which situation best illustrates a criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. Anna scored higher than 82% of examinees.
B. Ben ranked 12th in his class.
C. Carla met the predefined mastery standard in algebra.
D. David obtained a T score of 60.
✅Answer: C. Carla met the predefined mastery standard in algebra.
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation compares performance against a defined
standard or mastery criterion rather than against other examinees.
9. A test developer wants items that best differentiate high scorers from low scorers. The most
relevant index is:
A. item difficulty index
B. item discrimination index
C. coefficient alpha
D. standard error of measurement
✅Answer: B. item discrimination index
Rationale: Item discrimination indicates how well an item separates high scorers from low
scorers on the overall test.
10. If a test has a large standard error of measurement, the examiner should conclude that:
A. the examinee’s obtained score is a precise estimate of true score.
B. the test has excellent content coverage.
C. there is more uncertainty around the examinee’s observed score.
D. the test is necessarily invalid.
✅Answer: C. there is more uncertainty around the examinee’s observed score.
Rationale: A larger standard error of measurement means the obtained score is a less
precise estimate of the person’s true score.
11. Which statement about norms is most accurate?
A. Norms are unnecessary if a test is standardized.
B. Norms are based on the performance of a reference group.
