C. Norms indicate causation between traits and test scores.
D. Norms eliminate all cultural influences on testing.
✅Answer: B. Norms are based on the performance of a reference group.
Rationale: Norms are descriptive data derived from a reference sample and are used to
interpret individual scores comparatively.
12. A psychometrician administers a test to a client whose primary language differs from that of
the test manual and the instrument has no validated local adaptation. The best action is to:
A. proceed and interpret the results without comment.
B. translate items informally and score normally.
C. use the results cautiously, note limitations, and consider referral or alternative procedures.
D. administer the test twice to improve reliability.
✅Answer: C. use the results cautiously, note limitations, and consider referral or alternative
procedures.
Rationale: Assessment tools should be appropriate to the examinee’s language and
characteristics. If not, interpretation must be cautious, limitations documented, and alternatives
considered.
13. Which correlation coefficient is most appropriate for rank-ordered data?
A. Pearson r
B. Spearman rho
C. Point-biserial r
D. Phi coefficient
✅Answer: B. Spearman rho
Rationale: Spearman rho is designed for ranked or ordinal data and is appropriate when
assumptions for Pearson r are not met.
14. A correlation of .80 between test scores and academic grades indicates that:
A. 80% of students passed.
B. the test causes high grades.
C. the relationship is strong and positive.
D. the test is free from measurement error.
✅Answer: C. the relationship is strong and positive.
Rationale: A correlation of .80 indicates a strong positive association, though not perfect and
not causal.
15. In a normal distribution, the greatest proportion of scores falls:
A. in the extreme tails.
B. around the mean.
C. exactly at the 25th percentile.
D. equally in all score intervals regardless of distance from the mean.
✅Answer: B. around the mean.
Rationale: In a normal curve, scores cluster most densely near the center, around the mean.
16. Which is the clearest example of an objective personality measure?
A. Rorschach Inkblot Test
B. Thematic Apperception Test
C. MMPI-type self-report inventory
D. Sentence completion task scored impressionistically
✅Answer: C. MMPI-type self-report inventory
Rationale: Objective personality inventories use standardized items, scoring, and
interpretation procedures and are less dependent on examiner impression.
17. The primary rationale of projective techniques is that:
A. all people interpret stimuli identically.
B. responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying needs, conflicts, or themes.
C. they are always more reliable than objective inventories.
D. they eliminate examiner bias.
✅Answer: B. responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying needs, conflicts, or
themes.
Rationale: Projective methods rely on the idea that individuals project aspects of personality
onto ambiguous stimuli.
18. A clinician collects interview data, behavioral observations, case history, and test scores
before making a conclusion. This best reflects:
A. monomethod assessment
B. actuarial negligence
C. multimethod assessment
D. ipsative scoring
✅Answer: C. multimethod assessment
Rationale: Using several methods and data sources is the hallmark of multimethod
assessment.
19. A child performs poorly on a test because of fatigue and hunger on the day of testing. This
most directly reflects:
A. construct validity
B. source of error variance
C. criterion contamination
D. range restriction
✅Answer: B. source of error variance
Rationale: Temporary influences such as hunger or fatigue can affect performance and
contribute to measurement error.
20. Which description best fits a T score?
A. A score with mean 0 and SD 1
B. A score with mean 50 and SD 10
C. A percentile rank transformed to 100
D. A raw score corrected for guessing
✅Answer: B. A score with mean 50 and SD 10
Rationale: T scores are standardized scores with mean 50 and standard deviation 10.
21. Alfred Binet is most closely associated with:
A. factor analysis of personality
B. the development of early intelligence testing for school placement
C. the first projective inkblot method
D. the Big Five model
✅Answer: B. the development of early intelligence testing for school placement
Rationale: Binet is historically linked with early intelligence testing designed to identify
children needing educational support.
22. Charles Spearman is best known for proposing:
A. triarchic intelligence
B. multiple intelligences
C. general intelligence, or g
D. emotional intelligence
✅Answer: C. general intelligence, or g
Rationale: Spearman proposed a general factor underlying diverse intellectual performances.
23. Raymond Cattell distinguished between:
A. fluid and crystallized intelligence
B. verbal and performance IQ only
C. reliability and validity
D. projective and objective methods
✅Answer: A. fluid and crystallized intelligence
Rationale: Cattell is associated with distinguishing fluid intelligence from crystallized
intelligence.
24. The Flynn effect refers to:
A. declining reliability coefficients across time
B. rising average IQ scores across generations
C. cultural bias in projective testing only
D. increased use of teleassessment
✅Answer: B. rising average IQ scores across generations
Rationale: The Flynn effect refers to observed increases in average scores on intelligence
tests over time.
25. Which is most important when selecting an assessment tool?
A. Popularity among examiners
B. Number of subtests only
C. Relevance to referral question and adequacy of psychometric support
D. Attractiveness of test materials
✅Answer: C. Relevance to referral question and adequacy of psychometric support
Rationale: The best assessment tools are selected because they fit the referral issue and
have adequate validity, reliability, and appropriate norms.
26. A teacher says a student is “lazy” based solely on one low test score. This is most
vulnerable to:
A. criterion referencing
B. overinterpretation from insufficient data
C. ipsative comparison
D. alternate-forms reliability
✅Answer: B. overinterpretation from insufficient data
Rationale: One low score does not justify a sweeping personality conclusion like laziness.
Adequate conclusions require broader evidence.
27. In educational assessment, response to intervention (RtI) is primarily used to:
A. replace all achievement tests permanently
B. identify and support struggling learners through increasing levels of intervention
C. eliminate the need for classroom instruction
D. diagnose personality disorders in children
✅Answer: B. identify and support struggling learners through increasing levels of
intervention
Rationale: RtI involves tiered support, progress monitoring, and increasingly intensive
interventions for learners who struggle.
28. Dynamic assessment emphasizes:
A. static ranking only
B. learning potential and responsiveness to guided intervention
C. strict avoidance of feedback during testing
D. interpretation of only normative scores
✅Answer: B. learning potential and responsiveness to guided intervention
Rationale: Dynamic assessment focuses not just on static performance but on how the
person learns with assistance.
29. Which is the best example of an aptitude test?
A. A measure of current mastery in algebra already taught
B. A test used to estimate potential for learning or future performance
C. A checklist of depressive symptoms
D. A rating scale of classroom behavior only
✅Answer: B. A test used to estimate potential for learning or future performance
Rationale: Aptitude tests are intended to estimate capacity for future learning or performance.
30. A psychologist compares a client’s WAIS-IV index scores to examine strengths and
weaknesses across cognitive domains. This is an example of:
A. ipsative interpretation within the individual
B. criterion contamination
C. content sampling
D. incidental observation
✅Answer: A. ipsative interpretation within the individual
Rationale: Comparing a person’s own index scores to one another is an ipsative,
within-person interpretation.
31. In intelligence testing, deviation IQ differs from ratio IQ because deviation IQ:
A. compares mental age to chronological age.
B. is based on relative standing within age-based norms.
C. eliminates the need for standardization.
D. can only be used with preschool children.
✅Answer: B. is based on relative standing within age-based norms.
Rationale: Deviation IQ reflects how far a score lies from the average performance of an age
group, not a mental-age ratio.
32. Which is the strongest reason a test manual should report reliability and validity evidence for
the local population whenever possible?
A. To shorten administration time
B. To reduce the need for informed consent
C. To support meaningful interpretation for the actual examinees being assessed
D. To guarantee fairness in all settings
✅Answer: C. To support meaningful interpretation for the actual examinees being assessed
Rationale: Psychometric evidence is most useful when it applies to the population for whom
the test will be interpreted.
33. A clinician suspects malingering in a compensation case. Which principle is most
appropriate?
A. Rely only on the client’s self-description
B. Use multiple sources of data and interpret cautiously
C. Avoid all standardized tests
D. Assume secondary gain is always present
✅Answer: B. Use multiple sources of data and interpret cautiously
Rationale: Suspected malingering requires careful, evidence-based, multimethod assessment
rather than assumption or overreliance on self-report.
34. The Barnum effect is most closely related to:
A. using extremely specific feedback
B. accepting vague, general descriptions as uniquely accurate
C. improving interrater reliability
D. item response theory
✅Answer: B. accepting vague, general descriptions as uniquely accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect refers to the tendency to accept broad, flattering, or vague
statements as personally precise.
35. Mechanical prediction generally refers to:
A. impressions derived from unstructured interviews
B. prediction based on explicit rules or statistical combination of data
C. interpretation based on projective storytelling
D. diagnosis through neurological imaging only
✅Answer: B. prediction based on explicit rules or statistical combination of data
Rationale: Mechanical prediction uses systematic rules or actuarial methods rather than
informal intuition.
36. In neuropsychological assessment, executive functions are most related to:
A. simple sensory detection only
B. planning, inhibition, set-shifting, and problem solving
C. visual acuity only
D. blood pressure regulation
✅Answer: B. planning, inhibition, set-shifting, and problem solving
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order control processes such as planning,
flexibility, inhibition, and organization.
37. Which finding most strongly warrants caution before interpreting neuropsychological test
scores?
A. The client completed all tasks.
B. The client had adequate sleep and rapport.
C. The client displayed poor effort and inconsistent responding.
D. The client asked for clarification once.
✅Answer: C. The client displayed poor effort and inconsistent responding.
Rationale: Poor effort undermines interpretability because the test may no longer reflect true
ability or functioning.
38. A psychologist is asked to comment on a person’s mental condition without conducting an
examination, using only prior records. According to ethical assessment principles, the
psychologist should:
A. present definitive conclusions without reservation.
B. discuss the limitations and basis of any opinion.
C. refuse to review records under all circumstances.
D. release all raw data publicly.
✅Answer: B. discuss the limitations and basis of any opinion.
Rationale: When no direct examination is conducted, ethical practice requires clearly stating
limitations and the basis of any opinion.
39. Which of the following best illustrates behavioral assessment?
A. Asking a client to interpret an inkblot
B. Observing frequency and antecedents of classroom disruption
C. Computing percentile ranks from an IQ test
D. Writing a narrative from a TAT card only
✅Answer: B. Observing frequency and antecedents of classroom disruption
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on observable behavior and the conditions under
which it occurs.
40. Functional analysis in behavioral assessment focuses on:
A. percentile conversion
B. the relationships among antecedents, behavior, and consequences
C. latent trait extraction
D. projective symbolism
✅Answer: B. the relationships among antecedents, behavior, and consequences
Rationale: Functional analysis examines what precedes behavior, the behavior itself, and
what follows it.
41. The MMPI was developed primarily through:
A. pure psychoanalytic theory
B. criterion-keying or empirical keying
C. item response theory only
D. random item sampling without validation
✅Answer: B. criterion-keying or empirical keying
Rationale: The MMPI is classically associated with empirical criterion-keying rather than pure
theory-driven item selection.
42. Which personality measure is most associated with the Five-Factor Model?
A. NEO inventory
B. Bender-Gestalt
C. Stanford-Binet
D. Rorschach Comprehensive System
✅Answer: A. NEO inventory
Rationale: The NEO family is closely linked to the Five-Factor Model of personality.
43. A client’s response style shows exaggerated symptom endorsement on a self-report
inventory. The clinician should first consider:
A. response validity and profile interpretability
B. abandoning all assessment permanently
C. converting the profile to percent correct
D. using only face validity
✅Answer: A. response validity and profile interpretability
Rationale: Before interpreting substantive scales, the examiner should determine whether the
response pattern is valid and interpretable.
44. Which is the best use of an interview in assessment?
A. It completely replaces all tests.
B. It can clarify referral issues, gather contextual data, and build rapport.
C. It guarantees objectivity.
D. It has no reliability concerns.
✅Answer: B. It can clarify referral issues, gather contextual data, and build rapport.
Rationale: The interview is valuable for contextualizing the case, clarifying concerns, and
promoting a productive assessment relationship.
45. In a clinical setting, case history data are most useful because they:
A. ensure diagnosis without error.
B. provide developmental, medical, family, educational, and psychosocial context.
C. eliminate the need for informed consent.
D. are superior to all direct methods.
✅Answer: B. provide developmental, medical, family, educational, and psychosocial
context.
Rationale: Case history enriches interpretation by situating present findings within the client’s
broader life context.
46. Which best describes a structured interview?
A. Questions vary entirely by examiner mood.
B. There is a standardized sequence and content of questions.
C. It cannot assess psychopathology.
D. It is always less reliable than casual conversation.
✅Answer: B. There is a standardized sequence and content of questions.
Rationale: Structured interviews increase consistency by standardizing question content and
often scoring rules.
47. In custody evaluations, the psychologist’s primary obligation is to:
A. advocate for whichever parent pays first.
B. determine which parent appears more articulate.
C. serve the best interests of the child through objective, evidence-based evaluation.
D. avoid interviewing collateral sources.
✅Answer: C. serve the best interests of the child through objective, evidence-based
evaluation.
Rationale: Custody evaluations should be child-centered, objective, and supported by
adequate data rather than partisan advocacy.
48. Suicide risk assessment is best conceptualized as:
A. a one-time act based only on intuition
B. a structured and ongoing evaluation of ideation, plan, intent, means, and protective factors
C. unnecessary when the client smiles
D. based solely on personality tests
✅Answer: B. a structured and ongoing evaluation of ideation, plan, intent, means, and
protective factors
Rationale: Suicide risk assessment requires systematic consideration of risk and protective
factors and is often ongoing rather than one-time.
49. Which is the strongest ethical justification for limiting confidentiality?
A. Client curiosity
B. Examiner convenience
C. Imminent danger to the client or others, or lawful court requirement
D. Supervisor preference alone
✅Answer: C. Imminent danger to the client or others, or lawful court requirement
Rationale: Confidentiality can be limited when there is a serious threat or legal mandate, but
disclosure should be limited to what is necessary.
50. A psychometrician leaves completed protocols in an unlocked public area. This is primarily
an issue of:
A. test speededness
B. confidentiality and record security
C. content validity
D. normative obsolescence
✅Answer: B. confidentiality and record security
Rationale: Leaving protocols unsecured risks unauthorized access to confidential assessment
information.
51. Under ethical standards, informed consent in assessment generally includes discussion of:
A. only the test title
B. nature and purpose of services, financial arrangements if relevant, risks, and limits of
confidentiality
C. only the expected diagnosis
D. the correct answers after each item
✅Answer: B. nature and purpose of services, financial arrangements if relevant, risks, and
limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Informed consent requires a reasonably understandable explanation of the nature
of services and their limits.
52. A court-ordered evaluation differs from ordinary self-referred assessment because the
examinee must be informed:
A. that results will always remain fully private.
B. that the service is mandated and confidentiality may be limited.
C. that testing is optional once begun.
D. that no documentation is needed.
✅Answer: B. that the service is mandated and confidentiality may be limited.
Rationale: In mandated or court-ordered services, the examinee should be informed of the
nature of the service and limits of confidentiality before proceeding.
53. A third-party referral, such as an employer requesting testing, requires the examiner to
clarify:
A. only the test battery
B. who the client is, the role of the examiner, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
C. only the employer’s budget
D. only whether interviews will be used
✅Answer: B. who the client is, the role of the examiner, probable uses of information, and
limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Third-party referrals require role clarification and transparent explanation of who
receives and uses the information.
54. Which action best reflects boundaries of competence?
A. Accepting any referral to gain experience
B. Providing services only within one’s education, training, supervision, and experience
C. Relying on internet summaries for unfamiliar techniques
D. Interpreting any specialized test if the manual is available
✅Answer: B. Providing services only within one’s education, training, supervision, and
experience
Rationale: Boundaries of competence require professionals to practice only within their
established competence.
55. A psychology practitioner encounters a case outside current competence. The best
response is to:
A. continue independently to avoid losing the client
B. make an appropriate referral or obtain sufficient supervision/training
C. guess cautiously
D. delay indefinitely without informing the client
✅Answer: B. make an appropriate referral or obtain sufficient supervision/training
Rationale: When current competence is insufficient, the professional should refer, consult, or
obtain proper supervision and training.
56. Which statement about teleassessment is most ethical?
A. Ethical rules differ completely online.
B. Online assessment is exempt from confidentiality rules.
C. Face-to-face ethical principles still apply, with additional attention to privacy and technical
limitations.
D. Timed tests are always invalid online.
✅Answer: C. Face-to-face ethical principles still apply, with additional attention to privacy
and technical limitations.
Rationale: Teleassessment remains governed by the same core ethical standards, with added
need to manage privacy, identity, security, and connectivity issues.
57. A client asks to see raw test responses and item content. The best response is:
A. release everything automatically to anyone who asks.
B. refuse under all circumstances.
C. follow ethical and legal rules, recognizing that raw data and test materials are protected
and not ordinarily released except when lawfully required.
D. post the materials online for transparency.
✅Answer: C. follow ethical and legal rules, recognizing that raw data and test materials are
protected and not ordinarily released except when lawfully required.
Rationale: Test security and ethical standards restrict ordinary release of raw data and secure
materials, though lawful exceptions may exist.
58. Which best reflects test security?
A. Using photocopied protocols to save money
B. Sharing secure items in study groups
C. Protecting original test materials and limiting access to qualified persons
D. Allowing clients to keep record forms
✅Answer: C. Protecting original test materials and limiting access to qualified persons
Rationale: Test security protects the integrity of instruments and prevents misuse or
compromise of secure materials.
59. An examiner interprets a depression inventory score without considering the client’s recent
bereavement, language proficiency, and sleep deprivation. This most directly violates the
principle that:
A. norms are unnecessary in clinical settings.
B. test results must be interpreted in context.
C. validity is irrelevant once reliability is high.
D. self-report data are always sufficient.
✅Answer: B. test results must be interpreted in context.
Rationale: Ethical interpretation requires considering situational, personal, cultural, and
ability-related factors relevant to the client.
60. Which ethical principle is most directly violated by entering a harmful dual relationship with a
current client?
A. Multiple relationships that risk impaired objectivity or exploitation must be avoided.
B. Test norms should be periodically updated.
C. Reliability coefficients should be reported.
D. Percentiles are preferable to standard scores.
✅Answer: A. Multiple relationships that risk impaired objectivity or exploitation must be
avoided.
Rationale: Dual or multiple relationships are ethically problematic when they threaten
objectivity, effectiveness, or client welfare.
61. A practitioner becomes aware that another professional may have committed a minor ethical
violation that can be resolved without breaching confidentiality. The PAP code suggests first
considering:
A. public accusation on social media
B. informal resolution when sufficient and appropriate
C. immediate media exposure
D. destruction of records
✅Answer: B. informal resolution when sufficient and appropriate
Rationale: If an ethical issue can be adequately addressed informally and confidentiality is not
violated, informal resolution may be appropriate first.
62. A psychologist files an ethics complaint based on rumor and without evidence. This most
directly violates:
A. unfair discrimination
B. improper complaints
C. utility analysis
D. informed assent
✅Answer: B. improper complaints
Rationale: Filing ethics complaints recklessly or without supporting factual evidence violates
ethical standards regarding improper complaints.
63. Which is the most defensible statement about culture and testing?
A. A valid test in one culture is automatically valid in all others.
B. Cultural factors may affect rapport, interpretation, item meaning, and normative relevance.
C. Culture matters only in personality testing.
D. Translation alone guarantees fairness.
✅Answer: B. Cultural factors may affect rapport, interpretation, item meaning, and
normative relevance.
Rationale: Culture can shape testing behavior, meaning of responses, communication style,
and appropriateness of norms and interpretations.
64. Stereotype threat is important in assessment because it:
A. can depress performance when examinees fear confirming a negative stereotype.
B. always improves effort.
C. affects only projective tests.
D. is the same as random measurement error.
✅Answer: A. can depress performance when examinees fear confirming a negative
stereotype.
Rationale: Stereotype threat can impair performance by increasing anxiety, self-monitoring,
and cognitive load.
65. Which is the best example of criterion contamination?
A. The predictor test includes content from the outcome measure itself.
B. The test manual is outdated.
C. The distribution is skewed.
D. The sample is too large.
✅Answer: A. The predictor test includes content from the outcome measure itself.
Rationale: Criterion contamination occurs when the criterion is polluted by overlap or
improper influence from the predictor or other extraneous factors.
66. A selection test is useful to an organization when it:
A. has face validity only
B. improves decision quality and yields practical benefits relative to costs
C. has the highest number of items
D. produces the widest score range
✅Answer: B. improves decision quality and yields practical benefits relative to costs
Rationale: Utility refers to practical value in decision-making, including benefits, costs,
selection ratios, and base rates.
67. The Taylor-Russell approach is most directly associated with:
A. neuropsychological localization
B. utility of personnel selection decisions
C. projective hypothesis
D. ratio IQ
✅Answer: B. utility of personnel selection decisions
Rationale: Taylor-Russell methods help estimate how selection tools improve decisions
relative to existing practices.
68. Base rate in personnel selection refers to:
A. the proportion of applicants who can succeed without using the test
B. the average raw score on the test
C. the number of items answered per minute
D. the reliability coefficient of the instrument
✅Answer: A. the proportion of applicants who can succeed without using the test
Rationale: Base rate refers to the proportion who would be successful even without the
selection instrument.
69. Incremental validity asks whether:
A. a new measure adds predictive value beyond what is already known.
B. the test was given individually.
C. a score can be converted into a percentile.
D. the test was written by a well-known author.
✅Answer: A. a new measure adds predictive value beyond what is already known.
Rationale: Incremental validity asks whether a measure improves prediction above existing
information or tools.
70. In career assessment, an interest inventory is most useful for:
A. diagnosing psychosis
B. identifying patterns of likes and dislikes related to occupational options
C. measuring organic brain damage
D. replacing aptitude measures in all decisions
✅Answer: B. identifying patterns of likes and dislikes related to occupational options
Rationale: Interest inventories help align preferences with possible careers and
environments.
71. Which assessment approach is most appropriate for examining person-job fit in career
counseling?
A. Combining interests, aptitudes, personality, and relevant background information
B. Using only one projective test
C. Relying only on first impressions during interview
D. Ignoring work values because they are subjective
✅Answer: A. Combining interests, aptitudes, personality, and relevant background
information
Rationale: Career decisions are best supported by integrating multiple relevant domains
rather than using a single source.
72. An achievement test differs from an aptitude test in that an achievement test focuses more
on:
A. future learning potential only
B. current knowledge or skill already acquired
C. unconscious conflicts
D. vocational interests
✅Answer: B. current knowledge or skill already acquired
Rationale: Achievement tests assess what has already been learned, whereas aptitude tests
target future potential.
73. Which score interpretation is correct for a z score of +2.00?
A. The score is two standard deviations below the mean.
B. The score is equal to the median only.
C. The score is two standard deviations above the mean.
D. The score indicates 20% correct.
✅Answer: C. The score is two standard deviations above the mean.
Rationale: A z score of +2.00 means the obtained score is two standard deviations above the
mean.
74. A negatively skewed distribution typically indicates that:
A. many scores cluster at the low end and few at the high end.
B. many scores cluster at the high end with a tail toward lower scores.
C. the mean is lower than the mode in every case by exactly one SD.
D. the test lacks any validity.
✅Answer: B. many scores cluster at the high end with a tail toward lower scores.
Rationale: Negative skew means the tail extends to the left, with most scores relatively high.
75. Which measure is most appropriate for a purely nominal variable such as diagnostic
category?
A. Mean
B. Median
C. Mode
D. Standard deviation
✅Answer: C. Mode
Rationale: Nominal data classify categories, so the most appropriate central tendency is the
mode.
76. A clinician wants to know whether two raters observing the same child in class agree in their
ratings. Which reliability evidence is most relevant?
A. Internal consistency
B. Interrater reliability
C. Test-retest reliability
D. Alternate-form reliability
✅Answer: B. Interrater reliability
Rationale: Interrater reliability assesses consistency between different observers or scorers.
77. Coefficient alpha is most commonly used to estimate:
A. internal consistency
B. predictive validity
C. interscorer agreement across essays
D. parallel-forms reliability over time
✅Answer: A. internal consistency
Rationale: Coefficient alpha estimates how consistently items within a test measure the same
construct.
78. Which is most likely to increase reliability, all else equal?
A. Very heterogeneous administration procedures
B. More well-functioning items measuring the same construct
C. Greater ambiguity in scoring
D. More transient state influence
✅Answer: B. More well-functioning items measuring the same construct
Rationale: Adding good items that measure the same domain tends to improve internal
consistency and reliability.
79. Face validity is best understood as:
A. evidence that test content adequately samples the domain
B. whether the test appears relevant and appropriate on its surface
C. the strongest form of construct validity
D. a statistical estimate of item homogeneity
✅Answer: B. whether the test appears relevant and appropriate on its surface
Rationale: Face validity concerns perceived relevance and appropriateness, not technical
psychometric evidence.
80. Which evidence would best support construct validity for an anxiety scale?
A. Test items are printed clearly.
B. Scores correlate positively with other anxiety measures and less strongly with unrelated
constructs.
C. Examinees say the test looks scientific.
D. The scale is short.
✅Answer: B. Scores correlate positively with other anxiety measures and less strongly with
unrelated constructs.
Rationale: Construct validity is supported by expected patterns of convergence and
discrimination among measures.
81. Which assessment report style is most appropriate when the referral question asks how
cognitive, emotional, behavioral, and contextual factors interact in a case?
A. A purely numerical score sheet
B. An integrative report
C. A raw-data release only
D. A one-line conclusion without background
✅Answer: B. An integrative report
Rationale: An integrative report synthesizes findings across domains and sources to answer
the referral question meaningfully.
82. A psychologist uses a battery that includes an interview, symptom inventory, performance
validity measure, and behavioral observation in a forensic case. The strongest justification is:
A. forensic cases should rely on single tests to avoid complexity.
B. converging evidence strengthens defensible opinions.
C. projective methods are always prohibited.
D. interviews are legally sufficient by themselves.
✅Answer: B. converging evidence strengthens defensible opinions.
Rationale: Forensic and other high-stakes opinions are stronger when supported by multiple
convergent data sources.
83. Which statement about test bias is most accurate?
A. Group differences alone prove bias.
B. A test is unbiased whenever reliability is high.
C. Bias concerns whether score meaning or use unfairly disadvantages groups beyond true
construct differences.
D. Bias exists only in intelligence tests.
✅Answer: C. Bias concerns whether score meaning or use unfairly disadvantages groups
beyond true construct differences.
Rationale: Bias is not simply any group difference; it concerns unfairness in meaning,
prediction, interpretation, or use.
84. An examiner uses an obsolete test with outdated norms and bases strong recommendations
on it. The main ethical problem is:
A. excessive rapport
B. use of outdated and potentially misleading assessment data
C. too much qualitative information
D. low face validity only
✅Answer: B. use of outdated and potentially misleading assessment data
Rationale: Using obsolete tests or norms can mislead interpretation and recommendations,
making practice ethically unsound.
85. A referral question asks whether a client currently has decisional capacity. Which
assessment principle is most relevant?
A. Use any test regardless of purpose
B. Select tools directly pertinent to the referral issue
C. Avoid interviews because they are subjective
D. Focus only on percentile ranks
✅Answer: B. Select tools directly pertinent to the referral issue
Rationale: Assessment tools should be chosen because they are relevant to the purpose of
the evaluation and referral question.
86. In report writing, which conclusion is most defensible?
A. “The test proves the client will fail in life.”
B. “Results should be considered alongside history, observation, and contextual factors.”
C. “One elevated score is sufficient for diagnosis in all cases.”
D. “Cultural factors are irrelevant because norms exist.”
✅Answer: B. “Results should be considered alongside history, observation, and contextual
factors.”
Rationale: Good assessment integrates scores with contextual and collateral information
rather than treating test scores as self-sufficient proof.
87. Which best captures the difference between a trait and a state?
A. A trait is temporary; a state is enduring.
B. A trait is an enduring disposition; a state is a more transient condition.
C. They are interchangeable terms.
D. Only states can be measured psychometrically.
✅Answer: B. A trait is an enduring disposition; a state is a more transient condition.
Rationale: Traits are relatively stable tendencies; states are temporary conditions that may
vary across situations and time.
88. A counseling psychologist helping a graduating student choose among careers would most
likely prioritize:
A. aptitude, interest, values, and personality information
B. only neurological examination
C. only projective measures
D. only classroom grades with no interview
✅Answer: A. aptitude, interest, values, and personality information
Rationale: Career counseling typically benefits from assessment of aptitudes, interests,
values, personality, and contextual constraints.
89. Which is the strongest reason to avoid overreliance on one test score?
A. Every test score contains some degree of measurement error and contextual limitation.
B. Multiple tests are always cheaper.
C. Single scores have no clinical value.
D. Percentiles cannot be interpreted.
✅Answer: A. Every test score contains some degree of measurement error and contextual
limitation.
Rationale: No score is perfect; responsible practice avoids basing major decisions on one
isolated result when richer information is available.
90. An examiner explains results to parents using simple, nontechnical language. This best
reflects:
A. score inflation
B. appropriate communication of findings
C. criterion contamination
D. test security violation
✅Answer: B. appropriate communication of findings
Rationale: Ethical explanation of results requires understandable, nontechnical language
when communicating to parents or other nonexperts.
91. A practitioner conducting assessment abroad through telepsychology must remember that:
A. the license no longer matters once services are online.
B. ethical and legal obligations still apply, including confidentiality and competent practice.
C. informed consent is unnecessary online.
D. standardized procedures cannot be used online.
✅Answer: B. ethical and legal obligations still apply, including confidentiality and competent
practice.
Rationale: Online delivery does not remove licensure, competence, documentation, privacy,
or informed-consent obligations.
92. When providing services in an emergency outside ordinary competence, the most ethical
course is to:
A. provide only what is necessary to prevent deprivation of emergency care, proceed
cautiously, and discontinue when competent services become available.
B. continue indefinitely as the primary provider.
C. avoid any help under all circumstances.
D. ignore referral options.
✅Answer: A. provide only what is necessary to prevent deprivation of emergency care,
proceed cautiously, and discontinue when competent services become available.
Rationale: Emergency exceptions allow limited assistance to prevent immediate deprivation
of care, but they do not justify indefinite out-of-competence practice.
93. Which statement best reflects professional integrity?
A. Withholding important limitations to appear more confident
B. Avoiding conflicts of interest and communicating honestly and accurately
C. Releasing results to impress third parties
D. Accepting testimonials from vulnerable clients
✅Answer: B. Avoiding conflicts of interest and communicating honestly and accurately
Rationale: Integrity includes honest communication, minimizing bias, and avoiding or properly
managing conflicts of interest.
94. Which is the clearest example of exploitative relationship?
A. Referring a client to a more qualified specialist
B. Using one’s authority over a supervisee or client for personal gain
C. Documenting informed consent
D. Clarifying confidentiality limits
✅Answer: B. Using one’s authority over a supervisee or client for personal gain
Rationale: Exploitative relationships misuse professional authority and harm those in
vulnerable or dependent positions.
95. A psychologist is asked by a school to share a child’s full report with all teachers. The most
ethical response is to:
A. distribute the full report to every staff member immediately.
B. share only with appropriate parties and limit disclosure to what is necessary and
authorized.
C. refuse any communication with the school.
D. post a summary in a group chat for convenience.
✅Answer: B. share only with appropriate parties and limit disclosure to what is necessary
and authorized.
Rationale: Confidential information should be disclosed only to those with legitimate need and
proper authorization, and only to the extent necessary.
96. Which principle is most relevant when an assessment conclusion could affect hiring, school
placement, or legal outcomes?
A. Random responding
B. The need for substantial information and appropriate procedures to support conclusions
C. Speed over accuracy
D. Preference for anecdote over data
✅Answer: B. The need for substantial information and appropriate procedures to support
conclusions
Rationale: High-stakes decisions demand adequate data and sound procedures before
expert conclusions are offered.
97. In test development, pilot work is important because it:
A. replaces item analysis.
B. helps identify problems in administration, wording, scoring, and item functioning before
finalization.
C. is only for projective methods.
D. guarantees external validity.
✅Answer: B. helps identify problems in administration, wording, scoring, and item
functioning before finalization.
Rationale: Pilot work allows early refinement of a test before large-scale use or
standardization.
98. Which of the following would most likely reduce item difficulty in a multiple-choice test?
A. Using highly technical distractors
B. Writing a clear stem that matches taught content
C. Increasing ambiguity in the question
D. Removing all easy items
✅Answer: B. Writing a clear stem that matches taught content
Rationale: Clear, familiar, taught content generally makes an item easier, reducing item
difficulty.
99. A psychometrician administers a standardized test exactly according to manual instructions.
The chief advantage is that it:
A. guarantees high validity in all populations.
B. reduces administration-related error and promotes comparability of scores.
C. eliminates the need for rapport.
D. permits unrestricted interpretation of any score.
✅Answer: B. reduces administration-related error and promotes comparability of scores.
Rationale: Following manualized procedures helps preserve standardization and improves
the comparability and defensibility of scores.
100. Which statement best reflects high-quality board-style psychological assessment practice?
A. Interpret scores mechanically without context.
B. Base conclusions on one preferred theory regardless of data.
C. Integrate psychometric evidence, behavioral data, referral needs, culture, ethics, and legal
limits in forming conclusions.
D. Avoid giving any interpretation to prevent error.
✅Answer: C. Integrate psychometric evidence, behavioral data, referral needs, culture,
ethics, and legal limits in forming conclusions.
Rationale: High-quality assessment practice is integrative, context-sensitive,
psychometrically informed, and ethically grounded.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 12
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 12
1. Psychological assessment is best described as
A. the administration of a single standardized test
B. a process of gathering and integrating data from multiple sources to answer a referral
question
C. the scoring of objective and projective instruments
D. the interpretation of norms without regard to context
✅Answer: B. a process of gathering and integrating data from multiple sources to answer a
referral question
Rationale: Assessment is broader than testing alone. It involves collecting, integrating, and
interpreting information from multiple methods and sources in order to answer a specific referral
concern.
2. Which statement best distinguishes a psychological test from psychological assessment?
A. A test is always qualitative, whereas assessment is always quantitative
B. A test is one tool, whereas assessment is a broader decision-making process
C. A test requires training, whereas assessment does not
D. A test is individualized, whereas assessment is always group-based
✅Answer: B. A test is one tool, whereas assessment is a broader decision-making process
Rationale: A psychological test is one instrument or procedure used to gather data, whereas
assessment is the overall evaluative process that uses tests and other sources of information to
make decisions.
3. A psychometrician is asked to administer a test outside the limits of training and experience.
The most ethical response is to
A. proceed if the client insists
B. proceed if a manual is available
C. decline or refer unless proper supervision and competence are ensured
D. administer only the easy subtests
✅Answer: C. decline or refer unless proper supervision and competence are ensured
Rationale: Ethical practice requires professionals to work only within the boundaries of their
competence. If adequate training or supervision is lacking, the proper response is to decline,
refer, or ensure appropriate supervision first.
4. Which is the best example of an assessment referral question?
A. “What chapter is being covered?”
B. “How many items are in the scale?”
C. “Does the examinee show cognitive strengths and weaknesses relevant to academic
difficulty?”
D. “What is the brand of the test kit?”
✅Answer: C. “Does the examinee show cognitive strengths and weaknesses relevant to
academic difficulty?”
Rationale: A referral question should be specific, functional, and directly tied to the purpose of
assessment and decision-making.
5. In assessment, behavioral observation is most useful because it
A. eliminates all measurement error
B. replaces the need for testing
C. provides direct information about behavior in context
D. guarantees causal conclusions
✅Answer: C. provides direct information about behavior in context
Rationale: Behavioral observation gives direct, context-based information about how a person
actually behaves, which adds important ecological validity to assessment.
6. Which is a state rather than a trait?
A. Introversion
B. Intellectual ability
C. Temporary test anxiety during an examination
D. Conscientiousness
✅Answer: C. Temporary test anxiety during an examination
Rationale: A state is a temporary condition, and test anxiety during an examination is
situational and short-term rather than enduring.
7. A clinician uses interview data, test scores, school records, and behavioral observations
before making a conclusion. This illustrates
A. item discrimination
B. multimethod assessment
C. ipsative scoring
D. incidental sampling
✅Answer: B. multimethod assessment
Rationale: Multimethod assessment involves using several different sources and methods of
data collection to arrive at a more accurate and defensible conclusion.
8. The primary purpose of standardization in testing is to
A. make all examinees identical
B. ensure uniform administration and meaningful score interpretation
C. guarantee cultural fairness
D. maximize response bias
✅Answer: B. ensure uniform administration and meaningful score interpretation
Rationale: Standardization ensures that testing procedures are administered consistently so
that scores can be interpreted fairly and compared meaningfully.
9. A test manual reports that the normative sample closely matches the population for age, sex,
and region. This mainly supports
A. content validity
B. representativeness of norms
C. interscorer reliability
D. face validity
✅Answer: B. representativeness of norms
Rationale: A normative sample that reflects the characteristics of the intended population
supports the appropriateness and usefulness of the test’s norms.
10. A score interpreted by comparison with the performance of a reference group is
A. criterion-referenced
B. domain-referenced
C. norm-referenced
D. content-sampled
✅Answer: C. norm-referenced
Rationale: A norm-referenced score is interpreted by comparing an examinee’s performance
with that of a reference or normative group.
11. Which raw score represents the highest relative standing?
A. A score at the 25th percentile
B. A score at the 50th percentile
C. A score at the 75th percentile
D. A score at the 10th percentile
✅Answer: C. A score at the 75th percentile
Rationale: The 75th percentile indicates higher relative standing than the 25th, 50th, or 10th
percentile because it reflects performance above a larger proportion of the norm group.
12. A percentile rank of 84 means that the examinee
A. answered 84% of items correctly
B. scored higher than 84% of the normative group
C. obtained a z score of +0.84
D. is in the top 84 examinees only
✅Answer: B. scored higher than 84% of the normative group
Rationale: A percentile rank indicates the percentage of people in the normative sample who
scored at or below the examinee’s score.
13. Which scale of measurement has equal intervals but no true zero?
A. Nominal
B. Ordinal
C. Interval
D. Ratio
✅Answer: C. Interval
Rationale: Interval scales have equal distances between values but do not have a true zero
point, so ratios are not meaningful.
14. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Median
B. Mode
C. Mean
D. Percentile
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean uses every score in the distribution, so it is especially sensitive to very
high or very low outliers.
15. If a distribution of scores has a mean of 100 and standard deviation of 15, a raw score of
130 has a z score of
A. +1.00
B. +1.50
C. +2.00
D. +2.50
✅Answer: C. +2.00
Rationale: The z score is computed by subtracting the mean from the raw score and dividing
by the standard deviation: (130 − 100) / 15 = 2.00.
16. A negatively skewed distribution usually indicates that
A. most scores are very low
B. the tail extends toward the lower scores
C. the test has no variance
D. scores are evenly distributed
✅Answer: B. the tail extends toward the lower scores
Rationale: In a negatively skewed distribution, the long tail extends in the direction of the
lower scores.
17. When two variables increase together, their correlation is
A. negative
B. zero
C. positive
D. curvilinear only
✅Answer: C. positive
Rationale: A positive correlation means that as one variable increases, the other tends to
increase as well.
18. Which correlation coefficient is most appropriate for ranked data?
A. Pearson r
B. Spearman rho
C. Phi coefficient
D. Point-biserial only
✅Answer: B. Spearman rho
Rationale: Spearman rho is designed for ordinal or ranked data and is appropriate when
variables are expressed in ranks.
19. The coefficient of determination indicates
A. test bias
B. the percentage of shared variance between two variables
C. the number of valid items
D. the standard error of measurement
✅Answer: B. the percentage of shared variance between two variables
Rationale: The coefficient of determination, r², shows how much variance two variables have
in common.
20. A researcher concludes that high stress causes poor test performance solely because
stress and poor performance are correlated. This conclusion is flawed because
A. correlation does not establish causation
B. stress cannot be measured
C. all correlations are spurious
D. poor performance always causes stress
✅Answer: A. correlation does not establish causation
Rationale: Correlation shows association, not cause-and-effect. Other explanations such as
reverse influence or third variables may account for the relationship.
21. Reliability refers to the
A. extent to which a test measures what it claims to measure
B. consistency of measurement
C. social acceptability of scores
D. usefulness of a test for treatment planning only
✅Answer: B. consistency of measurement
Rationale: Reliability is the degree to which a test yields consistent, stable, and dependable
scores.
22. A test administered to the same individuals on two occasions yields similar scores. This
provides evidence of
A. alternate-forms reliability
B. internal consistency
C. test-retest reliability
D. content validity
✅Answer: C. test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability evaluates temporal stability by examining whether scores
remain similar across repeated administrations.
23. Split-half reliability is primarily an estimate of
A. temporal stability
B. internal consistency
C. interrater agreement
D. criterion validity
✅Answer: B. internal consistency
Rationale: Split-half reliability estimates how consistently the items within a single test
measure the same construct.
24. Which coefficient is commonly used to estimate internal consistency for dichotomously
scored items?
A. KR-20
B. Phi
C. Kappa
D. Eta
✅Answer: A. KR-20
Rationale: KR-20 is a standard internal consistency estimate for tests with dichotomously
scored items such as right-wrong responses.
25. Interrater reliability is most crucial when scores depend heavily on
A. computer scoring
B. normative conversion
C. examiner judgment
D. percentile interpretation
✅Answer: C. examiner judgment
Rationale: Interrater reliability is essential when scoring involves subjective judgment by
different examiners or raters.
26. The standard error of measurement is used to
A. eliminate error variance
B. estimate the range within which a person’s true score likely falls
C. determine face validity
D. compute item difficulty only
✅Answer: B. estimate the range within which a person’s true score likely falls
Rationale: The standard error of measurement provides an estimate of how much an
observed score may differ from the examinee’s true score because of measurement error.
27. A test with very low reliability will most likely
A. have perfect validity
B. limit confidence in score interpretation
C. produce no score variance
D. become criterion-referenced automatically
✅Answer: B. limit confidence in score interpretation
Rationale: When reliability is low, scores contain more random error, so interpretations based
on those scores become less trustworthy.
28. Validity is best defined as the
A. consistency of scores over time
B. degree to which evidence supports the interpretations of test scores for intended uses
C. speed of test administration
D. popularity of a test among practitioners
✅Answer: B. degree to which evidence supports the interpretations of test scores for
intended uses
Rationale: Validity concerns whether the evidence justifies the meaning and uses assigned to
test scores.
29. Which is the best example of content validity evidence?
A. Correlation with future job performance
B. Judgment that test items adequately sample the domain being measured
C. Correlation with another measure taken at the same time
D. Factor analysis showing clusters of traits
✅Answer: B. Judgment that test items adequately sample the domain being measured
Rationale: Content validity is supported when the items appropriately represent the full
content area or domain the test is intended to measure.
30. A college entrance exam predicts first-year grades. This is evidence of
A. face validity
B. predictive validity
C. convergent validity
D. internal consistency
✅Answer: B. predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity is shown when a test score successfully forecasts future
performance on a relevant criterion.
31. A depression inventory strongly correlates with another established depression measure
taken at the same time. This is evidence of
A. concurrent validity
B. discriminant validity
C. utility
D. interscorer reliability
✅Answer: A. concurrent validity
Rationale: Concurrent validity is demonstrated when a test correlates well with an established
measure of the same construct collected at the same time.
32. Construct validity is strengthened when a test
A. correlates with similar constructs and does not correlate too highly with unrelated
constructs
B. has a large number of items only
C. uses only essay items
D. is brief and easy to score
✅Answer: A. correlates with similar constructs and does not correlate too highly with
unrelated constructs
Rationale: Construct validity is supported by convergent evidence with related constructs and
discriminant evidence showing lower relations with unrelated constructs.
33. Face validity refers to
A. actual predictive power
B. expert scoring accuracy
C. whether the test appears, on its surface, to measure what it claims to measure
D. the degree of internal homogeneity
✅Answer: C. whether the test appears, on its surface, to measure what it claims to measure
Rationale: Face validity concerns the apparent relevance of the test to what it is supposed to
measure.
34. An item answered correctly by almost everyone will generally have
A. high discrimination
B. low difficulty
C. very high difficulty
D. perfect validity
✅Answer: B. low difficulty
Rationale: If nearly all examinees answer an item correctly, the item is very easy and
therefore has low difficulty in ordinary item analysis terms.
35. The item discrimination index tells the test developer how well an item
A. predicts external criteria only
B. distinguishes high scorers from low scorers on the total test
C. fits a legal standard
D. reduces social desirability
✅Answer: B. distinguishes high scorers from low scorers on the total test
Rationale: Item discrimination indicates whether an item effectively separates examinees who
perform well overall from those who do not.
36. In classical test theory, an observed score is composed of
A. norm + standard score
B. true score + error
C. validity + utility
D. item difficulty + discrimination
✅Answer: B. true score + error
Rationale: Classical test theory states that an observed score consists of the examinee’s true
score plus measurement error.
37. Which action is most appropriate when a test item is frequently endorsed by both high
scorers and low scorers?
A. Retain it automatically
B. Revise or discard it because it poorly discriminates
C. Convert it into a speeded item
D. Double its score weight
✅Answer: B. Revise or discard it because it poorly discriminates
Rationale: An item endorsed similarly by both stronger and weaker examinees does not
distinguish well between them and is therefore a weak discriminator.
38. An aptitude test is designed primarily to measure
A. current mastery of a learned body of knowledge only
B. future potential for learning or performance
C. emotional adjustment
D. malingering tendency
✅Answer: B. future potential for learning or performance
Rationale: Aptitude tests are intended to estimate an individual’s capacity or potential to learn
or perform in the future.
39. An achievement test is best used to assess
A. potential to learn
B. current level of acquired knowledge or skill
C. unconscious conflict
D. vocational satisfaction
✅Answer: B. current level of acquired knowledge or skill
Rationale: Achievement tests are designed to measure what a person has already learned or
currently knows.
40. The concept of g is most strongly associated with
A. Alfred Binet’s projective theory
B. Charles Spearman’s general intelligence
C. Thurstone’s affective factors
D. Skinner’s operant conditioning
✅Answer: B. Charles Spearman’s general intelligence
Rationale: Spearman proposed the concept of general intelligence, or g, as a common factor
underlying performance on many cognitive tasks.
41. Binet’s early work was especially important because it
A. introduced projective methods
B. was designed to identify schoolchildren needing educational assistance
C. replaced all interviews
D. eliminated examiner judgment
✅Answer: B. was designed to identify schoolchildren needing educational assistance
Rationale: Binet’s early scale was developed to help identify children who needed special
educational support.
42. Wechsler’s major contribution to intelligence testing included the idea that intelligence is
A. exclusively verbal
B. a global capacity reflected in diverse abilities, not just one narrow skill
C. identical to academic achievement
D. best measured only with nonverbal tasks
✅Answer: B. a global capacity reflected in diverse abilities, not just one narrow skill
Rationale: Wechsler viewed intelligence as a broad, overall capacity expressed across
multiple kinds of abilities.
43. A major advantage of deviation IQ over ratio IQ is that deviation IQ
A. is unaffected by age
B. is based on comparison with age peers in a standardized distribution
C. is computed by mental age divided by chronological age
D. guarantees absence of bias
✅Answer: B. is based on comparison with age peers in a standardized distribution
Rationale: Deviation IQ reflects how an individual compares with others of the same age in a
standardized normative distribution.
44. An examiner suspects that an examinee’s Full Scale IQ underestimates actual ability
because of severe working memory weakness and anxiety. The best interpretation is to
A. ignore the profile and report only FSIQ
B. consider index and subtest patterns in context
C. stop the assessment permanently
D. average FSIQ with academic grades
✅Answer: B. consider index and subtest patterns in context
Rationale: When the overall IQ score may be affected by uneven performance or situational
factors, interpretation should include a contextual analysis of index and subtest patterns.
45. Dynamic assessment differs from traditional static testing because it emphasizes
A. only timed multiple-choice items
B. learning process and responsiveness to intervention
C. norms without teaching
D. projective interpretation
✅Answer: B. learning process and responsiveness to intervention
Rationale: Dynamic assessment focuses on how well the examinee responds to assistance
or teaching, highlighting learning potential rather than static performance alone.
46. Response to Intervention is primarily used in educational settings to
A. replace all assessment
B. identify and address learning difficulties through graduated support and progress
monitoring
C. diagnose personality disorders
D. measure vocational interests
✅Answer: B. identify and address learning difficulties through graduated support and
progress monitoring
Rationale: Response to Intervention uses systematic, increasingly intensive support and
continuous monitoring to identify and help students with learning problems.
47. Portfolio assessment is most useful when the goal is to
A. obtain only a single standardized score
B. sample real-world performance over time
C. eliminate subjective judgment
D. measure only reaction time
✅Answer: B. sample real-world performance over time
Rationale: Portfolio assessment collects multiple examples of work across time, making it
useful for evaluating authentic, ongoing performance.
48. A school psychologist evaluating a child with reading problems should be most cautious
about
A. using multiple data sources
B. concluding disability based on one score alone
C. reviewing classroom performance
D. considering developmental history
✅Answer: B. concluding disability based on one score alone
Rationale: Educational and diagnostic conclusions should not be based on a single score
because valid assessment requires multiple sources of evidence.
49. Objective personality tests are generally considered objective because
A. they do not require interpretation
B. they use standardized stimuli and scoring procedures
C. they measure only conscious traits
D. they are always culture-free
✅Answer: B. they use standardized stimuli and scoring procedures
Rationale: Objective personality tests are considered objective mainly because their
administration, scoring, and often interpretation are standardized.
50. Projective techniques are based on the assumption that
A. people never distort self-report
B. responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying personality dynamics
C. only children can be assessed
D. reliability is always higher than objective tests
✅Answer: B. responses to ambiguous stimuli may reveal underlying personality dynamics
Rationale: Projective methods assume that people project inner needs, conflicts, or themes
onto ambiguous stimuli.
51. Which is the best example of a projective method?
A. MMPI
B. NEO inventory
C. Rorschach
D. Strong Interest Inventory
✅Answer: C. Rorschach
Rationale: The Rorschach is a classic projective technique that uses ambiguous inkblot
stimuli to elicit responses thought to reflect personality dynamics.
52. A major criticism of many projective techniques is that they often
A. cannot be administered individually
B. show weaker reliability and validity than more structured measures
C. contain no stimuli
D. are always computerized
✅Answer: B. show weaker reliability and validity than more structured measures
Rationale: Many projective methods have been criticized because their psychometric support
is often less consistent and less robust than that of structured measures.
53. Behavioral assessment focuses primarily on
A. inferred unconscious symbolism
B. directly observable behavior and its antecedents and consequences
C. global IQ scores
D. historical norms alone
✅Answer: B. directly observable behavior and its antecedents and consequences
Rationale: Behavioral assessment emphasizes observable actions and the environmental
conditions associated with them.
54. Functional analysis in behavioral assessment examines
A. only the person’s diagnosis
B. relationships among antecedents, behavior, and consequences
C. item-total correlations
D. examiner bias only
✅Answer: B. relationships among antecedents, behavior, and consequences
Rationale: Functional analysis identifies how antecedents and consequences are related to
the occurrence and maintenance of a behavior.
55. In clinical assessment, the mental status examination is most directly concerned with
A. job placement
B. current cognitive, emotional, and behavioral functioning
C. childhood achievement only
D. socioeconomic classification only
✅Answer: B. current cognitive, emotional, and behavioral functioning
Rationale: The mental status examination is used to evaluate present functioning, including
orientation, thought processes, mood, behavior, and cognition.
56. A psychologist suspects malingering in a compensation case. The most appropriate next
step is to
A. assume the client is lying
B. integrate test data, interview findings, records, and validity indicators before concluding
C. terminate the assessment immediately
D. report malingering based on intuition alone
✅Answer: B. integrate test data, interview findings, records, and validity indicators before
concluding
Rationale: Malingering is a serious conclusion that must be based on careful, evidence-based
integration of multiple sources of information.
57. The Barnum effect refers to
A. the tendency to interpret vague personality descriptions as uniquely accurate
B. the inability of tests to predict anything
C. the superiority of projective tests
D. the legal requirement to release raw scores
✅Answer: A. the tendency to interpret vague personality descriptions as uniquely accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect occurs when individuals accept broad, general statements as if
they were highly specific and personally accurate.
58. Mechanical prediction is often contrasted with clinical prediction because mechanical
prediction
A. relies on explicit statistical or actuarial rules
B. ignores all data
C. is always inferior
D. cannot be replicated
✅Answer: A. relies on explicit statistical or actuarial rules
Rationale: Mechanical prediction uses formal rules or statistical combinations of data rather
than relying solely on clinician intuition.
59. In suicide risk assessment, the most defensible practice is to
A. rely on one self-report item only
B. assess ideation, intent, plan, means, history, and protective factors
C. avoid asking direct questions
D. assume denial means no risk
✅Answer: B. assess ideation, intent, plan, means, history, and protective factors
Rationale: A sound suicide risk assessment requires a comprehensive evaluation of multiple
risk and protective factors, not a single indicator.
60. A neuropsychological evaluation is most indicated when there is concern about
A. fashion preference
B. possible brain-behavior dysfunction affecting cognition or behavior
C. only job satisfaction
D. only marital adjustment
✅Answer: B. possible brain-behavior dysfunction affecting cognition or behavior
Rationale: Neuropsychological evaluation is used when brain-related conditions may be
influencing cognitive, emotional, or behavioral functioning.
61. Which cognitive function is most closely linked to executive functioning?
A. Color blindness
B. Planning, inhibition, and cognitive flexibility
C. Hearing acuity
D. Handedness only
✅Answer: B. Planning, inhibition, and cognitive flexibility
Rationale: Executive functioning includes higher-order control processes such as planning,
response inhibition, problem solving, and mental flexibility.
62. A patient performs poorly on memory tasks after traumatic brain injury. The best
interpretation is to
A. conclude immediately that the patient is globally unintelligent
B. consider neurological history, effort, emotional status, and pattern of strengths and
weaknesses
C. discard the data because memory tests are useless
D. interpret the memory score without context
✅Answer: B. consider neurological history, effort, emotional status, and pattern of strengths
and weaknesses
Rationale: Neuropsychological interpretation requires integration of the patient’s history,
emotional condition, effort, and cognitive profile rather than relying on a single isolated score.
63. A screening test for dementia is most appropriately used to
A. replace comprehensive evaluation in all cases
B. identify individuals who may need further assessment
C. establish definitive diagnosis by itself
D. measure vocational preference
✅Answer: B. identify individuals who may need further assessment
Rationale: Screening tools are used to flag possible impairment and determine whether more
comprehensive evaluation is needed.
64. In career assessment, interest inventories are most useful for identifying
A. current levels of psychopathology
B. patterns of occupational likes and preferences
C. neurocognitive impairment
D. malingering
✅Answer: B. patterns of occupational likes and preferences
Rationale: Interest inventories help identify areas, activities, and occupations that are likely to
be attractive or engaging to the person.
65. Measures of aptitude in vocational assessment are designed to estimate
A. only occupational satisfaction
B. probable capacity to learn or perform in certain areas
C. defense mechanisms
D. past trauma severity
✅Answer: B. probable capacity to learn or perform in certain areas
Rationale: Aptitude measures estimate an individual’s likelihood of learning or performing
successfully in specific occupational or training areas.
66. In personnel selection, incremental validity refers to
A. the legal status of a test
B. the added predictive value of a measure beyond what is already known
C. the percentage of applicants hired
D. the number of items added annually
✅Answer: B. the added predictive value of a measure beyond what is already known
Rationale: Incremental validity asks whether a new measure improves prediction beyond
existing information or methods.
67. Utility analysis is concerned primarily with
A. the moral worth of a test
B. the practical value and consequences of using a test for decision making
C. only internal consistency
D. only examiner preference
✅Answer: B. the practical value and consequences of using a test for decision making
Rationale: Utility analysis evaluates whether a test improves decisions in ways that are
practically beneficial and worthwhile.
68. A company uses a cognitive ability test for hiring. Before adopting it, the most important
psychometric question is whether the test
A. looks impressive to applicants
B. predicts relevant job performance and is used fairly
C. contains difficult vocabulary
D. is longer than competing tests
✅Answer: B. predicts relevant job performance and is used fairly
Rationale: A hiring test must demonstrate job-related predictive validity and fair use to justify
its application in personnel decisions.
69. Which personality variable is often examined in workplace assessment because it relates to
dependability and organization?
A. Openness only
B. Conscientiousness
C. Somatization
D. Dissociation
✅Answer: B. Conscientiousness
Rationale: Conscientiousness is associated with organization, dependability, self-discipline,
and responsible work behavior.
70. Test bias is best understood as
A. any group difference in average score
B. unfairness arising when score meaning or prediction differs systematically across groups
C. all standardized testing
D. any unpopular test result
✅Answer: B. unfairness arising when score meaning or prediction differs systematically
across groups
Rationale: Test bias concerns systematic unfairness in interpretation or prediction across
groups, not simply the existence of score differences.
71. A test may be culturally inappropriate if it
A. uses standardized procedures
B. assumes language, experiences, or values not shared by the examinee
C. has a manual
D. is individually administered
✅Answer: B. assumes language, experiences, or values not shared by the examinee
Rationale: A test becomes culturally inappropriate when its content or assumptions do not fit
the examinee’s linguistic or cultural background.
72. A Filipino examinee with limited proficiency in the language of the test is being evaluated.
The best practice is to
A. administer the test anyway and ignore language effects
B. select instruments appropriate to the examinee’s language and characteristics
C. translate items spontaneously without documentation
D. interpret low scores as evidence of low intelligence
✅Answer: B. select instruments appropriate to the examinee’s language and characteristics
Rationale: Valid assessment requires using tools that are appropriate to the examinee’s
language, background, and relevant characteristics.
73. Republic Act No. 10029 is especially relevant to assessment practice because it governs
A. traffic violations
B. the regulation of psychology and psychometrics practice in the Philippines
C. copyright law for textbooks only
D. hospital accreditation only
✅Answer: B. the regulation of psychology and psychometrics practice in the Philippines
Rationale: Republic Act No. 10029 is the Philippine Psychology Act of 2009, which regulates
the professional practice of psychology and psychometrics in the country.
74. Under ethical practice, a psychometrician who delegates part of the work to an assistant
must ensure that the assistant
A. is a relative
B. can perform the task competently and under appropriate supervision
C. is unpaid
D. has access to all raw data without restriction
✅Answer: B. can perform the task competently and under appropriate supervision
Rationale: Ethical delegation requires that the person performing the delegated work be
qualified for the task and properly supervised.
75. Informed consent in assessment generally includes information about
A. only the test name
B. the nature and purpose of services, risks, financial arrangements, and limits of
confidentiality
C. only the final diagnosis
D. the examinee’s percentile rank before testing
✅Answer: B. the nature and purpose of services, risks, financial arrangements, and limits of
confidentiality
Rationale: Informed consent requires that the client be given understandable information
about what the assessment involves and the important conditions surrounding it.
76. An assessment is court-ordered. Before proceeding, the psychologist should
A. promise absolute confidentiality
B. explain the nature of services and the limits of confidentiality
C. refuse the case automatically
D. disclose nothing unless asked
✅Answer: B. explain the nature of services and the limits of confidentiality
Rationale: In court-ordered cases, the examinee must be told the purpose of the assessment
and the limits on confidentiality before the evaluation proceeds.
77. Which is the most ethical way to explain results to a parent who has little background in
testing?
A. Use raw scores and technical jargon only
B. Provide a clear, nontechnical explanation of findings
C. Refuse to discuss results
D. Give the parent all test booklets
✅Answer: B. Provide a clear, nontechnical explanation of findings
Rationale: Ethical feedback requires that results be communicated in language the recipient
can understand.
78. A teacher requests a student’s raw test responses for classroom curiosity. The most ethical
response is to
A. release them immediately
B. refuse release unless legally required and appropriately authorized
C. post them for transparency
D. send them without explanation
✅Answer: B. refuse release unless legally required and appropriately authorized
Rationale: Raw responses and test materials are protected information and should not be
released casually or without proper authorization.
79. A psychologist uses an outdated test with obsolete norms to make high-stakes decisions.
This practice is
A. acceptable if the test is familiar
B. acceptable if the report is brief
C. unethical because conclusions should not be based on obsolete tests or outdated results
D. ethical if the client signs consent
✅Answer: C. unethical because conclusions should not be based on obsolete tests or
outdated results
Rationale: Outdated tests or obsolete norms can produce misleading and unfair
interpretations, especially in high-stakes decisions.
80. Test security primarily requires that professionals
A. allow photocopying for convenience
B. protect materials and prevent unauthorized access or misuse
C. disclose items on social media
D. give all stimuli to clients after testing
✅Answer: B. protect materials and prevent unauthorized access or misuse
Rationale: Test security exists to preserve the integrity of assessment materials and prevent
improper exposure or misuse.
81. During teleassessment, poor internet connectivity affects the timed subtest. The examiner
should
A. ignore the disruption
B. document the limitation and consider its impact on interpretation
C. inflate the score
D. score the missed items as correct
✅Answer: B. document the limitation and consider its impact on interpretation
Rationale: Disruptions in teleassessment can affect score validity, so they must be
documented and taken into account during interpretation.
82. A psychologist stores confidential reports on an unlocked shared device accessible to
unqualified persons. This is primarily a violation of
A. utility
B. confidentiality safeguards
C. content validity
D. rapport building
✅Answer: B. confidentiality safeguards
Rationale: Confidential information must be stored securely to prevent unauthorized access
and protect client privacy.
83. Which situation best illustrates a multiple relationship that may impair objectivity?
A. A psychologist assesses an unknown referral from another clinic
B. A psychologist provides therapy to a close friend while also supervising that friend at work
C. A psychologist reviews school records before testing
D. A psychologist writes an integrated report
✅Answer: B. A psychologist provides therapy to a close friend while also supervising that
friend at work
Rationale: A multiple relationship exists when overlapping roles can impair objectivity or
create a risk of exploitation or harm.
84. Third-party referral cases require early clarification of
A. only fee arrangements
B. the role of the psychologist, who the client is, probable uses of information, and
confidentiality limits
C. the client’s political beliefs
D. the color of the test booklet
✅Answer: B. the role of the psychologist, who the client is, probable uses of information,
and confidentiality limits
Rationale: Third-party referrals require clear role definition at the outset so all involved
understand the purpose of the service and the limits of confidentiality.
85. An examinee asks whether the assessment session may be recorded online during
feedback. The most appropriate response is to
A. always prohibit recording without discussion
B. manage the request professionally while protecting confidentiality and ethical standards
C. post the recording publicly
D. let any third party store the recording without safeguards
✅Answer: B. manage the request professionally while protecting confidentiality and ethical
standards
Rationale: Requests involving recording should be handled carefully by balancing
professional judgment, privacy, consent, and confidentiality protections.
86. Which action best reflects the principle of doing no harm in assessment?
A. Administering every available test
B. Selecting only procedures relevant to the referral question and appropriate to the client
C. Relying on unsupported interpretations
D. Ignoring client distress during testing
✅Answer: B. Selecting only procedures relevant to the referral question and appropriate to
the client
Rationale: Doing no harm means avoiding unnecessary or inappropriate procedures and
using only those methods that are justified and suitable for the client.
