87. A psychometrician experiences serious personal problems that substantially impair
concentration and judgment. The ethical course is to
A. continue all duties unchanged
B. seek consultation or assistance and determine whether to limit, suspend, or terminate
duties
C. hide the impairment from colleagues
D. compensate by working faster
✅Answer: B. seek consultation or assistance and determine whether to limit, suspend, or
terminate duties
Rationale: When personal problems interfere with competent practice, the practitioner must
seek help and determine whether duties should be modified or suspended.
88. A psychology practitioner is asked to provide an expert opinion without examining the
person, based only on existing records. The best practice is to
A. present the opinion as definitive
B. discuss the limitations and basis of conclusions
C. avoid mentioning the lack of examination
D. guarantee diagnostic certainty
✅Answer: B. discuss the limitations and basis of conclusions
Rationale: Opinions based only on records should clearly identify the limits of the available
information and the basis for the conclusions drawn.
89. Which is the best example of converging evidence in assessment?
A. A single low subtest score
B. Interview, history, observation, and test results pointing to the same conclusion
C. Conflicting data from all sources
D. One unusually high percentile rank
✅Answer: B. Interview, history, observation, and test results pointing to the same conclusion
Rationale: Converging evidence occurs when multiple sources of information independently
support the same interpretation.
90. In report writing, the most defensible conclusion is one that
A. goes beyond the data to sound impressive
B. is supported by substantial information and appropriate assessment procedures
C. avoids mentioning limitations
D. is based mainly on intuition
✅Answer: B. is supported by substantial information and appropriate assessment
procedures
Rationale: A defensible conclusion is one that follows from adequate data collected through
appropriate and professionally sound procedures.
91. An assessment report should answer the referral question and
A. list only raw scores
B. integrate findings, note limitations, and provide relevant recommendations
C. avoid behavioral observations
D. exclude contextual factors
✅Answer: B. integrate findings, note limitations, and provide relevant recommendations
Rationale: A useful report synthesizes information, acknowledges limitations, and gives
recommendations that are relevant to the referral concern.
92. Which recommendation is most appropriate after finding significant academic
underachievement with intact reasoning ability and attention difficulties?
A. “No action needed”
B. “Consider targeted educational support and further evaluation/intervention for attentional
concerns”
C. “The student is intellectually incapable”
D. “Discontinue all schooling”
✅Answer: B. “Consider targeted educational support and further evaluation/intervention for
attentional concerns”
Rationale: Appropriate recommendations should be practical, linked to the findings, and
directed toward intervention and support rather than overgeneralized negative conclusions.
93. Which of the following is the best example of criterion-referenced interpretation?
A. Comparing an examinee’s score with age peers
B. Determining whether an examinee has mastered a specific set of skills
C. Converting a raw score to a z score
D. Ranking examinees from highest to lowest
✅Answer: B. Determining whether an examinee has mastered a specific set of skills
Rationale: Criterion-referenced interpretation focuses on whether performance meets a
defined standard or level of mastery.
94. A counselor administers an interest inventory to a client choosing between careers. The
most appropriate interpretation is that the inventory
A. determines with certainty the one correct occupation
B. suggests areas of potential fit to be considered with abilities, values, and context
C. replaces counseling
D. measures psychopathology directly
✅Answer: B. suggests areas of potential fit to be considered with abilities, values, and
context
Rationale: Interest inventories help guide career exploration by identifying possible areas of
fit, but they must be considered alongside other personal and contextual factors.
95. In a forensic context, the examiner must be especially careful to
A. act primarily as the examinee’s advocate
B. maintain objectivity and clarify role expectations
C. promise therapeutic benefit
D. conceal limits of confidentiality
✅Answer: B. maintain objectivity and clarify role expectations
Rationale: Forensic assessment requires neutrality and clear communication about the
evaluator’s role and the limits of confidentiality.
96. Which statement about accommodations in testing is most accurate?
A. Accommodations are always unfair
B. Appropriate accommodations may be necessary to permit valid assessment of individuals
with disabilities
C. Accommodations invalidate all scores automatically
D. Accommodations should be granted only for intelligence tests
✅Answer: B. Appropriate accommodations may be necessary to permit valid assessment of
individuals with disabilities
Rationale: Properly selected accommodations can improve access and make testing more
valid for individuals with disabilities without automatically invalidating the results.
97. Which finding would most strongly support the usefulness of a selection test?
A. Applicants say they like the test
B. Test scores meaningfully predict later job performance and improve decision quality
C. The test is difficult
D. The test has many items
✅Answer: B. Test scores meaningfully predict later job performance and improve decision
quality
Rationale: A selection test is most useful when it predicts relevant outcomes and enhances
the quality of selection decisions.
98. A psychometrician explains results to a self-referred adult and asks permission before
releasing the report to the employer. This primarily reflects
A. random administration
B. respect for consent and confidentiality
C. norm obsolescence
D. mechanical prediction
✅Answer: B. respect for consent and confidentiality
Rationale: Asking permission before releasing results to a third party reflects the ethical
principles of informed consent and confidentiality.
99. The best reason to avoid overreliance on a single test score is that
A. all tests are invalid
B. psychological functioning is complex and scores must be interpreted within a larger body
of evidence
C. norms are never useful
D. interviews are always superior
✅Answer: B. psychological functioning is complex and scores must be interpreted within a
larger body of evidence
Rationale: A single score cannot fully capture complex psychological functioning, so sound
conclusions require integration with other relevant evidence.
100. The overall goal of sound psychological assessment is to
A. generate as many scores as possible
B. arrive at useful, fair, evidence-based conclusions that inform decisions and benefit the
client or referral process
C. prove the examiner is knowledgeable
D. replace professional judgment with formulas alone
✅Answer: B. arrive at useful, fair, evidence-based conclusions that inform decisions and
benefit the client or referral process
Rationale: The purpose of psychological assessment is to produce fair, evidence-based
conclusions that meaningfully guide decisions and serve the needs of the client or referral
context.
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL
ASSESSMENT EXAM 13
MOCK EXAM- PSYCHOLOGICAL ASSESSMENT EXAM 13
1. A test manual states that examinees who take the same test twice under similar conditions
tend to obtain highly similar scores over time. This is strongest evidence of:
A. Content validity
B. Test-retest reliability
C. Interrater reliability
D. Face validity
✅Answer: B. Test-retest reliability
Rationale: Test-retest reliability refers to the stability of scores over time when the same
individuals are tested again under similar conditions.
2. Which statement best reflects the relationship between reliability and validity?
A. A test can be valid even when it is unreliable
B. A test can be reliable without being valid
C. Reliability is identical to validity
D. Validity always exceeds reliability
✅Answer: B. A test can be reliable without being valid
Rationale: A test may consistently measure something, yet still fail to measure the intended
construct, which means it can be reliable without being valid.
3. A guidance counselor wants to know whether a newly developed scholastic aptitude test
predicts first-year college GPA. The most relevant form of validity evidence is:
A. Predictive validity
B. Face validity
C. Split-half reliability
D. Content sampling
✅Answer: A. Predictive validity
Rationale: Predictive validity concerns how well test scores forecast a future outcome, such as
first-year college GPA.
4. Which of the following best illustrates content validity?
A. A depression scale correlates with another established depression scale
B. A board exam samples the full domain of competencies specified in its blueprint
C. A personality inventory distinguishes depressed from nondepressed patients
D. A test appears acceptable to examinees
✅Answer: B. A board exam samples the full domain of competencies specified in its
blueprint
Rationale: Content validity is established when the items adequately represent the domain of
knowledge or skills the test is intended to measure.
5. An item answered correctly by almost all examinees is likely to have:
A. High discrimination
B. Low difficulty index
C. Ceiling tendency and weak discrimination
D. High predictive validity by itself
✅Answer: C. Ceiling tendency and weak discrimination
Rationale: When almost everyone answers an item correctly, it produces little score variation
and therefore does a poor job distinguishing stronger from weaker examinees.
6. In test construction, the item discrimination index is primarily concerned with an item’s ability
to:
A. Reduce test length
B. Differentiate high scorers from low scorers
C. Increase face validity
D. Standardize administration procedures
✅Answer: B. Differentiate high scorers from low scorers
Rationale: The item discrimination index shows how well an item separates examinees who
perform well overall from those who perform poorly overall.
7. A score of z = -1.50 means that the examinee’s score is:
A. 1.5 standard deviations above the mean
B. 1.5 standard deviations below the mean
C. 15 points below the raw score mean
D. In the 50th percentile
✅Answer: B. 1.5 standard deviations below the mean
Rationale: A negative z score indicates performance below the mean, and the value 1.50
shows the distance in standard deviation units.
8. The primary purpose of norms is to:
A. Guarantee test validity
B. Eliminate measurement error
C. Provide a basis for comparing an individual’s score with a reference group
D. Replace interpretation
✅Answer: C. Provide a basis for comparing an individual’s score with a reference group
Rationale: Norms allow an individual’s performance to be interpreted by comparison with a
defined reference group.
9. A test is said to be standardized when it has:
A. Only multiple-choice items
B. Equal numbers of easy and hard items
C. Uniform administration and scoring procedures plus normative data
D. Items written by experts only
✅Answer: C. Uniform administration and scoring procedures plus normative data
Rationale: Standardization means the test is administered and scored in a consistent way and
interpreted using established norms.
10. Which measure of central tendency is most affected by extreme scores?
A. Mode
B. Median
C. Mean
D. Percentile rank
✅Answer: C. Mean
Rationale: The mean incorporates all scores in the distribution, so extreme values affect it
more than the median or mode.
11. If a distribution has a mean of 100 and standard deviation of 15, what is the z score of a raw
score of 130?
A. 1.00
B. 1.50
C. 2.00
D. 2.50
✅Answer: C. 2.00
Rationale: The z score is computed as (130 − 100) / 15 = 2.00.
12. The standard error of measurement is most useful for:
A. Estimating the range in which a person’s true score likely falls
B. Determining item content relevance
C. Computing percentile ranks only
D. Establishing face validity
✅Answer: A. Estimating the range in which a person’s true score likely falls
Rationale: The standard error of measurement is used to estimate the band around an
observed score within which the true score is likely to fall.
13. A clinician says, “This test looks like it measures anxiety, so it must be valid.” The clinician is
relying mainly on:
A. Face validity
B. Construct validity
C. Criterion validity
D. Concurrent validity
✅Answer: A. Face validity
Rationale: Face validity refers to the extent to which a test appears, on its surface, to
measure what it claims to measure.
14. Which correlation coefficient is most appropriate for rank-ordered data?
A. Pearson r
B. Spearman rho
C. Phi coefficient
D. Point-biserial
✅Answer: B. Spearman rho
Rationale: Spearman rho is specifically designed for ordinal or rank-ordered data.
15. In classical test theory, observed score is best expressed as:
A. True score minus validity
B. Error score only
C. True score plus error
D. Norm plus deviation IQ
✅Answer: C. True score plus error
Rationale: Classical test theory states that an observed score consists of a true score
component plus measurement error.
16. A test developer revises items after pilot testing because many examinees misunderstood
them. This action primarily aims to reduce:
A. Administration error
B. Guessing
C. Item ambiguity
D. Norm obsolescence
✅Answer: C. Item ambiguity
Rationale: Revising misunderstood items targets ambiguity so that the items are interpreted
more clearly and consistently.
17. Which situation best exemplifies interscorer reliability?
A. Scores remain stable after six months
B. Two examiners assign similar ratings to the same essay responses
C. Items measure all areas in the table of specifications
D. Scores correlate with job performance
✅Answer: B. Two examiners assign similar ratings to the same essay responses
Rationale: Interscorer reliability refers to the degree of agreement between different scorers
or raters evaluating the same responses.
18. A school uses a math mastery test to determine whether students meet a predefined
competency standard rather than compare them with peers. This is:
A. Norm-referenced testing
B. Criterion-referenced testing
C. Projective testing
D. Ipsative testing
✅Answer: B. Criterion-referenced testing
Rationale: Criterion-referenced testing evaluates performance against a predefined standard
or mastery level rather than against other examinees.
19. Which statement about validity is most accurate?
A. Validity refers to the consistency of scores
B. Validity concerns the appropriateness of interpretations made from test scores
C. Validity is established once and never reexamined
D. Validity depends only on examiner skill
✅Answer: B. Validity concerns the appropriateness of interpretations made from test scores
Rationale: Validity concerns whether the interpretations and uses of test scores are
appropriate and supported by evidence.
20. A test has excellent reliability but poor validity. The best interpretation is that the test:
A. Produces consistent but not meaningful scores for the intended purpose
B. Produces unstable but accurate scores
C. Needs no revision
D. Is automatically fair
✅Answer: A. Produces consistent but not meaningful scores for the intended purpose
Rationale: A test with high reliability but poor validity yields stable scores that do not
adequately measure the intended construct or support the intended use.
21. Alfred Binet’s early intelligence testing work was primarily designed to:
A. Diagnose personality disorders in adults
B. Identify schoolchildren needing educational assistance
C. Predict occupational success in industry
D. Screen military recruits for malingering
✅Answer: B. Identify schoolchildren needing educational assistance
Rationale: Binet developed early intelligence tests to help identify children who needed
special educational support.
22. Spearman’s theory proposed that intellectual performance is influenced by:
A. Id, ego, and superego
B. A general factor plus specific factors
C. Fluid ability only
D. Emotional intelligence only
✅Answer: B. A general factor plus specific factors
Rationale: Spearman proposed that performance on intellectual tasks reflects a general
ability factor, g, along with task-specific factors, s.
23. The Flynn effect refers to:
A. Higher validity coefficients in modern tests
B. Rising average intelligence test scores across generations
C. Declining reliability of group tests
D. Gender differences in verbal ability
✅Answer: B. Rising average intelligence test scores across generations
Rationale: The Flynn effect describes the long-term increase in average intelligence test
scores across generations.
24. Which test is most closely associated with deviation IQ?
A. Early Stanford-Binet mental age formula exclusively
B. Modern intelligence scales comparing performance to age peers
C. TAT scoring systems
D. Rorschach comprehensive system
✅Answer: B. Modern intelligence scales comparing performance to age peers
Rationale: Deviation IQ is based on comparison of an examinee’s performance with that of
age-matched peers rather than on the mental-age ratio formula.
25. A child obtains a mental age of 12 and chronological age of 10 on an older ratio-IQ model.
The IQ is:
A. 80
B. 100
C. 120
D. 140
✅Answer: C. 120
Rationale: Ratio IQ is computed as mental age divided by chronological age times 100, so
12/10 × 100 = 120.
26. Which of the following is most characteristic of the Wechsler scales?
A. Exclusive use of projective tasks
B. Separate verbal and performance traditions leading to multiple index scores
C. Ratio IQ as the primary score
D. No norms are required
✅Answer: B. Separate verbal and performance traditions leading to multiple index scores
Rationale: The Wechsler scales are known for their verbal and performance subtests and
their use of composite and index scores.
27. An achievement test differs from an aptitude test because an achievement test focuses
more on:
A. Potential to learn in the future
B. Previously acquired knowledge or skill
C. Unconscious motives
D. Emotional adjustment
✅Answer: B. Previously acquired knowledge or skill
Rationale: Achievement tests measure what an individual has already learned, whereas
aptitude tests are more concerned with potential for future learning or performance.
28. Response to Intervention (RtI) in educational assessment is most concerned with:
A. Using projective tests before classroom instruction
B. Monitoring students’ response to increasingly intensive instruction
C. Replacing all psychoeducational testing
D. Diagnosing only intellectual disability
✅Answer: B. Monitoring students’ response to increasingly intensive instruction
Rationale: RtI focuses on how students respond to progressively more intensive instructional
interventions.
29. Dynamic assessment places greatest emphasis on:
A. Static ranking against norms only
B. Learning potential and responsiveness to mediated assistance
C. Projective interpretation
D. Purely nonverbal performance
✅Answer: B. Learning potential and responsiveness to mediated assistance
Rationale: Dynamic assessment evaluates how well a person learns or improves when
provided with teaching, cues, or assistance.
30. A school psychologist interpreting a cognitive score for a bilingual student should be most
cautious about:
A. Using any observations
B. Ignoring language and cultural variables
C. Reviewing educational history
D. Explaining results in plain language
✅Answer: B. Ignoring language and cultural variables
Rationale: Language background and cultural context can strongly affect test performance
and must be considered in interpretation.
31. The objective or structured approach to personality assessment is best described as:
A. Highly ambiguous stimuli with unrestricted responses
B. Clear stimuli with more specified response options
C. Free storytelling to pictures
D. Interpretation based only on unconscious symbolism
✅Answer: B. Clear stimuli with more specified response options
Rationale: Structured personality measures use relatively clear items and constrained
response formats, making responses easier to score and compare.
32. The MMPI is historically significant because it emphasized:
A. Purely theoretical keying
B. Empirical criterion keying
C. Inkblot interpretation
D. Physiological recording
✅Answer: B. Empirical criterion keying
Rationale: The MMPI became notable for developing scales empirically by identifying
response patterns that distinguished criterion groups.
33. Which test is most clearly projective?
A. NEO-PI
B. CPI
C. TAT
D. EPPS
✅Answer: C. TAT
Rationale: The TAT is a projective test that uses ambiguous pictures to elicit stories revealing
needs, conflicts, and interpersonal themes.
34. The Rorschach differs from most structured inventories because it:
A. Uses true-false questions
B. Requires storytelling to ambiguous pictures
C. Uses ambiguous inkblots as stimuli
D. Measures only intelligence
✅Answer: C. Uses ambiguous inkblots as stimuli
Rationale: The defining feature of the Rorschach is its use of ambiguous inkblots to elicit
perceptual and associative responses.
35. The TAT is commonly used to elicit:
A. Motor speed
B. Stories reflecting needs, conflicts, and interpersonal themes
C. Pure reaction time
D. Only verbal IQ
✅Answer: B. Stories reflecting needs, conflicts, and interpersonal themes
Rationale: The TAT asks examinees to create stories about ambiguous scenes, which are
then interpreted for motives, conflicts, and relational patterns.
36. Cattell’s 16PF is most closely associated with which test development strategy?
A. Factor analytic approach
B. Mental age approach
C. Criterion-referenced mastery
D. Behavioral observation only
✅Answer: A. Factor analytic approach
Rationale: Cattell developed the 16PF through factor analysis to identify basic personality
dimensions.
37. A counselor selects a broad personality inventory to describe normal-range interpersonal
style, self-control, and socialization rather than psychopathology. The best choice is:
A. TAT
B. CPI
C. Bender-Gestalt
D. Halstead-Reitan
✅Answer: B. CPI
Rationale: The CPI is designed to assess normal personality characteristics and interpersonal
functioning rather than severe clinical psychopathology.
38. Which statement best captures a major criticism of projective tests?
A. They are too brief
B. Their reliability and validity are often questioned
C. They cannot be administered individually
D. They are always invalid in every circumstance
✅Answer: B. Their reliability and validity are often questioned
Rationale: A major criticism of projective tests is that many of their interpretations have been
challenged on psychometric grounds, especially reliability and validity.
39. Behavioral assessment differs from traditional trait-oriented assessment because it
emphasizes:
A. Global inferences only
B. Specific observable behavior in context
C. Symbolic meaning of drawings only
D. Mental age estimates
✅Answer: B. Specific observable behavior in context
Rationale: Behavioral assessment focuses on concrete, observable actions and the situations
in which they occur.
40. A clinician asks a client to record the frequency, antecedents, and consequences of panic
episodes. This is primarily:
A. Criterion keying
B. Behavioral assessment
C. Projective testing
D. Factor analysis
✅Answer: B. Behavioral assessment
Rationale: Recording behavior frequency along with antecedents and consequences is a
classic behavioral assessment method.
41. Which of the following best distinguishes structured from projective methods?
A. Structured methods require no norms
B. Projective methods present more ambiguous stimuli and less constrained responses
C. Structured methods cannot assess personality
D. Projective methods have no administration procedures at all
✅Answer: B. Projective methods present more ambiguous stimuli and less constrained
responses
Rationale: Projective methods use ambiguous stimuli and allow freer responses, whereas
structured methods use clearer items and more limited response formats.
42. The NEO inventory is most associated with assessment of:
A. Neurocognitive impairment
B. The Five-Factor Model of personality
C. Psychotic thought disorder exclusively
D. Visual-motor integration
✅Answer: B. The Five-Factor Model of personality
Rationale: The NEO inventory is specifically designed to assess the major dimensions of the
Five-Factor Model of personality.
43. A psychologist wants to compare a client’s self-description with peer ratings across
personality dimensions. This approach is most compatible with:
A. Multimethod personality assessment
B. Exclusive projective interpretation
C. Ratio IQ computation
D. Neurological screening only
✅Answer: A. Multimethod personality assessment
Rationale: Comparing self-report and peer ratings reflects a multimethod approach that
strengthens personality assessment through multiple sources of data.
44. Which statement about figure-drawing techniques is most accurate?
A. Their interpretation is entirely free from criticism
B. They are universally superior to structured inventories
C. Their psychometric support for diagnostic inference has often been debated
D. They measure IQ directly
✅Answer: C. Their psychometric support for diagnostic inference has often been debated
Rationale: Figure-drawing techniques have often been criticized because the empirical
support for many diagnostic interpretations remains controversial.
45. A clinician wants to assess overt avoidance behavior in social situations rather than infer
deep motives. The most appropriate primary strategy is:
A. TAT administration
B. Behavioral observation and self-monitoring
C. Free association
D. Word association alone
✅Answer: B. Behavioral observation and self-monitoring
Rationale: Direct observation and self-monitoring are most appropriate when the goal is to
assess specific, overt behaviors in context.
46. In clinical assessment, the interview is best understood as:
A. A useless pretest ritual
B. A flexible assessment tool that can generate data on symptoms, history, and mental status
C. A projective technique only
D. A substitute for all psychometric testing
✅Answer: B. A flexible assessment tool that can generate data on symptoms, history, and
mental status
Rationale: The interview is a core clinical tool because it can gather a wide range of relevant
information, including presenting problems, background, and current functioning.
47. Which of the following is most characteristic of a mental status examination?
A. It measures only IQ
B. It assesses current appearance, mood, thought processes, orientation, and related
functions
C. It replaces case history
D. It is used only in research
✅Answer: B. It assesses current appearance, mood, thought processes, orientation, and
related functions
Rationale: A mental status examination evaluates the client’s current psychological
functioning across important observable domains.
48. In clinical diagnosis, case history data are most valuable because they:
A. Eliminate the need for tests
B. Provide developmental, medical, educational, and psychosocial context
C. Are always more accurate than direct observation
D. Require no verification
✅Answer: B. Provide developmental, medical, educational, and psychosocial context
Rationale: Case history data help place test findings and current symptoms within the
person’s broader life background.
49. A psychologist who writes a report that merely lists test scores without integrating referral
question, observations, and background data is most clearly failing in:
A. Score conversion
B. Interpretive synthesis
C. Test security
D. Standardization
✅Answer: B. Interpretive synthesis
Rationale: Interpretive synthesis involves integrating test findings with observations, history,
and referral issues to form meaningful conclusions.
50. The Barnum effect refers to the tendency for:
A. Highly specific feedback to be rejected
B. Vague, general personality descriptions to be accepted as uniquely accurate
C. Norms to become obsolete
D. Reliability to inflate validity
✅Answer: B. Vague, general personality descriptions to be accepted as uniquely accurate
Rationale: The Barnum effect occurs when people accept broad, generic statements as if
they were highly specific to themselves.
51. In suicide assessment, which factor is generally most urgent?
A. Favorite school subject
B. Access to lethal means plus intent and plan
C. Birth order
D. Number of siblings
✅Answer: B. Access to lethal means plus intent and plan
Rationale: Immediate suicide risk is most strongly shaped by the presence of intent, a specific
plan, and access to lethal means.
52. A custody evaluation should primarily focus on:
A. Which parent the evaluator personally prefers
B. Best interests of the child and parenting-related evidence
C. The child’s test score alone
D. Which party pays more
✅Answer: B. Best interests of the child and parenting-related evidence
Rationale: Custody evaluations are centered on the child’s welfare and on evidence relevant
to parenting capacity and family functioning.
53. In forensic assessment, the evaluator should be especially careful to:
A. Promise absolute confidentiality in all circumstances
B. Clarify role, purpose, and limits of confidentiality
C. Avoid documentation
D. Act as therapist and expert witness simultaneously whenever possible
✅Answer: B. Clarify role, purpose, and limits of confidentiality
Rationale: Forensic evaluators must clearly explain their role, the purpose of the evaluation,
and the limits of confidentiality because the context differs from therapy.
54. Which statement best reflects culturally informed clinical assessment?
A. Culture is relevant only in language testing
B. Cultural context may affect symptom expression, rapport, and interpretation
C. Standardized tests remove all cultural considerations
D. Cultural variables should be ignored to ensure fairness
✅Answer: B. Cultural context may affect symptom expression, rapport, and interpretation
Rationale: Culture can shape how symptoms are expressed, how rapport develops, and how
assessment findings should be interpreted.
55. A clinician assesses substance use, withdrawal symptoms, functional impairment, and
readiness for change. This is best described as:
A. Neuropsychological screening only
B. Comprehensive addiction assessment
C. Face validity estimation
D. Purely projective assessment
✅Answer: B. Comprehensive addiction assessment
Rationale: This approach evaluates multiple clinically relevant aspects of substance-related
functioning and treatment readiness.
56. Mechanical prediction is often contrasted with clinical prediction because mechanical
prediction:
A. Always ignores data
B. Uses explicit rules or formulas to combine information
C. Is equivalent to intuition
D. Cannot be studied empirically
✅Answer: B. Uses explicit rules or formulas to combine information
Rationale: Mechanical prediction relies on systematic, explicit methods for combining data
rather than subjective judgment alone.
57. A referral question asks whether a client’s memory complaints are better explained by
depression than by dementia. This requires the clinician to integrate:
A. Only one projective test
B. Differential diagnosis using multiple data sources
C. Only the client’s self-report
D. Norms from unrelated populations
✅Answer: B. Differential diagnosis using multiple data sources
Rationale: Distinguishing depression from dementia requires integration of interviews, history,
test results, observations, and other relevant data.
58. A psychologist receives a third-party referral from an employer. Ethically, the psychologist
should first clarify:
A. The brand of test materials to use
B. Who the client is, the evaluator’s role, probable uses of information, and limits of
confidentiality
C. How to maximize company profit only
D. Whether the employee is likable
✅Answer: B. Who the client is, the evaluator’s role, probable uses of information, and limits
of confidentiality
Rationale: In third-party referrals, the psychologist must clearly define the professional
relationship and the expected use and limits of the information obtained.
59. Which is the best example of a situational assessment item?
A. Asking for the definition of validity
B. Presenting a client vignette and requiring the most defensible assessment decision
C. Asking for the year Binet published his scale
D. Memorizing T scores only
✅Answer: B. Presenting a client vignette and requiring the most defensible assessment
decision
Rationale: Situational items assess the ability to apply knowledge and judgment to realistic
professional scenarios.
60. Which statement is most accurate regarding psychological reports?
A. Reports should be written so only specialists can understand them
B. Reports should answer the referral question and communicate findings clearly and
responsibly
C. Reports should include every raw score
D. Reports should avoid limitations
✅Answer: B. Reports should answer the referral question and communicate findings clearly
and responsibly
Rationale: A good psychological report should address the referral concern directly and
present findings in a clear, useful, and professionally responsible manner.
61. Neuropsychological assessment is most directly concerned with relationships between:
A. Personality style and astrology
B. Brain functioning and behavior
C. Moral reasoning and religion
D. Study habits and motivation only
✅Answer: B. Brain functioning and behavior
Rationale: Neuropsychological assessment focuses on how brain processes relate to
behavior and cognitive functioning.
62. A neuropsychological evaluation is especially indicated when there is concern about:
A. Favorite leisure activity
B. Possible cognitive effects of brain injury, dementia, seizure disorder, or neurological illness
C. Occupational interests only
D. Marital satisfaction only
✅Answer: B. Possible cognitive effects of brain injury, dementia, seizure disorder, or
neurological illness
Rationale: Neuropsychological evaluation is most appropriate when there is reason to
suspect cognitive or behavioral effects of neurological conditions.
63. Executive functions are most closely related to:
A. Color preference
B. Planning, inhibition, cognitive flexibility, and problem solving
C. Hearing acuity
D. Reading speed only
✅Answer: B. Planning, inhibition, cognitive flexibility, and problem solving
Rationale: Executive functions involve higher-order control processes needed for
goal-directed thinking and behavior.
64. Which test domain is most relevant when assessing aphasia?
A. Verbal functioning and language
B. Mechanical comprehension
C. Interest inventories
D. Figure drawing alone
✅Answer: A. Verbal functioning and language
Rationale: Aphasia is a disorder of language, so verbal and language assessment is the most
relevant domain.
65. The Bender-Gestalt and similar tasks are most often associated with assessment of:
A. Projective motivation
B. Visual-motor or perceptual-motor functioning
C. Career maturity
D. Creativity only
✅Answer: B. Visual-motor or perceptual-motor functioning
Rationale: The Bender-Gestalt is commonly used to assess visual-motor integration and
perceptual-motor functioning.
66. A patient with intact recognition but poor free recall on memory tasks may be showing:
A. A pattern relevant to memory process analysis
B. Proof of malingering automatically
C. Evidence of personality disorder only
D. No deficit at all
✅Answer: A. A pattern relevant to memory process analysis
Rationale: Differences between recognition and free recall can help identify the nature of
memory difficulties, such as retrieval versus storage problems.
67. Which of the following is most characteristic of dementia evaluation?
A. It relies on one score only
B. It may require integration of history, cognitive testing, behavioral observations, and medical
data
C. It excludes functional information
D. It is identical to aptitude testing
✅Answer: B. It may require integration of history, cognitive testing, behavioral observations,
and medical data
Rationale: Dementia evaluation requires multiple sources of information to understand
cognitive decline and its functional significance.
68. A neuropsychologist comparing current functioning with estimated premorbid ability is trying
to determine:
A. Astrological compatibility
B. Degree of decline from prior level of functioning
C. Occupational interests
D. Face validity
✅Answer: B. Degree of decline from prior level of functioning
Rationale: Comparing current performance with estimated premorbid ability helps determine
whether there has been cognitive decline.
69. Which pattern would most strongly warrant caution in interpreting neuropsychological test
results?
A. Adequate effort and valid responding
B. Severe fatigue, poor cooperation, or questionable effort
C. Clear referral question
D. Use of multiple measures
✅Answer: B. Severe fatigue, poor cooperation, or questionable effort
Rationale: Fatigue, poor cooperation, or questionable effort can undermine the validity of
neuropsychological test results.
70. In neuropsychological assessment, ecological validity refers most closely to:
A. Whether the test harms the physical environment
B. How well test performance relates to real-world functioning
C. Whether the test is projective
D. Whether the test is group-administered
✅Answer: B. How well test performance relates to real-world functioning
Rationale: Ecological validity concerns the extent to which test performance reflects
functioning in everyday life.
71. In industrial assessment, selection ratio refers to:
A. Number hired divided by number of applicants
B. Number of test items divided by number of scales
C. Number of supervisors divided by staff
D. Number of interviews divided by tests
✅Answer: A. Number hired divided by number of applicants
Rationale: The selection ratio is the proportion of applicants who are actually hired.
72. Utility analysis in personnel testing is primarily concerned with:
A. Whether a test looks fair
B. The practical value and cost-benefit consequences of using a test
C. The amount of item ambiguity
D. The projective quality of a measure
✅Answer: B. The practical value and cost-benefit consequences of using a test
Rationale: Utility analysis evaluates whether the benefits of using a test justify its costs in
real-world personnel decisions.
73. A structured behavioral interview is often preferred over an unstructured interview because
it:
A. Has no scoring criteria
B. Tends to improve consistency and job-relatedness
C. Eliminates all adverse impact
D. Measures personality unconsciously
✅Answer: B. Tends to improve consistency and job-relatedness
Rationale: Structured interviews increase consistency across applicants and better align
questions with job-relevant criteria.
74. Interest inventories are most useful for:
A. Diagnosing dementia
B. Identifying patterns of vocational preferences
C. Measuring raw intellectual power only
D. Replacing aptitude tests in all cases
✅Answer: B. Identifying patterns of vocational preferences
Rationale: Interest inventories help identify the types of activities, occupations, and work
environments a person tends to prefer.
75. The Strong Interest Inventory is primarily designed to assess:
A. Mood disorder severity
B. Vocational interests
C. Neurological soft signs
D. Response bias in malingering
✅Answer: B. Vocational interests
Rationale: The Strong Interest Inventory is a classic instrument used to assess vocational
interest patterns.
76. Which statement best reflects the use of cognitive ability tests in personnel selection?
A. They are irrelevant to job performance
B. They often predict performance but also raise fairness and diversity concerns
C. They should replace all other data
D. They are projective
✅Answer: B. They often predict performance but also raise fairness and diversity concerns
Rationale: Cognitive ability tests can be strong predictors of job performance, but their use
also raises concerns about fairness and subgroup differences.
77. A company wants to place employees into roles that match both their interests and abilities.
This is most consistent with:
A. Classification and placement
B. Random assignment
C. Pure psychotherapy
D. Forensic referral
✅Answer: A. Classification and placement
Rationale: Classification and placement involve assigning individuals to roles that best fit their
abilities, characteristics, and interests.
78. Job analysis is important because it:
A. Makes all interviews unnecessary
B. Identifies the tasks and KSAs relevant to job performance
C. Guarantees no bias
D. Measures employee satisfaction directly
✅Answer: B. Identifies the tasks and KSAs relevant to job performance
Rationale: Job analysis identifies the duties of a job and the knowledge, skills, and abilities
required for effective performance.
79. A counselor using Holland-type themes is most likely working within:
A. Vocational interest assessment
B. Neuropsychological battery interpretation
C. Projective personality testing only
D. Forensic malingering detection
✅Answer: A. Vocational interest assessment
Rationale: Holland themes are used in vocational assessment to classify interests and
occupational environments.
80. In business settings, organizational culture assessment is most relevant for understanding:
A. Only employee IQ
B. Shared values, norms, and work environment characteristics
C. Visual-motor deficits
D. Mental age
✅Answer: B. Shared values, norms, and work environment characteristics
Rationale: Organizational culture assessment examines the values, norms, and
environmental characteristics that shape workplace behavior.
81. Under RA 10029 as reflected in the PAP Code, who may legally practice the profession of
psychology and psychometrics?
A. Any graduate of psychology
B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians
C. Any counselor with field experience
D. Any teacher trained in guidance
✅Answer: B. Only licensed and registered psychologists and psychometricians
Rationale: RA 10029 and the PAP Code limit legal practice of psychology and psychometrics
to those who are licensed and registered.
82. According to the PAP Code, psychometricians:
A. May independently practice psychotherapy routinely
B. Are prohibited from therapy except in emergency situations
C. May release raw test data freely
D. Need no supervision under any circumstance
✅Answer: B. Are prohibited from therapy except in emergency situations
Rationale: The PAP Code states that psychometricians are not allowed to provide therapy
except in emergency situations.
83. Which action is most consistent with the PAP Code on test materials?
A. Using photocopied test booklets when the originals are unavailable
B. Using only original copies of test materials
C. Posting sample secure items online for convenience
D. Allowing any staff member to handle answer keys
✅Answer: B. Using only original copies of test materials
Rationale: Ethical use of test materials requires original copies in order to preserve test
integrity and security.
84. Which statement best reflects ethical test security?
A. Secure materials may be handled by anyone in the clinic
B. Test materials should be handled only by qualified or licensed users/personnel
C. Test security matters only for intelligence tests
D. Answer sheets may be left in public workspaces
✅Answer: B. Test materials should be handled only by qualified or licensed users/personnel
Rationale: Ethical test security requires that secure materials be handled only by persons
qualified or authorized to use them.
85. Which of the following is generally prohibited unless regulated by the court?
A. Explaining results in simple language
B. Releasing raw and scaled scores, item responses, and behavioral notes to unauthorized
persons
C. Obtaining informed consent
D. Using standardized instruments
✅Answer: B. Releasing raw and scaled scores, item responses, and behavioral notes to
unauthorized persons
Rationale: Raw and scaled scores, item responses, and behavioral notes are protected
assessment data and are not to be released to unauthorized persons unless legally required.
86. A client self-refers for assessment and later asks that results be sent to an employer. Under
the PAP Code, release is proper when:
A. The employer requests it verbally
B. The psychologist decides independently
C. There is written permission from the client
D. The results are favorable
✅Answer: C. There is written permission from the client
Rationale: When a client self-refers, release of results to a third party requires the client’s
written authorization.
87. Which is an ethical exception to obtaining informed consent prior to assessment?
A. Whenever the assessor is in a hurry
B. When assessment is mandated by law, implied in routine institutional activity, or for
decisional capacity
C. When the client seems anxious
D. When the referral source prefers secrecy
✅Answer: B. When assessment is mandated by law, implied in routine institutional activity,
or for decisional capacity
Rationale: Informed consent may not be required in certain legally or institutionally mandated
contexts, as recognized by ethical standards.
88. A psychologist is asked to provide an expert opinion without personally examining the
individual but only by reviewing old records. Ethically, the psychologist should:
A. Present the conclusion as definitive
B. Discuss the limitations and basis of the opinion
C. Refuse to document anything
D. Assume the records are sufficient in all cases
✅Answer: B. Discuss the limitations and basis of the opinion
Rationale: When an opinion is based on records rather than direct examination, the
psychologist must clearly state its basis and limitations.
89. Which action best reflects competence under the PAP Code?
A. Accepting every referral regardless of training
B. Practicing beyond one’s competence if the fee is high
C. Making appropriate referrals when existing competence is insufficient
D. Using outdated methods because they are familiar
✅Answer: C. Making appropriate referrals when existing competence is insufficient
Rationale: Ethical competence includes recognizing one’s limits and referring clients when the
required expertise is lacking.
90. A practitioner wants to begin using a new teleassessment platform never before used in the
clinic. The most ethical course is to:
A. Start immediately without training
B. Undertake relevant training, study, consultation, or supervised experience first
C. Delegate the task to untrained staff
D. Ignore internet-related limitations
✅Answer: B. Undertake relevant training, study, consultation, or supervised experience first
Rationale: Ethical practice requires developing competence in new techniques or
technologies before using them in professional work.
91. Which of the following best reflects the PAP Code on confidentiality?
A. Confidentiality applies only to written notes
B. Confidentiality applies regardless of the medium in which information is stored
C. Confidentiality ends once testing is over
D. Confidentiality does not apply to digital records
✅Answer: B. Confidentiality applies regardless of the medium in which information is stored
Rationale: Confidentiality covers all client information, whether stored in written, electronic, or
other formats.
92. A psychologist conducting online assessment should specifically inform the client about:
A. Favorite color of the examiner
B. Risks to privacy and, in teleassessment, implications of poor internet connectivity
C. The scorer’s salary
D. National passing rates only
✅Answer: B. Risks to privacy and, in teleassessment, implications of poor internet
connectivity
Rationale: Ethical online assessment requires informing clients about privacy risks and
practical limitations such as unstable internet connections.
93. Which situation best illustrates a problematic multiple relationship?
A. A psychologist administers a test to a stranger in a hospital
B. A psychologist begins assessment of a close friend whose welfare may impair objectivity
C. A psychologist explains limits of confidentiality
D. A psychologist consults a colleague anonymously
✅Answer: B. A psychologist begins assessment of a close friend whose welfare may impair
objectivity
Rationale: A multiple relationship is problematic when it creates a risk of impaired objectivity,
exploitation, or harm.
94. A practitioner becomes aware that personal stress is seriously impairing professional
judgment. Ethical practice requires the practitioner to:
A. Continue working as usual
B. Obtain consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or terminating duties
C. Conceal the problem
D. Shift blame to clients
✅Answer: B. Obtain consultation or assistance and consider limiting, suspending, or
terminating duties
Rationale: When personal problems impair competence, the practitioner must seek help and
consider reducing or suspending professional duties.
95. Which statement best reflects the Code regarding use of assessment by unqualified
persons?
A. It is encouraged to maximize service reach
B. It is not promoted except for training purposes with adequate supervision
C. It is allowed if the test is brief
D. It is acceptable if the unqualified person has seen the test before
✅Answer: B. It is not promoted except for training purposes with adequate supervision
Rationale: Assessment by unqualified persons is generally not permitted except in supervised
training situations.
96. In explaining assessment results to relatives or teachers, the ethical standard is to:
A. Use highly technical terminology to preserve prestige
B. Explain results in nontechnical language
C. Release the raw protocol instead
D. Avoid any explanation
✅Answer: B. Explain results in nontechnical language
Rationale: Ethical communication of results requires using language that the intended
recipient can reasonably understand.
97. Which practice best aligns with the PAP Code on outdated tests?
A. Continue using obsolete tests if clients know them
B. Base conclusions on outdated results if they save time
C. Avoid basing interpretations and recommendations on obsolete tests or outdated results
D. Use outdated norms if no one notices
✅Answer: C. Avoid basing interpretations and recommendations on obsolete tests or
outdated results
Rationale: Ethical assessment requires using current tests and data because obsolete
instruments or outdated results can lead to invalid conclusions.
98. A psychometrician working in an assessment center should understand that, when
applicable, practice occurs:
A. Entirely independently from any psychologist
B. Under the supervision of a registered psychologist and within RA 10029 boundaries
C. Without any ethical constraints
D. Only in educational settings
✅Answer: B. Under the supervision of a registered psychologist and within RA 10029
boundaries
Rationale: The practice of psychometricians is governed by legal and ethical limits, including
supervision requirements where applicable under RA 10029.
99. A psychologist providing services requested by a third party should clarify all of the following
at the outset except:
A. Expected role
B. Who the client is
C. Probable uses of information and limits of confidentiality
D. A promise that all results will remain absolutely secret from everyone
✅Answer: D. A promise that all results will remain absolutely secret from everyone
Rationale: Absolute secrecy cannot be promised in third-party referrals because the
psychologist must clarify the likely uses of information and the limits of confidentiality.
100. Which of the following best captures the core ethical stance for board-level psychological
assessment practice?
A. Maximize income even if validity is uncertain
B. Use any available tool as long as it is quick
C. Base conclusions on substantial information, appropriate techniques, competence, and
protection of client welfare
D. Release all data to avoid complaints
✅Answer: C. Base conclusions on substantial information, appropriate techniques,
competence, and protection of client welfare
Rationale: Ethical board-level assessment requires competent, evidence-based practice that
protects client welfare and supports defensible conclusions.
